---

# 47. HARAPPAN ANIMALS IN ART AND LIFE

## Unicorn
Most common seal animal, mythical or symbolic.

## Bull
Symbol of strength and agriculture.

## Elephant
Wild and possibly domesticated animal known to Harappans.

## Rhinoceros
Wild animal shown on seals.

## Tiger
Wild animal shown in art.

## Buffalo
Animal shown on seals and known in life.

## Goat
Domestic animal.

## Sheep
Domestic animal.

## Dog
Domestic animal.

## Monkey
Shown in figurines and known in environment.

## Bird
Bird motifs appear in pottery and figurines.

## Peacock
Bird motif known in Indian environment.

## Fish
Important in diet and symbolism.

## Crocodile
Aquatic animal known in river regions.

## Snake
Symbolic and natural animal.

## Composite Animal
Imaginary animal combining features of several animals.

---

# 48. HARAPPAN PLANTS AND SYMBOLIC FLORA

## Pipal
A tree shown in Harappan imagery and sacred in later Indian tradition.

## Acacia
A tree known in dry regions.

## Date Palm
A useful tree producing dates.

## Cotton Plant
Plant used for textile production.

## Wheat Plant
Main cereal crop.

## Barley Plant
Main cereal crop.

## Sesame Plant
Oilseed crop.

## Mustard Plant
Oilseed crop.

## Rice Plant
Known in some Harappan regions.

## Millet Plant
Cultivated in some regions.

## Tree Motif
Tree symbol used in pottery and seals.

## Leaf Motif
Leaf-like decorative design.

---

# 49. HARAPPAN CITIES AND ABSENCE OF CERTAIN FEATURES

## No Deciphered Literature
Harappans had writing, but it cannot yet be read.

## No Known Kings
No king names are known because the script is undeciphered.

## No Known Laws
No legal code has been found or read.

## No Known Epic
No Harappan literary text is known.

## No Clear Temple
No definite temple has been identified.

## No Clear Palace
No definite palace has been identified.

## No Massive Royal Tombs
Harappan burials are modest compared to Egyptian royal tombs.

## No Monumental Statues of Rulers
Harappan art lacks huge ruler statues.

## No Clear War Scenes
Harappan art does not commonly show battle scenes.

## No Coinage
Harappans did not use coins. Exchange likely used barter, weights, and goods.

## No Iron
Mature Harappan civilization was Bronze Age; iron was not a normal Harappan metal.

---

# 50. COMMONLY CONFUSED TERMS

## Harappa vs Harappan Civilization
Harappa is one site. Harappan Civilization is the entire civilization.

## Mohenjo-daro vs Harappa
Both are major cities, but Mohenjo-daro is in Sindh and Harappa is in Punjab.

## Dholavira vs Lothal
Dholavira is famous for water management and signboard. Lothal is famous for dockyard-like structure and bead trade.

## Kalibangan vs Lothal
Kalibangan is famous for ploughed field and fire altars. Lothal is famous for dockyard-like basin and bead-making.

## Rakhigarhi vs Harappa
Rakhigarhi is in Haryana and is among the largest sites. Harappa is in Pakistan and gave the civilization its name.

## Ganeriwala vs Mohenjo-daro
Ganeriwala is a large but less excavated site. Mohenjo-daro is extensively excavated and famous for the Great Bath.

## Sutkagendor vs Alamgirpur
Sutkagendor is near the western coastal limit. Alamgirpur marks the eastern limit.

## Daimabad vs Manda
Daimabad is often considered the southern limit. Manda in Jammu is often considered the northern limit.

## Mature Harappan vs Late Harappan
Mature Harappan is the urban peak. Late Harappan is the post-urban regional phase.

## Indus Script vs Brahmi
Indus script is older and undeciphered. Brahmi is later and deciphered.

## Harappan Seals vs Coins
Harappan seals were not coins. They were used for identity, trade, or administration.

## Baked Brick vs Mud Brick
Baked bricks are kiln-fired and stronger. Mud bricks are sun-dried.

## Bronze vs Iron
Bronze was used by Harappans. Iron became common much later.

## Aryan Invasion Theory vs Harappan Decline
The old idea that Aryans destroyed Harappan cities is not accepted in its earlier simplistic form.

## Saraswati Debate vs Proven Fact
Many Harappan sites are on Ghaggar-Hakra, but identifying it directly with the Vedic Saraswati remains debated.

---

# 51. IMPORTANT HARAPPAN LIMITS

## Northern Limit
Manda in Jammu is often cited as the northern limit of Harappan influence.

## Southern Limit
Daimabad in Maharashtra is often cited as the southern limit.

## Eastern Limit
Alamgirpur in western Uttar Pradesh is often cited as the eastern limit.

## Western Limit
Sutkagendor near the Makran coast is often cited as the western limit.

## Largest Sites
Rakhigarhi, Mohenjo-daro, Harappa, Dholavira, and Ganeriwala are among the largest Harappan sites.

---

# 52. SITE-WISE QUICK GLOSSARY FOR PRELIMS

## Harappa
First discovered major site; located in Punjab, Pakistan; known for cemetery, granary-like structures, seals, and urban planning.

## Mohenjo-daro
Located in Sindh, Pakistan; known for Great Bath, Dancing Girl, Priest-King, drainage, wells, and large buildings.

## Dholavira
Located in Kachchh, Gujarat; known for water reservoirs, signboard, stone architecture, and three-part city plan.

## Rakhigarhi
Located in Haryana; among the largest Harappan sites; important for burials, settlement scale, and DNA studies.

## Ganeriwala
Located in Cholistan, Pakistan; one of the largest sites but less excavated.

## Lothal
Located in Gujarat; known for dockyard-like basin, warehouse, bead factory, and trade.

## Kalibangan
Located in Rajasthan; known for ploughed field, fire altars, and fortified settlement.

## Banawali
Located in Haryana; known for pre-Harappan and Harappan levels, fortification, and town planning.

## Chanhudaro
Located in Sindh; known for bead-making, seal-making, and craft specialization.

## Surkotada
Located in Kachchh, Gujarat; known for fortification and debated horse remains.

## Rangpur
Located in Gujarat; known for late Harappan levels and rice-related evidence.

## Rojdi
Located in Gujarat; regional Harappan settlement.

## Daimabad
Located in Maharashtra; southern limit; known for bronze objects and late Harappan association.

## Alamgirpur
Located in western Uttar Pradesh; eastern limit of Harappan influence.

## Sutkagendor
Located near Makran coast; western limit and coastal trade outpost.

## Balakot
Located in Balochistan; known for coastal trade and shell industry.

## Nageshwar
Located in Gujarat; known for shell-working.

## Kuntasi
Located in Gujarat; craft and trade center.

## Farmana
Located in Haryana; known for cemetery and settlement remains.

## Bhirrana
Located in Haryana; known for early cultural levels.

## Kunal
Located in Haryana; early Harappan site with ornaments and craft evidence.

## Mitathal
Located in Haryana; early and mature Harappan occupation.

## Bhagwanpura
Located in Haryana; late Harappan and PGW overlap.

## Ropar
Located in Punjab; Harappan and later cultural sequence.

## Kot Diji
Located in Sindh; important early Harappan fortified site.

## Amri
Located in Sindh; early Harappan regional culture.

## Mehrgarh
Located in Balochistan; early farming village and pre-Harappan background.

## Nausharo
Located in Balochistan; transition from early farming to Harappan phases.

---

# 53. HIGH-YIELD HARAPPAN FIRSTS AND SPECIAL FEATURES

## First Urbanization
Harappan Civilization represents the first urbanization in the Indian subcontinent.

## Earliest Cotton Evidence
Harappans were among the earliest known users of cotton.

## Earliest Ploughed Field
Kalibangan provides important early evidence of a ploughed field.

## Advanced Drainage
Harappan cities had highly developed covered drains and soak pits.

## Great Bath
Mohenjo-daro’s Great Bath is one of the most famous public structures.

## Dholavira Water Management
Dholavira is the best example of Harappan water conservation and reservoir planning.

## Lothal Dockyard
Lothal is famous for a dockyard-like basin associated with trade.

## Standardized Weights
Harappans used a highly standardized weight system.

## Standardized Bricks
Harappan bricks often followed the 1:2:4 ratio.

## Undeciphered Script
The Indus script remains undeciphered.

## No Coins
Harappans did not use coinage.

## No Iron
Mature Harappan civilization was Bronze Age, not Iron Age.

## No Clear King
No king or dynasty is known from Harappan evidence.

## No Clear Temple
No definite temple has been found.

## No Clear Palace
No definite palace has been found.

---

# 54. UPSC PRELIMS FACT CLUSTERS

## Main Civilization Name
Indus Valley Civilization or Harappan Civilization.

## Main Period
Mature phase: c. 2600–1900 BCE.

## Main Material Culture
Bronze, copper, baked bricks, seals, pottery, beads, faience, shell, terracotta.

## Main Urban Features
Citadel, lower town, grid planning, drainage, wells, bathrooms, public buildings.

## Main Economic Base
Agriculture, animal husbandry, crafts, and trade.

## Main Crops
Wheat, barley, peas, lentils, sesame, mustard, cotton, and regional rice/millets.

## Main Animals
Cattle, buffalo, sheep, goat, pig, dog, elephant, camel, and wild animals in art.

## Main Crafts
Bead-making, pottery, metallurgy, shell work, faience, seal-making, weaving.

## Main Trade Partners
Mesopotamia, Dilmun, Magan, Afghanistan, Iran, Oman, and Persian Gulf regions.

## Main Script Feature
Undeciphered, short inscriptions, mostly on seals.

## Main Religious Evidence
Mother goddess figurines, Pashupati seal, fire altars, pipal motif, Great Bath, amulets.

## Main Decline Factors
Climate change, river shifts, trade decline, floods, ecological stress, and regionalization.

## Main Post-Urban Cultures
Cemetery H, Jhukar, Rangpur, Bara, and other regional late Harappan cultures.

---

# 55. CHRONOLOGICAL SNAPSHOT

## Stage 1: Neolithic-Chalcolithic Background
Mehrgarh and similar sites show farming, animal domestication, pottery, village life, and early crafts.

## Stage 2: Early Harappan / Regionalization
Sites like Kot Diji, Amri, Kalibangan, Banawali, Kunal, Bhirrana, and Rehman Dheri show fortified settlements, regional pottery, craft growth, and proto-urban features.

## Stage 3: Mature Harappan / Urban Integration
Large planned cities like Harappa, Mohenjo-daro, Dholavira, Rakhigarhi, Ganeriwala, Lothal, and Kalibangan show standard bricks, seals, weights, drainage, trade, craft specialization, and urban administration.

## Stage 4: Late Harappan / Localization
Urban centers declined, seals and script reduced, standardization weakened, and regional cultures like Cemetery H, Jhukar, Rangpur, and Bara emerged.

## Stage 5: Post-Harappan Legacy
Some rural settlements, crops, crafts, symbols, and regional traditions continued, while later cultures developed separately in different parts of the subcontinent.

---

# 56. FINAL REVISION CLUSTER FOR UPSC PRELIMS

## Must Remember Sites
Harappa, Mohenjo-daro, Dholavira, Rakhigarhi, Ganeriwala, Lothal, Kalibangan, Banawali, Chanhudaro, Surkotada, Rangpur, Daimabad, Alamgirpur, Sutkagendor, Mehrgarh.

## Must Remember Site Features
Mohenjo-daro: Great Bath, Dancing Girl, Priest-King.
Harappa: cemetery, granary-like structures.
Dholavira: reservoirs, signboard, three-part city.
Lothal: dockyard-like basin, warehouse, bead factory.
Kalibangan: ploughed field, fire altars.
Chanhudaro: bead-making and seal-making.
Surkotada: debated horse remains.
Rakhigarhi: large site, burials, DNA importance.
Daimabad: southern limit and bronze objects.
Alamgirpur: eastern limit.
Sutkagendor: western limit.

## Must Remember Economy
Agriculture, cattle-rearing, bead-making, metallurgy, pottery, shell work, cotton, internal trade, external trade.

## Must Remember Trade Terms
Meluhha, Dilmun, Magan, Mesopotamia, Persian Gulf, Oman copper, lapis lazuli, carnelian, shell, seals, weights.

## Must Remember Urban Features
Citadel, lower town, grid planning, baked bricks, covered drains, soak pits, wells, bathrooms, reservoirs, warehouses.

## Must Remember Script and Seals
Indus script, undeciphered, short inscriptions, steatite seals, unicorn motif, Pashupati seal, Dholavira signboard.

## Must Remember Religion
Mother goddess, Pashupati seal, pipal tree, fire altars, Great Bath, amulets, swastika, animal motifs.

## Must Remember Decline
Not a sudden collapse everywhere; caused by multiple factors including climate change, river shifts, floods, trade decline, and deurbanization.

## Must Remember What Harappans Did Not Have Clearly
No deciphered script, no known kings, no coins, no iron in mature phase, no clear temples, no clear palaces, no huge royal tombs.

## Must Remember Comparison
Harappan Civilization = urban, bronze age, planned cities, script, seals, trade.
Early Vedic Culture = pastoral, oral, tribal, Sanskrit hymns, cattle-centered society.

## One-Line Essence
The Harappan Civilization was the first great urban civilization of the Indian subcontinent, marked by planned cities, drainage, standardized weights and bricks, craft specialization, long-distance trade, undeciphered script, and gradual regional decline after c. 1900 BCE.



------


# VEDIC PERIOD GLOSSARY FOR UPSC PRELIMS
## Chronological Coverage: Early Rigvedic Period → Later Vedic Period → Upanishadic/Sutra Transition

> Note: The Vedic period is generally divided into:
> 1. Early Rigvedic Period: c. 1500–1000 BCE
> 2. Later Vedic Period: c. 1000–600 BCE
> 3. Upanishadic/Sutra Transition: c. 700–500 BCE, overlapping with the end of the Later Vedic age

---

# 1. BASIC SOURCE TERMS OF THE VEDIC PERIOD

## Veda
The oldest sacred literature of India. The word means “knowledge”. The four Vedas are Rigveda, Samaveda, Yajurveda, and Atharvaveda.

## Shruti
Literally “that which is heard”. It refers to the most sacred texts believed to be revealed, including the Vedas, Brahmanas, Aranyakas, and Upanishads.

## Smriti
Literally “that which is remembered”. These are later traditional texts like Dharmasutras, Dharmashastras, Epics, and Puranas.

## Samhita
A collection of hymns, prayers, chants, or formulas. Each Veda has a Samhita.

## Brahmana
A prose text attached to a Veda. It explains rituals, sacrifices, priests, meanings of offerings, and religious duties.

## Aranyaka
Literally “forest text”. These texts discuss meditation, symbolic meanings of rituals, and spiritual ideas. They form a bridge between Brahmanas and Upanishads.

## Upanishad
Philosophical texts dealing with Brahman, Atman, karma, rebirth, moksha, and ultimate reality.

## Vedanga
Auxiliary disciplines used to understand and preserve the Vedas. The six Vedangas are Shiksha, Kalpa, Vyakarana, Nirukta, Chandas, and Jyotisha.

## Shakha
A branch or school of Vedic learning. Different shakhas preserved different versions of Vedic texts.

## Charana
A Vedic school or group of students following a particular tradition of recitation and interpretation.

## Mantra
A sacred verse or formula recited during rituals.

## Sukta
A hymn in the Rigveda. It usually contains several verses dedicated to a deity.

## Richa
A single verse of the Rigveda.

## Yajna
A sacrificial ritual in which offerings are made into fire.

## Havis
An offering made in a Vedic sacrifice, such as ghee, grain, milk, or Soma.

## Ghrita
Clarified butter or ghee, commonly used as an offering in Vedic rituals.

## Soma
A sacred plant, drink, and deity in the Rigveda. It was used in rituals and associated with energy, inspiration, and immortality.

## Srauta
Related to large public Vedic sacrifices based on Shruti texts.

## Grihya
Related to domestic rituals performed by householders.

## Kalpa
A Vedanga dealing with ritual procedure.

## Sutra
A short rule-like text. Sutras are concise and easy to memorize.

## Shrauta Sutra
A text explaining large public sacrifices.

## Grihya Sutra
A text explaining domestic ceremonies like marriage, birth rituals, and upanayana.

## Dharma Sutra
A text dealing with social duties, law, conduct, and varna-ashrama norms.

## Shulba Sutra
A text dealing with geometry used in constructing Vedic sacrificial altars.

---

# 2. EARLY RIGVEDIC PERIOD: GENERAL CHARACTER

## Early Rigvedic Period
The earliest phase of the Vedic age, mainly reflected in the Rigveda. Society was largely pastoral, tribal, semi-nomadic, and located mostly in the north-western subcontinent.

## Rigvedic Civilization
The civilization described in the Rigveda. It was based on cattle wealth, clan organization, tribal assemblies, simple rituals, and worship of natural forces.

## Pastoralism
A way of life based mainly on cattle-rearing. Early Vedic society gave great importance to cows, bulls, horses, and other animals.

## Semi-nomadic Life
A lifestyle in which people moved with their cattle but also had temporary or semi-permanent settlements.

## Tribal Society
A society organized around tribes, clans, and kinship rather than large territorial states.

## Clan
A group of people claiming common ancestry.

## Kinship
Social relations based on family, lineage, and clan ties.

## Patriarchal Society
A society in which the father or eldest male had authority in the family.

## Oral Tradition
The system by which Vedic texts were memorized and transmitted by word of mouth for generations.

## Vedic Sanskrit
The language of the Vedas. It is older than Classical Sanskrit.

---

# 3. EARLY RIGVEDIC GEOGRAPHY

## Sapta Sindhu
The “land of seven rivers”. It refers to the north-western region where early Vedic people lived.

## Sindhu
The Indus River. It was one of the most important rivers mentioned in the Rigveda.

## Sarasvati
A river praised highly in the Rigveda. It was considered mighty and sacred.

## Drishadvati
A river associated with the Vedic region, especially later with Brahmavarta.

## Parushni
The Ravi River. It is associated with the Battle of Ten Kings.

## Vipasha
The Beas River.

## Shutudri
The Sutlej River.

## Asikni
The Chenab River.

## Vitasta
The Jhelum River.

## Kubha
The Kabul River.

## Krumu
The Kurram River.

## Gomati
The Gomal River in the north-western region.

## Suvastu
The Swat River.

## Rasā
A river mentioned in the Rigveda, sometimes interpreted as a distant or mythical river.

## Ganga
The Ganges. It is mentioned rarely in the Rigveda, showing that the early Vedic focus was not yet the middle Ganga plains.

## Yamuna
The Yamuna River. It is mentioned more than the Ganga but was still not the main focus of early Rigvedic society.

## Brahmavarta
A later Vedic sacred region between the Sarasvati and Drishadvati rivers.

## Aryavarta
The “land of the Aryas”. In later texts, it referred to the region of Vedic culture in northern India.

## Madhyadesha
The “middle country”, especially the Ganga-Yamuna doab and nearby regions in later Vedic culture.

---

# 4. EARLY RIGVEDIC TEXTUAL TERMS

## Rigveda
The oldest Veda and the oldest Indo-Aryan text. It contains hymns dedicated mainly to deities like Indra, Agni, Soma, Varuna, and Ushas.

## Mandala
A book or section of the Rigveda. The Rigveda has 10 Mandalas.

## Family Books
Mandalas 2 to 7 of the Rigveda. They are considered the oldest parts and are linked with specific priestly families.

## Later Mandalas
Mandalas 1, 8, 9, and 10 are generally considered later than the family books.

## Ninth Mandala
The Mandala mainly dedicated to Soma.

## Tenth Mandala
A later Mandala containing important hymns like Purusha Sukta and Nasadiya Sukta.

## Gayatri Mantra
A famous Rigvedic mantra dedicated to Savitr. It is found in the third Mandala.

## Nasadiya Sukta
A philosophical hymn in the Rigveda about creation. It questions how the universe came into existence.

## Purusha Sukta
A hymn in the tenth Mandala describing the cosmic being Purusha and the origin of the four varnas.

## Hiranyagarbha Sukta
A hymn referring to the “golden embryo” or cosmic source of creation.

## Nadi Sukta
A hymn praising rivers, especially the rivers of the north-western region.

## Devi Sukta
A hymn in which the goddess speaks as the supreme power.

## Aksha Sukta
A hymn dealing with gambling and its harmful effects.

## Dana Stuti
Hymns praising generous gift-givers or patrons.

## Apri Sukta
A ritual hymn used during sacrifices to invite deities.

## Vivaha Sukta
A marriage hymn in the Rigveda.

## Antyeshti Hymn
A funeral hymn dealing with death and afterlife ideas.

## Manduka Sukta
A hymn comparing frogs to chanting priests, often linked with the rainy season.

## Tryambaka Mantra
A mantra addressed to Rudra, later known as the Mahamrityunjaya Mantra.

---

# 5. EARLY RIGVEDIC TRIBES AND PEOPLES

## Arya
A term used in the Vedas meaning noble, respectable, or belonging to the Vedic cultural group.

## Jana
A tribe or people. It was the main political unit in the Early Vedic period.

## Vish
A clan or group of common people within a jana.

## Grama
A village or moving group of families. In early usage, it could also mean a group on the move.

## Kula
Family or household.

## Gotra
Lineage or clan identity. In later times, it became important in marriage rules.

## Bharata
An important Rigvedic tribe. The name later became associated with India as Bharat.

## Puru
A major Rigvedic tribe. The Bharatas and Purus later became important in the formation of the Kuru people.

## Tritsu
A group associated with King Sudas in the Battle of Ten Kings.

## Yadu
One of the five major tribes mentioned in the Rigveda.

## Turvasha
One of the major Rigvedic tribes.

## Anu
One of the major Rigvedic tribes.

## Druhyu
One of the major Rigvedic tribes.

## Pancha Jana
The “five peoples” or five major tribes often identified as Yadu, Turvasha, Anu, Druhyu, and Puru.

## Dasa
A term used in the Rigveda for hostile groups or outsiders. It later came to mean servant or slave.

## Dasyu
A term used for non-Vedic or hostile groups. They are described as not following Vedic rituals.

## Pani
A group described in the Rigveda as wealthy but ungenerous and sometimes hostile. They are associated with cattle and trade-like activity.

## Nishada
A non-Vedic or forest-dwelling group mentioned in later Vedic literature.

## Kirata
A term later used for hill or forest tribes.

## Mleccha
A later term for people considered outside the Sanskritic/Vedic cultural order.

---

# 6. EARLY RIGVEDIC POLITY

## Rajan
The tribal chief or king. In the Early Vedic period, he was not an absolute monarch.

## Gopa
Protector of cattle. The king was sometimes described as protector of cattle and people.

## Gopati
Lord or protector of cattle.

## Janasya Gopa
Protector of the tribe or people; an expression used for the king.

## Vispati
Leader of the vish or clan.

## Gramani
Head of the grama. He may have led a village group or fighting unit.

## Senani
Military commander.

## Purohita
The priest and adviser of the king. He performed rituals for victory and prosperity.

## Duta
Messenger or envoy.

## Spasha
Spy or observer.

## Sabha
An assembly of elders or important people. It had social, political, and judicial functions.

## Samiti
A general tribal assembly. It was broader than the sabha and could influence the choice of king.

## Vidatha
An early assembly connected with military, religious, and social activities. It was important in early Rigvedic society.

## Gana
A group, tribe, or corporate body. Later it also meant a republican group.

## Vrat
A band or group of warriors.

## Sardha
A troop or fighting group.

## Bali
A voluntary offering or tribute given to the chief. It was not yet a regular tax in the early period.

## Bhaga
Share or portion. In later times, it became associated with the king’s share of produce.

## Kara
Tax or payment. It became clearer in later Vedic and post-Vedic times.

## Rashtra
Territory or kingdom. The idea became more important in the Later Vedic period.

## Rajya
Kingship or kingdom.

## Samraj
A great king or overlord. The idea became stronger in later Vedic texts.

---

# 7. EARLY RIGVEDIC CONFLICTS AND EVENTS

## Dasarajna
The Battle of Ten Kings. It was fought on the banks of the Parushni River.

## Battle of Ten Kings
A major Rigvedic battle in which King Sudas of the Bharata/Tritsu group defeated a confederacy of tribes.

## Sudas
A famous Rigvedic king associated with the Bharatas and the Battle of Ten Kings.

## Vasistha
A major Rigvedic priest. He was associated with King Sudas.

## Vishvamitra
A famous sage who was also connected with early Rigvedic political traditions.

## Parushni Battle
Another name for the Battle of Ten Kings because it took place near the Parushni River.

## Bharata-Puru Merger
The process by which the Bharata and Puru groups later contributed to the rise of the Kuru people.

## Cattle Raid
A common form of conflict in the Early Vedic period, as cattle were the main form of wealth.

## Gavishthi
Literally “search for cows”. It often meant battle or cattle raid.

## Goshu
Conflict or struggle for cattle.

## Gavyuti
A measure of distance related to cattle movement.

---

# 8. EARLY RIGVEDIC ECONOMY

## Cattle Wealth
Cows were the main form of wealth in Early Vedic society.

## Go
Cow. The most important economic animal of the Rigvedic people.

## Aghnya
A cow “not to be killed”. It shows the special value attached to cows.

## Gomati
Rich in cattle.

## Gavishti
Search for cows; also used for war.

## Gopa
Cowherd or protector of cattle.

## Ashva
Horse. It was important for mobility, war, and prestige.

## Ratha
Chariot. It was used in warfare and elite display.

## Chakra
Wheel. Spoked wheels were important for chariots.

## Anas
Cart or wagon.

## Yava
Barley. It was the main grain mentioned in the Rigveda.

## Dhanya
Grain in general.

## Urvara
Fertile land.

## Kshetra
Cultivated field. More important in later Vedic literature.

## Krishi
Agriculture. It was present but less dominant in the Early Rigvedic period.

## Langala
Plough. It became more important in the Later Vedic period.

## Sita
Furrow. Later also personified as an agricultural goddess.

## Ayas
Metal. In the Rigveda it probably referred mainly to copper or bronze, not necessarily iron.

## Hiranya
Gold. Used for ornaments and prestige goods.

## Nishka
A gold ornament or neck-piece. It was not a regular coin in the Rigvedic period.

## Vanij
Trader or merchant.

## Pani
A group associated with wealth, cattle, and exchange; often shown negatively in the Rigveda.

## Dana
Gift. Gift-giving was important for chiefs and patrons.

## Dakshina
Gift or fee given to priests after rituals.

## Shulka
Toll, fee, or price. It becomes more visible in later texts.

## Samudra
Sea or large body of water. The exact meaning in the Rigveda can vary.

## Nau
Boat.

---

# 9. EARLY RIGVEDIC SOCIAL LIFE

## Griha
House or household.

## Grihapati
Head of the household.

## Dampati
Husband and wife as joint householders.

## Patni
Wife. The wife had ritual importance in many sacrifices.

## Putra
Son. Sons were valued for lineage and rituals.

## Duhitr
Daughter. The word is often linked with milking, reflecting pastoral imagery.

## Pitr
Father or ancestor.

## Matri
Mother.

## Bhratri
Brother.

## Jami
Kin or relative.

## Varna
A broad social category. In the Early Vedic period, varna divisions were not yet rigid.

## Brahmana
Priestly group associated with hymns and rituals.

## Kshatra
Power or warrior authority.

## Kshatriya
Warrior or ruling group. The term became clearer in later Vedic society.

## Vaishya
Common people associated with cattle-rearing, agriculture, and trade. The term became clearer later.

## Shudra
The fourth varna, mentioned in the Purusha Sukta. The position of Shudras became more defined in later Vedic society.

## Purusha Sukta Varna Scheme
The idea that Brahmana, Rajanya/Kshatriya, Vaishya, and Shudra emerged from different parts of the cosmic being Purusha.

## Rajanya
A term for the ruling or warrior class, later closely linked with Kshatriya.

## Dvija
“Twice-born”. A later term for Brahmana, Kshatriya, and Vaishya males after upanayana.

## Anuloma
Marriage or union between a higher-varna male and lower-varna female. More clearly discussed in later texts.

## Pratiloma
Marriage or union between a lower-varna male and higher-varna female. Later texts considered it improper.

## Niyoga
A practice where a widow could have a child through a designated male relative for lineage continuation. It appears in early tradition but became regulated later.

## Monogamy
Marriage with one spouse. It appears to have been common.

## Polygyny
A man having multiple wives. It existed especially among chiefs and elites.

## Widow Remarriage
The possibility of remarriage or levirate-like practices appears in early Vedic contexts.

## Swayamvara
A form of marriage where a woman chose her husband. It is more visible in later epic tradition but has early roots.

## Brahmavadini
A learned woman devoted to Vedic knowledge and spiritual discussion.

## Rishika
A female seer or composer of Vedic hymns.

## Apala
A woman seer mentioned in the Rigveda.

## Ghosha
A woman seer associated with Rigvedic hymns.

## Lopamudra
A woman seer associated with a Rigvedic dialogue hymn.

## Vishvavara
A woman seer of the Rigveda.

## Romasha
A female seer mentioned in Vedic tradition.

## Shashvati
A woman associated with Rigvedic tradition.

---

# 10. EARLY RIGVEDIC RELIGION

## Nature Worship
Worship of natural forces like fire, rain, wind, dawn, sun, and sky.

## Polytheism
Belief in many gods. Rigvedic religion had many deities.

## Henotheism
Worship of one deity as supreme at a time without denying other gods.

## Monism
Belief in one ultimate reality. Some later Rigvedic hymns show early monistic ideas.

## Rita
Cosmic order, natural law, and moral order. It was a central Early Vedic idea.

## Satya
Truth. It was closely connected with Rita.

## Vrata
Divine law, vow, or rule.

## Shraddha
Faith or reverence.

## Deva
God or shining one.

## Asura
In early Vedic usage, a powerful divine being. Later it came to mean demon.

## Yajna
Sacrifice performed to maintain cosmic order and please deities.

## Agni
Fire god. He carried offerings from humans to gods.

## Indra
The most important Rigvedic deity. He was god of war, rain, thunder, and victory.

## Soma
Sacred drink and deity associated with inspiration, energy, and immortality.

## Varuna
God associated with Rita, moral order, and cosmic law.

## Mitra
A deity associated with friendship, contracts, and social order.

## Aryaman
A deity associated with hospitality, social bonds, and nobility.

## Bhaga
A deity associated with fortune and share.

## Aditi
Mother of the Adityas and symbol of boundlessness.

## Adityas
A group of deities associated with cosmic and moral order.

## Maruts
Storm gods associated with Indra.

## Rudra
A fierce god associated with storm, disease, healing, and wild forces. Later linked with Shiva.

## Vishnu
A deity known for his three strides. In the Rigveda he is less prominent than Indra but important.

## Pushan
God associated with paths, cattle, journeys, and protection.

## Savitr
Solar deity associated with stimulation and inspiration. The Gayatri Mantra is addressed to him.

## Surya
The sun god.

## Ushas
Goddess of dawn. She is praised for beauty and renewal.

## Ashvins
Twin gods associated with healing, rescue, and light.

## Dyaus
Sky father.

## Prithvi
Earth mother.

## Dyaus-Prithvi
Heaven and earth as a divine pair.

## Parjanya
Rain god.

## Vayu
Wind god.

## Tvastr
Divine craftsman.

## Brihaspati
Priestly deity associated with prayer and sacred speech.

## Brahmanaspati
Lord of sacred prayer.

## Sarasvati
River goddess and later goddess of learning and speech.

## Apas
Waters, often treated as divine.

## Ribhus
Divine artisans known for skill and craftsmanship.

## Yama
The first mortal and lord of the dead in later Vedic thought.

## Pitrs
Ancestors.

## Svarga
Heaven or heavenly world.

## Naraka
Hell-like idea; clearer in later literature than in early Rigveda.

## Amrita
Immortality or nectar of immortality.

## Maya
Power, skill, or magical ability in early usage; later it came to mean illusion in philosophy.

---

# 11. EARLY VEDIC RITUAL AND PRIESTLY TERMS

## Hotri
The priest who recited Rigvedic hymns.

## Adhvaryu
The priest who performed physical actions of the sacrifice using Yajurvedic formulas.

## Udgatri
The priest who sang Samavedic chants.

## Brahman
The supervising priest who corrected ritual errors.

## Purodasha
A sacrificial cake offered in rituals.

## Vedi
Sacrificial altar.

## Yupa
Sacrificial post.

## Barhis
Sacred grass spread for ritual purposes.

## Samidh
Fuel sticks used in fire rituals.

## Sruk
A sacrificial ladle.

## Sruva
A smaller ladle used in ritual offerings.

## Juhu
A ladle used for pouring offerings into fire.

## Ahuti
An offering poured into the sacred fire.

## Dakshina
Fee or gift given to priests after a sacrifice.

## Mantra Recitation
Chanting sacred verses during ritual.

## Soma Pressing
The ritual extraction of Soma juice.

## Gravan
Pressing stones used in Soma rituals.

## Agnihotra
A daily fire offering that became especially important in later Vedic ritual.

## Homa
A fire offering.

---

# 12. EARLY VEDIC METRES AND RECITATION

## Chandas
Metre or poetic rhythm of Vedic hymns.

## Gayatri
A Vedic metre of 24 syllables. The famous Gayatri Mantra uses this metre.

## Anushtubh
A metre of 32 syllables. It later became common in epic poetry.

## Trishtubh
A metre of 44 syllables. It is very common in the Rigveda.

## Jagati
A metre of 48 syllables.

## Pankti
A metre of 40 syllables.

## Brihati
A metre of 36 syllables.

## Ushnih
A metre of 28 syllables.

## Svara
Accent or tone in Vedic recitation.

## Udatta
Raised accent.

## Anudatta
Unraised or lower accent.

## Svarita
Falling or mixed accent.

## Samhita Patha
Continuous recitation of the Vedic text.

## Pada Patha
Word-by-word recitation of the Vedic text.

## Krama Patha
A method of recitation in which words are repeated in pairs.

## Jata Patha
A complex method of Vedic recitation used to preserve accuracy.

## Ghana Patha
One of the most elaborate methods of Vedic recitation.

## Anukramani
An index of Vedic hymns listing seer, deity, and metre.

## Rishi
Seer of a Vedic hymn.

## Devata
The deity addressed in a hymn.

## Chandas
The metre of a hymn.

---

# 13. TRANSITION FROM EARLY TO LATER VEDIC PERIOD

## Later Vedic Transition
The movement from a pastoral tribal society to a more settled agricultural and territorial society.

## Eastward Expansion
The spread of Vedic culture from the north-west to the Ganga-Yamuna doab and further east.

## Ganga-Yamuna Doab
The fertile region between the Ganga and Yamuna rivers. It became important in the Later Vedic period.

## Kuru-Panchala Region
The main cultural and political center of the Later Vedic period.

## Kuru
A major Later Vedic kingdom formed partly from earlier Bharata-Puru elements.

## Panchala
A major Later Vedic kingdom east of Kuru, associated with ritual learning and philosophy.

## Videha
A kingdom in eastern India associated with King Janaka and Upanishadic thought.

## Kosala
A kingdom in the middle Ganga region.

## Kashi
A kingdom centered around Varanasi.

## Magadha
An eastern region that was initially outside the core Vedic area but later became historically important.

## Anga
An eastern region mentioned in later Vedic and early Buddhist contexts.

## Gandhara
A north-western region known for learning and trade.

## Madra
A north-western people/region mentioned in later Vedic texts.

## Kekaya
A north-western kingdom mentioned in later Vedic tradition.

## Matsya
A kingdom in the Rajasthan region.

## Shurasena
A region around Mathura.

## Chedi
A region in central India.

## Kurukshetra
A sacred region associated with the Kurus and later Vedic rituals.

## Hastinapura
A Kuru center associated with Painted Grey Ware culture and later epic tradition.

## Indraprastha
A later tradition-associated site near Delhi, connected with the Kuru-Pandava story.

## Asandivat
A Kuru capital mentioned in later Vedic literature.

## Kampilya
A Panchala center.

## Ahichhatra
A north Panchala center.

## Mithila
Capital of Videha, associated with King Janaka.

---

# 14. ARCHAEOLOGICAL CULTURES RELATED TO THE VEDIC PERIOD

## Ochre Coloured Pottery
A pottery culture found in the western Ganga plains and Rajasthan region. It is sometimes discussed in relation to early Indo-Gangetic cultures.

## OCP
Short form for Ochre Coloured Pottery.

## Copper Hoard Culture
A culture known for copper objects such as antenna swords, harpoons, and axes. Found in parts of north India.

## Painted Grey Ware
A fine grey pottery painted with black designs. It is associated with the Later Vedic period, especially the Kuru-Panchala region.

## PGW
Short form for Painted Grey Ware.

## Northern Black Polished Ware
A glossy pottery associated with the second urbanization after the Vedic period, around the Mahajanapada age.

## NBPW
Short form for Northern Black Polished Ware.

## Atranjikhera
An archaeological site in Uttar Pradesh showing PGW levels and evidence of iron.

## Noh
A PGW site in Rajasthan.

## Jakhera
A PGW site in western Uttar Pradesh.

## Bhagwanpura
A site in Haryana showing late Harappan and PGW overlap.

## Alamgirpur
A site near the Yamuna-Hindon region, relevant for late Harappan and later cultural phases.

## Hastinapura Excavation
Excavations at Hastinapura revealed PGW levels and flood evidence, often discussed in relation to later Vedic and epic traditions.

## Iron Use
Iron became important in the Later Vedic period, helping agriculture, forest clearance, and warfare.

## Shyama Ayas
Dark metal, usually interpreted as iron.

## Krishna Ayas
Black metal, generally interpreted as iron.

## Loha
Iron or metal; the word becomes common in later literature.

---

# 15. LATER VEDIC TEXTS

## Samaveda
The Veda of melodies and chants. It is mainly based on Rigvedic verses but arranged for singing during Soma sacrifices.

## Yajurveda
The Veda of sacrificial formulas. It gives prose and verse formulas used by the Adhvaryu priest.

## Krishna Yajurveda
The “Black Yajurveda”. It mixes mantras and explanatory prose.

## Shukla Yajurveda
The “White Yajurveda”. It separates mantras from explanatory prose.

## Atharvaveda
The fourth Veda. It includes charms, spells, healing hymns, household rituals, royal rituals, and philosophical ideas.

## Aitareya Brahmana
A Brahmana text of the Rigveda dealing with rituals and royal consecration.

## Kaushitaki Brahmana
A Brahmana text of the Rigveda.

## Shatapatha Brahmana
A major Brahmana of the Shukla Yajurveda. It contains detailed ritual explanations and important myths.

## Taittiriya Brahmana
A Brahmana text of the Krishna Yajurveda.

## Panchavimsha Brahmana
A Brahmana text of the Samaveda.

## Jaiminiya Brahmana
A Brahmana text of the Samaveda tradition.

## Gopatha Brahmana
The Brahmana text of the Atharvaveda.

## Aitareya Aranyaka
An Aranyaka of the Rigveda.

## Taittiriya Aranyaka
An Aranyaka of the Krishna Yajurveda.

## Brihadaranyaka Upanishad
One of the oldest and most important Upanishads. It contains teachings of Yajnavalkya, Gargi, Maitreyi, and Janaka.

## Chandogya Upanishad
A major Upanishad of the Samaveda. It contains teachings like “Tat Tvam Asi”.

## Aitareya Upanishad
An Upanishad of the Rigveda discussing consciousness and creation.

## Kaushitaki Upanishad
An Upanishad linked with the Rigveda.

## Taittiriya Upanishad
An Upanishad of the Krishna Yajurveda, known for the five sheaths theory.

## Kena Upanishad
An Upanishad asking by whom the mind, speech, and senses are directed.

## Katha Upanishad
An Upanishad containing the dialogue between Nachiketa and Yama.

## Isha Upanishad
A short Upanishad attached to the Shukla Yajurveda, discussing renunciation and action.

## Mundaka Upanishad
An Upanishad distinguishing higher knowledge and lower knowledge.

## Mandukya Upanishad
A short Upanishad dealing with Om and states of consciousness.

## Prashna Upanishad
An Upanishad structured around six questions.

## Shvetashvatara Upanishad
A later Upanishad with theistic ideas, especially linked with Rudra-Shiva.

## Maitri Upanishad
A later Upanishad dealing with mind, self, and liberation.

---

# 16. VEDIC SHAKHAS

## Shakala Shakha
The surviving major branch of the Rigveda.

## Bashkala Shakha
An ancient branch of the Rigveda.

## Kauthuma Shakha
A major branch of the Samaveda.

## Ranayaniya Shakha
A branch of the Samaveda.

## Jaiminiya Shakha
A branch of the Samaveda.

## Taittiriya Shakha
A major Krishna Yajurveda branch.

## Maitrayani Shakha
A Krishna Yajurveda branch.

## Katha Shakha
A Krishna Yajurveda branch.

## Kapisthala Shakha
A Krishna Yajurveda branch.

## Madhyandina Shakha
A Shukla Yajurveda branch.

## Kanva Shakha
A Shukla Yajurveda branch.

## Shaunaka Shakha
A branch of the Atharvaveda.

## Paippalada Shakha
A branch of the Atharvaveda.

---

# 17. LATER VEDIC POLITY

## Janapada
A territorial state. It literally means “foothold of a tribe”.

## Rashtra
A territory or kingdom. It became clearer in the Later Vedic period.

## Rajya
Kingdom or rule.

## Rajan
King. In the Later Vedic period, the king became more powerful than in the Early Vedic age.

## Samrat
An emperor or overlord.

## Ekarat
A sole ruler or universal ruler.

## Svarat
A self-ruling sovereign.

## Bhoja
A title used for certain rulers or chiefs.

## Virat
A ruler or powerful chief.

## Rajasuya
A royal consecration sacrifice performed to legitimize kingship.

## Vajapeya
A royal ritual associated with strength, prestige, and chariot race symbolism.

## Ashvamedha
Horse sacrifice performed by powerful kings to show political supremacy.

## Abhisheka
Ritual consecration or anointing of the king.

## Ratnin
A royal functionary or “jewel” of the king who participated in royal rituals.

## Purohita
Royal priest and adviser.

## Senani
Commander of the army.

## Gramani
Village head or leader of a local unit.

## Suta
Charioteer, bard, or royal announcer.

## Kshatta
Chamberlain or palace official.

## Samgrahitri
Treasurer or collector.

## Bhagadugha
Collector of the king’s share of produce.

## Akshavapa
Keeper of dice or accounts.

## Govikarta
Officer connected with forests, cattle, or hunting.

## Palagala
Messenger or courier.

## Mahishi
Chief queen.

## Vavata
Favourite queen.

## Parivrikti
Discarded or neglected queen.

## Parishad
Council or assembly, often of elders, priests, or advisers.

## Sabha
Assembly; in later Vedic times it became more aristocratic.

## Samiti
General assembly; its importance declined compared to the Early Vedic period.

## Vidatha
Earlier assembly whose importance declined in the Later Vedic period.

## Danda
Punishment or coercive authority of the ruler.

## Bali
Offering or tribute, increasingly becoming a regular payment.

## Bhaga
King’s share of agricultural produce.

## Kara
Tax or compulsory payment.

## Shulka
Toll or customs duty.

## Sangrahitri
Revenue-related official.

## Senabhakta
Supply or contribution for the army.

## Ayudha
Weapon.

## Sena
Army.

## Ratha
Chariot.

## Ashva
Horse.

## Gaja
Elephant; elephants became more visible in later texts.

---

# 18. LATER VEDIC SOCIETY

## Varna System
The fourfold social classification of Brahmana, Kshatriya, Vaishya, and Shudra. It became more rigid in the Later Vedic period.

## Brahmana
The priestly varna. Brahmanas gained importance because rituals became complex.

## Kshatriya
The ruling and warrior varna.

## Vaishya
The producing varna associated with agriculture, cattle-rearing, and trade.

## Shudra
The service varna. Shudras were placed below the three twice-born varnas.

## Dvija
“Twice-born”. Brahmanas, Kshatriyas, and Vaishyas were called twice-born after the upanayana ceremony.

## Upanayana
Sacred thread initiation ceremony marking entry into Vedic student life.

## Yajnopavita
Sacred thread worn after upanayana.

## Brahmacharya
Student stage of life devoted to learning, discipline, and celibacy.

## Grihastha
Householder stage. It was considered central because householders supported rituals and society.

## Vanaprastha
Forest-dweller stage involving gradual withdrawal from worldly life.

## Sannyasa
Renunciation stage focused on liberation.

## Ashrama System
The four stages of life: Brahmacharya, Grihastha, Vanaprastha, and Sannyasa.

## Purusharthas
The four aims of life: Dharma, Artha, Kama, and Moksha. The full scheme becomes clearer later.

## Dharma
Duty, moral order, law, and right conduct.

## Artha
Material prosperity and power.

## Kama
Desire, pleasure, and emotional fulfillment.

## Moksha
Liberation from birth and death.

## Gotra
Lineage traced from a common ancestor. Marriage within the same gotra was generally avoided later.

## Pravara
List of ancestral sages linked with a gotra.

## Jati
Birth group or caste-like community. It was not fully developed in the early Vedic period but later social divisions became more complex.

## Kula
Family.

## Griha
Household.

## Grihapati
Household head.

## Patriarchy
Male-dominated family and social structure. It became stronger in the Later Vedic period.

## Putreshana
Desire for sons.

## Stri
Woman.

## Patni
Wife. She was necessary for many household rituals.

## Brahmavadini
A woman who studied and discussed Vedic knowledge.

## Sadyovadhu
A woman who married soon after education.

## Gargi
A woman philosopher in the Brihadaranyaka Upanishad who debated Yajnavalkya.

## Maitreyi
A woman philosopher and wife of Yajnavalkya, known for discussions on immortality and Atman.

## Lopamudra
A female seer associated with Vedic tradition.

## Apala
Female seer of the Rigveda.

## Ghosha
Female seer of the Rigveda.

## Satyakama Jabala
A student in the Chandogya Upanishad whose story emphasizes truthfulness over birth status.

## Jabala
Mother of Satyakama; associated with the idea that truthfulness matters in spiritual learning.

## Janaka
King of Videha, famous as a patron of philosophers and Upanishadic debates.

## Yajnavalkya
A major Upanishadic thinker associated with the Brihadaranyaka Upanishad.

## Uddalaka Aruni
An Upanishadic teacher known for teaching “Tat Tvam Asi” to Shvetaketu.

## Shvetaketu
Student and son of Uddalaka Aruni in the Chandogya Upanishad.

## Nachiketa
A young seeker in the Katha Upanishad who questions Yama about death and immortality.

## Yama
God of death and teacher of Nachiketa in the Katha Upanishad.

## Pravahana Jaivali
A Kshatriya teacher associated with teachings on rebirth and the five fires doctrine.

## Ajatashatru
A king appearing in Upanishadic discussions, not to be confused automatically with the later Magadhan king unless context is clear.

## Raikva
A sage in the Chandogya Upanishad associated with spiritual knowledge.

---

# 19. LATER VEDIC SAMSKARAS

## Samskara
A life-cycle ritual marking important stages of life.

## Garbhadhana
Conception ritual.

## Pumsavana
Ritual for the birth of a son.

## Simantonnayana
Ritual performed during pregnancy.

## Jatakarma
Birth ritual.

## Namakarana
Naming ceremony.

## Nishkramana
First outing of the child.

## Annaprashana
First feeding of solid food.

## Chudakarana
First tonsure or hair-cutting ceremony.

## Karnavedha
Ear-piercing ceremony.

## Vidyarambha
Beginning of education.

## Upanayana
Initiation into Vedic learning.

## Vedarambha
Beginning of Vedic study.

## Keshanta
First shaving of beard.

## Samavartana
Completion of student life and return from the teacher’s house.

## Vivaha
Marriage ceremony.

## Antyeshti
Funeral rites.

---

# 20. LATER VEDIC MARRIAGE TERMS

## Vivaha
Marriage.

## Brahma Marriage
Marriage where the daughter is given to a learned groom without expectation of wealth.

## Daiva Marriage
Marriage where the daughter is given to a priest as part of ritual context.

## Arsha Marriage
Marriage involving symbolic bride-price, usually cattle.

## Prajapatya Marriage
Marriage based on duty and household life.

## Gandharva Marriage
Marriage by mutual consent or love.

## Asura Marriage
Marriage involving payment of bride-price.

## Rakshasa Marriage
Marriage by force or capture.

## Paishacha Marriage
A condemned form of marriage involving exploitation or violation.

## Anuloma Marriage
Union of a higher-varna man with a lower-varna woman.

## Pratiloma Marriage
Union of a lower-varna man with a higher-varna woman.

## Niyoga
Levirate-like practice for producing offspring in special circumstances.

## Stridhana
Woman’s property; clearer in later legal texts but rooted in marriage-related gifts.

---

# 21. LATER VEDIC ECONOMY

## Settled Agriculture
Agriculture became the main economic activity in the Later Vedic period.

## Forest Clearance
Clearing forests for agriculture, helped by iron tools and fire.

## Kshetra
Cultivated field.

## Urvara
Fertile land.

## Krishi
Agriculture.

## Krishti
People or cultivators.

## Hala
Plough.

## Langala
Plough.

## Sira
Ploughshare or plough.

## Phala
Ploughshare.

## Sita
Furrow.

## Bij
Seed.

## Vrihi
Rice. It became important in the Later Vedic period, especially with eastward expansion.

## Yava
Barley.

## Godhuma
Wheat.

## Tila
Sesame.

## Masha
Black gram.

## Mudga
Green gram.

## Priyangu
Millet-like grain.

## Ikshu
Sugarcane.

## Dugdha
Milk.

## Dadhi
Curd.

## Ghee
Clarified butter, important in diet and ritual.

## Go-dhana
Cattle wealth.

## Pashu
Animal or cattle.

## Gopa
Cowherd.

## Goshtha
Cattle enclosure.

## Avika
Sheep.

## Aja
Goat.

## Ashva
Horse.

## Hastin
Elephant.

## Bali
Tribute or offering to the king.

## Bhaga
King’s share of produce.

## Kara
Tax.

## Shulka
Customs duty or toll.

## Vanij
Merchant.

## Vyavahara
Transaction or legal/economic dealing.

## Nishka
Gold ornament or unit of value.

## Satamana
A weight or value term, often linked with silver/gold.

## Krishnala
A small weight measure.

## Pada
A quarter-unit or measure.

## Hiranya
Gold.

## Rajata
Silver.

## Ayas
Metal.

## Shyama Ayas
Iron or dark metal.

## Krishna Ayas
Iron or black metal.

## Loha
Iron or metal.

## Trapu
Tin.

## Sisa
Lead.

## Tamra
Copper.

## Karmara
Smith or metalworker.

## Takshan
Carpenter.

## Rathakara
Chariot-maker.

## Kulala
Potter.

## Charmakara
Leather worker.

## Vaya
Weaver.

## Hiranyakara
Goldsmith.

## Manikara
Jewel-maker.

## Ishukara
Arrow-maker.

## Dhanushkara
Bow-maker.

## Rajju-sarja
Rope-maker.

## Vapa
Barber.

## Rajaka
Washerman.

## Sura-kara
Maker of alcoholic drink.

## Sura
Alcoholic drink, generally disapproved in many ritual contexts.

## Madhu
Honey or sweet drink.

## Shreni
Guild or professional association; clearer in later periods but early occupational grouping began developing.

## Nigama
Market settlement or corporate group; more visible in later periods.

---

# 22. LATER VEDIC RELIGION

## Ritualism
Emphasis on correct performance of rituals and sacrifices.

## Sacrificial Religion
A religious system centered on yajna, offerings, priests, and sacred fire.

## Brahmanical Religion
The religion led by Brahmana priests, based on Vedic rituals and texts.

## Prajapati
Creator deity who became very important in the Later Vedic period.

## Brahma
Later creator god; connected with the concept of Brahman but distinct from it.

## Rudra
A fierce deity who became increasingly important and later developed into Shiva.

## Shiva
Later form associated with Rudra; not fully developed as the later Puranic Shiva in the Vedic period.

## Vishnu
A Vedic deity whose importance increased over time; later became a major god.

## Indra
Still important but less dominant than in the Early Rigvedic period.

## Agni
Fire god, central to sacrifices.

## Soma
Deity and ritual drink, central to Soma sacrifices.

## Varuna
His importance declined compared to early Rigvedic times.

## Pushan
Pastoral and path-protecting deity.

## Savitr
Solar deity.

## Surya
Sun deity.

## Ushas
Dawn goddess.

## Aditi
Mother of Adityas.

## Adityas
Solar and moral-order deities.

## Maruts
Storm deities.

## Ashvins
Twin healing deities.

## Sarasvati
River goddess and later associated with speech and learning.

## Vak
Speech, sometimes personified as a goddess.

## Sri
Auspiciousness and prosperity; later connected with Lakshmi.

## Lakshmi
Goddess of prosperity; clearer in later tradition.

## Prithvi
Earth goddess.

## Dyaus
Sky god.

## Apas
Waters.

## Pitr
Ancestors.

## Shraddha
Faith and ancestor-related ritual reverence.

## Pitr-yajna
Offering to ancestors.

## Deva-yajna
Offering to gods.

## Brahma-yajna
Study and recitation of Veda.

## Bhuta-yajna
Offering to living beings.

## Manushya-yajna
Hospitality to humans or guests.

## Pancha Mahayajna
Five great daily sacrifices of a householder: Brahma-yajna, Deva-yajna, Pitr-yajna, Bhuta-yajna, and Manushya-yajna.

## Atithi
Guest.

## Atithi Devo Bhava
The idea that a guest should be treated like a deity.

## Tapas
Austerity, heat, discipline, or spiritual effort.

## Vrata
Vow or sacred observance.

## Dana
Gift or charity.

## Dakshina
Gift to priests.

---

# 23. LATER VEDIC SACRIFICES

## Nitya Karma
Regular obligatory ritual.

## Naimittika Karma
Ritual performed on special occasions.

## Kamya Karma
Ritual performed for a desired result.

## Paka Yajna
Simple domestic sacrifice.

## Haviryajna
Sacrifice using offerings like grain, milk, and ghee.

## Soma Yajna
Sacrifice involving Soma juice.

## Agnihotra
Daily morning and evening milk offering into fire.

## Darsha-Purnamasa
New moon and full moon sacrifices.

## Chaturmasya
Seasonal sacrifice performed every four months.

## Agrahayana
Harvest-related sacrifice.

## Nirudha Pashubandha
Animal sacrifice performed under strict ritual rules.

## Sautramani
A ritual connected with Indra and Soma.

## Ashvamedha
Horse sacrifice showing royal power and territorial supremacy.

## Rajasuya
Royal consecration sacrifice.

## Vajapeya
Prestige sacrifice involving chariot race symbolism.

## Purushamedha
Human sacrifice in textual ritual theory; often interpreted as symbolic or theoretical.

## Sarvamedha
A sacrifice of “all” possessions, associated with extreme ritual giving.

## Gomedha
Cow sacrifice in ritual texts; its interpretation varies.

## Agnichayana
Construction of a special fire altar using bricks.

## Syena Chiti
Falcon-shaped fire altar.

## Garhapatya Fire
Householder’s circular domestic fire.

## Ahavaniya Fire
Eastern sacrificial fire where offerings are made to gods.

## Dakshina Fire
Southern fire associated with ancestors and certain rituals.

## Vedi
Sacrificial altar.

## Yupa
Sacrificial post.

## Chiti
Piled fire altar made of bricks.

## Ishti
A small sacrifice or offering.

## Purodasha
Sacrificial cake.

## Charu
Cooked offering of grain or porridge.

## Payasa
Milk-rice or sweet offering.

## Ajya
Clarified butter used in ritual.

## Barhis
Sacred grass seat for deities.

## Idhma
Fuel wood.

## Samidh
Sacrificial fuel sticks.

## Pavitra
Purifying filter or sacred purifier.

## Sruva
Small ritual ladle.

## Sruk
Large ritual ladle.

## Juhu
Offering ladle.

## Upabhrit
Secondary ladle.

## Gravan
Soma-pressing stone.

## Drona
Wooden vessel used in Soma rituals.

## Kalasha
Ritual pot.

## Chamasa
Cup used in Soma rituals.

## Avabhritha
Final ritual bath after a sacrifice.

---

# 24. VEDIC PRIESTS

## Ritvij
A sacrificial priest.

## Hotri
Priest who recites Rigvedic hymns.

## Adhvaryu
Priest who performs the physical ritual using Yajurvedic formulas.

## Udgatri
Priest who sings Samavedic chants.

## Brahman
Supervising priest who watches for mistakes.

## Maitravaruna
Assistant of the Hotri.

## Acchavaka
Assistant priest in Soma rituals.

## Gravastut
Priest who praises the Soma-pressing stones.

## Prastotri
Priest who begins the Samavedic chant.

## Pratiharti
Priest who responds in Samavedic chanting.

## Subrahmanya
Priest who calls the gods to the sacrifice.

## Pratiprasthata
Assistant of the Adhvaryu.

## Neshtṛ
Priest who leads the sacrificer’s wife or performs guiding functions.

## Unnetṛ
Priest who pours Soma.

## Potṛ
Purifying priest.

## Agnidh
Priest who kindles or tends the fire.

## Sacrificer
The person who sponsors the sacrifice.

## Yajamana
The patron or sponsor of the sacrifice.

## Patni
Wife of the sacrificer; required in many rituals.

---

# 25. UPANISHADIC PHILOSOPHY

## Brahman
The ultimate reality or universal principle.

## Atman
The inner self or soul.

## Brahman-Atman Unity
The idea that the individual self and ultimate reality are one.

## Tat Tvam Asi
“That thou art.” A famous teaching from the Chandogya Upanishad meaning the self is identical with ultimate reality.

## Aham Brahmasmi
“I am Brahman.” A famous statement from the Brihadaranyaka Upanishad.

## Prajnanam Brahma
“Consciousness is Brahman.” A major Upanishadic statement.

## Ayam Atma Brahma
“This self is Brahman.” A major Upanishadic statement.

## Neti Neti
“Not this, not this.” A method used by Yajnavalkya to describe Brahman by negation.

## Sat
Being or truth.

## Asat
Non-being or non-existence.

## Satya
Truth.

## Rta
Cosmic order; in Upanishadic thought it is increasingly connected with truth and moral order.

## Dharma
Duty, law, moral order, and right conduct.

## Karma
Action and its moral result. In Upanishads, karma becomes linked with rebirth.

## Samsara
Cycle of birth, death, and rebirth.

## Moksha
Liberation from samsara.

## Vidya
Knowledge, especially spiritual knowledge.

## Avidya
Ignorance.

## Para Vidya
Higher knowledge, knowledge of Brahman.

## Apara Vidya
Lower knowledge, including ritual and ordinary learning.

## Jnana
Knowledge.

## Upasana
Meditation or worship.

## Dhyana
Meditation.

## Tapas
Austerity and spiritual discipline.

## Tyaga
Renunciation.

## Sannyasa
Renunciation of worldly life.

## Shravan
Listening to spiritual teaching.

## Manana
Reflection on spiritual teaching.

## Nididhyasana
Deep meditation on spiritual truth.

## Prana
Life breath or vital energy.

## Apana
Downward-moving vital breath.

## Vyana
Pervasive vital energy.

## Udana
Upward-moving vital breath.

## Samana
Balancing vital breath.

## Pancha Prana
Five vital airs: prana, apana, vyana, udana, and samana.

## Pancha Kosha
Five sheaths of the self described in the Taittiriya Upanishad.

## Annamaya Kosha
Food sheath or physical body.

## Pranamaya Kosha
Vital breath sheath.

## Manomaya Kosha
Mental sheath.

## Vijnanamaya Kosha
Knowledge or intellect sheath.

## Anandamaya Kosha
Bliss sheath.

## Panchagni Vidya
Doctrine of five fires explaining rebirth and cosmic processes.

## Om
Sacred syllable representing ultimate reality.

## Aum
Another form of Om; discussed deeply in the Mandukya Upanishad.

## Jagrat
Waking state.

## Svapna
Dream state.

## Sushupti
Deep sleep state.

## Turiya
The fourth state beyond waking, dream, and deep sleep.

## Antaryamin
Inner controller or inner self.

## Hiranyagarbha
Cosmic embryo or universal source.

## Purusha
Cosmic person or spiritual principle.

## Prakriti
Nature or material principle; clearer in later philosophy.

## Maya
Power of illusion or appearance; more developed in later Vedanta.

## Avyakta
Unmanifest.

## Akshara
Imperishable reality.

## Kshara
Perishable existence.

## Sreyas
The good or spiritually beneficial path.

## Preyas
The pleasant or worldly attractive path.

## Nachiketa Agni
Sacred fire knowledge taught to Nachiketa by Yama.

---

# 26. VEDIC EDUCATION

## Gurukula
Teacher’s household where students lived and studied.

## Guru
Teacher.

## Acharya
Spiritual or Vedic teacher.

## Upadhyaya
Teacher, especially one who teaches a specific text or subject.

## Antevasin
Resident student living near the teacher.

## Brahmacharin
Student observing discipline and celibacy.

## Upanayana
Initiation into student life.

## Samidha
Fuel sticks carried by students as a sign of service.

## Swadhyaya
Self-study or recitation of the Veda.

## Pravachana
Teaching or exposition.

## Patha
Recitation.

## Adhyayana
Study.

## Adhyapana
Teaching.

## Gurudakshina
Gift given to the teacher after completion of study.

## Samavartana
Return home after completing education.

## Parishad
Council or group of learned persons.

## Shastrartha
Philosophical debate; clearer in later tradition but rooted in debate culture.

---

# 27. SIX VEDANGAS

## Shiksha
Phonetics; teaches correct pronunciation of Vedic sounds.

## Kalpa
Ritual procedure; explains how rituals should be performed.

## Vyakarana
Grammar; helps preserve correct language.

## Nirukta
Etymology; explains difficult Vedic words.

## Chandas
Metre; studies poetic metres of Vedic hymns.

## Jyotisha
Astronomy and calendar science used for fixing ritual times.

## Vedanga Jyotisha
Early text dealing with time calculation for rituals.

## Lagadha
Traditional author associated with Vedanga Jyotisha.

---

# 28. SUTRA LITERATURE

## Kalpa Sutra
A broad category of ritual manuals.

## Shrauta Sutra
Manual for large public sacrifices.

## Grihya Sutra
Manual for domestic rituals.

## Dharma Sutra
Manual for law, duty, social conduct, and varna-ashrama rules.

## Shulba Sutra
Manual dealing with altar geometry.

## Baudhayana Shulba Sutra
A Shulba text containing geometric rules, including a statement similar to the Pythagorean theorem.

## Apastamba Shulba Sutra
A Shulba text dealing with altar construction and geometry.

## Katyayana Shulba Sutra
A later Shulba text.

## Manava Shulba Sutra
A Shulba text of the Manava tradition.

## Vedi Geometry
Geometry used for constructing sacrificial altars.

## Rope Geometry
Use of ropes to measure and construct altars.

## Square Altar
A common altar shape in Vedic ritual geometry.

## Falcon Altar
A bird-shaped altar used in Agnichayana.

## Circle-Square Transformation
A geometric problem in Shulba texts involving conversion between circular and square areas.

---

# 29. VEDIC CALENDAR AND TIME TERMS

## Samvatsara
Year.

## Ritu
Season.

## Masa
Month.

## Paksha
Fortnight.

## Shukla Paksha
Bright fortnight, from new moon to full moon.

## Krishna Paksha
Dark fortnight, from full moon to new moon.

## Tithi
Lunar day.

## Nakshatra
Lunar mansion or star group used in calendrical calculation.

## Muhurta
A unit of time.

## Ahoratra
Day and night.

## Uttarayana
Northward movement of the sun.

## Dakshinayana
Southward movement of the sun.

## Vishuva
Equinox.

## Ayana
Half-yearly solar movement.

## Adhimasa
Intercalary month added to adjust lunar and solar calendars.

## Vasanta
Spring season.

## Grishma
Summer season.

## Varsha
Rainy season.

## Sharad
Autumn season.

## Hemanta
Pre-winter season.

## Shishira
Winter season.

---

# 30. VEDIC MUSIC AND PERFORMANCE

## Saman
Melodic chant of the Samaveda.

## Stotra
Hymn of praise.

## Stoma
Chant arrangement used in Soma rituals.

## Udgitha
A Samavedic chant, also philosophically discussed in the Chandogya Upanishad.

## Prastava
Introductory chant.

## Pratihara
Responsive chant.

## Nidhana
Conclusion of a chant.

## Vina
Stringed musical instrument.

## Dundubhi
Drum.

## Venu
Flute.

## Nritta
Dance; clearer as a technical term later.

## Gita
Song.

---

# 31. ATHARVAVEDIC TERMS

## Atharvan
Priestly tradition associated with the Atharvaveda.

## Angiras
Priestly family/tradition associated with Atharvavedic hymns.

## Bheshaja
Medicine or healing.

## Bhishaj
Physician or healer.

## Oshadhi
Medicinal herb.

## Raksha
Protection.

## Abhichara
Magical or hostile ritual.

## Shanti
Peace ritual.

## Pushti
Ritual for prosperity and nourishment.

## Yakshma
Disease, often interpreted as consumption or wasting disease.

## Takman
Fever.

## Krimi
Worm or germ-like harmful organism.

## Mantra for Healing
Atharvavedic charm used to cure disease.

## Royal Rituals
Atharvaveda includes rituals for kingship, protection, and victory.

## Household Rituals
Atharvaveda contains many rituals related to family, health, marriage, and daily life.

---

# 32. VEDIC ETHICAL AND MORAL TERMS

## Rta
Cosmic and moral order.

## Satya
Truth.

## Dharma
Duty and right conduct.

## Papa
Sin or wrong action.

## Punya
Merit from good action.

## Dana
Charity or gift.

## Ahimsa
Non-violence; not central in early Vedic religion but becomes more important in later Indian thought.

## Daya
Compassion.

## Dama
Self-control.

## Shama
Calmness or control of mind.

## Tapas
Austerity.

## Brahmacharya
Celibacy and disciplined student life.

## Shraddha
Faith and reverence.

## Rina
Debt or obligation.

## Deva Rina
Debt to gods, repaid through sacrifice.

## Rishi Rina
Debt to sages, repaid through study of Veda.

## Pitri Rina
Debt to ancestors, repaid through offspring and ancestor rites.

## Atithi Satkara
Hospitality to guests.

---

# 33. VEDIC IDEAS ABOUT DEATH AND AFTERLIFE

## Yama
Lord of the dead.

## Pitrloka
World of ancestors.

## Svarga
Heaven.

## Preta
Departed spirit before final rites.

## Antyeshti
Funeral rite.

## Agni and Funeral
Fire was used in cremation and as a carrier of the dead to the next world.

## Cremation
Burning of the dead body, common in Vedic funeral practice.

## Burial
Also known in some early contexts, though cremation became dominant.

## Shraddha
Ritual offering to ancestors.

## Pinda
Rice-ball offering to ancestors; clearer in later ritual tradition.

## Punarjanma
Rebirth. It becomes clearer in Upanishadic thought.

## Samsara
Cycle of birth and death.

## Moksha
Freedom from rebirth.

---

# 34. IMPORTANT VEDIC AND UPANISHADIC PERSONALITIES

## Vasistha
A major Rigvedic sage and priest of Sudas.

## Vishvamitra
A major sage associated with the Gayatri Mantra and early Vedic politics.

## Bharadvaja
A Rigvedic sage and priestly family name.

## Gritsamada
A Rigvedic seer.

## Atri
A Vedic sage and seer.

## Vamadeva
A Rigvedic sage.

## Kanva
A Vedic sage and priestly lineage.

## Angiras
A priestly family and seer group.

## Bhrigu
An ancient sage family.

## Agastya
A sage associated with Vedic tradition and later southern expansion legends.

## Lopamudra
Female seer associated with Agastya.

## Apala
Female seer of the Rigveda.

## Ghosha
Female seer of the Rigveda.

## Vishvavara
Female seer of the Rigveda.

## Gargi Vachaknavi
Woman philosopher in the Brihadaranyaka Upanishad.

## Maitreyi
Woman philosopher in the Brihadaranyaka Upanishad.

## Yajnavalkya
Major Upanishadic philosopher.

## Uddalaka Aruni
Teacher in the Chandogya Upanishad.

## Shvetaketu
Student and son of Uddalaka Aruni.

## Satyakama Jabala
Truthful student accepted for Vedic learning.

## Janaka of Videha
King and philosopher-patron of Upanishadic debates.

## Nachiketa
Young seeker in the Katha Upanishad.

## Yama
Teacher of Nachiketa.

## Pravahana Jaivali
Kshatriya teacher of rebirth doctrine.

## Raikva
Sage in Chandogya Upanishad.

## Mahidasa Aitareya
Associated with Aitareya tradition.

## Shaunaka
Vedic teacher associated with Atharvaveda and later tradition.

## Pippalada
Sage associated with the Prashna Upanishad.

---

# 35. IMPORTANT VEDIC CONCEPTS OF KNOWLEDGE

## Brahmavidya
Knowledge of Brahman.

## Atmavidya
Knowledge of the self.

## Para Vidya
Higher spiritual knowledge.

## Apara Vidya
Lower knowledge, including ritual, grammar, phonetics, and ordinary learning.

## Vidya
Knowledge.

## Avidya
Ignorance.

## Medha
Intelligence or wisdom.

## Smriti
Memory.

## Shruti
Revealed knowledge.

## Pratibha
Insight or brilliance.

## Manas
Mind.

## Buddhi
Intellect.

## Chitta
Mental field; more developed in later philosophy.

## Ahamkara
Ego-sense; clearer in later philosophy.

## Prajna
Consciousness or wisdom.

---

# 36. VEDIC TERMS RELATED TO SPEECH AND LANGUAGE

## Vak
Speech, often sacred and sometimes personified as a goddess.

## Mantra
Sacred utterance.

## Brahman
In early usage, sacred prayer or powerful utterance; later ultimate reality.

## Brahmana
One who knows sacred utterance; priestly class.

## Chandas
Metre.

## Shabda
Sound or word.

## Svara
Accent.

## Pada
Word or foot of a verse.

## Akshara
Syllable or imperishable sound.

## Om
Sacred syllable.

## Nirukta
Etymological explanation of Vedic words.

## Vyakarana
Grammar.

## Shiksha
Phonetics.

## Griha

## Grihapati

## Grihini

## Dampati

## Agni

---

# 40. VEDIC MYTHOLOGICAL TERMS

## Vritra
Demon-serpent who held back waters and was killed by Indra.

## Vritrahan
“Slayer of Vritra”; title of Indra.

## Ahi
Serpent.

## Ahi Budhnya
Serpent of the deep.

## Namuchi
Demon defeated by Indra.

## Shambara
Enemy of Indra.

## Vala
Cave or demon associated with hidden cows.

## Sarama
Divine dog who discovers hidden cows of the Panis.

## Panis and Cows
Myth where Panis hide cows and divine forces recover them.

## Trivikrama
Three strides of Vishnu.

## Manu
Primordial human or ancestor of mankind.

## Manu Vaivasvata
A flood-survivor figure in later Vedic myth.

## Flood Myth
A story in the Shatapatha Brahmana where Manu is saved by a fish.

## Matsya
Fish that saves Manu in the flood myth; later linked with Vishnu’s Matsya avatar.

## Purusha
Cosmic being sacrificed to create the universe and society.

## Hiranyagarbha
Golden embryo or cosmic source.

---

# 41. VEDIC WOMEN AND GENDER TERMS

## Rishika
Female seer.

## Brahmavadini
Woman devoted to sacred learning.

## Sadyovadhu
Woman who married after basic education.

## Patni
Wife.

## Jaya
Wife.

## Duhitr
Daughter.

## Mata
Mother.

## Mahishi
Chief queen.

## Vavata
Favourite queen.

## Parivrikti
Neglected queen.

## Gargi
Woman philosopher.

## Maitreyi
Woman philosopher.

## Apala
Female seer.

## Ghosha
Female seer.

## Lopamudra
Female seer.

## Vishvavara
Female seer.

## Romasha
Female seer.

## Stri Shiksha
Women’s education; available to some women, especially elite or learned families.

## Women in Sabha
Women may have participated in some early assemblies, but their role declined later.

## Patriliny
Lineage traced through the father.

## Putra Preference
Preference for sons, stronger in later Vedic society.

---

# 42. VEDIC POLITICAL AND SOCIAL CHANGE

## From Jana to Janapada
The transition from tribe-based society to territory-based state.

## From Pastoralism to Agriculture
The economic shift from cattle wealth to settled farming.

## From Voluntary Bali to Taxation
The shift from voluntary tribute to more regular royal dues.

## From Sabha-Samiti to Monarchy
The decline of popular assemblies and rise of stronger kingship.

## From Fluid Varna to Hereditary Varna
The shift from flexible social categories to more birth-based hierarchy.

## From Ritual Simplicity to Ritual Complexity
The growth of elaborate sacrifices and specialist priests.

## From Nature Worship to Philosophical Speculation
The shift from hymns to natural deities toward Upanishadic questions about self and reality.

---

# 43. IMPORTANT VEDIC REGIONS AND KINGDOMS

## Kuru
Major Later Vedic kingdom; center of Brahmanical ritual culture.

## Panchala
Important kingdom associated with Vedic learning and Upanishadic thought.

## Kuru-Panchala
The cultural heartland of the Later Vedic period.

## Videha
Eastern kingdom associated with Janaka and Upanishadic philosophy.

## Kosala
Kingdom in the middle Ganga region.

## Kashi
Kingdom centered on Varanasi.

## Magadha
Eastern region that later became the base of large empires.

## Anga
Eastern region mentioned in later Vedic and early historic sources.

## Gandhara
North-western region associated with learning and wider contacts.

## Madra
North-western region.

## Kekaya
North-western kingdom.

## Matsya
Region in present Rajasthan area.

## Shurasena
Region around Mathura.

## Chedi
Central Indian region.

## Vatsa
Region around Kaushambi, more prominent in the Mahajanapada period.

---

# 44. IMPORTANT VEDIC SITES FOR UPSC

## Sapta Sindhu
Early Vedic region of seven rivers.

## Kurukshetra
Later Vedic sacred-political region.

## Hastinapura
Kuru center associated with PGW archaeology.

## Atranjikhera
PGW site with iron evidence.

## Noh
PGW site in Rajasthan.

## Jakhera
PGW site in western Uttar Pradesh.

## Bhagwanpura
Site showing late Harappan and PGW cultural contact.

## Alamgirpur
Late Harappan-related site in the upper Ganga-Yamuna region.

## Ahichhatra
Important Panchala center.

## Kampilya
Panchala center.

## Mithila
Videha capital.

## Kashi
Ancient city and kingdom.

## Kaushambi
Later Vedic/early historic settlement, important in Mahajanapada age.

## Vrata

# 46. VEDIC ADMINISTRATIVE AND REVENUE TERMS

## Rajan
King.

## Purohita

## Senani

## Gramani

## Vispati

## Shulka

## Dakshina

Gift.

---

# 47. VEDIC LEGAL AND SOCIAL ORDER TERMS

## Dharma
Duty and social order.

## Vyavahara
Legal or social transaction.

## Danda
Punishment.

## Rita
Cosmic order.

## Satya
Truth.

## Sabha as Court
The sabha may have had judicial functions.

## Samiti as Popular Body
The samiti represented broader tribal participation in early society.

## Purohita as Adviser
The priest advised the king and legitimized authority through rituals.

## King as Protector
The king protected cattle, tribe, territory, and social order.

## Varna Dharma
Duties based on varna; more developed in later texts.

## Ashrama Dharma
Duties based on stage of life.

---

# 48. VEDIC RITUAL FIRES

## Agni
Fire deity and ritual fire.

## Garhapatya
Domestic fire of the householder.

## Ahavaniya
Fire for offerings to gods.

## Dakshina
Southern fire used in specific rituals.

## Agnyadheya
Ritual establishment of sacred fires.

## Agnihotra
Daily fire ritual.

## Agnistoma
Basic Soma sacrifice.

## Ukthya
A Soma sacrifice variation.

## Atiratra
Overnight Soma sacrifice.

## Aptoryama
A Soma sacrifice.

## Jyotishtoma
A Soma sacrifice aimed at heavenly reward.

---

# 49. VEDIC RITUAL CLASSIFICATION

## Deva Rituals
Rituals directed to gods.

## Pitr Rituals
Rituals directed to ancestors.

## Domestic Rituals
Household rituals of birth, marriage, food, and death.

## Public Rituals
Large sacrifices sponsored by kings or wealthy householders.

## Royal Rituals
Rituals like Rajasuya, Vajapeya, and Ashvamedha.

## Fertility Rituals
Rituals for children, crops, cattle, and prosperity.

## Healing Rituals
Especially found in Atharvaveda.

## Protective Rituals
Rituals for protection from enemies, disease, demons, and misfortune.

---

# 50. VEDIC PHILOSOPHICAL SCHOOLS IN SEED FORM

## Karma Theory
The idea that actions produce consequences.

## Rebirth Theory
The idea that the soul is born again after death.

## Liberation Theory
The idea that knowledge can free one from rebirth.

## Ritualism
Belief that correct rituals maintain cosmic and social order.

## Knowledge Path
The Upanishadic idea that true knowledge leads to liberation.

## Renunciation
Withdrawal from worldly desires, increasingly valued in Upanishadic thought.

## Internalization of Sacrifice
Upanishadic shift from external fire rituals to inner meditation and knowledge.

## Brahmanism
Religious system centered on Veda, Brahmanas, priests, sacrifice, and social order.

## Early Vedanta
Philosophical ideas based on the Upanishads; later systematized as Vedanta.

---

# 51. COMMON UPSC COMPARISON TERMS

## Early Vedic vs Later Vedic
Early Vedic society was more pastoral, tribal, and relatively flexible. Later Vedic society was more agricultural, territorial, ritualistic, and hierarchical.

## Rigvedic vs Later Vedic Polity
Rigvedic polity was tribal with assemblies. Later Vedic polity had stronger kingship and territorial states.

## Rigvedic Economy vs Later Vedic Economy
Rigvedic economy centered on cattle. Later Vedic economy centered more on agriculture.

## Rigvedic Religion vs Later Vedic Religion
Rigvedic religion praised natural deities. Later Vedic religion emphasized rituals, Prajapati, and priestly authority.

## Brahmana vs Upanishad
Brahmanas explain rituals. Upanishads question rituals and focus on knowledge, self, and ultimate reality.

## Shruti vs Smriti
Shruti is revealed sacred literature. Smriti is remembered tradition composed later.

## Sabha vs Samiti
Sabha was a smaller elite assembly. Samiti was a broader popular assembly.

## Jana vs Janapada
Jana means tribe. Janapada means territory occupied by a tribe.

## Bali vs Bhaga
Bali was tribute or offering. Bhaga was the king’s share of produce.

## Ayas vs Shyama Ayas
Ayas meant metal, often copper/bronze in early usage. Shyama Ayas usually meant iron in later usage.

## Nishka vs Coin
Nishka was a gold ornament or value object, not a regular coin in the early Vedic period.

## Rta vs Dharma
Rta is cosmic order. Dharma is moral, social, and legal duty.

## Brahman vs Brahmana
Brahman means sacred power or ultimate reality. Brahmana means priest or ritual text, depending on context.

## Atman vs Brahman
Atman is inner self. Brahman is ultimate reality.

## Karma in Brahmanas vs Upanishads
In Brahmanas, karma often means ritual action. In Upanishads, it means moral action linked to rebirth.

---

## Oldest Veda
Rigveda.

## Veda of Melodies
Samaveda.

## Veda of Sacrificial Formulae

## Veda of Charms and Healing

## Oldest Mandalas of Rigveda

## Soma Mandala

## Purusha Sukta Location
Tenth Mandala of Rigveda.

## Gayatri Mantra Deity
Savitr.

## Battle of Ten Kings River
Parushni or Ravi.

## Battle of Ten Kings Winner
Sudas.

## Main Early Vedic Wealth
Cattle.

## Main Early Vedic Grain
Yava or barley.

## Main Later Vedic Grain
Rice became increasingly important.

## Early Vedic Region
Sapta Sindhu.

## Later Vedic Core Region
Kuru-Panchala.

## Pottery Linked with Later Vedic Period
Painted Grey Ware.

## Metal Linked with Later Vedic Expansion
Iron.

## Early Vedic Political Unit
Jana.

## Later Vedic Political Unit
Janapada.

## Early Vedic Assemblies
