## Royal Later Vedic Sacrifices
Rajasuya, Vajapeya, Ashvamedha.

## Main Rigvedic God
Indra.

## Fire God
Agni.

## Cosmic Order
Rta.

## Ultimate Reality in Upanishads
Brahman.

## Inner Self in Upanishads
Atman.

## Liberation
Moksha.

## Cycle of Rebirth
Samsara.

## Law of Action
Karma.

## Famous Woman Philosopher
Gargi.

## Famous Upanishadic Thinker
Yajnavalkya.

## King Associated with Upanishadic Debates
Janaka of Videha.

## Student Who Questioned Yama
Nachiketa.

## “Tat Tvam Asi” Source
Chandogya Upanishad.

## “Neti Neti” Source
Brihadaranyaka Upanishad.

## Geometry Texts
Shulba Sutras.

## Six Vedangas
Shiksha, Kalpa, Vyakarana, Nirukta, Chandas, Jyotisha.

---

# 53. CHRONOLOGICAL SNAPSHOT

## Stage 1: Early Rigvedic Period
Pastoral tribal society in Sapta Sindhu; cattle wealth; Indra, Agni, Soma worship; sabha, samiti, vidatha; Battle of Ten Kings; Rigvedic hymns.

## Stage 2: Late Rigvedic Transition
Expansion eastward; Purusha Sukta; stronger social differentiation; beginning of more complex rituals.

## Stage 3: Later Vedic Period
Kuru-Panchala heartland; settled agriculture; iron use; janapadas; stronger kingship; Brahmanas; royal sacrifices; varna hierarchy.

## Stage 4: Upanishadic Phase
Shift from ritual to philosophy; Brahman, Atman, karma, rebirth, moksha; Janaka, Yajnavalkya, Gargi, Maitreyi, Uddalaka, Shvetaketu, Nachiketa.

## Stage 5: Sutra Transition
Codification of rituals, domestic rites, social duties, altar geometry, and Vedic pronunciation through Sutras and Vedangas.

---

# 54. FINAL REVISION CLUSTER FOR UPSC PRELIMS

## Must Remember Texts
Rigveda, Samaveda, Yajurveda, Atharvaveda, Brahmanas, Aranyakas, Upanishads, Vedangas, Sutras.

## Must Remember Regions
Sapta Sindhu, Sarasvati, Parushni, Ganga-Yamuna Doab, Kuru-Panchala, Videha, Kosala, Kashi.

## Must Remember Archaeology
OCP, Copper Hoards, PGW, iron, Hastinapura, Atranjikhera, Bhagwanpura.

## Must Remember Economy
Cattle, yava, vrihi, plough, iron, bali, bhaga, kara, nishka, vanij.

## Must Remember Polity
Jana, vish, grama, kula, rajan, purohita, senani, sabha, samiti, vidatha, janapada, rashtra, ratnins.

## Must Remember Society
Varna, Brahmana, Kshatriya, Vaishya, Shudra, gotra, ashrama, samskara, patriarchy, women seers, Brahmavadini.

## Must Remember Religion
Indra, Agni, Soma, Varuna, Rudra, Vishnu, Prajapati, yajna, rta, dakshina, Agnihotra, Rajasuya, Vajapeya, Ashvamedha.

## Must Remember Philosophy
Brahman, Atman, karma, samsara, moksha, neti neti, tat tvam asi, aham brahmasmi, Om, prana, pancha kosha.

## Must Remember Personalities
Sudas, Vasistha, Vishvamitra, Yajnavalkya, Gargi, Maitreyi, Janaka, Uddalaka Aruni, Shvetaketu, Satyakama Jabala, Nachiketa.

## Must Remember Shift
Early Vedic = pastoral, tribal, north-western, simpler rituals.
Later Vedic = agricultural, territorial, Ganga-Yamuna region, complex rituals, stronger varna hierarchy, Upanishadic philosophy.

# JAINISM GLOSSARY FOR UPSC PRELIMS
## Chronological Coverage: Early Tirthankara Tradition → Parshvanatha → Mahavira → Early Jain Sangha → Councils and Sects → Jain Philosophy → Literature → Art, Architecture, and Legacy

> Note:
> Jainism is one of the ancient Shramana traditions of India.
> It rejects the authority of the Vedas, emphasizes non-violence, self-discipline, karma, rebirth, and liberation.
> For UPSC Prelims, focus especially on: Tirthankaras, Mahavira, Triratna, Panch Mahavrata, Anekantavada, Syadvada, Jain councils, sects, scriptures, art, architecture, and patronage.

---

# 1. BASIC TERMS OF JAINISM

## Jainism
An ancient Indian religion that teaches non-violence, truth, non-stealing, celibacy, non-possession, and liberation of the soul from karma.

## Jaina
A follower of Jina. The word means one who follows the path shown by the spiritual conquerors.

## Jina
“Conqueror”. A person who has conquered attachment, desire, anger, ego, and ignorance.

## Tirthankara
A spiritual teacher who creates a “ford” or path across the ocean of worldly suffering. Jainism has 24 Tirthankaras in the current time cycle.

## Tirtha
A crossing place or spiritual ford. In Jainism, it means the path to liberation.

## Arihant
A perfected being who has destroyed inner enemies such as anger, pride, deceit, and greed, but is still embodied.

## Siddha
A liberated soul that has left the body and reached the top of the universe, free from karma forever.

## Kevalin
One who has attained Kevala Jnana or perfect knowledge.

## Nirgrantha
Literally “free from bonds”. An early term used for Jain monks, especially followers of Mahavira.

## Shramana
A renunciant or wandering ascetic tradition outside orthodox Vedic ritualism. Jainism and Buddhism belong to the Shramana tradition.

## Nastika
A school that does not accept the authority of the Vedas. Jainism is called Nastika in the Brahmanical classification, though it is deeply religious.

## Heterodox School
A term used for traditions like Jainism and Buddhism that did not accept Vedic authority.

## Orthodox School
A school that accepts Vedic authority, such as Nyaya, Vaisheshika, Samkhya, Yoga, Mimamsa, and Vedanta.

## Moksha
Liberation from the cycle of birth and death.

## Nirvana
Final liberation or release from bondage. In Jainism, it means the soul is free from all karma.

## Samsara
The cycle of birth, death, and rebirth.

## Karma
In Jainism, karma is a subtle material substance that attaches to the soul because of actions, passions, and desires.

## Ahimsa
Non-violence. It is the central principle of Jainism.

## Aparigraha
Non-possession or non-attachment to property, wealth, objects, and desires.

## Tapas
Austerity or disciplined hardship used to destroy karma.

## Samyama
Self-control.

## Vrata
A vow or disciplined rule of conduct.

## Dharma
In Jainism, dharma can mean righteous conduct, teaching, or also the principle that helps motion in Jain metaphysics.

## Sangha
The Jain community of monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen.

## Shravaka
A Jain layman.

## Shravika
A Jain laywoman.

## Sadhu
A Jain monk.

## Sadhvi
A Jain nun.

## Muni
A Jain monk or ascetic.

## Aryika
A Digambara Jain nun.

## Upadhyaya
A Jain teacher-monk who teaches scriptures.

## Acharya
Head of a Jain monastic order.

## Panch Parameshthi
The five supreme beings in Jainism: Arihant, Siddha, Acharya, Upadhyaya, and Sadhu.

---

# 2. CHRONOLOGICAL BACKGROUND: PRE-MAHAVIRA JAIN TRADITION

## Tirthankara Tradition
The Jain belief that spiritual teachers appear in every time cycle to revive the path of liberation.

## Twenty-Four Tirthankaras
The 24 spiritual teachers of Jainism in the current descending time cycle.

## Rishabhanatha
The first Tirthankara of Jainism. He is also called Adinatha.

## Adinatha
Another name for Rishabhanatha, meaning “first lord”.

## Bharata
Son of Rishabhanatha according to Jain tradition. India’s name Bharat is sometimes traditionally linked with him.

## Bahubali
Son of Rishabhanatha and brother of Bharata. He is famous for renunciation and meditation. His huge statue is at Shravanabelagola.

## Ajitanatha
The second Tirthankara.

## Sambhavanatha
The third Tirthankara.

## Abhinandananatha
The fourth Tirthankara.

## Sumatinatha
The fifth Tirthankara.

## Padmaprabha
The sixth Tirthankara.

## Suparshvanatha
The seventh Tirthankara.

## Chandraprabha
The eighth Tirthankara.

## Pushpadanta
The ninth Tirthankara, also called Suvidhinatha.

## Suvidhinatha
Another name of Pushpadanta, the ninth Tirthankara.

## Shitalanatha
The tenth Tirthankara.

## Shreyansanatha
The eleventh Tirthankara.

## Vasupujya
The twelfth Tirthankara.

## Vimalanatha
The thirteenth Tirthankara.

## Anantanatha
The fourteenth Tirthankara.

## Dharmanatha
The fifteenth Tirthankara.

## Shantinatha
The sixteenth Tirthankara.

## Kunthunatha
The seventeenth Tirthankara.

## Aranatha
The eighteenth Tirthankara.

## Mallinatha
The nineteenth Tirthankara. Svetambaras believe Mallinatha was female, while Digambaras believe Mallinatha was male.

## Munisuvrata
The twentieth Tirthankara.

## Naminatha
The twenty-first Tirthankara.

## Neminatha
The twenty-second Tirthankara, also called Arishtanemi.

## Arishtanemi
Another name for Neminatha. Jain tradition associates him with Krishna’s family and with renunciation before marriage.

## Parshvanatha
The twenty-third Tirthankara. He is considered a historical figure by many scholars and lived before Mahavira.

## Mahavira
The twenty-fourth and last Tirthankara of the present time cycle. He organized and revived the Jain community.

---

# 3. TIRTHANKARA SYMBOLS AND ICONOGRAPHY

## Lanchhana
The identifying symbol of a Tirthankara, usually shown below the image.

## Rishabhanatha Symbol
Bull.

## Ajitanatha Symbol
Elephant.

## Sambhavanatha Symbol
Horse.

## Abhinandananatha Symbol
Monkey.

## Sumatinatha Symbol
Curlew or heron-like bird.

## Padmaprabha Symbol
Red lotus.

## Suparshvanatha Symbol
Swastika.

## Chandraprabha Symbol
Crescent moon.

## Pushpadanta Symbol
Crocodile or makara.

## Shitalanatha Symbol
Shrivatsa or kalpavriksha, depending on tradition.

## Shreyansanatha Symbol
Rhinoceros.

## Vasupujya Symbol
Buffalo.

## Vimalanatha Symbol
Boar.

## Anantanatha Symbol
Falcon or porcupine, depending on tradition.

## Dharmanatha Symbol
Vajra or thunderbolt.

## Shantinatha Symbol
Deer or antelope.

## Kunthunatha Symbol
Goat.

## Aranatha Symbol
Fish.

## Mallinatha Symbol
Water pot or kalasha.

## Munisuvrata Symbol
Tortoise.

## Naminatha Symbol
Blue lotus.

## Neminatha Symbol
Conch.

## Parshvanatha Symbol
Snake hood.

## Mahavira Symbol
Lion.

## Kayotsarga
A standing meditation posture in which the body is abandoned and the soul is the focus.

## Padmasana
Lotus sitting posture used in Jain images.

## Srivatsa
An auspicious mark often shown on the chest of Tirthankara images.

## Halo
Circular glow behind the head, symbolizing spiritual greatness.

## Chauri Bearers
Attendants shown holding fly-whisks near Tirthankaras.

## Triple Umbrella
Three-tiered umbrella shown above Tirthankara images, symbolizing spiritual sovereignty.

## Ashta Pratiharya
Eight auspicious signs or miraculous features associated with a Tirthankara’s preaching assembly.

## Samavasarana
The divine preaching hall of a Tirthankara after attaining Kevala Jnana.

## Yaksha
Male attendant deity of a Tirthankara.

## Yakshi
Female attendant deity of a Tirthankara.

## Chakreshvari
Yakshi associated with Rishabhanatha.

## Padmavati
Yakshi associated with Parshvanatha.

## Ambika
Important Jain Yakshi, often associated with Neminatha.

## Dharanendra
Serpent Yaksha associated with Parshvanatha.

---

# 4. PARSHVANATHA AND PRE-MAHAVIRA JAINISM

## Parshvanatha
The 23rd Tirthankara. He is associated with four vows and is believed to have lived before Mahavira.

## Four Vows of Parshvanatha
The four vows taught by Parshvanatha: non-violence, truth, non-stealing, and non-possession.

## Chaturyama Dharma
The fourfold discipline of Parshvanatha.

## Ahimsa under Parshvanatha
Non-violence was already central before Mahavira.

## Satya under Parshvanatha
Truthfulness was one of the four vows.

## Asteya under Parshvanatha
Non-stealing was one of the four vows.

## Aparigraha under Parshvanatha
Non-possession was one of the four vows.

## Mahavira’s Fifth Vow
Mahavira added Brahmacharya or celibacy as a separate fifth vow.

## Parshvanatha Followers
Followers of Parshvanatha existed before Mahavira and were later integrated into Mahavira’s Jain Sangha.

---

# 5. MAHAVIRA: LIFE AND CHRONOLOGY

## Mahavira
The 24th Tirthankara of Jainism. He was a contemporary of the early Mahajanapada age.

## Vardhamana
The birth name of Mahavira.

## Mahavira Meaning
“Great hero”. The title was given because of his extreme courage and self-control.

## Jina Mahavira
Mahavira as the spiritual conqueror.

## Nataputta
A term used for Mahavira in early Buddhist texts, meaning son of the Nata or Jnatrika clan.

## Nigantha Nataputta
The name for Mahavira in Buddhist Pali texts.

## Kundagrama
Traditional birthplace of Mahavira near Vaishali.

## Vaishali
A major city of the Vajji confederacy, connected with Mahavira’s life.

## Jnatrika Clan
The clan to which Mahavira belonged. It is also called Naya or Nata.

## Naya Clan
Another name for Mahavira’s clan.

## Kshatriya Background
Mahavira was born into a Kshatriya family.

## Siddhartha
Father of Mahavira.

## Trishala
Mother of Mahavira. She is also called Priyakarini in some traditions.

## Yashoda
Mahavira’s wife according to Jain tradition.

## Priyadarshana
Mahavira’s daughter according to tradition. She is also called Anojja or Anavadya in some accounts.

## Jamali
Mahavira’s son-in-law and an early dissenter in Jain tradition.

## Renunciation of Mahavira
Mahavira renounced worldly life at about the age of 30.

## Mahabhinishkramana in Jain Context
The great renunciation of Mahavira, similar in idea to the renunciation of other Shramana teachers.

## Twelve Years of Austerity
Mahavira practiced severe austerities for about twelve and a half years before attaining enlightenment.

## Kevala Jnana of Mahavira
Perfect knowledge attained by Mahavira after long austerity.

## Jambhiyagrama
Place traditionally associated with Mahavira’s enlightenment.

## Rijupalika River
River near which Mahavira is said to have attained Kevala Jnana.

## Sal Tree
Tree associated in tradition with Mahavira’s enlightenment.

## Kevalin Mahavira
Mahavira after attaining perfect knowledge.

## Preaching Career
After enlightenment, Mahavira preached for about thirty years.

## Pavapuri
Place in Bihar where Mahavira attained nirvana.

## Pava
Another name associated with Mahavira’s final liberation.

## Nirvana of Mahavira
Mahavira attained final liberation at Pavapuri around the age of 72 according to tradition.

## Mahavira and Bimbisara
Mahavira was a contemporary of Bimbisara of Magadha.

## Mahavira and Ajatashatru
Mahavira was also a contemporary of Ajatashatru.

## Mahavira and Buddha
Mahavira and Buddha lived in the same broad period of the 6th century BCE, but founded different traditions.

---

# 6. HISTORICAL CONTEXT OF JAINISM

## Sixth Century BCE
The period when Jainism and Buddhism became prominent in north India.

## Second Urbanization
The growth of towns and cities in the Ganga valley around the 6th century BCE. It formed the background for Jainism and Buddhism.

## Mahajanapadas
The sixteen major states of north India during the time of Mahavira and Buddha.

## Magadha
A powerful Mahajanapada associated with the spread of Jainism and Buddhism.

## Vajji
A republican confederacy associated with Vaishali and Mahavira’s background.

## Vaishali
A major republican center and important place in Jain and Buddhist traditions.

## Rajagriha
Capital of Magadha under Bimbisara and Ajatashatru; important for early Jain and Buddhist activity.

## Champa
An ancient city associated with Jain tradition.

## Mithila
An ancient city in Videha, associated with intellectual and religious activity.

## Shramana Movement
A broad movement of renunciation, meditation, austerity, and rejection of ritualism.

## Reaction against Vedic Ritualism
Jainism emerged partly in a context where many groups questioned expensive sacrifices and Brahmanical ritual authority.

## Urban Merchant Support
Jainism received support from merchants because of its ethics of non-violence, truth, trade discipline, and non-possession.

## Gahapati
A wealthy householder or landholder in early historic society.

## Setthi
A wealthy merchant or banker who often supported religious communities.

## Shreni
A guild or association of traders or artisans. Jainism had important links with mercantile groups.

---

# 7. EARLY JAIN COMMUNITY

## Jain Sangha
The organized community of Jain monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen.

## Chaturvidha Sangha
The fourfold Jain community: monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen.

## Sadhu
Male renunciant.

## Sadhvi
Female renunciant.

## Shravaka
Male lay follower.

## Shravika
Female lay follower.

## Gana
A monastic group or order.

## Ganadhara
Chief disciple of a Tirthankara.

## Eleven Ganadharas
Mahavira had eleven chief disciples according to Jain tradition.

## Indrabhuti Gautama
The most important Ganadhara of Mahavira.

## Gautama Swami
Another name for Indrabhuti Gautama.

## Sudharma
A Ganadhara who continued the Jain tradition after Mahavira.

## Jambu Swami
Traditionally regarded as the last omniscient teacher after Mahavira.

## Kevali Lineage
The lineage of teachers believed to have possessed perfect knowledge after Mahavira.

## Shruta Kevali
A teacher who had complete knowledge of Jain scriptures, though not necessarily Kevala Jnana.

## Bhadrabahu
Important Jain teacher traditionally associated with the migration to Karnataka and with Chandragupta Maurya.

## Sthulabhadra
Important Jain teacher associated with the tradition that preserved scriptures during the early council.

---

# 8. CORE JAIN DOCTRINES

## Triratna
The Three Jewels of Jainism: right faith, right knowledge, and right conduct.

## Ratnatraya
Another name for the Three Jewels.

## Samyak Darshana
Right faith or right perception.

## Samyak Jnana
Right knowledge.

## Samyak Charitra
Right conduct.

## Ahimsa
Non-violence in thought, speech, and action.

## Satya
Truthfulness.

## Asteya
Non-stealing.

## Brahmacharya
Celibacy or control of sexual desire.

## Aparigraha
Non-possession and non-attachment.

## Panch Mahavrata
The five great vows followed by Jain monks and nuns.

## Mahavrata
A great vow followed strictly by monks and nuns.

## Anuvrata
A smaller or limited vow followed by laypersons.

## Guna Vrata
Supplementary vows that strengthen lay discipline.

## Shiksha Vrata
Training vows for laypersons to practice religious discipline.

## Sallekhana
Voluntary peaceful fasting unto death under strict spiritual conditions. It is meant to reduce attachment, not to escape suffering casually.

## Santhara
Another term for Sallekhana, especially used in some Jain communities.

## Samvara
Stopping the inflow of karma into the soul.

## Nirjara
Shedding or destruction of accumulated karma.

## Bandha
Bondage of the soul due to karma.

## Ashrava
Inflow of karmic matter into the soul.

## Moksha Marga
The path to liberation.

## Jiva Shuddhi
Purification of the soul.

## Self-Conquest
The conquest of passions and desires, central to Jain ethics.

---

# 9. THE FIVE GREAT VOWS

## Ahimsa Mahavrata
The vow of complete non-violence. A monk or nun must avoid harming even the smallest living beings.

## Satya Mahavrata
The vow of truthfulness. One must avoid lies, harmful speech, and deception.

## Asteya Mahavrata
The vow of non-stealing. One must not take anything not willingly given.

## Brahmacharya Mahavrata
The vow of celibacy. It was emphasized separately by Mahavira.

## Aparigraha Mahavrata
The vow of non-possession. A monk or nun gives up property, attachment, and ownership.

## Ahimsa as Supreme Vow
In Jainism, non-violence is the highest religious duty.

## Mental Violence
Violence caused by harmful thoughts, anger, hatred, or intention.

## Verbal Violence
Violence caused by harsh, false, or harmful speech.

## Physical Violence
Violence caused by bodily action.

## Intentional Violence
Violence done deliberately. Jainism treats intention as very important.

## Careful Action
A Jain ethical practice of moving, speaking, eating, and living carefully to avoid harm.

---

# 10. LAY VOWS AND HOUSEHOLDER ETHICS

## Twelve Vows of Laypersons
The standard vows followed by Jain householders: five Anuvratas, three Gunavratas, and four Shikshavratas.

## Five Anuvratas
Limited vows of non-violence, truth, non-stealing, chastity, and non-possession for lay followers.

## Ahimsa Anuvrata
Limited vow of non-violence for laypersons.

## Satya Anuvrata
Limited vow of truthfulness.

## Achaurya Anuvrata
Limited vow of non-stealing.

## Brahmacharya Anuvrata
Limited vow of sexual restraint or marital fidelity.

## Aparigraha Anuvrata
Limited vow of reducing possessions and attachment.

## Digvrata
Vow to limit movement in different directions to reduce harm and desire.

## Bhogopabhoga Parimana
Vow to limit consumable and non-consumable objects.

## Anartha Danda Viramana
Vow to avoid purposeless sinful activities.

## Samayika
Periodic meditation and practice of equanimity.

## Desavakasika
Vow to further restrict movement for a limited time.

## Posadha
A practice where laypersons live like monks for a limited period.

## Atithi Samvibhaga
Offering food and support to monks, nuns, and deserving persons.

## Dana
Charity or giving.

## Abhaya Dana
Gift of fearlessness, meaning protection of living beings.

## Ahara Dana
Gift of food.

## Aushadha Dana
Gift of medicine.

## Jnana Dana
Gift of knowledge.

## Shravaka Dharma
Religious duties of Jain laymen.

## Shravika Dharma
Religious duties of Jain laywomen.

---

# 11. JAIN METAPHYSICS: BASIC SUBSTANCES

## Dravya
Substance or reality. Jainism believes reality is made of eternal substances.

## Six Dravyas
The six substances: Jiva, Pudgala, Dharma, Adharma, Akasha, and Kala.

## Jiva
Soul or living substance. Every living being has a soul.

## Ajiva
Non-living substance.

## Pudgala
Matter. It includes physical objects, body, speech, mind, and karmic particles.

## Dharma Dravya
The medium that allows motion. It does not mean religion or morality in this metaphysical context.

## Adharma Dravya
The medium that allows rest. It does not mean sin in this metaphysical context.

## Akasha
Space.

## Kala
Time.

## Astikaya
An extended substance occupying space.

## Panchastikaya
The five extended substances: Jiva, Pudgala, Dharma, Adharma, and Akasha.

## Jivastikaya
The category of souls as extended substances.

## Pudgalastikaya
Matter as an extended substance.

## Dharmastikaya
Medium of motion as an extended substance.

## Adharmastikaya
Medium of rest as an extended substance.

## Akashastikaya
Space as an extended substance.

## Kala as Non-Astikaya
Time is a substance but not considered an astikaya in the same way as the other five.

## Guna
Quality of a substance.

## Paryaya
Mode or changing state of a substance.

## Substance and Change
Jainism teaches that reality has both permanence and change.

---

# 12. JAIN TATTVAS

## Tattva
A fundamental truth or category of reality.

## Seven Tattvas
Jiva, Ajiva, Ashrava, Bandha, Samvara, Nirjara, and Moksha.

## Nine Tattvas
The seven tattvas plus Punya and Papa.

## Jiva Tattva
The truth of living soul.

## Ajiva Tattva
The truth of non-living reality.

## Ashrava Tattva
The inflow of karmic matter into the soul.

## Bandha Tattva
Bondage of karma with the soul.

## Samvara Tattva
Stopping the inflow of karma.

## Nirjara Tattva
Shedding accumulated karma.

## Moksha Tattva
Liberation of the soul.

## Punya
Merit-producing karma.

## Papa
Sinful or harmful karma.

## Karmic Bondage
Attachment of karmic particles to the soul.

## Karmic Shedding
Removal of karmic particles through austerity and right conduct.

---

# 13. JAIN THEORY OF SOUL

## Soul
The conscious principle present in all living beings.

## Consciousness
The essential quality of the soul.

## Upayoga
Conscious activity of the soul, including knowledge and perception.

## Infinite Knowledge
A natural quality of the pure soul.

## Infinite Perception
A natural quality of the pure soul.

## Infinite Bliss
A natural quality of the pure soul.

## Infinite Energy
A natural quality of the pure soul.

## Bound Soul
A soul attached to karma and trapped in samsara.

## Liberated Soul
A soul free from karma, birth, and death.

## Siddha Soul
A liberated soul residing at Siddhashila.

## Embodied Soul
A soul living in a body due to karma.

## Mobile Beings
Living beings that can move, such as humans, animals, insects, and gods.

## Immobile Beings
One-sensed beings such as earth-bodied, water-bodied, fire-bodied, air-bodied, and plant-bodied beings.

## One-Sensed Beings
Living beings with only touch as a sense.

## Two-Sensed Beings
Beings with touch and taste.

## Three-Sensed Beings
Beings with touch, taste, and smell.

## Four-Sensed Beings
Beings with touch, taste, smell, and sight.

## Five-Sensed Beings
Beings with touch, taste, smell, sight, and hearing.

## Trasa
Mobile living beings.

## Sthavara
Immobile living beings.

## Nigoda
Extremely minute living beings in Jain cosmology.

## Prithvikaya
Earth-bodied living beings.

## Apkaya
Water-bodied living beings.

## Tejaskaya
Fire-bodied living beings.

## Vayukaya
Air-bodied living beings.

## Vanaspatikaya
Plant-bodied living beings.

---

# 14. JAIN THEORY OF KARMA

## Karma in Jainism
A fine material substance that binds to the soul because of passions and actions.

## Karmic Particles
Subtle matter that attaches to the soul.

## Kashaya
Passion that causes karmic bondage.

## Four Kashayas
Anger, pride, deceit, and greed.

## Krodha
Anger.

## Mana
Pride.

## Maya
Deceit.

## Lobha
Greed.

## Ghatiya Karma
Destructive karma that directly harms the soul’s qualities.

## Aghatiya Karma
Non-destructive karma that affects body, lifespan, status, and experience.

## Jnanavaraniya Karma
Knowledge-obscuring karma.

## Darshanavaraniya Karma
Perception-obscuring karma.

## Mohaniya Karma
Deluding karma, which creates wrong belief and conduct.

## Antaraya Karma
Obstructing karma, which blocks energy and action.

## Vedaniya Karma
Feeling-producing karma, causing pleasure or pain.

## Nama Karma
Body-making karma.

## Gotra Karma
Status-determining karma.

## Ayushya Karma
Lifespan-determining karma.

## Leshya
Coloring or condition of the soul caused by mental and karmic states.

## Six Leshyas
Black, blue, grey, yellow, red, and white soul-colorations.

## Krishna Leshya
Black leshya, associated with highly harmful mental states.

## Nila Leshya
Blue leshya, associated with negative mental states.

## Kapota Leshya
Grey leshya, associated with dull or harmful conduct.

## Tejo Leshya
Red leshya, associated with improving conduct.

## Padma Leshya
Yellow or lotus-like leshya, associated with good conduct.

## Shukla Leshya
White leshya, associated with purity and spiritual progress.

---

# 15. JAIN EPISTEMOLOGY

## Jnana
Knowledge.

## Pramana
Valid means of knowledge.

## Naya
Partial standpoint or viewpoint.

## Anekantavada
Doctrine of many-sided reality. It teaches that truth has many aspects.

## Syadvada
Doctrine of conditional expression. It teaches that statements should be made with qualification, such as “from one perspective”.

## Saptabhangi
Sevenfold logical predication used in Syadvada.

## Nayavada
Doctrine of standpoints. It explains that every statement expresses only one aspect of reality.

## Absolute Statement
A statement claiming complete truth from one perspective only; Jain logic warns against it.

## Conditional Statement
A statement made with awareness of perspective and limitation.

## Intellectual Non-Violence
The idea that one should avoid dogmatism and respect multiple viewpoints.

## Pratyaksha Jnana
Direct knowledge.

## Paroksha Jnana
Indirect knowledge.

## Mati Jnana
Sensory and mental knowledge.

## Shruta Jnana
Scriptural or verbal knowledge.

## Avadhi Jnana
Clairvoyant knowledge of material things.

## Manahparyaya Jnana
Telepathic knowledge of others’ thoughts.

## Kevala Jnana
Perfect and infinite knowledge.

## Mithya Jnana
Wrong knowledge.

## Samyak Jnana
Right knowledge.

## Darshana
Perception or faith.

## Samyak Darshana
Right faith.

## Mithyatva
Wrong belief or false worldview.

---

# 16. SAPTABHANGI: SEVENFOLD PREDICATION

## Syad Asti
From one perspective, it exists.

## Syad Nasti
From one perspective, it does not exist.

## Syad Asti Nasti
From one perspective, it exists and does not exist.

## Syad Avaktavya
From one perspective, it is indescribable.

## Syad Asti Avaktavya
From one perspective, it exists and is indescribable.

## Syad Nasti Avaktavya
From one perspective, it does not exist and is indescribable.

## Syad Asti Nasti Avaktavya
From one perspective, it exists, does not exist, and is indescribable.

## Syat
“From a certain standpoint” or “in some respect”.

## Relative Truth
Truth understood according to context, standpoint, and condition.

## Non-Absolutism
The refusal to treat one partial view as the whole truth.

---

# 17. JAIN COSMOLOGY

## Loka
The inhabited universe.

## Aloka
The empty space beyond the inhabited universe.

## Lokakasha
The space occupied by the universe.

## Alokakasha
Space outside the universe.

## Urdhva Loka
Upper world where celestial beings live.

## Madhya Loka
Middle world where humans, animals, and plants live.

## Adho Loka
Lower world where hellish beings live.

## Siddhashila
The top of the universe where liberated souls reside.

## Jambudvipa
The central continent in Jain cosmology where humans live.

## Mount Meru
The cosmic mountain at the center of Jambudvipa.

## Bharata Kshetra
Region of Jambudvipa where humans like us live and where Tirthankaras appear.

## Airavata Kshetra
Another region in Jain cosmology where Tirthankaras can appear.

## Videha Kshetra
A region where spiritual activity is always possible.

## Kalachakra
Wheel of time.

## Utsarpini
Ascending half-cycle of time, when conditions gradually improve.

## Avasarpini
Descending half-cycle of time, when conditions gradually decline.

## Ara
A time period within a half-cycle.

## Six Aras
Six stages of time in each ascending or descending cycle.

## Tiryanch
Animal and plant forms of life.

## Naraki
Hellish beings.

## Deva
Celestial beings or gods.

## Manusya
Human beings.

## Samsari Jiva
Soul still moving through rebirth.

## Siddha Jiva
Liberated soul.

---

# 18. JAIN PATH OF LIBERATION

## Moksha Marga
The path to liberation through right faith, right knowledge, and right conduct.

## Gunasthana
Fourteen stages of spiritual development.

## First Gunasthana
Stage of wrong belief.

## Fourth Gunasthana
Stage of right faith.

## Seventh Gunasthana
Stage of advanced self-restraint.

## Thirteenth Gunasthana
Stage of embodied omniscience.

## Fourteenth Gunasthana
Final stage before liberation.

## Samvara Practice
Stopping new karma through vows, carefulness, and self-control.

## Nirjara Practice
Destroying old karma through austerity and meditation.

## Tapas Practice
Austerity used to reduce karma.

## External Austerities
Physical disciplines such as fasting, limiting food, and bodily endurance.

## Internal Austerities
Mental and spiritual disciplines such as repentance, humility, meditation, and self-study.

## Kayotsarga
Abandonment of body-consciousness during meditation.

## Dhyana
Meditation.

## Shukla Dhyana
Pure meditation leading toward liberation.

## Pratikramana
Repentance and review of one’s faults.

## Alochana
Confession of faults.

## Pratyakhyana
Renunciation or resolve to avoid future faults.

## Samayika
Practice of equanimity.

## Equanimity
Mental balance toward pleasure, pain, friend, enemy, gain, and loss.

---

# 19. JAIN AUSTERITIES

## Upavasa
Fasting.

## Unodari
Eating less than one’s hunger.

## Vritti Parisankhyana
Limiting the types or sources of food one accepts.

## Rasa Parityaga
Giving up tasty foods.

## Kaya Klesha
Enduring bodily hardship.

## Sanlinata
Withdrawal or solitude.

## Prayashchitta
Repentance.

## Vinaya
Humility and respect.

## Vaiyavritya
Service to monks, nuns, teachers, or the needy.

## Svadhyaya
Self-study of scriptures.

## Vyutsarga
Abandonment of attachment to the body.

## Dhyana
Meditation.

## Bahya Tapas
External austerities.

## Abhyantara Tapas
Internal austerities.

---

# 20. JAIN MONASTIC DISCIPLINE

## Mahavrata
Great vows followed by monks and nuns.

## Gochari
Alms collection by Jain monks and nuns.

## Bhiksha
Alms or food received by ascetics.

## Ahara
Food.

## Vihar
Movement or wandering of monks and nuns.

## Chaturmas
Four-month rainy season stay, when monks and nuns avoid travel to reduce harm to living beings.

## Paryushan
Major Jain festival of repentance, self-discipline, and forgiveness.

## Das Lakshana
A Digambara Jain festival emphasizing ten virtues.

## Muhapatti
A cloth covering used by some Jain monks and nuns to avoid harming tiny organisms through breath.

## Rajoharana
A broom used by Svetambara monks and nuns to gently clear the ground.

## Picchi
Peacock-feather broom used by Digambara monks.

## Kamandalu
Water pot used by some Jain monks.

## Nudity in Digambara Monasticism
Digambara male monks give up clothing as a sign of complete non-possession.

## White Robe in Svetambara Monasticism
Svetambara monks and nuns wear white clothes.

## Alms Rules
Strict rules governing what food can be accepted, from whom, and how.

## Non-Cooking Rule
Many Jain monks and nuns do not cook because cooking may harm living beings.

## Walking Barefoot
A common monastic practice showing simplicity and care.

## Night Eating Restriction
Many Jains avoid eating after sunset to reduce harm to small organisms.

## Water Filtering
Filtering water to avoid harming tiny living beings.

## Careful Speech
Speaking truthfully and non-harmfully.

## Careful Movement
Walking and moving with attention to avoid harming life.

---

# 21. JAIN SECTS: EARLY DIVISION

## Digambara
A major Jain sect meaning “sky-clad”. Digambara monks traditionally renounce all clothing.

## Svetambara
A major Jain sect meaning “white-clad”. Svetambara monks and nuns wear white robes.

## Digambara-Svetambara Split
The major sectarian division in Jainism, traditionally linked to differences over monastic practice, scriptures, and migration.

## Bhadrabahu Migration Tradition
Tradition that Bhadrabahu and Chandragupta Maurya migrated to Karnataka during a famine in Magadha.

## Magadhan Famine
A famine traditionally associated with the division between Jain groups that stayed in Magadha and those who migrated south.

## Chandragupta Maurya and Jainism
Jain tradition says Chandragupta Maurya became a Jain monk and died by Sallekhana at Shravanabelagola.

## Shravanabelagola Migration
The Karnataka site associated with Bhadrabahu and Chandragupta Maurya.

## Scriptural Dispute
Digambaras believe the original Jain scriptures were lost, while Svetambaras preserve Agamas as canonical.

## Clothing Dispute
Digambaras emphasize complete nudity for male monks; Svetambaras allow white clothing.

## Women and Liberation Debate
Svetambaras believe women can attain liberation; Digambaras traditionally hold that women must be reborn as men before final liberation.

## Mallinatha Debate
Svetambaras believe Mallinatha, the 19th Tirthankara, was female; Digambaras believe Mallinatha was male.

---

# 22. LATER JAIN SECTS AND SUB-SECTS

## Murtipujaka
Image-worshipping Svetambara Jains.

## Sthanakvasi
A non-image-worshipping Svetambara sect that emphasizes meditation, ethics, and scripture.

## Terapanthi Svetambara
A reformist Svetambara sect founded by Acharya Bhikshu.

## Deravasi
Another term for temple-going or image-worshipping Svetambaras.

## Digambara Bisapanthi
A Digambara sub-sect with temple and ritual practices.

## Digambara Terapanthi
A Digambara reformist sub-sect that opposed certain ritual practices.

## Taranapanthi
A Digambara-related sect founded by Taran Svami, emphasizing scriptures over image worship.

## Yapaniya
An extinct Jain sect that had features of both Digambara and Svetambara traditions.

## Gaccha
A monastic lineage, especially among Svetambaras.

## Kharatara Gaccha
An important Svetambara monastic lineage.

## Tapa Gaccha
A major Svetambara monastic lineage.

## Mula Sangha
Important Digambara monastic lineage.

## Kashtha Sangha
A Digambara monastic lineage.

## Sena Gana
A Digambara monastic group.

## Balatkara Gana
A Digambara monastic group.

---

# 23. JAIN COUNCILS

## Jain Council
A gathering of Jain monks to preserve, organize, or compile scriptures.

## First Jain Council
Traditionally held at Pataliputra under Sthulabhadra after a famine. It is associated with preservation of Jain teachings.

## Pataliputra Council
Another name for the first Jain council in some traditions.

## Sthulabhadra
Teacher associated with the Pataliputra council and the preservation of Jain scriptures.

## Second Jain Council
Associated with Vallabhi in Gujarat, where Svetambara scriptures were compiled in written form.

## Vallabhi Council
Council where the Svetambara canon was finally compiled, traditionally under Devardhigani Kshamashramana.

## Devardhigani Kshamashramana
Jain teacher associated with the final redaction of the Svetambara canon at Vallabhi.

## Mathura Council
A Jain council or textual activity center sometimes mentioned in relation to early scripture preservation.

## Loss of Drishtivada
The twelfth Anga, Drishtivada, is considered lost.

## Oral Transmission
The early Jain scriptures were transmitted orally before being written down.

## Canon Formation
The process by which Jain scriptures were organized into accepted collections.

---

# 24. JAIN SCRIPTURES: BASIC TERMS

## Agama
Canonical scripture of Svetambara Jainism.

## Siddhanta
Doctrine or canon; sometimes used for Jain scriptures.

## Purva
Ancient teachings said to have been contained in the lost Drishtivada.

## Anga
Main canonical texts of Svetambara Jainism.

## Twelve Angas
The twelve major canonical texts, of which the twelfth, Drishtivada, is lost.

## Upanga
Secondary canonical texts attached to the Angas.

## Cheda Sutra
Texts dealing with monastic discipline and rules.

## Mula Sutra
Basic texts studied by monks and nuns.

## Prakirnaka
Miscellaneous canonical texts.

## Chulika Sutra
Appendix-like texts.

## Ardhamagadhi
A Prakrit language used in early Jain scriptures.

## Prakrit
Middle Indo-Aryan language used widely in Jain and Buddhist literature.

## Jain Prakrit
Prakrit used in Jain texts.

## Shauraseni
Prakrit used in several Jain texts, especially Digambara literature.

## Maharashtri Prakrit
Prakrit used in Jain literary works.

## Apabhramsha
Later Middle Indo-Aryan language used in Jain literature.

## Sanskrit in Jainism
Jains also composed many philosophical, narrative, and scientific works in Sanskrit.

## Kannada Jain Literature
Jain authors made major contributions to early Kannada literature.

## Tamil Jain Literature
Jains contributed to early Tamil literature and ethical works.

---

# 25. TWELVE ANGAS

## Acharanga Sutra
Text dealing with conduct of monks and Mahavira’s ascetic life.

## Sutrakritanga
Text refuting rival doctrines and explaining Jain teachings.

## Sthananga
Text arranged by numerical categories.

## Samavayanga
Text arranged by numerical groupings.

## Vyakhyaprajnapti
A major text also called Bhagavati Sutra, containing dialogues and doctrinal explanations.

## Bhagavati Sutra
Another name for Vyakhyaprajnapti.

## Jnatadharmakatha
Text containing religious stories and teachings.

## Upasakadasa
Text dealing with lay followers.

## Antakriddasha
Text about those who ended rebirth through austerity.

## Anuttaropapatika
Text about beings reborn in highest heavens before liberation.

## Prashnavyakarana
Text dealing with questions and explanations.

## Vipaka Sutra
Text explaining the results of karma.

## Drishtivada
The twelfth Anga, considered lost.

---

# 26. IMPORTANT JAIN TEXTS OUTSIDE THE ANGAS

## Kalpa Sutra
A Svetambara text containing lives of Tirthankaras, especially Mahavira, Parshvanatha, Neminatha, and Rishabhanatha. It is recited during Paryushan.

## Uttaradhyayana Sutra
A popular Jain text containing teachings, stories, and ethical lessons.

## Dasavaikalika Sutra
A text on monastic conduct.

## Nandi Sutra
A text dealing with knowledge categories.

## Anuyogadvara Sutra
A text explaining methods of scriptural interpretation.

## Avashyaka Sutra
A text dealing with essential duties and rituals.

## Ogha Niryukti
A Jain text related to monastic rules.

## Shatkhandagama
A major Digambara scripture dealing with karma theory.

## Kasayapahuda
A Digambara text dealing with passions.

## Tattvartha Sutra
A major Jain philosophical text by Umasvati or Umaswami. It is accepted by both Digambaras and Svetambaras.

## Samayasara
A famous Digambara philosophical text by Kundakunda on the nature of the soul.

## Pravachanasara
A text by Kundakunda explaining Jain doctrine.

## Panchastikayasara
A text by Kundakunda on five extended substances.

## Niyamasara
A text by Kundakunda on right conduct and spiritual discipline.

## Gommatasara
A Digambara text by Nemichandra Siddhanta Chakravarti dealing with soul and karma.

## Dravyasamgraha
A concise Jain philosophical text by Nemichandra.

## Ratnakaranda Shravakachara
A text by Samantabhadra on lay conduct.

## Mulachara
A Digambara text on monastic conduct.

## Trilokasara
A Jain cosmological text.

## Adipurana
A Jain text dealing with Rishabhanatha and early Jain legends.

## Mahapurana
A Jain universal history text associated with Jinasena and Gunabhadra.

## Harivamsha Purana
A Jain text giving Jain versions of stories related to Krishna and the Yadavas.

## Paumachariya
A Jain Ramayana by Vimalasuri, presenting Rama’s story from a Jain perspective.

## Trishashti Shalaka Purusha Charitra
A major Jain work by Hemachandra on the lives of 63 great persons.

## Parishishtaparvan
A work by Hemachandra containing historical and legendary Jain narratives.

---

# 27. IMPORTANT JAIN AUTHORS AND ACHARYAS

## Bhadrabahu
Important early Jain teacher associated with Chandragupta Maurya and Karnataka migration tradition.

## Sthulabhadra
Teacher associated with preservation of Jain scriptures.

## Kundakunda
Great Digambara philosopher and author of Samayasara, Pravachanasara, and Panchastikayasara.

## Umasvati
Author of Tattvartha Sutra, one of the most important Jain philosophical texts.

## Umaswami
Another form of the name Umasvati.

## Samantabhadra
Digambara philosopher and author associated with Ratnakaranda Shravakachara.

## Siddhasena Divakara
Jain philosopher known for works on logic and epistemology.

## Haribhadra Suri
Svetambara Jain scholar known for works on philosophy, yoga, and comparative religion.

## Hemachandra
Great Jain scholar from Gujarat, patronized by Kumarapala. He wrote grammar, history, poetry, and Jain religious texts.

## Devardhigani Kshamashramana
Scholar associated with compilation of the Svetambara canon at Vallabhi.

## Jinasena
Digambara author associated with Mahapurana and Adipurana tradition.

## Gunabhadra
Digambara author who completed parts of Mahapurana.

## Virasena
Digambara scholar associated with commentary on Shatkhandagama.

## Nemichandra Siddhanta Chakravarti
Digambara scholar and author of Gommatasara and Dravyasamgraha.

## Vimalasuri
Author of Paumachariya, the Jain Ramayana.

## Pampa
A major Kannada Jain poet, author of Adipurana and Vikramarjuna Vijaya.

## Ranna
A major Kannada Jain poet.

## Ponna
A major Kannada Jain poet.

## Janna
A Kannada Jain poet.

## Chamundaraya
Western Ganga minister who commissioned the Bahubali statue at Shravanabelagola.

## Acharya Bhikshu
Founder of the Svetambara Terapanth sect.

## Taran Svami
Founder of the Taranapanthi tradition.

---

# 28. JAIN UNIVERSAL HISTORY

## Shalaka Purusha
A great person in Jain universal history.

## Trishashti Shalaka Purusha
The 63 great persons of Jain tradition.

## Twenty-Four Tirthankaras
The 24 spiritual teachers.

## Twelve Chakravartins
Universal monarchs in Jain universal history.

## Nine Baladevas
Gentle heroic figures in Jain universal history.

## Nine Vasudevas
Warrior heroes in Jain universal history.

## Nine Prativasudevas
Anti-heroes or opponents of Vasudevas.

## Chakravartin
Universal emperor.

## Baladeva
Non-violent or less violent heroic figure in Jain universal history.

## Vasudeva
Powerful heroic figure who defeats a Prativasudeva.

## Prativasudeva
Enemy figure defeated by a Vasudeva.

## Jain Ramayana
Jain retelling of the Rama story, where characters follow Jain moral patterns.

## Jain Mahabharata
Jain retellings of Mahabharata themes with Jain ethical interpretation.

## Rama in Jainism
Rama is often treated as a Baladeva in Jain universal history.

## Lakshmana in Jainism
Lakshmana is often treated as a Vasudeva who kills Ravana.

## Ravana in Jainism
Ravana is often treated as a Prativasudeva.

## Krishna in Jainism
Krishna appears as a Vasudeva in Jain universal history.

## Neminatha and Krishna
Neminatha is traditionally associated with Krishna’s family.

---

# 29. JAIN ETHICS AND DAILY CONDUCT

## Ahimsa Paramo Dharma
Non-violence is the highest religion.

## Vegetarianism
Jains follow vegetarianism because of ahimsa.

## Vegan Tendencies
Some modern Jains avoid dairy because of concerns about harm to animals.

## Root Vegetable Avoidance
Many Jains avoid root vegetables because uprooting them kills the whole plant and may harm many tiny organisms.

## Onion and Garlic Avoidance
Many Jains avoid onion and garlic because they are root vegetables and are considered to stimulate passions.

## Filtered Water
Water is filtered to avoid harming tiny living beings.

## No Night Eating
Many Jains avoid eating after sunset to avoid harming insects and microorganisms.

## Compassion
Kindness toward all living beings.

## Forgiveness
A major Jain virtue, especially emphasized during Paryushan and Samvatsari.

## Kshamapana
Asking forgiveness.

## Micchami Dukkadam
A phrase meaning “May the harm I have done be forgiven”.

## Maitri
Friendliness toward all beings.

## Pramoda
Joy at the virtues of others.

## Karuna
Compassion for suffering beings.

## Madhyastha
Equanimity toward those who do wrong.

## Jiva Daya
Compassion for living beings.

## Panjrapole
Animal shelter traditionally supported by Jain communities.

## Aparigraha in Daily Life
Limiting possessions, consumption, and greed.

## Ethical Trade
Jain merchants historically emphasized honesty, non-violence, and trust in trade.

---

# 30. JAIN FESTIVALS AND OBSERVANCES

## Paryushan
The most important Svetambara Jain festival, focused on fasting, repentance, scripture reading, and forgiveness.

## Das Lakshana Parva
Important Digambara Jain festival emphasizing ten virtues.

## Samvatsari
Final day of Paryushan, focused on forgiveness.

## Kshamavani
Forgiveness day, especially associated with Digambara practice.

## Mahavir Jayanti
Birth anniversary of Mahavira.

## Diwali in Jainism
Commemorates Mahavira’s nirvana at Pavapuri.

## Kartik Purnima
Important for pilgrimages in some Jain traditions.

## Ayambil
A form of disciplined eating with simple food, often done for austerity.

## Oli
A period of Ayambil observance.

## Upavas
Fasting.

## Ekasana
Eating one meal in one sitting.

## Beasana
Eating two meals in a day under restrictions.

## Varsitap
A long austerity associated with alternate-day fasting.

## Pratikramana
Ritual of repentance and self-examination.

## Kalpa Sutra Recitation
Important Svetambara practice during Paryushan.

## Ratha Yatra
Procession of Jain images in some communities.

## Snatra Puja
A Jain ritual symbolically celebrating the birth bath of a Tirthankara.

## Panch Kalyanaka
Five auspicious events in a Tirthankara’s life.

---

# 31. PANCH KALYANAKA

## Garbha Kalyanaka
Auspicious conception of a Tirthankara.

## Janma Kalyanaka
Birth of a Tirthankara.

## Diksha Kalyanaka
Renunciation of a Tirthankara.

## Kevala Jnana Kalyanaka
Attainment of perfect knowledge.

## Nirvana Kalyanaka
Final liberation of a Tirthankara.

## Panch Kalyanaka Pratishtha
Temple consecration ceremony celebrating the five auspicious events.

---

# 32. JAIN ART: BASIC TERMS

## Jain Art
Art connected with Jain Tirthankaras, monks, scriptures, symbols, temples, and sacred stories.

## Tirthankara Image
A sculpture of a Jina, usually shown in meditation, either standing or seated.

## Jina Image
Image of a liberated spiritual teacher.

## Kayotsarga Image
Standing image of a Tirthankara in body-abandonment posture.

## Seated Jina
Tirthankara image in lotus posture.

## Lanchhana in Art
Symbol used to identify each Tirthankara.

## Srivatsa Mark
Auspicious mark on the chest of Jina images.

## Unclothed Image
Typical of Digambara Tirthankara images.

## Clothed Image
Often found in Svetambara tradition.

## Open Eyes
Some Svetambara images have inlaid or painted open eyes.

## Downcast Eyes
Many Jain images show meditative, detached expression.

## Jain Iconography
The system of visual signs used to identify Jain deities and Tirthankaras.

## Ayagapata
A Jain votive tablet, especially found at Mathura.

## Votive Tablet
An object offered by devotees.

## Manastambha
A tall pillar in front of Jain temples symbolizing humility before the Jina.

## Chaumukha
A four-faced Jain image or shrine showing Tirthankaras in four directions.

## Jinalaya
Jain temple.

## Derasar
A Jain temple, especially in western India.

## Basadi
Jain temple, especially in Karnataka.

## Basti
Another term for Jain temple in parts of South India.

## Mandapa
Pillared hall in a temple.

## Garbhagriha
Sanctum of a temple.

## Shikhara
Temple tower in north Indian style.

## Vimana
Temple tower or superstructure in south Indian style.

## Devakulika
Small shrine around a main Jain temple.

## Torana
Decorative gateway.

## Pradakshina Patha
Circumambulatory path around a shrine.

---

# 33. EARLY JAIN ART AND ARCHAEOLOGICAL SITES

## Mathura
A major early center of Jain art and sculpture.

## Kankali Tila
An important Jain archaeological site at Mathura with images, inscriptions, and ayagapatas.

## Lohanipur Torso
A polished stone torso from near Patna, often linked with early Jain or ascetic art.

## Udayagiri-Khandagiri Caves
Jain cave complex in Odisha associated with King Kharavela.

## Hathigumpha Inscription
Inscription of Kharavela at Udayagiri, important for Jain and early historical studies.

## Kharavela
King of Kalinga associated with Jainism and the Hathigumpha inscription.

## Ellora Jain Caves
Jain caves at Ellora, mainly belonging to the later phase of Ellora development.

## Indra Sabha
A famous Jain cave at Ellora.

## Jagannatha Sabha
A Jain cave at Ellora.

## Sittanavasal
Jain cave site in Tamil Nadu famous for paintings.

## Kalugumalai
Important Jain site in Tamil Nadu with rock-cut images.

## Badami Jain Cave
Jain cave at Badami in Karnataka.

## Aihole Jain Temple
Jain temple at Aihole, showing Jain presence in Chalukyan region.

## Deogarh Jain Temples
Important Jain temple complex in Uttar Pradesh.

## Gwalior Jain Images
Large rock-cut Jain images at Gwalior.

## Sonagiri
Important Jain pilgrimage site in Madhya Pradesh.

---

# 34. MAJOR JAIN PILGRIMAGE CENTRES

## Shravanabelagola
Major Jain pilgrimage center in Karnataka, famous for the Bahubali or Gommateshwara statue.

## Gommateshwara
Another name for Bahubali.

## Bahubali Statue
Huge monolithic statue at Shravanabelagola, commissioned by Chamundaraya.

## Chandragiri
Hill at Shravanabelagola associated with Bhadrabahu and Chandragupta Maurya tradition.

## Vindhyagiri
Hill at Shravanabelagola where the Bahubali statue stands.

## Palitana
Major Jain pilgrimage center on Shatrunjaya hill in Gujarat.

## Shatrunjaya
Sacred hill at Palitana associated with Rishabhanatha.

## Girnar
Sacred Jain site in Gujarat associated especially with Neminatha.

## Mount Abu
Jain pilgrimage site in Rajasthan, famous for Dilwara temples.

## Dilwara Temples
Famous marble Jain temples at Mount Abu, known for intricate carving.

## Ranakpur
Famous Jain temple site in Rajasthan dedicated to Adinatha.

## Sammed Shikharji
One of the most sacred Jain pilgrimage sites in Jharkhand, associated with nirvana of many Tirthankaras.

## Parasnath Hill
Hill associated with Sammed Shikharji.

## Pawapuri
Place of Mahavira’s nirvana in Bihar.

## Jal Mandir
Temple at Pavapuri located in a water tank, associated with Mahavira’s nirvana.

## Rajgir
Ancient Rajagriha, important for Jain and Buddhist traditions.

## Champapuri
Jain pilgrimage site associated with Vasupujya.

## Hastinapur
Jain pilgrimage site associated with several Tirthankaras.

## Kumbharia
Jain temple site in Gujarat.

## Taranga
Jain temple site in Gujarat.

## Osian
Jain and Hindu temple site in Rajasthan.

## Moodabidri
Important Jain center in Karnataka, known for manuscripts and basadis.

## Karkala
Jain center in Karnataka with a Bahubali statue.

## Dharmasthala
Jain-associated pilgrimage center in Karnataka with a Bahubali statue.

## Venur
Jain site in Karnataka with a Bahubali statue.

---

# 35. JAIN ARCHITECTURAL FEATURES

## Marble Architecture
Highly polished and carved marble temples, especially in western India.

## Intricate Carving
Detailed stone carving seen in Dilwara and Ranakpur temples.

## Pillared Hall
A temple hall supported by many pillars.

## Domed Ceiling
Decorated ceiling common in Jain temples.

## Lotus Ceiling
Ceiling decoration shaped like a lotus.

## Chaumukha Temple
Temple with four entrances or four-faced shrine.

## Adinatha Temple
Temple dedicated to Rishabhanatha.

## Neminatha Temple
Temple dedicated to Neminatha.

## Parshvanatha Temple
Temple dedicated to Parshvanatha.

## Mahavira Temple
Temple dedicated to Mahavira.

## Samavasarana Temple
Temple design inspired by the divine preaching assembly.

## Temple Patronage
Support given by kings, ministers, merchants, and guilds for Jain temples.

## Merchant Patronage
Jain temples were often built or supported by wealthy merchants.

## Monolithic Statue
A statue carved from a single stone, like Bahubali at Shravanabelagola.

---

# 36. JAINISM AND ROYAL PATRONAGE

## Bimbisara
King of Magadha, traditionally associated with support or interest in Jain and Buddhist teachers.

## Ajatashatru
King of Magadha, connected with the religious environment of Mahavira and Buddha.

## Chandragupta Maurya
According to Jain tradition, he became a Jain monk and migrated to Karnataka with Bhadrabahu.

## Samprati
A Mauryan ruler traditionally remembered as a great patron of Jainism.

## Kharavela
King of Kalinga and major patron associated with Jainism.

## Western Ganga Dynasty
South Indian dynasty that patronized Jainism and supported monuments like Shravanabelagola.

## Rashtrakutas
Deccan dynasty that patronized Jainism along with other religions.

## Chalukyas
Dynasty of the Deccan with Jain patronage in places like Badami and Aihole.

## Hoysalas
South Indian dynasty with important Jain connections before stronger Vaishnava and Shaiva patronage.

## Solankis
Also called Chaulukyas of Gujarat, known for patronage of Jainism.

## Kumarapala
Chaulukya ruler of Gujarat associated with Jain scholar Hemachandra and Jain patronage.

## Vastupala
Minister and Jain patron associated with temple building in Gujarat and Rajasthan.

## Tejapala
Brother of Vastupala and Jain temple patron.

## Chamundaraya
Western Ganga minister who commissioned the Bahubali statue at Shravanabelagola.

## Merchant Guilds
Trade associations that often supported Jain monks, temples, and manuscript production.

---

# 37. JAINISM IN REGIONAL HISTORY

## Jainism in Magadha
Early Jainism flourished in the Magadha-Vaishali region.

## Jainism in Bihar
Bihar contains key Jain places such as Vaishali, Rajgir, Pavapuri, and Champapuri.

## Jainism in Odisha
Associated with Kharavela and Udayagiri-Khandagiri caves.

## Jainism in Mathura
Mathura was a major early Jain art and religious center.

## Jainism in Gujarat
Gujarat became a major Jain center, especially under merchant and Solanki patronage.

## Jainism in Rajasthan
Rajasthan has major Jain temples such as Dilwara and Ranakpur.

## Jainism in Karnataka
A major Digambara center, associated with Shravanabelagola, Western Gangas, and Jain Kannada literature.

## Jainism in Tamil Nadu
Jains contributed to Tamil literature and built cave and rock-cut sites.

## Jainism in Maharashtra
Jainism had presence through trade routes, caves, and later temple traditions.

## Jainism in Madhya Pradesh
Important Jain sites include Deogarh, Sonagiri, and Gwalior images.

---

# 38. JAINISM AND LANGUAGE/LITERATURE

## Ardhamagadhi Literature
Early Jain canonical literature was composed mainly in Ardhamagadhi Prakrit.

## Prakrit Literature
Jain monks used Prakrit to reach common people.

## Sanskrit Jain Literature
Jain scholars wrote philosophical and narrative works in Sanskrit.

## Apabhramsha Jain Literature
Jains made major contributions to Apabhramsha poetry.

## Kannada Jain Literature
Jains contributed greatly to early Kannada literature.

## Tamil Jain Literature
Jain monks and scholars contributed to Tamil ethical and narrative literature.

## Jain Ramayana Tradition
Jain versions of the Ramayana reinterpret the story according to Jain ethics.

## Jain Mahabharata Tradition
Jain versions of Mahabharata themes present heroes within Jain moral frameworks.

## Grammar by Hemachandra
Hemachandra wrote an important grammar covering Sanskrit and Prakrit.

## Lexicography
Jain scholars contributed to dictionaries and word-lists.

## Narrative Literature
Jain literature contains stories teaching karma, morality, renunciation, and non-violence.

## Charita
Biography or sacred life-story.

## Purana in Jainism
Narrative religious texts about Tirthankaras and great persons, different from Hindu Puranas.

## Prabandha
Narrative prose tradition including historical and semi-historical stories.

---

# 39. JAINISM AND PHILOSOPHY: COMPARATIVE TERMS

## Jainism and Buddhism
Both are Shramana traditions, reject Vedic authority, emphasize karma and liberation, and arose in the 6th century BCE context.

## Jainism vs Buddhism on Soul
Jainism accepts an eternal soul. Buddhism rejects a permanent self through the doctrine of anatta.

## Jainism vs Buddhism on Austerity
Jainism strongly emphasizes severe austerity. Buddhism teaches the Middle Path.

## Jainism vs Buddhism on Ahimsa
Both value non-violence, but Jainism makes ahimsa more absolute and central.

## Jainism vs Vedic Religion
Jainism rejects Vedic authority and animal sacrifice, while Vedic religion centered on sacrifice and priestly ritual.

## Jainism vs Ajivikas
Both were Shramana traditions, but Ajivikas emphasized fate or determinism, while Jainism emphasized self-effort and karma.

## Jainism and Materialism
Jainism rejects purely materialist views because it accepts soul, karma, and liberation.

## Jainism and Theism
Jainism does not depend on a creator god. Liberated beings are worshipped as perfected souls, not creators.

## Non-Creator Universe
Jainism teaches that the universe is eternal and was not created by a god.

## Self-Effort
Liberation depends on one’s own discipline and purification.

---

# 40. JAINISM AND OTHER SHRAMAṆA TRADITIONS

## Ajivika
Ancient Shramana sect associated with Makkhali Gosala, emphasizing fate.

## Makkhali Gosala
Founder or major teacher of Ajivika tradition and contemporary of Mahavira and Buddha.

## Materialists
Thinkers who denied soul and afterlife; often associated with Charvaka/Lokayata.

## Charvaka
Materialist school rejecting afterlife, karma, and Vedic authority.

## Lokayata
Another name for materialist thought.

## Parivrajaka
Wandering ascetic or religious seeker.

## Tapasvin
Ascetic practicing austerity.

## Yati
Ascetic or renunciant.

## Shramana-Brahmana Debate
Intellectual conflict between renunciant traditions and Vedic ritual traditions.

---

# 41. JAIN SYMBOLS

## Swastika
A Jain symbol representing the four states of existence: heavenly beings, humans, animals/plants, and hellish beings.

## Three Dots
Represent the Three Jewels: right faith, right knowledge, and right conduct.

## Crescent and Dot
Symbol of Siddhashila and liberated souls.

## Ahimsa Hand
Modern Jain symbol showing a hand with a wheel, representing non-violence.

## Dharma Chakra in Jainism
Wheel symbol representing dharma and spiritual progress.

## Om in Jainism
A sacred sound representing the five supreme beings.

## Jain Emblem
Modern symbol combining hand, wheel, swastika, three dots, crescent, and the outline of the universe.

## Parasparopagraho Jivanam
Jain aphorism meaning “souls render service to one another” or “living beings support one another”.

## Kalasha
Auspicious pot, used in rituals and temple symbolism.

## Mirror
Sometimes used symbolically for self-reflection.

## Lotus
Symbol of purity and detachment.

---

# 42. JAIN RITUAL TERMS

## Puja
Worship or reverence.

## Abhisheka
Ritual bathing of a Tirthankara image.

## Jina Puja
Worship of the Jina image.

## Ashta Prakari Puja
Eightfold Jain worship using substances such as water, sandalwood, flowers, incense, lamp, rice, sweets, and fruit.

## Jal Puja
Offering of water.

## Chandan Puja
Offering of sandal paste.

## Pushpa Puja
Offering of flowers.

## Dhupa Puja
Offering of incense.

## Dipa Puja
Offering of lamp.

## Akshata Puja
Offering of rice grains.

## Naivedya Puja
Offering of food.

## Phala Puja
Offering of fruit.

## Pratishtha
Consecration of an image or temple.

## Arati
Lamp ritual.

## Mangal Divo
Auspicious lamp ritual.

## Stavana
Hymn of praise.

## Sutra Recitation
Reading or chanting Jain scriptures.

## Namokar Mantra
The most important Jain mantra, saluting the five supreme beings.

## Navkar Mantra
Another name for Namokar Mantra.

## Logassa Sutra
A Jain prayer praising Tirthankaras.

## Bhaktamara Stotra
Famous Jain devotional hymn.

## Uvasaggaharam Stotra
A hymn associated with Parshvanatha.

---

# 43. NAMOKAR MANTRA TERMS

## Namo Arihantanam
Salutation to the Arihants.

## Namo Siddhanam
Salutation to the Siddhas.

## Namo Ayariyanam
Salutation to the Acharyas.

## Namo Uvajjhayanam
Salutation to the Upadhyayas.

## Namo Loe Savva Sahunam
Salutation to all monks and saints in the world.

## Panch Parameshthi in Mantra
The Namokar Mantra worships qualities of perfected and advanced beings, not a creator god.

---

# 44. JAIN TEMPLE PRACTICES

## Darshan
Reverential viewing of the Jina image.

## Pradakshina
Circumambulation around the shrine.

## Vandana
Respectful salutation.

## Chaitya Vandana
Worship or reverence of a Jain temple or shrine.

## Dev Darshan
Viewing and revering the deity image.

## Guru Vandana
Respect to monks, nuns, and teachers.

## Samavasarana Visualization
Meditative or artistic representation of the Tirthankara’s preaching assembly.

## Temple Donation
Offering money, food, lamps, manuscripts, or materials to temples and monks.

## Manuscript Donation
Donation of copied scriptures, an important medieval Jain practice.

---

# 45. IMPORTANT JAIN INSCRIPTIONS AND HISTORICAL RECORDS

## Hathigumpha Inscription
Inscription of Kharavela at Udayagiri in Odisha, important for early Jain history.

## Mathura Jain Inscriptions
Inscriptions from Mathura showing early Jain worship, donors, monks, nuns, and images.

## Shravanabelagola Inscriptions
Inscriptions documenting Jain monks, donors, dynasties, and Sallekhana practices.

## Gwalior Jain Inscriptions
Inscriptions associated with large Jain images and patronage.

## Mount Abu Inscriptions
Records connected with Jain temple patronage.

## Donative Inscription
An inscription recording a gift to a temple, image, monk, or religious community.

## Prashasti
Eulogistic inscription praising a ruler, patron, or teacher.

---

# 46. JAINISM AND ECONOMY

## Merchant Religion
Jainism is often associated with merchant communities because of its stress on honesty, non-violence, and disciplined living.

## Trade Ethics
Truthfulness, non-stealing, trust, and restraint in commercial life.

## Urban Support
Jainism grew strongly in towns and trade centers.

## Guild Patronage
Guilds and merchant groups supported Jain monks, temples, and manuscripts.

## Banking Communities
Some Jain communities became prominent in banking and finance.

## Donation Economy
Religious merit was gained through temple building, feeding monks, manuscript copying, and charity.

## Non-Agricultural Preference
Some Jains preferred trade because agriculture can involve harm to plants, insects, and soil organisms.

## Animal Protection
Jain communities supported shelters and protection of animals.

---

# 47. JAINISM AND SOCIETY

## Caste and Jainism
Jainism rejected Vedic ritual hierarchy in principle but Jain communities later developed caste-like social groups.

## Varna and Jainism
Jainism did not base liberation on varna.

## Women in Jainism
Women played important roles as nuns, lay followers, donors, and teachers, though sects differ on liberation for women.

## Jain Nuns
Female renunciants; historically very numerous in Jain communities.

## Lay Community
Householders who support monks and follow limited vows.

## Ascetic Ideal
The highest Jain ideal is renunciation and liberation, not worldly power.

## Non-Possession
A social and spiritual value limiting greed and accumulation.

## Charity
Important duty of lay Jains.

## Education
Jain communities historically supported learning, manuscripts, and libraries.

## Jain Libraries
Repositories of manuscripts, especially in Gujarat, Rajasthan, and Karnataka.

## Bhandara
Jain manuscript library.

---

# 48. JAINISM AND SCIENCE/KNOWLEDGE TRADITIONS

## Jain Mathematics
Jain scholars contributed to ideas of large numbers, infinity, permutations, and cosmological measurement.

## Large Numbers
Jain texts use extremely large numerical categories.

## Infinity
Jain thought distinguishes different kinds of infinity.

## Cosmological Measurement
Jain texts describe vast cosmic distances and time cycles.

## Logic
Jain philosophers developed sophisticated logic through Anekantavada, Syadvada, and Nayavada.

## Grammar
Jain scholars like Hemachandra contributed to grammar.

## Lexicography
Jain scholars compiled dictionaries and word lists.

## Astronomy and Cosmology
Jain texts developed detailed cosmological models.

## Medicine and Ethics
Jain emphasis on non-violence influenced attitudes toward health, animals, and diet.

---

# 49. COMMONLY CONFUSED TERMS

## Jina vs Jaina
Jina is the spiritual conqueror. Jaina is a follower of the Jina.

## Arihant vs Siddha
Arihant has perfect knowledge but still has a body. Siddha is fully liberated without a body.

## Tirthankara vs Siddha
A Tirthankara teaches the path and later becomes a Siddha after liberation.

## Sadhu vs Shravaka
Sadhu is a monk. Shravaka is a layman.

## Sadhvi vs Shravika
Sadhvi is a nun. Shravika is a laywoman.

## Mahavrata vs Anuvrata
Mahavrata is a strict great vow for monks and nuns. Anuvrata is a limited vow for laypersons.

## Digambara vs Svetambara
Digambaras are sky-clad and reject the preserved Svetambara canon. Svetambaras wear white and preserve Agamas.

## Kevala Jnana vs Moksha
Kevala Jnana is perfect knowledge while living. Moksha is final liberation after all karma is destroyed.

## Ahimsa vs Aparigraha
Ahimsa means non-violence. Aparigraha means non-possession.

## Anekantavada vs Syadvada
Anekantavada says reality is many-sided. Syadvada explains how to speak conditionally about that reality.

## Dharma in Jain Metaphysics vs Moral Dharma
Dharma Dravya means medium of motion. Moral dharma means right conduct.

## Adharma in Jain Metaphysics vs Sin
Adharma Dravya means medium of rest. Sin is papa.

## Sallekhana vs Suicide
Sallekhana is a regulated spiritual fast undertaken with detachment under strict conditions. It is not meant as impulsive self-harm.

## Agama vs Veda
Agamas are Jain scriptures. Vedas are Brahmanical sacred texts.

## Jain Purana vs Hindu Purana
Jain Puranas present Jain universal history and ethics, different from Hindu Puranic theology.

---

# 50. JAINISM VS BUDDHISM: UPSC COMPARISON

## Founder
Jainism recognizes 24 Tirthankaras, with Mahavira as the 24th. Buddhism was founded by Gautama Buddha.

## Soul
Jainism accepts an eternal soul. Buddhism denies a permanent soul.

## Karma
Jainism sees karma as subtle matter. Buddhism sees karma mainly as intentional action.

## Liberation
Jainism calls liberation Moksha or Nirvana. Buddhism calls it Nirvana.

## Austerity
Jainism supports severe austerity. Buddhism follows the Middle Path.

## Non-Violence
Jainism gives absolute importance to ahimsa. Buddhism also values ahimsa but is less extreme in practice.

## Scriptures
Jain scriptures are Agamas. Buddhist scriptures are Tripitakas.

## Monastic Clothing
Digambara Jain monks may be nude; Buddhist monks wear robes.

## Metaphysics
Jainism has detailed doctrines of jiva, ajiva, karma matter, and cosmology. Buddhism emphasizes impermanence, no-self, and dependent origination.

## Epistemology
Jainism is famous for Anekantavada and Syadvada.

---

# 51. JAINISM VS BRAHMANISM: UPSC COMPARISON

## Vedic Authority
Jainism rejects Vedic authority. Brahmanism accepts it.

## Sacrifice
Jainism rejects animal sacrifice. Vedic Brahmanism historically included sacrificial rituals.

## Priesthood
Jainism emphasizes monks and personal discipline. Brahmanism emphasizes Brahmanical ritual specialists.

## Social Equality in Liberation
Jainism does not make liberation dependent on birth-based varna.

## Creator God
Jainism does not accept a creator god. Brahmanical traditions vary but often include creator or supreme deity ideas.

## Ahimsa
Jainism makes ahimsa the highest principle.

## Renunciation
Jainism gives high importance to renunciation and ascetic life.

---

# 52. HIGH-YIELD JAIN PLACES FOR UPSC

## Kundagrama
Birthplace of Mahavira.

## Vaishali
Region associated with Mahavira’s clan and early Jainism.

## Rajagriha
Important city of Magadha linked with Mahavira’s preaching.

## Pavapuri
Place of Mahavira’s nirvana.

## Champa
Ancient city associated with Jain tradition.

## Pataliputra
Associated with the first Jain council tradition.

## Vallabhi
Associated with compilation of Svetambara scriptures.

## Mathura
Early Jain art and inscription center.

## Kankali Tila
Important Jain site at Mathura.

## Udayagiri-Khandagiri
Jain caves in Odisha associated with Kharavela.

## Shravanabelagola
Major Digambara center with Bahubali statue.

## Mount Abu
Famous for Dilwara Jain temples.

## Palitana
Major Jain pilgrimage site in Gujarat.

## Girnar
Sacred hill associated with Neminatha.

## Sammed Shikharji
Sacred site associated with nirvana of many Tirthankaras.

## Ranakpur
Famous Jain temple in Rajasthan.

## Ellora
Has important Jain caves.

## Sittanavasal
Jain cave painting site in Tamil Nadu.

---

# 53. HIGH-YIELD JAIN PERSONALITIES FOR UPSC

## Rishabhanatha
First Tirthankara.

## Neminatha
Twenty-second Tirthankara, associated with Krishna tradition.

## Parshvanatha
Twenty-third Tirthankara; taught four vows.

## Mahavira
Twenty-fourth Tirthankara; organized Jainism and taught five vows.

## Indrabhuti Gautama
Chief disciple of Mahavira.

## Bhadrabahu
Jain teacher associated with Chandragupta Maurya and southern migration.

## Sthulabhadra
Teacher associated with early scripture preservation.

## Chandragupta Maurya
Traditionally associated with Jainism in later life.

## Kharavela
Jain-associated ruler of Kalinga.

## Kundakunda
Great Digambara philosopher.

## Umasvati
Author of Tattvartha Sutra.

## Haribhadra Suri
Important Svetambara scholar.

## Hemachandra
Great Jain scholar of Gujarat.

## Kumarapala
Gujarat ruler associated with Jain patronage.

## Chamundaraya
Patron of Bahubali statue.

## Vimalasuri
Author of Paumachariya.

## Jinasena
Digambara author of Jain Puranic literature.

## Gunabhadra
Digambara author associated with Mahapurana.

## Nemichandra
Author of Gommatasara and Dravyasamgraha.

---

# 54. HIGH-YIELD JAIN TEXTS FOR UPSC

## Agamas
Canonical scriptures of Svetambara Jainism.

## Acharanga Sutra
Important text on monastic conduct and Mahavira’s life.

## Sutrakritanga
Text criticizing rival doctrines and explaining Jain views.

## Bhagavati Sutra
Major Jain canonical text with doctrinal material.

## Kalpa Sutra
Text on lives of Tirthankaras, especially recited during Paryushan.

## Tattvartha Sutra
Important philosophical text accepted by both major sects.

## Samayasara
Kundakunda’s text on the soul.

## Shatkhandagama
Major Digambara scripture on karma.

## Kasayapahuda
Digambara text on passions.

## Paumachariya
Jain Ramayana by Vimalasuri.

## Adipurana
Jain text on Rishabhanatha.

## Mahapurana
Jain universal history text.

## Trishashti Shalaka Purusha Charitra
Hemachandra’s work on 63 great persons.

---

# 55. HIGH-YIELD DOCTRINE CLUSTER

## Three Jewels
Right faith, right knowledge, right conduct.

## Five Great Vows
Ahimsa, Satya, Asteya, Brahmacharya, Aparigraha.

## Seven Tattvas
Jiva, Ajiva, Ashrava, Bandha, Samvara, Nirjara, Moksha.

## Nine Tattvas
Seven tattvas plus Punya and Papa.

## Six Dravyas
Jiva, Pudgala, Dharma, Adharma, Akasha, Kala.

## Five Astikayas
Jiva, Pudgala, Dharma, Adharma, Akasha.

## Five Types of Knowledge
Mati, Shruta, Avadhi, Manahparyaya, Kevala.

## Four Kashayas
Anger, pride, deceit, greed.

## Four States of Existence
Heavenly beings, humans, animals/plants, and hellish beings.

## Fourfold Sangha
Monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen.

---

# 56. CHRONOLOGICAL SNAPSHOT

## Stage 1: Early Tirthankara Tradition
Jainism traces its origin through 24 Tirthankaras, beginning with Rishabhanatha.

## Stage 2: Parshvanatha Phase
Parshvanatha, the 23rd Tirthankara, taught four vows: ahimsa, satya, asteya, and aparigraha.

## Stage 3: Mahavira Phase
Mahavira, the 24th Tirthankara, added brahmacharya as a separate fifth vow and organized the Jain Sangha.

## Stage 4: Early Sangha Phase
Mahavira’s disciples, especially Indrabhuti Gautama and Sudharma, continued the Jain tradition.

## Stage 5: Famine and Migration Tradition
Bhadrabahu and Chandragupta Maurya are traditionally associated with migration to Karnataka, while Sthulabhadra stayed in Magadha.

## Stage 6: Sectarian Formation
The Digambara and Svetambara traditions developed differences over clothing, scriptures, women’s liberation, and monastic practice.

## Stage 7: Canon Formation
Svetambara scriptures were preserved as Agamas, while Digambaras held that original scriptures were lost and developed their own textual tradition.

## Stage 8: Jain Expansion
Jainism spread to Mathura, Odisha, Gujarat, Rajasthan, Karnataka, Tamil Nadu, and Maharashtra through monks, merchants, and royal patrons.

## Stage 9: Jain Art and Temple Phase
Major Jain art and architecture developed at Mathura, Udayagiri-Khandagiri, Shravanabelagola, Mount Abu, Palitana, Girnar, Ranakpur, Ellora, and Sittanavasal.

## Stage 10: Medieval Scholastic Phase
Jain scholars such as Kundakunda, Umasvati, Haribhadra, Hemachandra, Jinasena, and Nemichandra developed philosophy, logic, grammar, literature, and cosmology.

---

# 57. FINAL REVISION CLUSTER FOR UPSC PRELIMS

## Must Remember Identity
Jainism is a Shramana, Nastika, non-Vedic tradition.

## Must Remember Founder Question
Mahavira was not the first Tirthankara; he was the 24th. Rishabhanatha was the first.

## Must Remember Before Mahavira
Parshvanatha was the 23rd Tirthankara and taught four vows.

## Must Remember Mahavira’s Addition
Mahavira added Brahmacharya as the fifth vow.

## Must Remember Core Doctrine
Triratna: right faith, right knowledge, right conduct.

## Must Remember Vows
Ahimsa, Satya, Asteya, Brahmacharya, Aparigraha.

## Must Remember Highest Principle
Ahimsa.

## Must Remember Philosophy
Anekantavada, Syadvada, Nayavada.

## Must Remember Metaphysics
Jiva, Ajiva, karma as matter, bondage, stoppage, shedding, liberation.

## Must Remember Sects
Digambara and Svetambara.

## Must Remember Sect Difference
Digambaras are sky-clad and believe original scriptures were lost. Svetambaras wear white and preserve Agamas.

## Must Remember Councils
Pataliputra and Vallabhi are important in Jain council tradition.

## Must Remember Scriptures
Agamas, Acharanga Sutra, Bhagavati Sutra, Kalpa Sutra, Tattvartha Sutra.

## Must Remember Authors
Bhadrabahu, Sthulabhadra, Kundakunda, Umasvati, Haribhadra, Hemachandra.

## Must Remember Places
Kundagrama, Vaishali, Rajagriha, Pavapuri, Mathura, Udayagiri-Khandagiri, Shravanabelagola, Mount Abu, Palitana, Girnar, Sammed Shikharji.

## Must Remember Patrons
Chandragupta Maurya by tradition, Kharavela, Western Gangas, Rashtrakutas, Chalukyas, Solankis, Kumarapala, Chamundaraya.

## Must Remember Art
Tirthankara images, Kayotsarga, Padmasana, Lanchhana, Srivatsa, Ayagapata, Manastambha, Bahubali statue, Dilwara temples, Ranakpur temple.

## Must Remember Comparison with Buddhism
Jainism accepts eternal soul and severe austerity. Buddhism rejects permanent soul and follows the Middle Path.

## Must Remember One-Line Essence
Jainism is an ancient Shramana religion of India that teaches liberation of the soul through right faith, right knowledge, right conduct, strict non-violence, austerity, and freedom from karmic bondage.


-----


# BUDDHISM GLOSSARY FOR UPSC PRELIMS
## Chronological Coverage: Pre-Buddhist Background → Life of Buddha → Early Sangha → Buddhist Doctrines → Councils → Schools → Literature → Art and Architecture → Spread and Legacy

> Note:
> Buddhism is one of the ancient Shramana traditions of India.
> It arose in the 6th century BCE context of urbanization, new kingdoms, questioning of Vedic ritualism, and the rise of renunciant movements.
> For UPSC Prelims, focus especially on: Buddha’s life events, Four Noble Truths, Eightfold Path, Sangha, Tripitaka, Buddhist councils, Hinayana/Theravada, Mahayana, Vajrayana, stupas, chaityas, viharas, Buddhist art, Ashoka, and major Buddhist sites.

---

# 1. BASIC TERMS OF BUDDHISM

## Buddhism
A religion and philosophical tradition founded by Gautama Buddha. It teaches the path to end suffering through ethical conduct, meditation, wisdom, and liberation.

## Buddha
“The Enlightened One” or “Awakened One”. It refers mainly to Gautama Buddha, who realized the truth and taught the path to liberation.

## Gautama Buddha
The historical founder of Buddhism. He was born as Siddhartha Gautama in the Shakya clan.

## Siddhartha
The birth name of Gautama Buddha. It means “one whose aim is accomplished”.

## Shakyamuni
“Sage of the Shakyas”. A title of Gautama Buddha.

## Tathagata
A title used by Buddha for himself, meaning “one who has thus gone” or “one who has thus come”.

## Sugata
“Well-gone one”. A title of Buddha.

## Bhagavan
Blessed one or revered one. A title used for Buddha.

## Dhamma
The teaching of Buddha in Pali. It also means truth, law, doctrine, or reality.

## Dharma
Sanskrit form of Dhamma.

## Sangha
The monastic community of Buddhist monks and nuns. In a wider sense, it includes all followers of Buddha.

## Bhikkhu
A Buddhist monk.

## Bhikshu
Sanskrit form of Bhikkhu.

## Bhikkhuni
A Buddhist nun.

## Bhikshuni
Sanskrit form of Bhikkhuni.

## Upasaka
A male lay follower of Buddhism.

## Upasika
A female lay follower of Buddhism.

## Shramana
A renunciant or wandering ascetic. Buddhism belongs to the Shramana tradition.

## Nastika
A tradition that does not accept the authority of the Vedas. Buddhism is Nastika in Brahmanical classification.

## Heterodox Tradition
A non-Vedic religious-philosophical tradition, such as Buddhism and Jainism.

## Middle Path
The path taught by Buddha that avoids both extreme luxury and extreme self-mortification.

## Nirvana
The extinction of craving, ignorance, and suffering. It is liberation from samsara.

## Nibbana
Pali form of Nirvana.

## Samsara
The cycle of birth, death, and rebirth.

## Karma
Intentional action that produces moral consequences.

## Kamma
Pali form of Karma.

## Rebirth
The continuation of existence after death according to karma, without a permanent soul.

## Anatta
The doctrine of no permanent self or soul.

## Anatman
Sanskrit form of Anatta.

## Dukkha
Suffering, dissatisfaction, or unsatisfactoriness of worldly existence.

## Trishna
Craving or desire, considered the cause of suffering.

## Tanha
Pali form of Trishna.

## Bodhi
