Awakening or enlightenment.

## Bodhisattva
A being who seeks enlightenment. In Mahayana, one who delays final Nirvana to help all beings.

## Bodhisatta
Pali form of Bodhisattva.

## Arhat
A perfected disciple who has destroyed desires and attained liberation.

## Arahant
Pali form of Arhat.

## Pratyekabuddha
A person who attains enlightenment independently but does not teach a full path to others.

## Samyaksambuddha
A perfectly enlightened Buddha who discovers and teaches the path.

---

# 2. HISTORICAL BACKGROUND OF BUDDHISM

## Sixth Century BCE
The period in which Buddhism and Jainism became prominent in north India.

## Second Urbanization
The rise of towns and cities in the Ganga valley around the 6th century BCE. It created new social and economic conditions for Buddhism.

## Mahajanapadas
The sixteen major states of north India during Buddha’s time.

## Magadha
A powerful Mahajanapada that became an important center for Buddhism.

## Kosala
A major kingdom associated with many events in Buddha’s life.

## Vajji
A republican confederacy associated with Vaishali.

## Malla
A republican state associated with Buddha’s Mahaparinirvana at Kushinagar.

## Shakya
The clan to which Buddha belonged.

## Kapilavastu
The Shakya capital associated with Buddha’s early life.

## Lumbini
Birthplace of Buddha, located in present-day Nepal.

## Urban Merchant Class
A rising group in the 6th century BCE that supported Buddhism through donations and monasteries.

## Setthi
A wealthy merchant or banker, often a supporter of Buddhist institutions.

## Gahapati
A wealthy householder or landholder in early Buddhist texts.

## Shreni
Guild or association of merchants or artisans.

## Vedic Ritualism
The ritual-centered religious system that many Shramana traditions questioned.

## Animal Sacrifice
A practice criticized by Buddhism because of its ethical emphasis on non-violence and compassion.

## Renunciation Movement
A broad movement of ascetics who left household life to seek liberation.

## Parivrajaka
A wandering seeker or ascetic.

## Tapasvin
Ascetic practicing austerities.

## Brahmana-Shramana Debate
Debate between Vedic ritual specialists and renunciant traditions such as Buddhism and Jainism.

---

# 3. LIFE OF BUDDHA: BIRTH AND EARLY LIFE

## Lumbini
The birthplace of Buddha. It is one of the four major sacred Buddhist sites.

## Kapilavastu
The city associated with Buddha’s childhood and youth.

## Shakya Clan
The republican clan into which Buddha was born.

## Kshatriya Background
Buddha was born into a Kshatriya family.

## Suddhodana
Father of Buddha and chief of the Shakyas.

## Mahamaya
Mother of Buddha. She is also called Maya Devi.

## Maya Devi
Another name for Buddha’s mother.

## Mahaprajapati Gotami
Buddha’s foster mother and maternal aunt. She later became the first Buddhist nun.

## Yashodhara
Wife of Siddhartha Gautama.

## Rahula
Son of Buddha. He later joined the Sangha.

## Asita
A sage who, according to tradition, predicted Buddha’s greatness.

## Birth Legend
Traditional accounts describe auspicious signs at Buddha’s birth.

## Seven Steps Legend
A traditional story that the newborn Buddha took seven steps, symbolizing his future greatness.

## Prince Siddhartha
Buddha before renunciation, living as a prince in the Shakya clan.

## Four Sights
The old man, sick man, dead body, and ascetic seen by Siddhartha, leading to renunciation.

## Old Man
One of the four sights, showing the reality of ageing.

## Sick Man
One of the four sights, showing the reality of disease.

## Corpse
One of the four sights, showing the reality of death.

## Ascetic
One of the four sights, showing the possibility of spiritual liberation.

---

# 4. LIFE OF BUDDHA: RENUNCIATION AND ENLIGHTENMENT

## Mahabhinishkramana
The Great Departure. Siddhartha left palace life to seek truth.

## Great Renunciation
Another term for Mahabhinishkramana.

## Kanthaka
The horse associated with Siddhartha’s renunciation.

## Channa
The charioteer associated with Siddhartha’s departure.

## Alara Kalama
One of Siddhartha’s early teachers in meditation.

## Uddaka Ramaputta
Another early teacher of Siddhartha.

## Uruvela
Place where Siddhartha practiced severe austerities before enlightenment.

## Severe Austerities
Extreme self-mortification practiced by Siddhartha before he rejected it.

## Five Ascetics
The group that practiced austerities with Siddhartha and later became his first disciples.

## Sujata
A woman who offered milk-rice to Siddhartha before his enlightenment.

## Milk-Rice Offering
Food offered by Sujata, symbolizing Siddhartha’s rejection of extreme fasting.

## Bodh Gaya
The place where Buddha attained enlightenment.

## Bodhi Tree
The tree under which Buddha attained enlightenment.

## Vajrasana
The “diamond throne” or seat of enlightenment at Bodh Gaya.

## Mara
The tempter who tried to distract Buddha before enlightenment.

## Mara Vijaya
Buddha’s victory over Mara.

## Bhumisparsha Mudra
The earth-touching gesture, symbolizing Buddha calling the earth to witness his enlightenment.

## Enlightenment
The awakening of Buddha to the truth of suffering, its cause, its end, and the path.

## Sambodhi
Complete enlightenment.

## Buddha at 35
According to tradition, Siddhartha attained enlightenment at the age of 35.

---

# 5. LIFE OF BUDDHA: FIRST SERMON AND TEACHING CAREER

## Sarnath
The place where Buddha gave his first sermon after enlightenment.

## Isipatana
Ancient name of Sarnath.

## Mrigadava
Deer Park at Sarnath, where Buddha preached the first sermon.

## Dhammacakkappavattana
“Turning of the Wheel of Dhamma”. It refers to Buddha’s first sermon.

## Dharma Chakra Pravartana
Sanskrit form of Dhammacakkappavattana.

## First Sermon
The sermon at Sarnath explaining the Four Noble Truths and Middle Path.

## Five First Disciples
The five ascetics who became Buddha’s first disciples.

## Kondanna
The first of the five ascetics to understand Buddha’s teaching.

## Vappa
One of the first five disciples.

## Bhaddiya
One of the first five disciples.

## Mahanama
One of the first five disciples.

## Assaji
One of the first five disciples.

## First Sangha
The early Buddhist community formed after the first sermon.

## Buddha’s Teaching Career
Buddha taught for about 45 years after enlightenment.

## Rajagriha
Capital of Magadha and an important place in Buddha’s life.

## Shravasti
A major city of Kosala where Buddha spent many rainy seasons.

## Jetavana
A monastery at Shravasti donated by Anathapindika.

## Anathapindika
A wealthy merchant and major lay supporter of Buddha.

## Veluvana
Bamboo Grove monastery at Rajagriha, donated by Bimbisara.

## Bimbisara
King of Magadha and an important patron of Buddha.

## Ajatashatru
King of Magadha who interacted with Buddha and later supported the first Buddhist council.

## Prasenajit
King of Kosala and contemporary of Buddha.

## Kosala King
Prasenajit, an important royal figure in early Buddhist tradition.

## Vaishali
Important city associated with Buddha’s visits and the foundation of the Bhikkhuni Sangha.

## Nalanda
A place visited by Buddha and later a great Buddhist university.

## Kaushambi
An important city visited by Buddha.

## Champa
An ancient city associated with early Buddhism.

## Mathura
A city later important for Buddhist art and monastic activity.

---

# 6. LIFE OF BUDDHA: FINAL JOURNEY AND MAHAPARINIRVANA

## Mahaparinirvana
The final passing away of Buddha, after which he was not reborn.

## Parinirvana
Final Nirvana after death.

## Kushinagar
The place where Buddha attained Mahaparinirvana.

## Kusinara
Pali form of Kushinagar.

## Malla Republic
The republican state in whose territory Buddha attained Mahaparinirvana.

## Cunda
A lay follower who offered Buddha his last meal according to tradition.

## Last Meal
The meal offered by Cunda before Buddha’s final passing.

## Sala Trees
Trees between which Buddha is said to have passed into Mahaparinirvana.

## Reclining Buddha
Artistic representation of Buddha at Mahaparinirvana.

## Buddha at 80
According to tradition, Buddha attained Mahaparinirvana at the age of 80.

## Relics of Buddha
Physical remains of Buddha distributed after his cremation.

## Stupa over Relics
Relic mounds built over Buddha’s remains.

## Eight Relic Stupas
Stupas built by different groups over divided relics of Buddha.

## Drona Brahmana
The Brahmana who is said to have divided Buddha’s relics among claimants.

---

# 7. FOUR GREAT BUDDHIST SITES

## Lumbini
Birthplace of Buddha.

## Bodh Gaya
Place of enlightenment.

## Sarnath
Place of first sermon.

## Kushinagar
Place of Mahaparinirvana.

## Four Sacred Places
The four most important places associated with Buddha’s life.

## Buddhist Pilgrimage
Travel to sacred places connected with Buddha, relics, monasteries, and major teachers.

---

# 8. OTHER IMPORTANT BUDDHIST PLACES

## Rajagriha
Place of early Buddhist activity and first council.

## Vulture Peak
A hill near Rajagriha where Buddha delivered important teachings.

## Griddhakuta
Sanskrit name for Vulture Peak.

## Shravasti
Place where Buddha spent many rainy seasons.

## Jetavana Monastery
Monastery at Shravasti donated by Anathapindika.

## Vaishali
Important city linked with Buddha, the Bhikkhuni Sangha, and the second council.

## Sankassa
Place associated with Buddha’s descent from heaven according to tradition.

## Kaushambi
Important Buddhist center.

## Kapilavastu
City of Buddha’s early life.

## Nalanda
Later major Buddhist university in Bihar.

## Sanchi
Major stupa site in Madhya Pradesh.

## Bharhut
Early Buddhist stupa site in Madhya Pradesh.

## Amaravati
Important Buddhist stupa and art center in Andhra region.

## Nagarjunakonda
Important Buddhist site in Andhra Pradesh.

## Ajanta
Buddhist cave site in Maharashtra famous for paintings and sculptures.

## Ellora Buddhist Caves
Buddhist caves at Ellora in Maharashtra.

## Karle
Buddhist cave site in Maharashtra famous for chaitya hall.

## Bhaja
Early Buddhist cave site in Maharashtra.

## Bedsa
Buddhist cave site in Maharashtra.

## Kanheri
Buddhist cave complex near Mumbai.

## Nasik Caves
Buddhist cave site with inscriptions.

## Junnar Caves
Large Buddhist cave complex in Maharashtra.

## Udayagiri Buddhist Site
Buddhist site in Odisha, part of the Ratnagiri-Udayagiri-Lalitgiri Buddhist complex.

## Ratnagiri
Major Buddhist site in Odisha, especially linked with later Buddhism.

## Lalitgiri
Important Buddhist site in Odisha with relic evidence.

## Vikramashila
Major Buddhist university founded under the Palas.

## Odantapuri
Important Buddhist monastic university in Bihar.

## Somapura Mahavihara
Major Buddhist monastery in present-day Bangladesh.

## Taxila
Ancient learning center in Gandhara region, associated with Buddhism and wider intellectual traditions.

---

# 9. CORE BUDDHIST DOCTRINES

## Four Noble Truths
The central teaching of Buddha: suffering exists, suffering has a cause, suffering can end, and there is a path to end suffering.

## Arya Satya
Noble Truth.

## Dukkha
Suffering or unsatisfactoriness.

## Samudaya
Origin or cause of suffering.

## Nirodha
Cessation or ending of suffering.

## Magga
The path leading to the end of suffering.

## Dukkha Arya Satya
The noble truth of suffering.

## Samudaya Arya Satya
The noble truth of the origin of suffering.

## Nirodha Arya Satya
The noble truth of the cessation of suffering.

## Magga Arya Satya
The noble truth of the path.

## Noble Eightfold Path
The path to end suffering, consisting of right view, intention, speech, action, livelihood, effort, mindfulness, and concentration.

## Ashtangika Marga
Sanskrit term for the Eightfold Path.

## Right View
Correct understanding of reality, especially Four Noble Truths.

## Right Intention
Thoughts of renunciation, goodwill, and non-harm.

## Right Speech
Avoiding lies, harsh speech, slander, and useless talk.

## Right Action
Ethical bodily conduct, including avoiding killing, stealing, and sexual misconduct.

## Right Livelihood
Earning a living without harming others.

## Right Effort
Effort to remove bad mental states and develop good ones.

## Right Mindfulness
Awareness of body, feelings, mind, and mental objects.

## Right Concentration
Meditative concentration leading to deep mental discipline.

## Middle Path
Avoidance of extreme sensual pleasure and extreme austerity.

## Threefold Training
The Buddhist path divided into morality, concentration, and wisdom.

## Shila
Morality or ethical conduct.

## Samadhi
Concentration or meditative absorption.

## Prajna
Wisdom or insight.

## Sila
Pali form of Shila.

## Panna
Pali form of Prajna.

---

# 10. THREE MARKS OF EXISTENCE

## Three Marks of Existence
The three basic characteristics of all conditioned existence: impermanence, suffering, and no-self.

## Anicca
Impermanence. Everything conditioned changes.

## Anitya
Sanskrit form of Anicca.

## Dukkha
Unsatisfactoriness or suffering.

## Anatta
No permanent self.

## Anatman
Sanskrit form of Anatta.

## Conditioned Existence
Everything that arises due to causes and conditions.

## Impermanence
The fact that all things arise, change, and pass away.

## No-Soul Doctrine
The Buddhist teaching that there is no eternal, unchanging soul.

## Five Aggregates
The five components that make up a person: form, feeling, perception, mental formations, and consciousness.

## Panch Skandha
Sanskrit term for five aggregates.

## Rupa
Form or material body.

## Vedana
Feeling or sensation.

## Samjna
Perception or recognition.

## Sankhara
Mental formations or volitional activities.

## Vijnana
Consciousness.

## Upadana
Clinging or attachment.

## Personality as Process
Buddhist idea that a person is a changing combination of aggregates, not a fixed soul.

---

# 11. DEPENDENT ORIGINATION

## Pratityasamutpada
Dependent origination. It means things arise due to causes and conditions.

## Paticca Samuppada
Pali form of Pratityasamutpada.

## Dependent Origination
The doctrine that nothing exists independently; everything arises in dependence on causes.

## Twelve Nidanas
Twelve links explaining the chain of suffering and rebirth.

## Nidana
Cause or link.

## Avidya
Ignorance.

## Avijja
Pali form of Avidya.

## Samskara
Volitional formations.

## Sankhara
Pali form of Samskara.

## Vijnana
Consciousness.

## Nama-Rupa
Name and form, meaning mind-body organism.

## Shadayatana
Six sense bases.

## Phassa
Contact between sense organ, object, and consciousness.

## Sparsha
Sanskrit form of contact.

## Vedana
Feeling.

## Trishna
Craving.

## Tanha
Pali form of craving.

## Upadana
Clinging.

## Bhava
Becoming or existence.

## Jati
Birth.

## Jara-Marana
Old age and death.

## Chain of Suffering
The process by which ignorance leads to rebirth and suffering.

## Breaking the Chain
Ending ignorance and craving to end suffering.

---

# 12. KARMA, REBIRTH, AND NIRVANA

## Karma in Buddhism
Intentional action that produces consequences.

## Kamma
Pali form of karma.

## Cetana
Intention. Buddhism emphasizes intention as the core of karma.

## Vipaka
Result or fruit of karma.

## Karmaphala
Fruit of action.

## Rebirth without Soul
Buddhism teaches rebirth but rejects an eternal soul.

## Stream of Consciousness
Continuity of mental processes across lives, without a permanent self.

## Nirvana
Extinction of craving, hatred, and ignorance.

## Nibbana
Pali form of Nirvana.

## Nirvana with Remainder
Liberation while still alive, when the body and aggregates continue.

## Nirvana without Remainder
Final Nirvana after death of an enlightened being.

## Parinirvana
Final passing beyond rebirth.

## Arhatship
State of becoming an Arhat and attaining liberation.

## Defilements
Mental impurities such as greed, hatred, and delusion.

## Klesha
Mental affliction or defilement.

## Lobha
Greed.

## Dosa
Hatred or aversion.

## Moha
Delusion.

## Three Poisons
Greed, hatred, and delusion.

## Asava
Mental outflows or deep-rooted impurities.

## Kilesa
Pali form of Klesha.

---

# 13. ETHICS IN BUDDHISM

## Panchasila
Five precepts followed by lay Buddhists.

## Five Precepts
Avoid killing, stealing, sexual misconduct, false speech, and intoxicants.

## Non-Killing
Avoiding taking life.

## Non-Stealing
Avoiding taking what is not given.

## Sexual Morality
Avoiding sexual misconduct.

## Truthful Speech
Avoiding false speech.

## Avoiding Intoxicants
Avoiding substances that cloud the mind.

## Ahimsa
Non-violence, important in Buddhism though less absolute than in Jainism.

## Karuna
Compassion.

## Maitri
Loving-kindness.

## Metta
Pali form of Maitri.

## Mudita
Sympathetic joy.

## Upeksha
Equanimity.

## Upekkha
Pali form of Upeksha.

## Brahmaviharas
Four sublime states: loving-kindness, compassion, sympathetic joy, and equanimity.

## Dana
Generosity or giving.

## Sila
Ethical conduct.

## Kshanti
Patience or forbearance.

## Virya
Energy or effort.

## Satya
Truthfulness.

## Appamada
Carefulness or heedfulness.

## Right Livelihood
Livelihood that avoids harm, deception, and exploitation.

## Ten Wholesome Actions
Avoiding harmful bodily, verbal, and mental actions.

## Ten Unwholesome Actions
Killing, stealing, sexual misconduct, false speech, divisive speech, harsh speech, idle speech, greed, ill-will, and wrong view.

---

# 14. MEDITATION AND MENTAL CULTIVATION

## Meditation
Mental training to develop concentration, mindfulness, and insight.

## Bhavana
Mental cultivation or meditation.

## Samatha
Calm meditation that develops concentration.

## Vipassana
Insight meditation that sees impermanence, suffering, and no-self.

## Vipashyana
Sanskrit form of Vipassana.

## Dhyana
Meditative absorption.

## Jhana
Pali form of Dhyana.

## Four Jhanas
Four stages of deep meditative absorption.

## Mindfulness
Awareness of present experience.

## Sati
Pali term for mindfulness.

## Smriti
Sanskrit term for mindfulness.

## Satipatthana
Foundations of mindfulness.

## Four Foundations of Mindfulness
Mindfulness of body, feelings, mind, and mental objects.

## Kayaanupassana
Contemplation of body.

## Vedanaanupassana
Contemplation of feelings.

## Cittaanupassana
Contemplation of mind.

## Dhammaanupassana
Contemplation of mental objects.

## Anapanasati
Mindfulness of breathing.

## Metta Bhavana
Meditation on loving-kindness.

## Karuna Bhavana
Meditation on compassion.

## Asubha Bhavana
Meditation on impurity of the body to reduce attachment.

## Maranasati
Mindfulness of death.

## Samadhi
Concentration.

## Ekaggata
One-pointedness of mind.

## Nimitta
Mental sign or image in meditation.

## Enlightenment Factors
Seven qualities that help awakening.

## Seven Factors of Enlightenment
Mindfulness, investigation, energy, joy, tranquility, concentration, and equanimity.

---

# 15. EARLY BUDDHIST SANGHA

## Sangha
The Buddhist monastic community.

## Bhikkhu Sangha
Community of monks.

## Bhikkhuni Sangha
Community of nuns.

## Lay Sangha
Community of lay followers.

## Upasaka
Male lay devotee.

## Upasika
Female lay devotee.

## Ordination
Formal entry into monastic life.

## Pabbajja
Going forth from household life into homelessness.

## Upasampada
Higher ordination as a full monk or nun.

## Novice Monk
A beginner in monastic life.

## Samanera
Pali term for novice monk.

## Samaneri
Pali term for novice nun.

## Vinaya
Monastic discipline.

## Patimokkha
Code of monastic rules recited regularly.

## Uposatha
Regular observance day when monks recite the Patimokkha.

## Vassa
Rainy season retreat when monks stay in one place.

## Chaturmas
Four-month rainy retreat, more broadly used in Indian religions.

## Kathina
Robe-offering ceremony after the rainy retreat.

## Alms Round
Daily practice of monks collecting food.

## Pindapata
Alms collection.

## Robe
Simple monastic clothing.

## Triple Robe
The three robes traditionally used by monks.

## Bowl
Alms bowl used by monks.

## Monastic Celibacy
Complete abstinence from sexual activity by monks and nuns.

## Monastic Poverty
Renunciation of personal property.

## Monastic Community Life
Living according to rules, discipline, teaching, meditation, and mutual support.

---

# 16. IMPORTANT DISCIPLES OF BUDDHA

## Sariputta
One of Buddha’s chief disciples, famous for wisdom.

## Maudgalyayana
One of Buddha’s chief disciples, famous for spiritual powers.

## Moggallana
Pali form of Maudgalyayana.

## Ananda
Buddha’s cousin and attendant, famous for memory of Buddha’s teachings.

## Mahakashyapa
Senior disciple who presided over the first Buddhist council.

## Mahakassapa
Pali form of Mahakashyapa.

## Upali
Disciple famous for knowledge of Vinaya.

## Rahula
Buddha’s son and disciple.

## Anuruddha
Disciple known for divine eye or spiritual vision.

## Mahakatyayana
Disciple known for explaining brief teachings in detail.

## Purna
Disciple known for preaching.

## Subhuti
Disciple associated with teachings on emptiness in Mahayana texts.

## Khema
Important nun known for wisdom.

## Uppalavanna
Important nun known for spiritual powers.

## Mahaprajapati Gotami
First Buddhist nun and Buddha’s foster mother.

## Kisagotami
Famous female disciple associated with the mustard seed story.

## Patacara
Important nun known for teaching discipline and overcoming suffering.

## Ambapali
Courtesan of Vaishali who became a supporter of Buddha.

## Anathapindika
Wealthy merchant donor of Jetavana monastery.

## Visakha
Important female lay donor and supporter of the Sangha.

## King Bimbisara
Royal patron of Buddha.

## King Prasenajit
Ruler of Kosala and supporter of Buddha.

## Ajatashatru
Ruler of Magadha associated with Buddha’s later life and the first council.

---

# 17. BUDDHIST SCRIPTURES: BASIC TERMS

## Tripitaka
The “Three Baskets” of Buddhist scriptures.

## Tipitaka
Pali form of Tripitaka.

## Vinaya Pitaka
Basket of monastic discipline.

## Sutta Pitaka
Basket of Buddha’s discourses.

## Sutra Pitaka
Sanskrit form of Sutta Pitaka.

## Abhidhamma Pitaka
Basket of higher doctrine and philosophical analysis.

## Abhidharma Pitaka
Sanskrit form of Abhidhamma Pitaka.

## Pali Canon
The canonical scripture of Theravada Buddhism preserved in Pali.

## Buddhist Canon
The accepted collection of Buddhist scriptures.

## Oral Tradition
Early Buddhist teachings were transmitted orally before being written down.

## Council Recitation
Collective recitation of teachings by monks to preserve doctrine.

## Dhamma-Vinaya
Buddha’s teaching and discipline.

## Nikaya
Collection of discourses in the Pali Canon.

## Agama
Collections of early Buddhist discourses preserved in Sanskrit/Chinese traditions.

## Commentary
Explanatory text on scripture.

## Atthakatha
Pali commentary.

## Tika
Sub-commentary.

---

# 18. VINAYA PITAKA

## Vinaya Pitaka
The collection of monastic rules and discipline.

## Suttavibhanga
Section of Vinaya explaining rules for monks and nuns.

## Khandhaka
Section dealing with monastic procedures and community life.

## Parivara
A later analytical summary of Vinaya rules.

## Patimokkha Rules
Rules of monastic conduct.

## Parajika
Most serious monastic offences leading to expulsion.

## Sanghadisesa
Serious offences requiring formal community discipline.

## Pacittiya
Offences requiring confession.

## Nissaggiya Pacittiya
Offences involving improper possession requiring forfeiture and confession.

## Sekhiya
Training rules about proper conduct.

## Adhikarana Samatha
Rules for settling disputes.

## Bhikkhuni Vinaya
Rules for Buddhist nuns.

## Garudhamma
Special rules traditionally imposed on nuns in early Buddhist texts.

---

# 19. SUTTA PITAKA

## Sutta Pitaka
Collection of Buddha’s discourses.

## Digha Nikaya
Collection of long discourses.

## Majjhima Nikaya
Collection of middle-length discourses.

## Samyutta Nikaya
Collection of connected discourses arranged by theme.

## Anguttara Nikaya
Collection of numerical discourses.

## Khuddaka Nikaya
Collection of minor or shorter texts.

## Dhammapada
Popular text of verses on Buddhist ethics and wisdom.

## Udana
Collection of inspired utterances.

## Itivuttaka
Collection of short sayings introduced by “thus it was said”.

## Sutta Nipata
Early collection of Buddhist verses and discourses.

## Theragatha
Verses of elder monks.

## Therigatha
Verses of elder nuns.

## Jataka
Stories of Buddha’s previous births.

## Buddhavamsa
Text on previous Buddhas.

## Cariyapitaka
Text on Bodhisattva conduct and perfections.

## Apadana
Biographical legends of monks and nuns.

## Petavatthu
Stories of hungry ghosts.

## Vimanavatthu
Stories of celestial mansions.

## Niddesa
Commentarial text on parts of Sutta Nipata.

## Patisambhidamagga
Analytical text in the Khuddaka Nikaya.

---

# 20. ABHIDHAMMA PITAKA

## Abhidhamma
Higher doctrine or systematic analysis of mental and physical phenomena.

## Dhammasangani
Enumeration of phenomena.

## Vibhanga
Book of analysis.

## Dhatukatha
Discussion of elements.

## Puggalapannatti
Description of personality types.

## Kathavatthu
Text discussing doctrinal controversies, traditionally linked with the Third Buddhist Council.

## Yamaka
Book of pairs.

## Patthana
Text on conditional relations.

## Dhamma Theory
Analysis of reality into momentary phenomena.

## Mental Factors
Elements of mind studied in Abhidhamma.

## Citta
Consciousness or mind moment.

## Cetasika
Mental factor.

## Rupa in Abhidhamma
Material form.

## Nibbana in Abhidhamma
Unconditioned reality.

---

# 21. IMPORTANT BUDDHIST TEXTS OUTSIDE THE PALI CANON

## Milindapanha
Dialogue between Indo-Greek king Menander/Milinda and monk Nagasena.

## Milinda
Indo-Greek king Menander, known in Buddhist tradition as Milinda.

## Nagasena
Buddhist monk who answers Milinda’s philosophical questions.

## Dipavamsa
Sri Lankan Buddhist chronicle.

## Mahavamsa
Important Sri Lankan Buddhist chronicle.

## Buddhacharita
Sanskrit biography of Buddha by Ashvaghosha.

## Saundarananda
Poem by Ashvaghosha on Nanda’s conversion.

## Mahavastu
Text of the Lokottaravada tradition containing Buddha legends.

## Lalitavistara
Sanskrit text narrating Buddha’s life, important in Mahayana tradition.

## Divyavadana
Collection of Buddhist stories in Sanskrit.

## Avadana
A Buddhist story showing karmic results of actions.

## Jatakamala
Garland of Jataka stories by Aryashura.

## Visuddhimagga
Theravada text by Buddhaghosa explaining path of purification.

## Abhidharmakosha
Important text by Vasubandhu on Abhidharma.

## Mulamadhyamakakarika
Text by Nagarjuna explaining Madhyamaka philosophy.

## Bodhicharyavatara
Text by Shantideva on the Bodhisattva path.

---

# 22. BUDDHIST COUNCILS

## Buddhist Council
A formal gathering of monks to preserve teachings, settle disputes, or organize doctrine.

## First Buddhist Council
Held at Rajagriha after Buddha’s Mahaparinirvana.

## Rajagriha Council
Another name for the First Buddhist Council.

## Saptaparni Cave
Cave near Rajagriha where the First Council is traditionally said to have been held.

## Mahakashyapa at First Council
Mahakashyapa presided over the First Council.

## Ananda at First Council
Ananda recited the Sutta teachings.

## Upali at First Council
Upali recited the Vinaya.

## Ajatashatru and First Council
Ajatashatru is traditionally associated as patron of the First Council.

## Second Buddhist Council
Held at Vaishali about a century after Buddha’s death.

## Vaishali Council
Another name for the Second Buddhist Council.

## Ten Points Controversy
Dispute over monastic practices at the Second Council.

## Vajjiputtaka Monks
Monks associated with controversial practices at Vaishali.

## Sthavira
Elders who insisted on stricter discipline.

## Mahasanghika
The “great community” associated with a split after early doctrinal and disciplinary disputes.

## First Schism
The division between Sthaviras and Mahasanghikas, traditionally linked to the period after the Second Council.

## Third Buddhist Council
Held at Pataliputra under Ashoka according to Theravada tradition.

## Pataliputra Council
Another name for the Third Buddhist Council.

## Moggaliputta Tissa
Elder associated with the Third Council and the Kathavatthu.

## Kathavatthu and Third Council
Text traditionally compiled to refute wrong views.

## Ashoka and Third Council
Ashoka is associated with purification of the Sangha and sending missions.

## Fourth Buddhist Council
Different traditions mention different fourth councils.

## Fourth Council under Kanishka
Associated with Kanishka and Sarvastivada tradition in Kashmir or nearby region.

## Vasumitra
Scholar associated with the Fourth Council under Kanishka.

## Ashvaghosha
Buddhist scholar-poet associated with the Kushana period.

## Fourth Council in Sri Lanka
Theravada tradition also refers to the writing down of the Pali Canon in Sri Lanka as an important council-like event.

---

# 23. ASHOKA AND BUDDHISM

## Ashoka
Mauryan emperor who became a major patron of Buddhism after the Kalinga War.

## Kalinga War
A violent war that deeply affected Ashoka and encouraged his turn toward Dhamma.

## Ashoka’s Dhamma
An ethical policy emphasizing compassion, non-violence, respect, self-control, and welfare.

## Dhamma Mahamatta
Officials appointed by Ashoka to promote Dhamma.

## Ashokan Edicts
Inscriptions issued by Ashoka on rocks and pillars.

## Major Rock Edicts
Important Ashokan inscriptions dealing with Dhamma, administration, and morality.

## Minor Rock Edicts
Shorter Ashokan inscriptions, some showing personal commitment to Buddhism.

## Pillar Edicts
Inscriptions on Ashokan pillars.

## Bhabru Edict
Ashokan edict showing respect for Buddhist texts.

## Rummindei Inscription
Ashokan inscription at Lumbini marking Buddha’s birthplace.

## Nigali Sagar Inscription
Ashokan inscription associated with Kanakamuni Buddha.

## Sarnath Pillar
Ashokan pillar at Sarnath, famous for the Lion Capital.

## Lion Capital
Capital of Ashokan pillar at Sarnath; now India’s National Emblem.

## Dharmachakra
Wheel of Dharma, symbol of Buddha’s teaching and Ashoka’s Dhamma.

## Ashoka’s Buddhist Missions
Missionary activity sent to different regions after the Third Council according to tradition.

## Mahinda
Ashoka’s son, traditionally credited with taking Buddhism to Sri Lanka.

## Sanghamitta
Ashoka’s daughter, traditionally associated with taking the Bodhi tree branch to Sri Lanka.

## Sri Lanka Mission
Important mission that established Theravada Buddhism in Sri Lanka.

## Devanampiya Tissa
Sri Lankan king associated with receiving Buddhism from Mahinda.

## Bodhi Tree at Anuradhapura
Sacred tree grown from a branch of the Bodhi tree, brought by Sanghamitta according to tradition.

## Stupa Building by Ashoka
Tradition says Ashoka built or enlarged many stupas.

## Relic Redistribution
Tradition says Ashoka redistributed Buddha’s relics into many stupas.

---

# 24. EARLY BUDDHIST SCHOOLS

## Early Buddhist Schools
Different monastic and doctrinal schools that developed after Buddha’s death.

## Sthaviravada
School of the Elders, an early branch emphasizing conservative discipline.

## Mahasanghika
Early school meaning “great community”, associated with more liberal interpretations.

## Theravada
“Doctrine of the Elders”. A surviving school based mainly on the Pali Canon.

## Sarvastivada
School that taught that dharmas exist in past, present, and future.

## Vaibhashika
A Sarvastivada sub-school associated with detailed Abhidharma.

## Sautrantika
School emphasizing sutras over Abhidharma texts.

## Dharmaguptaka
Early Buddhist school important in Central Asia and China.

## Mahishasaka
Early Buddhist school.

## Kashyapiya
Early Buddhist school.

## Lokottaravada
Mahasanghika-related school that saw Buddha as transcendental.

## Pudgalavada
School that proposed a “person” concept to explain continuity.

## Vatsiputriya
A Pudgalavada-related school.

## Hinayana
Literally “lesser vehicle”, a Mahayana polemical term for non-Mahayana schools. It should be used carefully.

## Non-Mahayana Buddhism
A better neutral term for early schools that were not Mahayana.

## Nikaya Buddhism
Buddhism of early monastic schools.

---

# 25. THERAVADA BUDDHISM

## Theravada
The surviving early Buddhist school, dominant in Sri Lanka, Myanmar, Thailand, Laos, and Cambodia.

## Pali Canon
Scriptural foundation of Theravada Buddhism.

## Arhat Ideal
The goal of becoming an Arhat and attaining liberation.

## Sri Lankan Theravada
Theravada tradition preserved in Sri Lanka.

## Mahavihara
Important Theravada monastery in Sri Lanka.

## Abhayagiri
A major Sri Lankan monastery with broader doctrinal influences.

## Buddhaghosa
Great Theravada commentator, author of Visuddhimagga.

## Visuddhimagga
“The Path of Purification”, a major Theravada meditation and doctrine manual.

## Dhammapala
Important Theravada commentator.

## Pali
Canonical language of Theravada Buddhism.

## Tipitaka
Three baskets of Theravada scripture.

## Vipassana Tradition
Insight meditation tradition especially associated with Theravada.

---

# 26. MAHAYANA BUDDHISM

## Mahayana
“Great Vehicle”. A major Buddhist tradition emphasizing Bodhisattva ideal, compassion, and universal liberation.

## Bodhisattva Ideal
The ideal of seeking enlightenment for the benefit of all beings.

## Bodhicitta
The awakened mind or aspiration to attain Buddhahood for all beings.

## Paramita
Perfection practiced by Bodhisattvas.

## Six Paramitas
Generosity, morality, patience, energy, meditation, and wisdom.

## Ten Paramitas
Expanded list including skillful means, vow, power, and knowledge.

## Prajnaparamita
Perfection of wisdom.

## Sunyata
Emptiness; the idea that all things lack independent permanent existence.

## Shunyata
Another form of Sunyata.

## Karuna in Mahayana
Compassion for all beings.

## Upaya
Skillful means used by Bodhisattvas to guide beings.

## Buddhahood
Complete enlightenment as a Buddha.

## Trikaya
Three bodies of Buddha: Dharmakaya, Sambhogakaya, and Nirmanakaya.

## Dharmakaya
Truth body of Buddha.

## Sambhogakaya
Enjoyment or celestial body of Buddha.

## Nirmanakaya
Manifested body of Buddha in the world.

## Adi-Buddha
Primordial Buddha in some later traditions.

## Buddha-Nature
The potential for Buddhahood in all beings.

## Tathagatagarbha
Buddha-womb or Buddha-nature doctrine.

## Pure Land Buddhism
Mahayana tradition centered on rebirth in a pure land through devotion.

## Amitabha
Buddha of infinite light, central to Pure Land Buddhism.

## Sukhavati
Pure Land of Amitabha.

## Lotus Sutra
Important Mahayana scripture teaching universal Buddhahood.

## Saddharma Pundarika Sutra
Sanskrit name of the Lotus Sutra.

## Heart Sutra
Short Prajnaparamita text teaching emptiness.

## Diamond Sutra
Prajnaparamita text emphasizing emptiness and non-attachment.

## Avatamsaka Sutra
Mahayana text describing vast interdependence and cosmic vision.

## Lankavatara Sutra
Mahayana text important for Yogachara and Zen traditions.

## Vimalakirti Nirdesha
Mahayana text featuring the lay Bodhisattva Vimalakirti.

---

# 27. MAHAYANA BODHISATTVAS

## Avalokiteshvara
Bodhisattva of compassion.

## Padmapani
Lotus-bearing form of Avalokiteshvara.

## Manjushri
Bodhisattva of wisdom.

## Vajrapani
Bodhisattva associated with power and protection.

## Maitreya
Future Buddha, currently a Bodhisattva in Tusita heaven.

## Kshitigarbha
Bodhisattva associated with helping beings in hell realms.

## Samantabhadra
Bodhisattva associated with practice and vows.

## Tara
Female Bodhisattva or goddess associated with compassion and protection.

## Green Tara
Form of Tara associated with active compassion.

## White Tara
Form of Tara associated with longevity and healing.

## Akashagarbha
Bodhisattva associated with vastness and wisdom.

## Mahasthamaprapta
Bodhisattva associated with wisdom and power.

---

# 28. MAJOR BUDDHIST PHILOSOPHICAL SCHOOLS

## Madhyamaka
Mahayana philosophical school founded by Nagarjuna, emphasizing emptiness and the middle way.

## Nagarjuna
Great Buddhist philosopher associated with Madhyamaka.

## Aryadeva
Disciple of Nagarjuna and Madhyamaka philosopher.

## Shunyavada
Doctrine of emptiness associated with Madhyamaka.

## Two Truths Doctrine
Distinction between conventional truth and ultimate truth.

## Conventional Truth
Everyday practical truth.

## Ultimate Truth
Truth of emptiness and lack of independent existence.

## Yogachara
Mahayana school emphasizing consciousness and mental construction.

## Vijnanavada
Another name for Yogachara, meaning consciousness-only doctrine.

## Asanga
Founder figure of Yogachara tradition.

## Vasubandhu
Important Buddhist philosopher associated with Abhidharma and Yogachara.

## Alaya Vijnana
Storehouse consciousness in Yogachara.

## Tathagatagarbha School
Tradition emphasizing Buddha-nature.

## Dignaga
Buddhist logician and epistemologist.

## Dharmakirti
Major Buddhist philosopher of logic and epistemology.

## Pramana School
Buddhist school of valid knowledge associated with Dignaga and Dharmakirti.

## Apoha Theory
Buddhist theory of meaning by exclusion.

## Momentariness
Doctrine that all conditioned things exist only moment by moment.

## Kshanika Vada
Doctrine of momentariness.

---

# 29. VAJRAYANA BUDDHISM

## Vajrayana
“Diamond Vehicle” or Tantric Buddhism. It uses mantras, mandalas, mudras, visualization, and guru-disciple transmission.

## Tantric Buddhism
Form of Buddhism using esoteric rituals and symbolic practices.

## Mantrayana
Vehicle of mantras.

## Esoteric Buddhism
Buddhism involving secret teachings and initiation.

## Vajra
Thunderbolt or diamond symbol representing indestructible wisdom.

## Mantra
Sacred sound or formula used in meditation and ritual.

## Mandala
Sacred diagram representing cosmic order or enlightened reality.

## Mudra
Symbolic hand gesture or ritual gesture.

## Deity Yoga
Meditative identification with a deity to realize enlightened qualities.

## Guru
Spiritual teacher in Vajrayana.

## Lama
Tibetan Buddhist teacher.

## Initiation
Formal empowerment into tantric practice.

## Abhisheka in Vajrayana
Ritual empowerment.

## Sadhana
Structured spiritual practice.

## Yidam
Meditational deity in Vajrayana.

## Dakini
Female enlightened energy or spiritual figure.

## Heruka
Wrathful enlightened deity.

## Vajrasattva
Purification deity in Vajrayana.

## Vajradhara
Primordial Buddha in some Vajrayana traditions.

## Hevajra
Important tantric deity and text tradition.

## Kalachakra
Tantric system meaning “Wheel of Time”.

## Sahajayana
A tantric Buddhist tradition emphasizing spontaneous realization.

## Siddha
Accomplished tantric practitioner.

## Mahasiddha
Great accomplished tantric master.

## Padmasambhava
Indian tantric master credited with spreading Vajrayana in Tibet.

## Atisha
Indian Buddhist teacher who helped reform Tibetan Buddhism.

## Tibetan Buddhism
Vajrayana Buddhism that developed in Tibet.

## Nyingma
Oldest school of Tibetan Buddhism.

## Kagyu
Tibetan Buddhist school emphasizing meditation lineage.

## Sakya
Tibetan Buddhist school linked with scholarship and tantric practice.

## Gelug
Tibetan Buddhist school associated with Tsongkhapa and the Dalai Lama lineage.

---

# 30. BUDDHIST ART: BASIC TERMS

## Buddhist Art
Art connected with Buddha, Bodhisattvas, Jataka stories, stupas, monasteries, and Buddhist symbols.

## Aniconic Art
Early Buddhist art where Buddha is represented through symbols rather than human form.

## Iconic Art
Art where Buddha is shown in human form.

## Anthropomorphic Buddha
Human-form image of Buddha.

## Buddha Image
Sculptural or painted representation of Buddha.

## Bodhisattva Image
Image of a Bodhisattva, often richly ornamented in Mahayana art.

## Yaksha Influence
Early Buddhist sculpture was influenced by earlier yaksha-yakshi traditions.

## Stupa Art
Relief sculpture on railings, gateways, and drum slabs of stupas.

## Narrative Relief
Sculpture showing stories from Buddha’s life or Jataka tales.

## Jataka Panel
Art panel showing a previous birth story of Buddha.

## Devotional Image
Image used for worship and meditation.

---

# 31. BUDDHIST SYMBOLS

## Dharmachakra
Wheel of Dharma, symbolizing Buddha’s teaching.

## Lotus
Symbol of purity and spiritual awakening.

## Bodhi Tree
Symbol of enlightenment.

## Empty Throne
Aniconic symbol of Buddha’s presence.

## Footprints of Buddha
Aniconic representation of Buddha.

## Buddhapada
Sacred footprints of Buddha.

## Stupa Symbol
Symbol of Buddha’s relics and enlightened mind.

## Riderless Horse
Symbol of Buddha’s renunciation.

## Parasol
Symbol of spiritual authority and protection.

## Triratna Symbol
Symbol of Buddha, Dhamma, and Sangha.

## Deer
Symbol of the Deer Park at Sarnath and the first sermon.

## Lion
Symbol of Buddha’s royal or spiritual power.

## Lion Capital
Ashokan capital at Sarnath symbolizing Dharma.

## Swastika
Auspicious symbol used in Buddhist contexts.

## Endless Knot
Symbol of interdependence in later Buddhist art.

## Vajra Symbol
Symbol of indestructible wisdom in Vajrayana.

---

# 32. BUDDHIST MUDRAS

## Mudra
Symbolic hand gesture in Buddhist art.

## Bhumisparsha Mudra
Earth-touching gesture, associated with Buddha’s enlightenment.

## Dharmachakra Mudra
Gesture of turning the wheel of Dharma, associated with first sermon.

## Dhyana Mudra
Meditation gesture.

## Abhaya Mudra
Gesture of fearlessness and protection.

## Varada Mudra
Gesture of charity or granting wishes.

## Vitarka Mudra
Gesture of teaching or discussion.

## Anjali Mudra
Gesture of reverence with folded hands.

## Karana Mudra
Gesture of warding off evil.

## Vajrahumkara Mudra
Tantric gesture associated with Vajrayana.

---

# 33. BUDDHIST ARCHITECTURE

## Stupa
A mound-like Buddhist monument containing relics or symbolizing Buddha.

## Chaitya
A Buddhist prayer hall, usually containing a stupa.

## Vihara
A Buddhist monastery or residence for monks.

## Mahavihara
A great monastery or large monastic university.

## Stupa Relic
Sacred remains of Buddha or saints kept in a stupa.

## Anda
The dome of a stupa.

## Harmika
Square railing on top of the stupa dome.

## Chhatra
Umbrella-like structure above a stupa.

## Chhatravali
Series of umbrellas above a stupa.

## Yasti
Central pole supporting the chhatras.

## Vedika
Railing around a stupa.

## Torana
Decorative gateway of a stupa.

## Medhi
Circular terrace or base for circumambulation.

## Pradakshina Patha
Path for clockwise circumambulation.

## Drum
Cylindrical base of a stupa.

## Ayaka Platform
Projecting platform associated especially with Amaravati and Nagarjunakonda stupas.

## Relic Casket
Container holding sacred relics.

## Rock-Cut Cave
Cave carved into rock for prayer or residence.

## Chaitya Hall
Prayer hall with apsidal end and stupa.

## Apsidal Plan
Plan with a rounded end, common in chaitya halls.

## Barrel-Vaulted Roof
Curved roof form seen in chaitya halls.

## Horseshoe Arch
Arched window motif in Buddhist cave architecture.

## Gavaksha
Chaitya-window or horseshoe-shaped architectural motif.

## Cells
Small rooms in viharas for monks.

## Monastic Courtyard
Open central space in some viharas.

## Pillared Hall
Hall supported by pillars.

## Rock-Cut Vihara
Monastery carved into rock.

## Structural Stupa
Stupa built with brick or stone.

## Brick Stupa
Stupa made mainly of brick.

## Stone Railing
Stone enclosure around a stupa.

---

# 34. MAJOR BUDDHIST ART SCHOOLS

## Mauryan Buddhist Art
Early imperial art under Ashoka, including pillars, stupas, and polished stone works.

## Sanchi Art
Early Buddhist stupa art with gateways, railings, and narrative reliefs.

## Bharhut Art
Early Buddhist art known for railings, inscriptions, and aniconic representations.

## Gandhara Art
Buddhist art style of north-west India influenced by Greco-Roman elements.

## Mathura Art
Indian art style centered at Mathura, using red sandstone and producing Buddha, Bodhisattva, Jain, and Hindu images.

## Amaravati Art
Buddhist art style of Andhra region known for elegant limestone reliefs.

## Nagarjunakonda Art
Buddhist art of Andhra region, continuing Amaravati traditions.

## Gupta Buddhist Art
Classical Buddhist art marked by spiritual calm, balanced proportions, and refined Buddha images.

## Sarnath School
Gupta-period art style known for smooth, refined Buddha images.

## Ajanta Painting
Buddhist cave paintings depicting Jataka stories, Buddha, Bodhisattvas, and royal scenes.

## Pala Buddhist Art
Eastern Indian Buddhist art under the Palas, important for Vajrayana images and monasteries.

## Himalayan Buddhist Art
Art of Tibetan and Himalayan Buddhism, rich in mandalas, thangkas, and tantric deities.

---

# 35. GANDHARA ART

## Gandhara
Region in north-west India/Pakistan/Afghanistan associated with Greco-Buddhist art.

## Greco-Buddhist Art
Buddhist art influenced by Greek and Roman artistic forms.

## Wavy Hair
Common feature of Gandhara Buddha images.

## Roman Toga-like Robe
Draped robe style seen in Gandhara Buddha images.

## Realistic Anatomy
Naturalistic body treatment in Gandhara art.

## Stucco
Material used in Gandhara sculpture.

## Grey Schist
Stone commonly used in Gandhara sculpture.

## Hellenistic Influence
Greek artistic influence visible in Gandhara.

## Bodhisattva Maitreya in Gandhara
Often shown with princely ornaments and water flask.

## Gandhara Buddha
Human Buddha image with western-influenced features.

## Taxila Art
Art from the Taxila region associated with Gandhara tradition.

---

# 36. MATHURA ART

## Mathura
Major art center in north India.

## Red Sandstone
Common material used in Mathura sculptures.

## Mathura Buddha
Buddha image with Indian features, often wearing thin robe and showing strong body.

## Standing Buddha
Common Mathura image type.

## Seated Buddha
Buddha seated in meditation or teaching posture.

## Ushnisha
Cranial protuberance on Buddha’s head, symbolizing wisdom.

## Urna
Mark between Buddha’s eyebrows.

## Halo in Mathura Art
Circular disc behind Buddha’s head.

## Bodhisattva in Mathura
Richly ornamented figure representing Bodhisattva ideal.

## Kushana Mathura Art
Mathura art flourished under the Kushanas.

---

# 37. AMARAVATI AND ANDHRA BUDDHIST ART

## Amaravati
Major Buddhist stupa and art center in Andhra region.

## Amaravati Stupa
Large Buddhist monument with elaborate limestone reliefs.

## White Limestone
Common material in Amaravati sculpture.

## Narrative Reliefs
Detailed scenes from Buddha’s life and Jataka stories.

## Dynamic Movement
Feature of Amaravati art with lively figures and flowing compositions.

## Nagarjunakonda
Important Buddhist center in Andhra Pradesh.

## Ikshvaku Patronage
Dynasty associated with Buddhist monuments in Nagarjunakonda region.

## Ayaka Pillars
Pillars associated with Andhra stupas.

---

# 38. SRI LANKA AND THERAVADA SPREAD

## Sri Lanka
Major center of Theravada Buddhism.

## Anuradhapura
Ancient Sri Lankan capital and Buddhist center.

## Mahavihara
Main Theravada monastery at Anuradhapura.

## Bodhi Tree Branch
Branch of the Bodhi tree brought by Sanghamitta according to tradition.

## Devanampiya Tissa
Sri Lankan king who accepted Buddhism.

## Mahinda
Missionary monk associated with Sri Lankan conversion.

## Sanghamitta
Nun associated with bringing the Bodhi tree branch to Sri Lanka.

## Dipavamsa
Sri Lankan Buddhist chronicle.

## Mahavamsa
Important Sri Lankan chronicle giving Buddhist historical traditions.

## Pali Canon Written Down
Theravada tradition says the Pali Canon was written down in Sri Lanka.

## Tooth Relic
Important Buddhist relic venerated in Sri Lanka.

## Kandy Tooth Relic Temple
Temple housing the tooth relic in Sri Lanka.

---

# 39. SPREAD OF BUDDHISM OUTSIDE INDIA

## Buddhist Missions
Efforts to spread Buddhism to different regions.

## Central Asia
Important route for Buddhism’s spread to China.

## Silk Route
Trade route through which Buddhism spread from India to Central Asia and China.

## China
Buddhism entered China through Central Asian and maritime routes.

## Faxian
Chinese Buddhist pilgrim who visited India during the Gupta period.

## Fa-Hien
Another spelling of Faxian.

## Xuanzang
Chinese Buddhist pilgrim who visited India in the 7th century CE.

## Hiuen Tsang
Older spelling of Xuanzang.

## Yijing
Chinese Buddhist pilgrim who visited India and Southeast Asia.

## Korea
Buddhism spread to Korea from China.

## Japan
Buddhism spread to Japan from Korea and China.

## Southeast Asia
Buddhism spread to Myanmar, Thailand, Cambodia, Laos, Vietnam, and Indonesia.

## Myanmar
Major Theravada Buddhist country.

## Thailand
Major Theravada Buddhist country.

## Cambodia
Historically influenced by Hinduism, Mahayana, and later Theravada Buddhism.

## Laos
Theravada Buddhist country.

## Indonesia
Historically important for Mahayana and Vajrayana Buddhism, especially Borobudur.

## Borobudur
Great Buddhist monument in Java, Indonesia.

## Tibet
Major center of Vajrayana Buddhism.

## Mongolia
Region influenced by Tibetan Buddhism.

## Nepal
Important Buddhist region associated with Lumbini and Newar Buddhism.

## Maritime Route
Sea route through which Buddhism spread to Sri Lanka and Southeast Asia.

---

# 40. BUDDHIST UNIVERSITIES AND MONASTIC CENTRES

## Nalanda
Great Buddhist monastic university in Bihar.

## Nalanda Mahavihara
Large residential Buddhist educational institution.

## Kumaragupta and Nalanda
Gupta ruler often associated with early patronage of Nalanda.

## Harsha and Nalanda
Harsha supported Buddhism and Nalanda.

## Pala Patronage
The Palas strongly supported Buddhist universities.

## Vikramashila
Major Buddhist university founded by Dharmapala of the Pala dynasty.

## Odantapuri
Important Buddhist university in Bihar.

## Somapura Mahavihara
Large Buddhist monastery in present-day Bangladesh.

## Jagaddala
Pala-period Buddhist monastery.

## Valabhi
Important learning center in western India, also associated with Buddhist and Jain studies.

## Taxila
Ancient center of learning in north-west India.

## Monastic Curriculum
Study of Buddhist doctrine, logic, grammar, medicine, philosophy, and debate.

## Residential University
A monastery where teachers and students lived and studied.

## Mahavihara Network
Network of large Buddhist monasteries supported by kings and donors.

---

# 41. BUDDHISM UNDER IMPORTANT DYNASTIES

## Mauryan Patronage
Ashoka gave major support to Buddhism through missions, stupas, edicts, and moral policy.

## Shunga Period Buddhism
Buddhist monuments like Sanchi and Bharhut continued to receive patronage, though older theories of persecution are debated.

## Satavahana Patronage
Satavahanas and related donors supported Buddhist caves and stupas in the Deccan.

## Kushana Patronage
Kushanas, especially Kanishka, supported Buddhism and Gandhara-Mathura art.

## Kanishka
Kushana ruler associated with Mahayana growth and the Fourth Buddhist Council tradition.

## Gupta Period Buddhism
Buddhism continued, with important art at Sarnath and institutions like Nalanda.

## Harsha
North Indian ruler who patronized Buddhism along with other religions.

## Pala Dynasty
Major patrons of late Indian Buddhism, especially Mahayana and Vajrayana.

## Dharmapala
Pala ruler associated with Vikramashila and Buddhist patronage.

## Devapala
Pala ruler known for supporting Buddhist institutions.

## Ikshvakus
Dynasty in Andhra region associated with Buddhist sites like Nagarjunakonda.

## Western Kshatrapas
Rulers in western India whose period saw Buddhist cave donations.

## Merchant Donors
Traders and guilds were major supporters of Buddhist monuments and caves.

---

# 42. BUDDHIST CAVE ARCHITECTURE IN WESTERN INDIA

## Western Deccan Caves
Rock-cut Buddhist caves in Maharashtra and nearby regions.

## Bhaja Caves
Early Buddhist caves with chaitya and viharas.

## Karle Chaitya
One of the largest and finest Buddhist chaitya halls.

## Bedsa Caves
Buddhist caves with chaitya architecture.

## Kanheri Caves
Large Buddhist cave complex near Mumbai.

## Nasik Caves
Buddhist caves with important inscriptions.

## Junnar Caves
Large group of Buddhist caves.

## Ajanta Caves
Buddhist caves famous for paintings, sculptures, chaityas, and viharas.

## Pitalkhora Caves
Early Buddhist cave site.

## Kondane Caves
Early Buddhist cave site.

## Ellora Buddhist Caves
Buddhist caves in the Ellora complex.

## Chaitya Window
Horseshoe-shaped window motif in cave architecture.

## Wooden Imitation in Stone
Stone carving imitating wooden architectural forms in caves.

## Donor Inscription
Inscription recording donations by merchants, monks, nuns, guilds, or rulers.

---

# 43. AJANTA

## Ajanta
Buddhist cave site in Maharashtra, famous for paintings and sculptures.

## Ajanta Phase I
Early Hinayana or non-Mahayana phase with chaitya halls and simpler forms.

## Ajanta Phase II
Later Mahayana phase with elaborate paintings and Bodhisattva images.

## Padmapani
Famous Bodhisattva painting at Ajanta.

## Vajrapani
Famous Bodhisattva painting at Ajanta.

## Jataka Paintings
Paintings showing previous births of Buddha.

## Mahajanaka Jataka
A Jataka story depicted at Ajanta.

## Vessantara Jataka
A popular Jataka story depicted in Buddhist art.

## Ajanta Murals
Wall paintings made using tempera-like techniques on prepared surfaces.

## Cave 1
Famous for Bodhisattva paintings.

## Cave 2
Famous for painted ceilings and narrative scenes.

## Cave 10
Early chaitya cave.

## Cave 19
Later chaitya cave with elaborate facade.

## Cave 26
Large chaitya cave with Mahaparinirvana sculpture.

---

# 44. MAJOR BUDDHIST STUPAS

## Sanchi Stupa
Major Buddhist stupa in Madhya Pradesh, originally associated with Ashoka and later enlarged.

## Great Stupa at Sanchi
Stupa 1 at Sanchi, famous for toranas and reliefs.

## Bharhut Stupa
Early Buddhist stupa known for railings, inscriptions, and narrative art.

## Amaravati Stupa
Large stupa in Andhra region, known for elaborate relief sculpture.

## Dhamek Stupa
Important stupa at Sarnath marking the site of Buddha’s first sermon.

## Dharmarajika Stupa
Stupa name associated with Ashokan relic stupas at various sites.

## Piprahwa Stupa
Stupa associated with relics and Shakya region.

## Ramabhar Stupa
Stupa at Kushinagar associated with Buddha’s cremation.

## Kesariya Stupa
Large Buddhist stupa in Bihar.

## Shanti Stupa
Modern Buddhist peace stupa tradition.

## Relic Stupa
Stupa containing relics.

## Commemorative Stupa
Stupa marking an event in Buddha’s life.

## Votive Stupa
Small stupa offered by devotees.

---

# 45. BUDDHIST RELICS

## Sarira
Physical relics of Buddha or saints.

## Paribhogika Relic
Object used by Buddha or a saint.

## Uddesika Relic
Symbolic or representational relic, such as an image.

## Relic Casket
Container holding relics.

## Relic Worship
Veneration of relics as sacred reminders of Buddha.

## Stupa Relic Cult
Religious practice centered on relic stupas.

## Tooth Relic
Important relic tradition, especially in Sri Lanka.

## Bone Relic
Physical bone remains worshipped in stupas.

## Ash Relic
Cremation remains preserved as relics.

---

# 46. BUDDHIST FESTIVALS

## Buddha Purnima
Festival celebrating Buddha’s birth, enlightenment, and Mahaparinirvana in many traditions.

## Vesak
International Buddhist festival corresponding to Buddha Purnima.

## Asalha Puja
Festival commemorating Buddha’s first sermon.

## Magha Puja
Festival commemorating a gathering of monks and Buddha’s teaching.

## Kathina
Robe offering ceremony after the rainy season retreat.

## Ullambana
Festival for ancestors in some Mahayana traditions.

## Losar
Tibetan New Year.

## Saga Dawa
Tibetan Buddhist festival commemorating Buddha’s life events.

## Obon
Japanese Buddhist festival for ancestors.

## Poson
Sri Lankan festival commemorating the arrival of Buddhism through Mahinda.

---

# 47. BUDDHIST RITUAL AND DEVOTION

## Puja
Worship or devotional offering.

## Vandana
Reverential salutation.

## Refuge Taking
Formal acceptance of Buddha, Dhamma, and Sangha.

## Trisharana
Three refuges: Buddha, Dhamma, and Sangha.

## Three Jewels
Buddha, Dhamma, and Sangha.

## Buddha Vandanā
Salutation to Buddha.

## Dhamma Vandanā
Salutation to the teaching.

## Sangha Vandanā
Salutation to the monastic community.

## Paritta
Protective chanting in Theravada Buddhism.

## Sutra Chanting
Recitation of Buddhist scriptures.

## Mantra Chanting
Recitation of sacred formulas, especially in Mahayana and Vajrayana.

## Circumambulation
Walking clockwise around a stupa or sacred object.

## Pradakshina
Clockwise circumambulation.

## Prostration
Bowing fully as a mark of devotion and humility.

## Lamp Offering
Offering of light.

## Incense Offering
Offering of fragrance.

## Flower Offering
Offering flowers as a reminder of impermanence.

## Merit
Positive karmic result of good actions.

## Merit Transfer
Dedication of merit to others.

## Punya
Merit.

---

# 48. BUDDHIST COSMOLOGY

## Samsara
Cycle of rebirth.

## Six Realms
Gods, demigods, humans, animals, hungry ghosts, and hell beings.

## Deva Realm
Realm of gods.

## Asura Realm
Realm of jealous demigods.

## Human Realm
Realm where enlightenment is especially possible.

## Animal Realm
Realm of ignorance and instinct.

## Preta Realm
Realm of hungry ghosts.

## Naraka Realm
Hell realm.

## Deva
Heavenly being.

## Asura
Powerful jealous being.

## Preta
Hungry ghost.

## Naraka
Hell.

## Mara
Personification of temptation, death, and spiritual obstruction.

## Brahma
High deity in Buddhist cosmology, not a creator god in the absolute sense.

## Sakra
King of gods, also called Indra in Buddhist texts.

## Tusita Heaven
Heaven where future Buddha Maitreya resides.

## Maitreya in Tusita
Maitreya waits in Tusita before becoming the next Buddha.

## Mount Meru
Cosmic mountain in Buddhist cosmology.

## Kalpa
A vast cosmic time period.

## World System
A universe or cosmic system in Buddhist cosmology.

---

# 49. BUDDHISM AND SOCIAL THOUGHT

## Rejection of Vedic Authority
Buddhism did not accept the Vedas as final authority.

## Critique of Ritualism
Buddha criticized empty rituals and emphasized ethics and wisdom.

## Critique of Caste
Buddhism challenged the idea that spiritual worth depends on birth.

## Conduct over Birth
Buddhism emphasized action and character over caste origin.

## Universal Accessibility
Buddhist path was open to monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen.

## Women in Buddhism
Women could join the Sangha as nuns, though under additional rules in traditional texts.

## Bhikkhuni Sangha
Order of Buddhist nuns.

## Mahaprajapati Gotami as First Nun
Buddha’s foster mother became the first nun according to tradition.

## Lay Participation
Lay followers supported monks and practiced ethics, generosity, and devotion.

## Merchant Patronage
Buddhism received strong support from merchants and urban classes.

## Monastic Economy
Monasteries depended on donations, land grants, trade routes, and royal support.

## Buddhist Education
Monasteries became centers of learning, debate, philosophy, medicine, grammar, and logic.

---

# 50. BUDDHISM AND ECONOMY

## Dana Economy
Religious economy based on donations by laypeople and rulers.

## Monastery Donation
Gift of land, caves, money, food, robes, or buildings to the Sangha.

## Cave Donation
Many Buddhist caves were donated by merchants, guilds, monks, nuns, and rulers.

## Trade Route Buddhism
Buddhism spread along trade routes because monasteries often developed near commercial paths.

## Caravan Merchants
Merchants who helped spread Buddhism through long-distance trade.

## Guild Donors
Artisan and merchant guilds donated to Buddhist monuments.

## Urban Monasteries
Monasteries located near towns and trade centers.

## Land Grants
Later Buddhist monasteries received land grants from kings and elites.

## Monastic Wealth
Some monasteries became wealthy due to donations and land endowments.

---

# 51. BUDDHIST LOGIC AND SCHOLASTICISM

## Buddhist Logic
System of reasoning developed by Buddhist philosophers.

## Epistemology
Theory of knowledge.

## Pramana
Valid means of knowledge.

## Perception
Direct knowledge through experience.

## Inference
Knowledge through reasoning.

## Dignaga
Founder of Buddhist logical tradition.

## Dharmakirti
Great Buddhist logician and philosopher.

## Hetuvidya
Science of reasoning or logic.

## Debate Tradition
Buddhist monks debated with other schools in universities and courts.

## Scholastic Buddhism
Systematic study and classification of doctrine.

## Abhidharma Analysis
Detailed analysis of mental and physical phenomena.

---

# 52. DECLINE OF BUDDHISM IN INDIA

## Decline of Buddhism
Gradual weakening of Buddhism in much of India after the early medieval period.

## Loss of Royal Patronage
Reduction of state support affected monasteries.

## Assimilation
Some Buddhist ideas and practices were absorbed into broader Hindu traditions.

## Rise of Bhakti
Popular devotional Hindu movements competed with Buddhism.

## Monastic Isolation
Some monasteries became separated from lay society and dependent on elite patronage.

## Tantric Assimilation
Overlap between Buddhist and Hindu tantric practices blurred boundaries.

## Invasions and Monastery Destruction
Destruction of major monasteries such as Nalanda and Vikramashila contributed to decline.

## Decline of Trade Routes
Changes in trade networks affected monastery economies.

## Survival in Himalayan Regions
Buddhism survived strongly in Tibet, Ladakh, Nepal, Bhutan, Sikkim, and Himalayan areas.

## Survival in Sri Lanka and Southeast Asia
Theravada Buddhism remained strong outside India.

## Modern Revival
Buddhism revived in modern India through figures like Anagarika Dharmapala and B. R. Ambedkar.

---

# 53. MODERN BUDDHIST REVIVAL

## Anagarika Dharmapala
Sri Lankan Buddhist reformer associated with revival of Bodh Gaya and modern Buddhist movements.

## Mahabodhi Society
Organization founded to revive and protect Buddhist sacred sites.

## B. R. Ambedkar
Indian leader who converted to Buddhism in 1956 and inspired Dalit Buddhist movement.

## Navayana Buddhism
Modern Buddhist movement associated with Ambedkar.

## Dalit Buddhist Movement
Movement of oppressed caste communities adopting Buddhism for dignity and equality.

## Deekshabhoomi
Place in Nagpur where Ambedkar converted to Buddhism.

## Twenty-Two Vows
Vows taken by Ambedkarite Buddhists rejecting caste and Hindu ritualism.

## Neo-Buddhism
Another term for modern Ambedkarite Buddhism.

---

# 54. BUDDHIST TERMS IN PALI AND SANSKRIT

## Dhamma / Dharma
Teaching, truth, or law.

## Sangha / Samgha
Monastic community.

## Nibbana / Nirvana
Liberation.

## Kamma / Karma
Intentional action.

## Anicca / Anitya
Impermanence.

## Anatta / Anatman
No-self.

## Dukkha / Duhkha
Suffering.

## Tanha / Trishna
Craving.

## Sutta / Sutra
Discourse.

## Bhikkhu / Bhikshu
Monk.

## Bhikkhuni / Bhikshuni
Nun.

## Panna / Prajna
Wisdom.

## Sila / Shila
Morality.

## Samadhi / Samadhi
Concentration.

## Metta / Maitri
Loving-kindness.

## Karuna / Karuna
Compassion.

## Upekkha / Upeksha
Equanimity.

## Paticca Samuppada / Pratityasamutpada
Dependent origination.

## Jhana / Dhyana
Meditative absorption.

---

# 55. IMPORTANT BUDDHIST KINGS AND PATRONS

## Bimbisara
King of Magadha and early patron of Buddha.

## Ajatashatru
King of Magadha associated with Buddha’s later life and the First Council.

## Prasenajit
King of Kosala and supporter of Buddha.

## Ashoka
Mauryan emperor and greatest early royal patron of Buddhism.

## Milinda
Indo-Greek ruler Menander, associated with Milindapanha.

## Kanishka
Kushana ruler associated with Mahayana and the Fourth Council tradition.

## Harsha
North Indian ruler who patronized Buddhism and hosted religious assemblies.

## Dharmapala
Pala ruler and patron of Vikramashila.

## Devapala
Pala ruler and patron of Buddhist institutions.

## Kumaragupta
Gupta ruler associated with early Nalanda patronage.

## Anathapindika
Merchant donor of Jetavana monastery.

## Visakha
Important female lay donor.

## Ambapali
Lay supporter from Vaishali.

---

# 56. IMPORTANT BUDDHIST SCHOLARS

## Ashvaghosha
Buddhist poet and author of Buddhacharita.

## Nagarjuna
Founder of Madhyamaka philosophy.

## Aryadeva
Madhyamaka philosopher and disciple of Nagarjuna.

## Asanga
Founder figure of Yogachara school.

## Vasubandhu
Philosopher associated with Abhidharma and Yogachara.

## Buddhaghosa
Theravada commentator and author of Visuddhimagga.

## Dignaga
Buddhist logician.

## Dharmakirti
Buddhist philosopher and logician.

## Shantideva
Author of Bodhicharyavatara.

## Atisha
Indian Buddhist teacher important in Tibet.

## Padmasambhava
Tantric teacher important in Tibetan Buddhism.

## Chandrakirti
Important Madhyamaka philosopher.

## Shantarakshita
Indian Buddhist scholar who helped establish Buddhism in Tibet.

## Kamalashila
Buddhist philosopher associated with Tibetan debates.

## Buddhapalita
Madhyamaka philosopher.

## Bhavaviveka
Madhyamaka philosopher.

---

# 57. COMMONLY CONFUSED TERMS

## Buddha vs Bodhisattva
Buddha is fully enlightened. Bodhisattva is one who seeks Buddhahood, especially for all beings in Mahayana.

## Arhat vs Bodhisattva
Arhat seeks personal liberation. Bodhisattva seeks Buddhahood for the benefit of all beings.

## Nirvana vs Parinirvana
Nirvana is liberation from craving. Parinirvana is final passing away after death.

## Dhamma vs Sangha
Dhamma is Buddha’s teaching. Sangha is the monastic community.

## Sutta vs Sutra
Sutta is Pali; Sutra is Sanskrit. Both mean discourse.

## Tripitaka vs Three Jewels
Tripitaka is scripture. Three Jewels are Buddha, Dhamma, and Sangha.

## Stupa vs Chaitya
Stupa is a relic mound. Chaitya is a prayer hall, often containing a stupa.

## Chaitya vs Vihara
Chaitya is a worship hall. Vihara is a monastery or residence.

## Hinayana vs Theravada
Hinayana is a polemical Mahayana term. Theravada is a living Buddhist tradition.

## Mahayana vs Vajrayana
Mahayana emphasizes Bodhisattva path. Vajrayana is tantric Buddhism using mantra, mandala, and initiation.

## Gandhara vs Mathura
Gandhara shows Greco-Roman influence. Mathura shows indigenous Indian style.

## Anatta vs Atman
Buddhism teaches no permanent self. Upanishadic traditions teach Atman.

## Karma in Buddhism vs Jainism
Buddhism sees karma as intention. Jainism sees karma as subtle matter.

## Middle Path vs Severe Austerity
Buddhism avoids extremes. Jainism emphasizes severe austerity more strongly.

---

# 58. BUDDHISM VS JAINISM: UPSC COMPARISON

## Common Background
Both arose in the 6th century BCE Shramana context.

## Vedic Authority
Both rejected Vedic authority.

## Caste
Both questioned birth-based superiority.

## Soul
Buddhism rejects permanent soul. Jainism accepts eternal soul.

## Karma
Buddhism treats karma as intention. Jainism treats karma as material particles binding the soul.

## Austerity
Buddhism teaches Middle Path. Jainism emphasizes strict austerity.

## Ahimsa
Both value non-violence, but Jainism makes it more absolute.

## Monasticism
Both created organized monastic communities.

## Language
Buddhism used Pali and other Prakrits; Jainism used Ardhamagadhi and other Prakrits.

## Liberation
Buddhism aims at Nirvana. Jainism aims at Moksha or liberation of the soul.

## Founder
Buddhism was founded by Gautama Buddha. Jainism recognizes 24 Tirthankaras, with Mahavira as the 24th.

---

# 59. BUDDHISM VS BRAHMANISM: UPSC COMPARISON

## Vedas
Buddhism rejects Vedic authority.

## Sacrifice
Buddhism rejects animal sacrifice and ritualism as a path to liberation.

## Priesthood
Buddhism does not require Brahmana priests for liberation.

## Caste
Buddhism emphasizes conduct over birth.

## Atman
Buddhism rejects permanent Atman.

## Ritual vs Ethics
Buddhism emphasizes ethics, meditation, and wisdom over ritual.

## Creator God
Buddhism does not depend on a creator god.

## Renunciation
Buddhism gives importance to monastic renunciation.

## Lay Path
Buddhism also gives duties and merit-making practices for lay followers.

---

# 60. HIGH-YIELD LIFE EVENTS FOR UPSC

## Birth
Buddha was born at Lumbini.

## Clan
Buddha belonged to the Shakya clan.

## Father
Suddhodana.

## Mother
Mahamaya or Maya Devi.

## Foster Mother
Mahaprajapati Gotami.

## Wife
Yashodhara.

## Son
Rahula.

## Renunciation
Mahabhinishkramana.

## Enlightenment
Bodh Gaya under the Bodhi tree.

## First Sermon
Sarnath, Deer Park.

## First Sermon Name
Dhammacakkappavattana or Dharma Chakra Pravartana.

## Death
Mahaparinirvana at Kushinagar.

## Age at Enlightenment
Traditionally 35.

## Age at Mahaparinirvana
Traditionally 80.

## Teaching Career
Traditionally about 45 years.

---

# 61. HIGH-YIELD DOCTRINE CLUSTER

## Four Noble Truths
Dukkha, Samudaya, Nirodha, Magga.

## Eightfold Path
Right view, intention, speech, action, livelihood, effort, mindfulness, concentration.

## Three Jewels
Buddha, Dhamma, Sangha.

## Three Marks
Anicca, Dukkha, Anatta.

## Three Poisons
Greed, hatred, delusion.

## Five Aggregates
Form, feeling, perception, mental formations, consciousness.

## Five Precepts
No killing, no stealing, no sexual misconduct, no false speech, no intoxicants.

## Four Brahmaviharas
Loving-kindness, compassion, sympathetic joy, equanimity.

## Dependent Origination
Everything arises due to causes and conditions.

## Nirvana
End of craving and suffering.

---

# 62. HIGH-YIELD SCRIPTURE CLUSTER

## Tripitaka
Three baskets of Buddhist scriptures.

## Vinaya Pitaka
Monastic discipline.

## Sutta Pitaka
Discourses of Buddha.

## Abhidhamma Pitaka
Philosophical and doctrinal analysis.

## Dhammapada
Popular Buddhist verse text.

## Jataka
Stories of Buddha’s previous births.

## Milindapanha
Dialogue of Milinda and Nagasena.

## Buddhacharita
Life of Buddha by Ashvaghosha.

## Mahavamsa
Sri Lankan Buddhist chronicle.

## Dipavamsa
Sri Lankan Buddhist chronicle.

## Visuddhimagga
Theravada text by Buddhaghosa.

## Lotus Sutra
Important Mahayana text.

## Prajnaparamita Texts
Mahayana wisdom texts.

---

# 63. HIGH-YIELD COUNCIL CLUSTER

## First Council
Rajagriha; Mahakashyapa; Ananda recited Suttas; Upali recited Vinaya.

## Second Council
Vaishali; dispute over monastic rules.

## Third Council
Pataliputra; Ashoka; Moggaliputta Tissa; associated with missions.

## Fourth Council
Kanishka; Kashmir region; associated with Sarvastivada tradition.

## Theravada Canon Written
Pali Canon written down in Sri Lanka according to Theravada tradition.

---

# 64. HIGH-YIELD SECT CLUSTER

## Theravada
Doctrine of elders; Pali Canon; Arhat ideal.

## Mahayana
Great Vehicle; Bodhisattva ideal; compassion and universal Buddhahood.

## Vajrayana
Tantric Buddhism; mantra, mandala, mudra, guru, deity yoga.

## Sarvastivada
School teaching existence of dharmas in past, present, and future.

## Madhyamaka
Nagarjuna’s school of emptiness.

## Yogachara
Consciousness-only school associated with Asanga and Vasubandhu.

## Zen
East Asian meditation tradition derived from Chan Buddhism.

## Chan
Chinese meditation Buddhism.

## Pure Land
Mahayana devotional tradition centered on Amitabha.

---

# 65. HIGH-YIELD ART AND ARCHITECTURE CLUSTER

## Stupa
Relic mound.

## Chaitya
Prayer hall.

## Vihara
Monastery.

## Sanchi
Great Stupa and toranas.

## Bharhut
Early stupa railings and aniconic art.

## Amaravati
Limestone reliefs and major stupa.

## Gandhara
Greco-Buddhist art.

## Mathura
Indigenous Indian Buddha images.

## Ajanta
Buddhist cave paintings.

## Karle
Great chaitya hall.

## Nalanda
Buddhist university.

## Dholak-shaped Stupa
Not a standard UPSC term; avoid confusing with ordinary stupa forms.

## Torana
Decorative gateway.

## Vedika
Railing.

## Harmika
Square railing above stupa dome.

## Chhatra
Umbrella above stupa.

---

# 66. CHRONOLOGICAL SNAPSHOT

## Stage 1: Pre-Buddhist Background
The 6th century BCE saw urbanization, Mahajanapadas, merchant growth, and Shramana movements questioning Vedic ritualism.

## Stage 2: Birth and Early Life
Siddhartha Gautama was born at Lumbini in the Shakya clan and lived in Kapilavastu.

## Stage 3: Renunciation
After seeing old age, sickness, death, and an ascetic, Siddhartha renounced palace life.

## Stage 4: Enlightenment
After rejecting extreme austerity, Siddhartha attained enlightenment at Bodh Gaya and became Buddha.

## Stage 5: First Sermon
Buddha preached the Four Noble Truths and Middle Path at Sarnath.

## Stage 6: Sangha Formation
The community of monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen developed around Buddha’s teaching.

## Stage 7: Mahaparinirvana
Buddha attained Mahaparinirvana at Kushinagar at the age of 80 according to tradition.

## Stage 8: Councils and Canon Formation
Teachings were preserved through councils and oral recitation, later forming the Tripitaka.

## Stage 9: Mauryan Patronage
Ashoka gave major support to Buddhism and helped spread it through missions and monuments.

## Stage 10: Sectarian Development
Early schools developed, followed by Theravada, Mahayana, and Vajrayana traditions.

## Stage 11: Artistic Expansion
Buddhist art flourished at Sanchi, Bharhut, Gandhara, Mathura, Amaravati, Ajanta, and many cave sites.

## Stage 12: Monastic Universities
Nalanda, Vikramashila, Odantapuri, Somapura, and other centers became major seats of learning.

## Stage 13: Spread Beyond India
Buddhism spread to Sri Lanka, Central Asia, China, Southeast Asia, Korea, Japan, Tibet, and Mongolia.

## Stage 14: Decline and Survival
Buddhism declined in much of India but survived in Himalayan regions and flourished outside India.

## Stage 15: Modern Revival
Buddhism revived in modern India through Mahabodhi movement and Ambedkar’s Navayana movement.

---

# 67. FINAL REVISION CLUSTER FOR UPSC PRELIMS

## Must Remember Identity
Buddhism is a Shramana, Nastika, non-Vedic tradition founded by Gautama Buddha.

## Must Remember Buddha’s Four Sites
Lumbini, Bodh Gaya, Sarnath, Kushinagar.

## Must Remember Core Teaching
Four Noble Truths and Noble Eightfold Path.

## Must Remember Middle Path
Buddhism avoids both luxury and extreme austerity.

## Must Remember Three Jewels
Buddha, Dhamma, Sangha.

## Must Remember Three Marks
Anicca, Dukkha, Anatta.

## Must Remember No-Soul Doctrine
Buddhism denies permanent Atman.

## Must Remember Dependent Origination
All things arise due to causes and conditions.

## Must Remember Tripitaka
Vinaya Pitaka, Sutta Pitaka, Abhidhamma Pitaka.

## Must Remember Councils
Rajagriha, Vaishali, Pataliputra, and Kanishka-associated Kashmir council.

## Must Remember Ashoka
Greatest royal patron; associated with Third Council, missions, stupas, edicts, and Dhamma.

## Must Remember Sects
Theravada, Mahayana, Vajrayana.

## Must Remember Philosophy
Madhyamaka by Nagarjuna; Yogachara by Asanga and Vasubandhu.

## Must Remember Art
Sanchi, Bharhut, Gandhara, Mathura, Amaravati, Ajanta.

## Must Remember Architecture
Stupa, Chaitya, Vihara, Torana, Vedika, Harmika, Chhatra.

## Must Remember Universities
Nalanda, Vikramashila, Odantapuri, Somapura, Taxila.

## Must Remember Pilgrims
Faxian, Xuanzang, Yijing.

## Must Remember Comparison with Jainism
Buddhism rejects permanent soul and severe austerity; Jainism accepts soul and emphasizes stricter austerity.

## Must Remember One-Line Essence
Buddhism teaches that suffering arises from craving and ignorance, and can end through the Middle Path of morality, meditation, and wisdom, leading to Nirvana.

---



# RISE OF MAHAJANAPADAS, MAGADHA, AND PRE-MAURYAN DYNASTIES
## UPSC PRELIMS GLOSSARY
## Chronological Coverage: Later Vedic Transition → Janapadas → Mahajanapadas → Second Urbanization → Rise of Magadha → Haryanka → Shishunaga → Nanda → Alexander and Immediate Pre-Mauryan Context

> Note:
> This glossary focuses on the period before Chandragupta Maurya.
> It covers the rise of Mahajanapadas, the emergence of Magadha, republican and monarchical states, early urbanization, economy, society, religion, and the dynasties that ruled Magadha before the Mauryas.

---

# 1. BASIC CHRONOLOGICAL FRAMEWORK

## Later Vedic Period
The period after the Early Rigvedic age when society moved eastward into the Ganga-Yamuna plains, agriculture expanded, iron use increased, and larger political units developed.

## Janapada Period
The stage when tribes settled in specific territories. The word Janapada means “foothold of a tribe”.

## Mahajanapada Period
The period around the 6th century BCE when sixteen large territorial states emerged in north India.

## Second Urbanization
The rise of towns and cities in the Ganga valley after the Harappan urban phase. It is called the second urbanization of the Indian subcontinent.

## Early Historic Period
The period beginning around the 6th century BCE, marked by cities, states, writing, coins, trade, and religious movements.

## Pre-Mauryan Period
The period before the rise of Chandragupta Maurya and the Mauryan Empire.

## Sixth Century BCE
A major turning point in ancient India marked by Mahajanapadas, urbanization, iron use, coinage, trade, Jainism, Buddhism, and powerful kingdoms.

## Fifth Century BCE
The period when Magadha expanded under rulers like Bimbisara and Ajatashatru.

## Fourth Century BCE
The period of Nanda power, Alexander’s invasion, and the rise of Chandragupta Maurya.

---

# 2. FROM JANA TO JANAPADA TO MAHAJANAPADA

## Jana
A tribe or people. In the Vedic period, political identity was mainly tribal.

## Janapada
A territory settled by a tribe or people. It marks the shift from tribal identity to territorial identity.

## Mahajanapada
A large and powerful Janapada. Sixteen Mahajanapadas are mentioned in Buddhist and Jain texts.

## Territorial State
A state based on control over land and population rather than only clan or tribe.

## Tribe
A kinship-based group claiming common ancestry.

## Clan
A smaller kinship group within a tribe.

## Chiefdom
A political system led by a chief, less complex than a kingdom.

## Kingdom
A territorial state ruled by a king.

## Monarchy
A political system in which power is held by a king.

## Gana
A corporate political group or assembly-based polity.

## Sangha
A republican or oligarchic political organization, especially in the context of Gana-Sanghas.

## Gana-Sangha
A republican or oligarchic state where power was held by a group of chiefs or clan elders rather than a single hereditary king.

## Republic
A political system where decision-making is shared among a group of members, not concentrated in one monarch.

## Oligarchy
Rule by a small group of powerful families or clans.

## Clan Oligarchy
A state ruled by leading clans, common among some Gana-Sanghas.

## Sabha
An assembly or council. In the Mahajanapada age, assemblies survived especially in republican states.

## Samiti
A broader assembly known from Vedic tradition; its importance declined in monarchies.

## Parishad
Council of advisers or elders.

## Raja
King.

## Maharaja
Great king.

## Samrat
Emperor or overlord.

## Senapati
Military commander.

## Purohita
Priest and adviser of a king.

## Amatya
Minister or high official.

## Duta
Messenger or envoy.

## Rashtra
Territory or kingdom.

## Rajya
Rule or kingdom.

---

# 3. CAUSES FOR THE RISE OF MAHAJANAPADAS

## Iron Technology
Use of iron tools helped forest clearance, agriculture, warfare, and territorial expansion.

## Iron Ploughshare
Iron part of a plough that helped deeper cultivation in the fertile Ganga plains.

## Forest Clearance
Removal of forests to create agricultural land, especially in the middle Ganga valley.

## Agricultural Expansion
Increase in farming due to iron tools, fertile soil, rainfall, and settled life.

## Rice Cultivation
Rice became important in the middle Ganga valley and supported larger populations.

## Surplus Production
