Extra agricultural produce beyond immediate consumption. It supported towns, armies, officials, artisans, and rulers.

## Population Growth
Increase in population due to better agriculture and settled life.

## Sedentary Life
Permanent settlement in villages and towns.

## Urbanization
Growth of towns and cities with trade, crafts, administration, and religious activity.

## Trade Expansion
Growth of exchange within and between regions.

## Coinage
Use of coins helped trade, taxation, and payments.

## Punch-Marked Coins
Early coins with symbols punched onto metal pieces, especially silver.

## Guilds
Associations of merchants or artisans that regulated trade and craft production.

## Shreni
A guild or professional association of merchants or craftsmen.

## Setthi
A wealthy merchant, banker, or financier.

## Gahapati
A wealthy householder, landowner, or rural elite.

## Taxation
Collection of revenue by the state from agriculture, trade, and other activities.

## Standing Army
A permanent army maintained by the state, unlike temporary tribal militias.

## Fortification
Construction of walls and defenses around cities and capitals.

## Administrative Organization
Development of officials, revenue systems, armies, and law enforcement.

## New Religious Movements
Jainism, Buddhism, Ajivikas, and other Shramana traditions emerged in this period.

## Decline of Tribal Polity
Tribal assemblies lost importance in monarchies as kingship became stronger.

---

# 4. SECOND URBANIZATION

## Second Urbanization
The rise of towns and cities in the Ganga valley around the 6th century BCE.

## First Urbanization
The Harappan urban civilization. The second urbanization came much later.

## Ganga Valley Urbanization
Growth of towns in the middle Ganga plains due to agriculture, trade, and political power.

## Urban Centre
A town or city with craft production, trade, administration, and dense population.

## Nagar
Town or city.

## Nagara
Urban settlement.

## Pura
Fortified town or city.

## Durga
Fort or fortified settlement.

## Nigama
Market town or trading settlement.

## Mahanagara
Large city.

## Rajadhani
Capital city.

## Pataligrama
The village that later developed into Pataliputra.

## Pataliputra
Capital of Magadha under later rulers. It became one of the greatest cities of ancient India.

## Rajagriha
Early capital of Magadha, located among hills.

## Girivraja
Another name for Rajagriha, meaning “enclosed by hills”.

## Vaishali
Capital of the Vajji confederacy and an important city of the period.

## Kaushambi
Capital of Vatsa and a major urban center.

## Ujjain
Capital of Avanti and an important trade and political center.

## Varanasi
Capital of Kashi and an important religious and commercial city.

## Shravasti
Capital of Kosala and an important Buddhist center.

## Champa
Capital of Anga and an important commercial city.

## Taxila
Capital or major city of Gandhara, famous as a learning and trade center.

## Mathura
Capital of Shurasena and an important city on trade routes.

## Northern Black Polished Ware
A fine, glossy pottery associated with the second urbanization and early historic urban culture.

## NBPW
Short form of Northern Black Polished Ware.

## Urban Craft Production
Specialized production of goods like pottery, metal objects, textiles, beads, and tools.

## Marketplace
An area where goods were bought and sold.

## Trade Route
A path used for movement of goods, merchants, and ideas.

## Uttarapatha
The northern trade route connecting the north-west with the Ganga valley.

## Dakshinapatha
The southern trade route connecting north India with the Deccan and south India.

---

# 5. ECONOMIC TERMS OF THE MAHAJANAPADA PERIOD

## Agrarian Economy
An economy mainly based on agriculture.

## Wet Rice Cultivation
Rice farming using water-rich fields, important in the middle Ganga valley.

## Plough Agriculture
Farming using ploughs, often pulled by oxen.

## Land Revenue
Tax collected from agricultural produce.

## Bali
Tribute or offering to the king; became more regular as states developed.

## Bhaga
The king’s share of agricultural produce.

## Kara
Tax or compulsory payment.

## Shulka
Toll or customs duty.

## Hiranya
Payment in gold or money.

## Tax Collector
Official responsible for collecting revenue.

## Royal Treasury
State store of wealth collected through taxes, tribute, and conquest.

## Kosa
Treasury.

## Panya
Commodity or trade good.

## Vanij
Merchant or trader.

## Sarthavaha
Caravan leader or chief of merchants.

## Sartha
Caravan of merchants.

## Setthi
Wealthy merchant or banker.

## Gahapati
Wealthy householder or landholding elite.

## Shreni
Guild or association of traders or artisans.

## Artisan
Skilled craft worker.

## Kammara
Smith or metalworker.

## Kumbhakara
Potter.

## Vaddhaki
Carpenter.

## Suvannakara
Goldsmith.

## Tantuvaya
Weaver.

## Leather Worker
Craftsperson working with hides and leather.

## Banker
Person who stored money, financed trade, or lent wealth.

## Money Economy
An economy using coins or metal currency for exchange.

## Barter
Exchange of goods without money.

## Punch-Marked Coin
Early coin with symbols punched on it, usually made of silver.

## Karshapana
A common early coin, often silver punch-marked.

## Mashaka
A small coin or unit of value.

## Nishka
An older term for gold ornament or value object, gradually replaced by coin terms.

## Pana
A coin or monetary unit.

## Silver Coinage
Silver punch-marked coins became common in trade and taxation.

## Market Regulation
Rules or practices controlling trade, prices, weights, and taxes.

## Weights and Measures
Systems used for measuring goods in trade.

## Trade Tax
Tax imposed on goods or merchants.

## Toll Station
A place where merchants paid taxes on goods.

---

# 6. SOCIAL BACKGROUND OF THE MAHAJANAPADA PERIOD

## Varna System
The fourfold social order of Brahmana, Kshatriya, Vaishya, and Shudra.

## Brahmana
Priestly and learned varna.

## Kshatriya
Warrior and ruling varna.

## Vaishya
Producer varna associated with agriculture, cattle-rearing, and trade.

## Shudra
Service varna.

## Jati
Birth-based social group or caste-like community.

## Gahapati Class
Wealthy householders and landowners who became socially important.

## Merchant Class
Traders and bankers who gained influence due to urbanization.

## Artisan Class
Craft workers who became important in towns.

## Urban Elite
Rich merchants, officials, landowners, and religious patrons.

## Rural Elite
Powerful landholders and householders in villages.

## Kshatriya Assertion
Rise of ruling warrior groups who challenged Brahmanical dominance in some contexts.

## Brahmanical Ritual Order
Social and religious system based on Vedic ritual and Brahmana authority.

## Shramana Challenge
Challenge posed by Jainism, Buddhism, Ajivikas, and other renunciant movements to Vedic ritualism.

## Slavery
Forms of servitude existed, though ancient Indian slavery differed from Greco-Roman slavery.

## Dasa
Servant, slave, or dependent person.

## Kammakara
Labourer or worker.

## Peasant
Agricultural cultivator.

## Landholder
Person controlling agricultural land.

## Clan Aristocracy
Powerful clan-based elites in republican states.

---

# 7. RELIGIOUS AND INTELLECTUAL BACKGROUND

## Shramana Tradition
Renunciant traditions that emphasized asceticism, meditation, karma, rebirth, and liberation.

## Jainism
Religion associated with Mahavira, emphasizing non-violence, austerity, and liberation of the soul.

## Buddhism
Religion founded by Gautama Buddha, emphasizing the Middle Path, Four Noble Truths, and Nirvana.

## Ajivika
A Shramana sect associated with Makkhali Gosala, emphasizing fate or determinism.

## Charvaka
Materialist school that rejected afterlife, karma, and Vedic authority.

## Lokayata
Another name for materialist thought.

## Brahmanism
Vedic ritual tradition based on sacrifice, varna, and Brahmanical authority.

## Upanishadic Thought
Philosophical tradition focusing on Brahman, Atman, karma, rebirth, and liberation.

## Karma
Action and its consequences, central to many religious traditions of the period.

## Samsara
Cycle of birth, death, and rebirth.

## Moksha
Liberation from rebirth.

## Nirvana
Liberation in Buddhism.

## Ahimsa
Non-violence, especially central to Jainism and important in Buddhism.

## Renunciation
Leaving household life for spiritual pursuit.

## Parivrajaka
Wandering ascetic or seeker.

## Tapas
Austerity or spiritual discipline.

## Debate Culture
Public philosophical debates among teachers of different traditions.

## Royal Patronage of Religions
Kings and elites supported monks, teachers, and religious communities.

---

# 8. SOURCES FOR THE MAHAJANAPADA PERIOD

## Buddhist Texts
Texts such as the Anguttara Nikaya mention the sixteen Mahajanapadas.

## Anguttara Nikaya
A Buddhist text that gives a list of sixteen Mahajanapadas.

## Digha Nikaya
Buddhist text containing political and social information of the period.

## Majjhima Nikaya
Buddhist text useful for understanding early society and religious life.

## Vinaya Pitaka
Buddhist monastic text containing information about cities, rulers, merchants, and society.

## Jataka Stories
Buddhist stories of previous births that contain social and economic information, though not always historically direct.

## Jain Texts
Texts like Bhagavati Sutra provide information about Mahajanapadas and contemporary society.

## Bhagavati Sutra
Jain text that mentions important political and religious details.

## Acharanga Sutra
Jain text associated with Mahavira’s life and monastic conduct.

## Sutrakritanga
Jain text that reflects debates with other doctrines.

## Puranas
Later Brahmanical texts that preserve dynastic lists, though with legendary material.

## Mahabharata
Epic text containing memories of early polities, lineages, and places.

## Panini’s Ashtadhyayi
A grammar text that provides evidence about Janapadas, social groups, and political terms.

## Ashtadhyayi
Panini’s grammar, important for linguistic and historical information.

## Archaeology
Material evidence such as pottery, coins, fortifications, settlements, and inscriptions.

## Northern Black Polished Ware
Archaeological marker of urbanization in the Ganga valley.

## Punch-Marked Coins
Important archaeological evidence of early money economy.

## Greek Accounts
Accounts related to Alexander’s invasion and north-western India.

## Megasthenes
Greek ambassador later at Chandragupta Maurya’s court; useful more for Mauryan India, but sometimes relevant for earlier context.

## Herodotus
Greek historian who mentions India in relation to the Persian Empire.

## Arrian
Greek writer who described Alexander’s campaigns.

## Strabo
Greek geographer whose writings preserve information about India from earlier sources.

## Curtius
Roman historian who wrote about Alexander’s campaigns.

---

# 9. SIXTEEN MAHAJANAPADAS: BASIC LIST

## Sixteen Mahajanapadas
The sixteen major states mentioned in early Buddhist texts.

## Anga
Mahajanapada in eastern India, with capital at Champa.

## Magadha
Powerful Mahajanapada in present-day Bihar, which later became the base of major empires.

## Kashi
Mahajanapada centered around Varanasi.

## Kosala
Powerful Mahajanapada with capitals at Shravasti and Ayodhya/Saketa.

## Vajji
Republican confederacy with capital at Vaishali.

## Malla
Republican Mahajanapada associated with Kushinagar and Pava.

## Chedi
Mahajanapada in central India.

## Vatsa
Mahajanapada with capital at Kaushambi.

## Kuru
Mahajanapada in the Delhi-Meerut region, earlier important in the Vedic period.

## Panchala
Mahajanapada in western Uttar Pradesh.

## Matsya
Mahajanapada in the Rajasthan region.

## Shurasena
Mahajanapada centered around Mathura.

## Ashmaka
Mahajanapada located in the Deccan region on the Godavari.

## Avanti
Powerful Mahajanapada in western India, with capital at Ujjain and Mahishmati.

## Gandhara
North-western Mahajanapada with capital at Taxila.

## Kamboja
North-western Mahajanapada, associated with horses and trans-regional trade.

---

# 10. ANGUTTARA NIKAYA LIST OF MAHAJANAPADAS

## Anguttara Nikaya List
A Buddhist list of sixteen Mahajanapadas important for UPSC.

## Anga in Anguttara Nikaya
Eastern Mahajanapada near Magadha.

## Magadha in Anguttara Nikaya
Most important rising power.

## Kashi in Anguttara Nikaya
Famous for Varanasi and trade.

## Kosala in Anguttara Nikaya
Powerful kingdom competing with Magadha.

## Vajji in Anguttara Nikaya
Republican confederacy.

## Malla in Anguttara Nikaya
Republican state.

## Chedi in Anguttara Nikaya
Central Indian state.

## Vatsa in Anguttara Nikaya
Kingdom centered at Kaushambi.

## Kuru in Anguttara Nikaya
Old Vedic region turned Mahajanapada.

## Panchala in Anguttara Nikaya
Important state of western Uttar Pradesh.

## Matsya in Anguttara Nikaya
State in Rajasthan.

## Shurasena in Anguttara Nikaya
State centered at Mathura.

## Ashmaka in Anguttara Nikaya
Only Mahajanapada located in the Deccan.

## Avanti in Anguttara Nikaya
Major western power.

## Gandhara in Anguttara Nikaya
North-western state.

## Kamboja in Anguttara Nikaya
North-western state linked with horses and trade.

---

# 11. MAHAJANAPADAS: CAPITALS AND LOCATIONS

## Anga Capital
Champa.

## Magadha Capital
Initially Rajagriha, later Pataliputra.

## Kashi Capital
Varanasi.

## Kosala Capital
Shravasti; Ayodhya/Saketa was also important.

## Vajji Capital
Vaishali.

## Malla Capitals
Kushinagar and Pava.

## Chedi Capital
Suktimati, according to tradition.

## Vatsa Capital
Kaushambi.

## Kuru Capital
Indraprastha or Hastinapura in different traditions.

## Panchala Capitals
Ahichhatra in northern Panchala and Kampilya in southern Panchala.

## Matsya Capital
Viratanagara, usually identified with Bairat region.

## Shurasena Capital
Mathura.

## Ashmaka Capital
Potana or Potali, associated with the Godavari region.

## Avanti Capitals
Ujjain in northern Avanti and Mahishmati in southern Avanti.

## Gandhara Capital
Taxila.

## Kamboja Capital
Rajapura according to some traditions.

---

# 12. ANGА MAHAJANAPADA

## Anga
An eastern Mahajanapada located around present-day eastern Bihar and parts of Bengal.

## Champa
Capital of Anga and an important commercial city.

## Anga-Magadha Rivalry
Anga and Magadha competed before Anga was conquered by Magadha.

## Bimbisara’s Conquest of Anga
Bimbisara conquered Anga and annexed it to Magadha.

## Champa as Trade Centre
Champa was an important city connected with riverine trade.

## Anga in Jain Tradition
Anga is mentioned in Jain texts and was connected with Mahavira’s travels.

## Anga in Buddhist Tradition
Anga appears in Buddhist texts as an important region.

---

# 13. MAGADHA MAHAJANAPADA

## Magadha
The most important Mahajanapada. It became the foundation of the Mauryan Empire.

## Rajagriha
Early capital of Magadha, located in a naturally protected hill region.

## Girivraja
Old name of Rajagriha.

## Pataliputra
Later capital of Magadha, located near the confluence of major rivers.

## Pataligrama
Earlier settlement that developed into Pataliputra.

## Magadha’s Natural Resources
Magadha had fertile soil, forests, iron ore, elephants, and river routes.

## Magadha’s Strategic Location
Magadha controlled important routes and river systems.

## Magadha’s Expansion
Magadha expanded by conquest, marriage alliances, diplomacy, and control of resources.

## Magadhan Imperialism
The process by which Magadha conquered and absorbed neighboring states.

## Magadha-Anga Conflict
Conflict ending with Anga’s annexation by Magadha.

## Magadha-Kosala Conflict
Conflict involving Kashi and royal marriages.

## Magadha-Vajji Conflict
Major war between Ajatashatru and the Vajji confederacy.

## Magadha-Avanti Rivalry
Conflict between Magadha and Avanti before Avanti was eventually absorbed.

---

# 14. KASHI MAHAJANAPADA

## Kashi
A Mahajanapada centered on Varanasi.

## Varanasi
Capital of Kashi and an important trade, textile, and religious city.

## Kashi-Kosala Rivalry
Kashi and Kosala fought for dominance.

## Kashi as Dowry
Kashi was given as dowry in a marriage alliance between Kosala and Magadha.

## Kashi Revenue
The revenue of Kashi became a source of conflict between Magadha and Kosala.

## Kashi Textiles
Kashi was famous for fine textiles and trade.

## Kashi in Buddhist Texts
Kashi appears frequently in Buddhist literature.

---

# 15. KOSALA MAHAJANAPADA

## Kosala
A powerful kingdom in the middle Ganga region.

## Shravasti
Capital of Kosala and an important Buddhist center.

## Saketa
Another important city of Kosala, associated with Ayodhya.

## Ayodhya
Ancient city associated with Kosala.

## Prasenajit
Important king of Kosala and contemporary of Buddha.

## Pasenadi
Pali name of Prasenajit.

## Kosala-Magadha Marriage Alliance
Bimbisara married Kosaladevi, sister of Prasenajit.

## Kosaladevi
Princess of Kosala married to Bimbisara.

## Kashi Dowry
Kashi was given to Bimbisara as dowry in his marriage to Kosaladevi.

## Vidudabha
Son of Prasenajit, associated with conflict involving the Shakyas.

## Kosala-Shakya Relationship
The Shakyas were connected with Kosala’s political sphere.

## Kosala-Magadha Conflict
Conflict after Ajatashatru killed Bimbisara and dowry issues arose.

---

# 16. VAJJI MAHAJANAPADA

## Vajji
A powerful republican confederacy in north Bihar.

## Vajji Confederacy
A union of clans including Licchavis, Videhas, and others.

## Vaishali
Capital of Vajji and one of the most important republican cities.

## Licchavi
A powerful clan of the Vajji confederacy.

## Videha
A clan/region that became part of the Vajji confederacy.

## Jnatrika
Clan associated with Mahavira, linked with the Vajji region.

## Vajji Republic
An oligarchic republican system with assemblies and clan chiefs.

## Vajji Assembly
Political assembly of the Vajji confederacy.

## Ajatashatru’s War with Vajji
A long war in which Magadha defeated the Vajji confederacy.

## Vassakara
Ajatashatru’s minister who allegedly helped weaken the Vajji confederacy through diplomacy.

## Sunidha
A Magadhan minister associated with fortifying Pataligrama.

## Pataligrama Fortification
Magadha fortified Pataligrama during the war against Vajji.

## Seven Conditions of Vajji Strength
Buddhist texts mention conditions such as regular assemblies, unity, respect for elders, and protection of women and shrines as reasons for Vajji strength.

## Republican Decline
The defeat of Vajji marked the decline of strong republican polities in the eastern Ganga region.

---

# 17. MALLA MAHAJANAPADA

## Malla
A republican Mahajanapada in eastern Uttar Pradesh.

## Kushinagar
One capital of the Mallas and the place of Buddha’s Mahaparinirvana.

## Pava
Another Malla center, associated with Jain and Buddhist traditions.

## Malla Republic
A Gana-Sangha polity ruled by clan chiefs.

## Mallas and Buddha
The Mallas received a share of Buddha’s relics after his Mahaparinirvana.

## Mallas and Mahavira
Pava is associated with Mahavira’s final days in some traditions.

---

# 18. CHEDI MAHAJANAPADA

## Chedi
A Mahajanapada located in central India, possibly around Bundelkhand.

## Suktimati
Traditional capital of Chedi.

## Chedi in Epic Tradition
Chedi is mentioned in the Mahabharata and other traditions.

## Chedi Location
Generally associated with parts of present-day Madhya Pradesh and Uttar Pradesh.

---

# 19. VATSA MAHAJANAPADA

## Vatsa
A Mahajanapada located around the lower Yamuna region.

## Kaushambi
Capital of Vatsa and an important city near the Yamuna River.

## Udayana
Famous king of Vatsa, known from Buddhist, Jain, and Sanskrit literary traditions.

## Vatsa-Avanti Rivalry
Vatsa and Avanti had political conflicts.

## Kaushambi as Trade Centre
Kaushambi was located on important trade routes and became a major urban center.

## Ghoshitarama
A monastery at Kaushambi donated by the banker Ghoshita.

## Ghoshita
A wealthy merchant and Buddhist patron in Kaushambi.

## Udayana Legends
Stories about King Udayana appear in Buddhist, Jain, and Sanskrit drama traditions.

---

# 20. KURU MAHAJANAPADA

## Kuru
An old Vedic region that became one of the Mahajanapadas.

## Indraprastha
A traditional Kuru capital.

## Hastinapura
An old Kuru center associated with Vedic and epic traditions.

## Kuru Decline
By the Mahajanapada period, Kuru had lost its earlier Vedic political dominance.

## Kuru in Buddhist Texts
Kuru appears as a region known for disciplined people and ethical stories.

---

# 21. PANCHALA MAHAJANAPADA

## Panchala
Mahajanapada located in western Uttar Pradesh.

## Northern Panchala
Part of Panchala with capital at Ahichhatra.

## Southern Panchala
Part of Panchala with capital at Kampilya.

## Ahichhatra
Capital of northern Panchala.

## Kampilya
Capital of southern Panchala.

## Panchala in Vedic Tradition
Panchala was an important center of Later Vedic learning.

## Panchala in Mahajanapada Period
By the 6th century BCE, Panchala was less dominant than Magadha, Kosala, Avanti, and Vatsa.

---

# 22. MATSYA MAHAJANAPADA

## Matsya
Mahajanapada located in the Rajasthan region.

## Viratanagara
Capital of Matsya, often identified with Bairat.

## Bairat
Archaeological site associated with ancient Viratanagara.

## Matsya Location
Region around Jaipur-Alwar-Bharatpur area in Rajasthan.

## Matsya in Epic Tradition
Associated with King Virata in Mahabharata tradition.

---

# 23. SHURASENA MAHAJANAPADA

## Shurasena
Mahajanapada centered around Mathura.

## Mathura
Capital of Shurasena and an important urban, trade, and religious center.

## Avantiputra
A ruler of Shurasena mentioned in Buddhist tradition.

## Shurasena and Buddhism
Mathura later became a major Buddhist, Jain, and Brahmanical center.

## Shurasena and Trade
Mathura was located on important trade routes connecting north India, western India, and the Deccan.

---

# 24. ASHMAKA MAHAJANAPADA

## Ashmaka
A Mahajanapada located in the Deccan, usually along the Godavari River.

## Assaka
Pali form of Ashmaka.

## Potana
Capital of Ashmaka according to some traditions.

## Potali
Another name associated with Ashmaka’s capital.

## Godavari Region
The river region associated with Ashmaka.

## Only Deccan Mahajanapada
Ashmaka is often noted as the only Mahajanapada located in the Deccan.

## Ashmaka and Dakshinapatha
Ashmaka was connected with the southern trade route.

---

# 25. AVANTI MAHAJANAPADA

## Avanti
A powerful Mahajanapada in western India.

## Ujjain
Capital of northern Avanti and an important city on trade routes.

## Mahishmati
Capital of southern Avanti.

## Pradyota Dynasty
Dynasty that ruled Avanti before its absorption into Magadha.

## Chanda Pradyota
Famous ruler of Avanti and contemporary of Bimbisara and Udayana.

## Avanti-Magadha Rivalry
Avanti was one of Magadha’s major rivals before being absorbed.

## Avanti-Vatsa Conflict
Avanti and Vatsa competed for power in central India.

## Ujjain as Trade Centre
Ujjain was important for trade between north India, western India, and the Deccan.

## Avanti and Buddhism
Avanti was connected with early Buddhist missionary activity.

## Mahakaccana
A disciple of Buddha associated with preaching in Avanti.

---

# 26. GANDHARA MAHAJANAPADA

## Gandhara
North-western Mahajanapada located around present-day north Pakistan and eastern Afghanistan.

## Taxila
Capital or major city of Gandhara, famous for learning and trade.

## Takshashila
Sanskrit form of Taxila.

## Pushkalavati
Another important city of Gandhara.

## Gandhara and Uttarapatha
Gandhara lay on the northern trade route.

## Gandhara and Persian Empire
Gandhara came under Achaemenid Persian influence.

## Gandhara and Learning
Taxila was a famous center of learning.

## Pukkusati
King of Gandhara mentioned in Buddhist tradition.

## Gandhara as Gateway
Gandhara served as a gateway between India, Central Asia, and Iran.

---

# 27. KAMBOJA MAHAJANAPADA

## Kamboja
North-western Mahajanapada associated with Afghanistan and adjoining regions.

## Kamboja Horses
Kamboja was famous for horses.

## Kamboja and Uttarapatha
Kamboja was connected with the northern trade route.

## Kamboja Polity
Some texts suggest Kamboja had republican or oligarchic features.

## Rajapura
Traditional capital associated with Kamboja.

## Kamboja and Iranic Contacts
Kamboja was located near regions with Iranian cultural influence.

---

# 28. MONARCHIES AND REPUBLICS

## Monarchical Mahajanapadas
States ruled by kings, such as Magadha, Kosala, Vatsa, Avanti, Kashi, and Anga.

## Republican Mahajanapadas
States governed by assemblies or oligarchic clans, such as Vajji and Malla.

## Gana-Sangha Polity
Political system based on assembly rule by clans.

## Raja in Republics
In some republics, several chiefs were called rajas, but they were not absolute monarchs.

## Clan Assembly
Assembly of clan heads in a republican state.

## Santhagara
Assembly hall of a republican polity.

## Licchavi Assembly
The political assembly of the Licchavi clan.

## Malla Assembly
The assembly of the Malla republic.

## Shakya Republic
The republican polity of Buddha’s clan, under Kosala’s influence.

## Koliya Republic
A republican clan related to the Shakyas.

## Moriya Republic
A clan republic associated with Pipphalivana; later tradition links it to the Mauryas.

## Bulis
A republican clan that received Buddha’s relics.

## Kalamas
A republican clan associated with Kesaputta and Buddha’s teachings.

## Republican Weakness
Republics could be weakened by internal divisions and diplomacy, as seen in Ajatashatru’s policy toward Vajji.

## Republican Strength
Unity, regular assemblies, respect for law, and clan solidarity made republics strong.

---

# 29. IMPORTANT NON-MAHAJANAPADA REPUBLICAN CLANS

## Shakyas
Republican clan of Buddha, located near Kapilavastu.

## Kapilavastu
Capital of the Shakyas.

## Koliyas
Republican clan related to the Shakyas.

## Ramagrama
Koliya center associated with Buddha’s relics.

## Moriyas
Republican clan of Pipphalivana, later linked with the Maurya name.

## Pipphalivana
Settlement associated with the Moriyas.

## Kalamas
Republican clan associated with Kesaputta.

## Kesaputta
Town associated with the Kalamas.

## Bulis
Republican clan of Allakappa.

## Allakappa
Settlement of the Bulis.

## Bhaggas
A clan group associated with Sumsumaragiri.

## Sumsumaragiri
Settlement associated with the Bhaggas.

---

# 30. WHY MAGADHA ROSE TO POWER

## Fertile Alluvial Soil
Magadha had fertile soil suitable for agriculture and surplus production.

## Iron Ore
Magadha had access to iron ore from nearby regions, especially south Bihar and Jharkhand.

## Forest Resources
Forests provided timber, elephants, and other resources.

## Elephants
War elephants gave Magadha a military advantage.

## River Network
Magadha was connected by rivers such as Ganga, Son, Gandak, and Champa.

## Ganga River
Major river route that helped transport, trade, and agriculture.

## Son River
Important river near Magadha and Pataliputra.

## Gandak River
River near the Magadha-Vajji region.

## Champa River
River associated with Anga and eastern trade.

## Control of Trade Routes
Magadha controlled important land and river routes.

## Strategic Capitals
Rajagriha was protected by hills, while Pataliputra controlled river routes.

## Rajagriha’s Defense
Rajagriha was surrounded by hills, making it naturally defensible.

## Pataliputra’s Location
Pataliputra was located near the confluence of major rivers, making it ideal for trade, defense, and administration.

## Strong Rulers
Magadha had ambitious rulers like Bimbisara, Ajatashatru, Shishunaga, and Mahapadma Nanda.

## Marriage Alliances
Magadhan rulers used marriage alliances to strengthen political power.

## Conquest
Magadha expanded by conquering Anga, Vajji, and other rivals.

## Diplomacy
Magadha used alliances and internal division among enemies.

## Standing Army
Magadha developed a strong military system.

## Taxation System
Agricultural surplus and trade allowed rulers to collect revenue.

## Administrative Centralization
Magadha developed stronger administrative control than many rival states.

## Absence of Strong Brahmanical Orthodoxy
Eastern regions like Magadha were less dominated by older Vedic orthodoxy, allowing new political and religious developments.

## Support from Urban Groups
Merchants and urban elites supported stable states and new religious movements.

---

# 31. EARLY MAGADHA: LEGENDARY BACKGROUND

## Brihadratha Dynasty
A legendary early dynasty of Magadha mentioned in Puranic and epic traditions.

## Brihadratha
Legendary founder of the Brihadratha dynasty.

## Jarasandha
Famous legendary king of Magadha in the Mahabharata tradition.

## Girivraja
Old capital associated with early Magadha and Jarasandha traditions.

## Legendary Magadha
The early phase of Magadha known mainly from epic and Puranic traditions, not firm historical evidence.

## Historical Magadha
The historically clearer phase begins with Bimbisara and the Haryanka dynasty.

---

# 32. HARYANKA DYNASTY

## Haryanka Dynasty
The first historically important ruling dynasty of Magadha.

## Bimbisara
Powerful ruler of Magadha and founder or major consolidator of Haryanka power.

## Seniya Bimbisara
Another name for Bimbisara in Buddhist texts.

## Bimbisara’s Capital
Rajagriha.

## Bimbisara’s Expansion Policy
Bimbisara used conquest, marriage alliances, and diplomacy to expand Magadha.

## Bimbisara’s Conquest of Anga
Bimbisara defeated Anga and annexed it, gaining control over Champa.

## Bimbisara and Kosala
Bimbisara married Kosaladevi, sister of Prasenajit of Kosala.

## Kosaladevi
Wife of Bimbisara and sister of Prasenajit.

## Kashi as Dowry
Kashi was given to Bimbisara as dowry through marriage with Kosaladevi.

## Bimbisara and Licchavis
Bimbisara married Chellana, a Licchavi princess.

## Chellana
Licchavi princess married to Bimbisara.

## Bimbisara and Madra
Bimbisara is said to have married a princess from Madra.

## Bimbisara and Buddhism
Bimbisara was a patron and contemporary of Buddha.

## Bimbisara and Jainism
Bimbisara was also contemporary with Mahavira and appears in Jain traditions.

## Veluvana
Bamboo Grove monastery donated by Bimbisara to Buddha.

## Rajagriha Fortification
Rajagriha’s natural and built defenses strengthened Magadha.

---

# 33. AJATASHATRU

## Ajatashatru
Son of Bimbisara and one of the greatest early rulers of Magadha.

## Kunika
Another name for Ajatashatru in some traditions.

## Patricide Tradition
Some texts say Ajatashatru killed or imprisoned his father Bimbisara to gain the throne.

## Ajatashatru and Buddha
Ajatashatru was contemporary with Buddha and is mentioned in Buddhist texts.

## Ajatashatru and Mahavira
Ajatashatru was also contemporary with Mahavira.

## Ajatashatru’s Expansion
He expanded Magadha through wars against Kosala and Vajji.

## Ajatashatru-Kosala War
Conflict over Kashi after the death of Kosaladevi and Bimbisara.

## Ajatashatru-Vajji War
Major war between Magadha and the Vajji confederacy.

## Vajji War
Long conflict that ended with Magadha’s victory over the Vajji confederacy.

## Vassakara
Ajatashatru’s minister who helped weaken the Vajji confederacy.

## Sunidha
Minister associated with Magadha and fortification of Pataligrama.

## Pataligrama
Fortified by Magadha during Ajatashatru’s period, later becoming Pataliputra.

## Rathamushala
A war machine associated with Ajatashatru, often described as a chariot with mace-like weapons.

## Mahashilakantaka
A war engine associated with Ajatashatru, possibly a stone-throwing device.

## Ajatashatru’s Military Innovation
Use of war engines and strong fortifications.

## Ajatashatru and First Buddhist Council
Ajatashatru is traditionally associated with patronage of the First Buddhist Council after Buddha’s Mahaparinirvana.

## First Buddhist Council
Held at Rajagriha according to tradition, under Ajatashatru’s patronage.

---

# 34. SUCCESSORS OF AJATASHATRU

## Udayin
Successor of Ajatashatru, credited with shifting the capital to Pataliputra.

## Udayabhadra
Another name or form associated with Udayin.

## Shift to Pataliputra
A major step that strengthened Magadha’s control over river routes.

## Pataliputra as Capital
Pataliputra became Magadha’s most important capital and later the Mauryan capital.

## Anuruddha
One of the later Haryanka rulers mentioned in traditions.

## Munda
A later Haryanka ruler.

## Nagadasaka
Last Haryanka ruler according to some traditions.

## Decline of Haryankas
The dynasty declined due to weak successors and internal instability.

## End of Haryanka Dynasty
The Haryankas were succeeded by the Shishunaga dynasty.

---

# 35. SHISHUNAGA DYNASTY

## Shishunaga Dynasty
Dynasty that ruled Magadha after the Haryankas.

## Shishunaga
Founder of the Shishunaga dynasty.

## Shishunaga’s Origin
Some traditions say he was an official or minister who became king.

## Shishunaga’s Capital
Rajagriha initially; Vaishali may also have been used as a capital according to some traditions.

## Shishunaga and Avanti
Shishunaga is credited with defeating Avanti and ending the long Magadha-Avanti rivalry.

## Annexation of Avanti
A major achievement of Shishunaga, bringing western India closer to Magadhan influence.

## Pradyota Dynasty End
The defeat of Avanti ended the Pradyota dynasty’s power.

## Magadha after Avanti
Magadha became the strongest power in north India after absorbing Avanti.

## Kalashoka
Important Shishunaga ruler, also called Kakavarna.

## Kakavarna
Another name for Kalashoka.

## Kalashoka’s Capital
Pataliputra became important during his reign.

## Second Buddhist Council
Traditionally held at Vaishali during Kalashoka’s reign.

## Vaishali Council
Another name for the Second Buddhist Council.

## Ten Points Controversy
Dispute over monastic practices at the Second Buddhist Council.

## Shishunaga Decline
The dynasty declined after Kalashoka and was replaced by the Nandas.

---

# 36. NANDA DYNASTY

## Nanda Dynasty
Powerful dynasty of Magadha before the Mauryas.

## Mahapadma Nanda
Founder and greatest ruler of the Nanda dynasty.

## Ugrasena
Another name sometimes associated with Mahapadma Nanda.

## Mahapadma Nanda’s Origin
Traditions describe him as of low or non-Kshatriya origin, though accounts differ.

## First Great Historical Empire Builder
Mahapadma Nanda is sometimes described as the first major empire-builder of north India before the Mauryas.

## Sarva-Kshatrantaka
Title meaning “destroyer of all Kshatriyas”, associated with Mahapadma Nanda in Puranic tradition.

## Ekarat
A sole ruler or universal monarch; associated with Mahapadma Nanda’s imperial claims.

## Nanda Expansion
The Nandas expanded Magadha over much of north India and possibly into parts of the Deccan.

## Nanda Empire
A large pre-Mauryan empire centered in Magadha.

## Nanda Military Power
The Nandas maintained a huge army according to Greek accounts.

## Nanda Wealth
The Nandas were famous for enormous wealth and a strong treasury.

## Nanda Taxation
Heavy taxation is associated with the Nanda state in some traditions.

## Nanda Treasury
Large royal treasury that supported army and administration.

## Nanda Administration
A centralized administration that probably influenced later Mauryan organization.

## Nanda Army
Greek sources describe the Nanda army as very large, including infantry, cavalry, chariots, and elephants.

## Dhana Nanda
The last Nanda ruler, overthrown by Chandragupta Maurya.

## Agrammes
Name used by some Greek writers, often identified with the last Nanda ruler.

## Xandrames
Another Greek form sometimes identified with the last Nanda ruler.

## Dhana Nanda’s Unpopularity
Traditions describe him as unpopular due to arrogance or heavy taxation.

## Chanakya and Nandas
Tradition says Chanakya was insulted by Dhana Nanda and helped Chandragupta overthrow the Nandas.

## Nanda-Maurya Transition
The overthrow of the Nandas by Chandragupta Maurya marked the beginning of the Mauryan Empire.

## Nine Nandas
Tradition often refers to nine Nanda rulers.

## Nava Nanda
The nine Nandas.

## Nanda Rule before Chandragupta
The Nandas were the immediate predecessors of the Mauryas in Magadha.

---

# 37. PRADYOTA DYNASTY OF AVANTI

## Pradyota Dynasty
Dynasty ruling Avanti before its absorption into Magadha.

## Chanda Pradyota
Famous king of Avanti, known for ambition and rivalry with neighboring states.

## Pradyota and Bimbisara
Pradyota was a contemporary of Bimbisara.

## Pradyota and Udayana
Traditions describe relations and conflicts between Pradyota of Avanti and Udayana of Vatsa.

## Avanti as Rival of Magadha
Before its conquest, Avanti was a major rival of Magadha.

## End of Pradyotas
Shishunaga is credited with ending Pradyota power and annexing Avanti.

---

# 38. VATSA DYNASTY AND UDAYANA

## Udayana
Famous king of Vatsa with capital at Kaushambi.

## Vatsa Dynasty
Ruling line of Vatsa, known especially through Udayana traditions.

## Udayana and Buddhism
Traditions connect Udayana with early Buddhist activity.

## Udayana and Avanti
Udayana had political and legendary links with Avanti.

## Vasavadatta
Princess of Avanti associated with Udayana in literary traditions.

## Svapnavasavadatta
Sanskrit drama by Bhasa based on Udayana and Vasavadatta legend.

## Kaushambi under Udayana
Kaushambi was an important urban and political center.

---

# 39. KOSALA DYNASTY AND PRASENAJIT

## Prasenajit
King of Kosala and contemporary of Buddha and Bimbisara.

## Pasenadi
Pali form of Prasenajit.

## Kosala Dynasty
Ruling line of Kosala during the Buddha’s time.

## Prasenajit and Buddha
Prasenajit was a patron and follower of Buddha.

## Prasenajit and Bimbisara
They were connected through marriage alliance.

## Prasenajit and Ajatashatru
They fought over Kashi but later relations improved.

## Vidudabha
Son of Prasenajit, associated with later Kosala politics and conflict with Shakyas.

## Decline of Kosala
Kosala was eventually overshadowed by Magadha.

---

# 40. REPUBLICAN POLITIES AND THEIR FEATURES

## Vajji Confederacy
A powerful republican union centered at Vaishali.

## Licchavis
Dominant clan in the Vajji confederacy.

## Videhas
A clan/people within the Vajji confederacy.

## Jnatrikas
Clan associated with Mahavira.

## Mallas
Republican clan associated with Kushinagar and Pava.

## Shakyas
Republican clan of Buddha.

## Koliyas
Republican clan related to the Shakyas.

## Moriyas
Republican clan later associated with the Maurya name.

## Republican Assembly
Main decision-making body in a Gana-Sangha.

## Santhagara
Assembly hall used by republican clans.

## Collective Decision-Making
Political decisions made by a group of chiefs or elders.

## Clan Chiefs
Leading members of aristocratic families in republics.

## Oligarchic Republic
A republic ruled by a limited aristocratic group, not by all people.

## Warrior Aristocracy
Kshatriya clan elites who controlled republican states.

## Republics and Buddhism
Many republican regions were closely connected with Buddha’s life.

## Republics and Jainism
Mahavira’s background was linked to the Vajji-Licchavi-Jnatrika region.

---

# 41. ADMINISTRATION IN MAHAJANAPADA AGE

## King
Central authority in monarchical Mahajanapadas.

## Council of Ministers
Advisory body assisting the king.

## Amatya
Minister or official.

## Mahamatra
High official; the term became more prominent later under the Mauryas.

## Senapati
Commander of the army.

## Purohita
Royal priest and adviser.

## Gramani
Village headman.

## Nagarika
Urban official, more clearly seen in later administrative texts.

## Revenue Officials
Officials collecting taxes and managing treasury.

## Treasurer
Officer managing state wealth.

## Fort Officer
Official responsible for fortifications.

## Judicial Authority
Power to settle disputes and punish crimes.

## Danda
Punishment or coercive power of the state.

## Dandaniti
Policy of punishment and statecraft.

## Law and Order
Maintenance of internal peace by rulers and officials.

## Spies
Secret agents used by rulers, more fully described in later texts like Arthashastra.

## Diplomacy
Use of treaties, envoys, marriage alliances, and intrigue.

## Marriage Alliance
Political marriage used to build alliances, as Bimbisara did.

## Annexation
Absorption of one state into another.

## Tribute
Payment made by subordinate rulers or groups.

---

# 42. MILITARY TERMS

## Army
Organized military force of a state.

## Standing Army
Permanent professional army maintained by the king.

## Infantry
Foot soldiers.

## Cavalry
Horse soldiers.

## Chariotry
War chariot units.

## Elephant Corps
War elephants used in battle.

## War Elephant
Elephant trained for war, a major advantage for Magadha.

## Fort
Defensive structure protecting a city or capital.

## Siege
Military operation to capture a fortified city.

## Rathamushala
War machine associated with Ajatashatru.

## Mahashilakantaka
Stone-throwing war engine associated with Ajatashatru.

## Weaponry
Weapons such as swords, spears, bows, arrows, and maces.

## Iron Weapons
Weapons made stronger by iron technology.

## Expansionist Warfare
Wars fought to conquer territory and resources.

## Defensive Warfare
Wars fought to protect a state from invasion.

---

# 43. URBAN AND ARCHAEOLOGICAL TERMS

## Northern Black Polished Ware
Fine glossy pottery associated with urbanization in the Ganga valley.

## NBPW Culture
Archaeological culture linked with the early historic period and Mahajanapada age.

## Fortified City
City protected by walls and gates.

## Moat
Water-filled or dry ditch around a fortification.

## Rampart
Defensive wall or embankment.

## City Wall
Wall surrounding an urban settlement.

## Ring Well
Circular well made of terracotta rings, common in early historic urban sites.

## Drainage
System to remove wastewater.

## Brick Architecture
Use of baked or mud bricks in urban buildings.

## Urban Stratigraphy
Archaeological layers showing settlement growth.

## Pottery Sequence
Changes in pottery styles used to date archaeological phases.

## Black-and-Red Ware
Earlier pottery tradition present in some regions before or alongside later developments.

## Painted Grey Ware
Earlier Iron Age pottery associated with Later Vedic culture, preceding NBPW urbanization.

## Punch-Marked Coin Hoards
Groups of early coins found together, showing money use.

## Terracotta Figurines
Clay figures found at early historic sites.

## Beads
Ornaments made from stone, glass, shell, or terracotta.

## Iron Tools
Tools used for agriculture, craft, and warfare.

---

# 44. IMPORTANT CITIES OF THE PERIOD

## Rajagriha
Early capital of Magadha, protected by hills.

## Pataliputra
Later Magadhan capital and future Mauryan imperial capital.

## Champa
Capital of Anga and important commercial city.

## Varanasi
Capital of Kashi and textile center.

## Shravasti
Capital of Kosala and major Buddhist center.

## Saketa
Important city of Kosala.

## Ayodhya
Important ancient city in Kosala.

## Vaishali
Capital of Vajji confederacy and major republican center.

## Kushinagar
Malla city and place of Buddha’s Mahaparinirvana.

## Pava
Malla city associated with Jain and Buddhist traditions.

## Kaushambi
Capital of Vatsa and major trading city.

## Ujjain
Capital of Avanti and major trade center.

## Mahishmati
Southern capital of Avanti.

## Mathura
Capital of Shurasena and major religious-trade center.

## Taxila
Capital of Gandhara and great learning center.

## Ahichhatra
Capital of northern Panchala.

## Kampilya
Capital of southern Panchala.

## Viratanagara
Capital of Matsya.

## Potana
Capital of Ashmaka.

## Rajapura
Traditional capital of Kamboja.

---

# 45. IMPORTANT TRADE ROUTES

## Uttarapatha
Northern trade route from the Ganga valley to Gandhara and beyond.

## Dakshinapatha
Southern trade route connecting north India with the Deccan.

## Ganga River Route
Riverine route connecting eastern and northern India.

## Yamuna Route
Route connecting Mathura, Kaushambi, and the Ganga region.

## Champa Route
Eastern trade route through Anga.

## Avanti Route
Route through Ujjain connecting north India, western India, and the Deccan.

## Gandhara Route
North-western route connecting India with Central Asia and Iran.

## Riverine Trade
Trade using rivers for transport.

## Overland Trade
Trade using roads and caravans.

## Caravan Trade
Long-distance trade by merchant groups.

## Maritime Links
Early trade links to coastal regions, becoming stronger in later periods.

---

# 46. MAHAJANAPADA PERIOD AND RELIGIOUS MOVEMENTS

## Buddhism and Mahajanapadas
Buddhism arose in the Mahajanapada age and received support from kings, merchants, and urban groups.

## Jainism and Mahajanapadas
Jainism spread in the same political and urban environment.

## Magadha and Buddhism
Magadha was closely associated with Buddha, Bimbisara, Ajatashatru, Rajagriha, and later councils.

## Magadha and Jainism
Mahavira spent much of his life in the Magadha-Vajji region.

## Kosala and Buddhism
Shravasti and Jetavana were major Buddhist centers in Kosala.

## Vajji and Jainism
Vaishali and the Jnatrika clan were linked with Mahavira.

## Malla and Buddhism
Kushinagar, a Malla city, was the place of Buddha’s Mahaparinirvana.

## Vatsa and Buddhism
Kaushambi was an important Buddhist center.

## Avanti and Buddhism
Buddhist teachers spread the faith in Avanti.

## Merchant Patronage
Merchants funded monasteries and religious teachers.

## Monasteries near Cities
Buddhist and Jain monastic centers often developed near urban settlements.

---

# 47. PERSIAN / ACHAEMENID CONNECTION

## Achaemenid Empire
The Persian Empire that controlled parts of north-western India.

## Cyrus
Achaemenid ruler associated with Persian expansion, though Indian connection is debated.

## Darius I
Achaemenid ruler who annexed parts of north-western India.

## Hindush
Persian name for the Indian satrapy under the Achaemenids.

## Satrapy
A province of the Persian Empire.

## Satrap
Governor of a Persian province.

## Gandhara under Persia
Gandhara came under Achaemenid influence.

## Indian Tribute to Persia
Greek sources mention Indian tribute to the Persian Empire.

## Persian Influence
Possible influence on administration, coinage, inscriptions, and art in north-western India.

## Kharosthi Script
Script used in north-western India, written right to left; it developed under Aramaic influence.

## Aramaic
Administrative language of the Achaemenid Empire, influencing north-western scripts.

## North-Western Contact
Contact between India, Iran, and Central Asia through Gandhara and Kamboja.

---

# 48. ALEXANDER’S INVASION AND PRE-MAURYAN CONTEXT

## Alexander
Macedonian king who invaded north-western India in 326 BCE.

## Macedonian Invasion
Alexander’s campaign into north-west India.

## Battle of Hydaspes
Battle between Alexander and Porus on the Jhelum River.

## Hydaspes
Greek name for the Jhelum River.

## Porus
Indian ruler who fought Alexander at the Battle of Hydaspes.

## Paurava Kingdom
Kingdom of Porus in the Punjab region.

## Ambhi
Ruler of Taxila who allied with Alexander.

## Omphis
Greek name associated with Ambhi of Taxila.

## Taxila and Alexander
Taxila submitted to Alexander and became an important base.

## Beas Mutiny
Alexander’s army refused to march further east beyond the Beas River.

## Hyphasis
Greek name for the Beas River.

## Return of Alexander
Alexander returned west after his troops refused further advance.

## Greek Satraps
Governors appointed by Alexander in conquered territories.

## Seleucus Nicator
Successor of Alexander who later fought Chandragupta Maurya.

## North-Western Political Vacuum
After Alexander’s retreat, instability in the north-west helped Chandragupta’s rise.

## Greek Accounts of Nandas
Greek writers mention a powerful ruler in the Gangetic region, usually identified with the Nanda king.

## Nanda Army in Greek Accounts
Greek sources describe the Nanda army as huge, discouraging Alexander’s troops.

## Chandragupta and Alexander Tradition
Some traditions say Chandragupta had contact with north-western politics during or after Alexander’s invasion.

---

# 49. IMMEDIATE BACKGROUND TO CHANDRAGUPTA MAURYA

## Dhana Nanda
Last Nanda ruler of Magadha, overthrown by Chandragupta Maurya.

## Chanakya
Political thinker and strategist who helped Chandragupta defeat the Nandas.

## Kautilya
Another name for Chanakya.

## Vishnugupta
Another name associated with Chanakya.

## Chandragupta Maurya
Founder of the Mauryan Empire who overthrew the Nandas.

## Nanda Overthrow
The political revolution that brought the Mauryas to power.

## Magadha as Imperial Base
Magadha’s resources, capital, and administration enabled Chandragupta to create a large empire.

## Pataliputra as Imperial Capital
The city became the capital of the Mauryan Empire.

## Pre-Mauryan Administrative Legacy
The Nandas and earlier Magadhan rulers created administrative and military foundations used by the Mauryas.

## Pre-Mauryan Military Legacy
Large armies, elephant corps, and fortified capitals prepared the ground for empire.

## Pre-Mauryan Economic Legacy
Agricultural surplus, taxation, trade, and coinage supported imperial growth.

---

# 50. DYNASTIC SEQUENCE BEFORE CHANDRAGUPTA MAURYA

## Legendary Brihadratha Dynasty
Early legendary rulers of Magadha, including Brihadratha and Jarasandha.

## Haryanka Dynasty
First historically clear Magadhan dynasty; important rulers include Bimbisara, Ajatashatru, and Udayin.

## Shishunaga Dynasty
Succeeded the Haryankas; important rulers include Shishunaga and Kalashoka.

## Nanda Dynasty
Succeeded the Shishunagas; important rulers include Mahapadma Nanda and Dhana Nanda.

## Maurya Dynasty
Founded by Chandragupta Maurya after overthrowing the Nandas.

## Pre-Mauryan Magadhan Sequence
Brihadratha tradition → Haryanka → Shishunaga → Nanda → Maurya.

---

# 51. IMPORTANT RULERS BEFORE CHANDRAGUPTA

## Brihadratha
Legendary early ruler of Magadha.

## Jarasandha
Legendary Magadhan ruler from epic tradition.

## Bimbisara
Haryanka ruler who expanded Magadha through conquest and alliances.

## Ajatashatru
Haryanka ruler who defeated Vajji and strengthened Magadha.

## Udayin
Haryanka ruler credited with shifting the capital to Pataliputra.

## Shishunaga
Founder of Shishunaga dynasty and conqueror of Avanti.

## Kalashoka
Shishunaga ruler associated with the Second Buddhist Council.

## Mahapadma Nanda
Founder and greatest ruler of the Nanda dynasty.

## Dhana Nanda
Last Nanda ruler defeated by Chandragupta Maurya.

## Prasenajit
King of Kosala and contemporary of Buddha.

## Udayana
King of Vatsa.

## Chanda Pradyota
King of Avanti.

## Porus
North-western ruler who fought Alexander.

## Ambhi
Ruler of Taxila who allied with Alexander.

---

# 52. IMPORTANT TERMS FROM BUDDHIST SOURCES

## Mahaparinibbana Sutta
Buddhist text containing information about Buddha’s last days and political conditions such as Vajji strength.

## Samaññaphala Sutta
Buddhist text mentioning Ajatashatru and several contemporary teachers.

## Anguttara Nikaya
Text listing sixteen Mahajanapadas.

## Digha Nikaya
Collection containing important political and social information.

## Vinaya Texts
Texts that show urban life, merchants, monasteries, and political contexts.

## Jataka Narratives
Stories reflecting social and economic life, though not always direct historical records.

## Pasenadi
Pali name for Prasenajit.

## Bimbisara in Pali Texts
A royal patron of Buddha.

## Ajatasattu
Pali form of Ajatashatru.

## Vajjis in Buddhist Texts
Republican confederacy praised for unity and assembly traditions.

---

# 53. IMPORTANT TERMS FROM JAIN SOURCES

## Bhagavati Sutra
Jain text containing information about Mahavira’s time and political regions.

## Mahavira
24th Tirthankara, contemporary of Bimbisara and Ajatashatru.

## Nigantha Nataputta
Name for Mahavira in Buddhist texts.

## Jnatrika Clan
Mahavira’s clan, associated with the Vajji region.

## Vaishali and Jainism
Important center connected with Mahavira’s life.

## Pava
Place associated with Mahavira’s final liberation in Jain tradition.

## Jain View of Bimbisara
Bimbisara appears in Jain traditions as a contemporary ruler.

## Jain View of Ajatashatru
Ajatashatru appears in Jain traditions under names like Kunika.

---

# 54. IMPORTANT ARCHAEOLOGICAL SITES OF THE PERIOD

## Rajgir
Modern site of ancient Rajagriha.

## Cyclopean Wall of Rajgir
Massive stone wall around Rajgir, associated with early fortification.

## Pataliputra
Archaeological site near modern Patna.

## Kumrahar
Site near Patna associated more with Mauryan remains but located in ancient Pataliputra.

## Bulandibagh
Site associated with ancient Pataliputra fortification.

## Vaishali
Archaeological site of the Vajji capital.

## Kaushambi
Excavated site of Vatsa capital with fortifications and urban remains.

## Shravasti
Important Buddhist and urban site.

## Rajghat
Archaeological site at Varanasi.

## Ujjain
Important early historic city in Madhya Pradesh.

## Taxila
Major archaeological and learning center in Gandhara.

## Bairat
Site associated with Matsya and later Ashokan remains.

## Mathura
Important early historic city and later religious-art center.

## Champa
Ancient city associated with Anga.

## Chirand
Important site in Bihar showing long cultural sequence.

## Sonpur
Site in Bihar with early historic remains.

---

# 55. IMPORTANT POTTERY AND MATERIAL CULTURE

## Painted Grey Ware
Earlier Iron Age pottery associated with Later Vedic culture and early Janapadas.

## PGW
Short form of Painted Grey Ware.

## Northern Black Polished Ware
Glossy pottery associated with second urbanization.

## NBPW
Short form of Northern Black Polished Ware.

## Black-and-Red Ware
Pottery tradition found in earlier and continuing cultural contexts.

## Red Ware
Common pottery type in early historic sites.

## Iron Implements
Iron tools and weapons used in agriculture and warfare.

## Punch-Marked Coins
Early coins used in trade and taxation.

## Terracotta Objects
Clay objects such as figurines, beads, seals, and toys.

## Beads
Objects used for ornamentation and trade.

## Fortification Remains
Archaeological evidence of city walls, ramparts, and defensive structures.

---

# 56. POLITICAL PROCESSES OF THE PERIOD

## State Formation
The process by which tribal societies became territorial states.

## Territorial Expansion
Growth of states through conquest and annexation.

## Annexation of Anga
Magadha’s conquest of Anga under Bimbisara.

## Annexation of Vajji
Magadha’s defeat of Vajji under Ajatashatru.

## Annexation of Avanti
Magadha’s absorption of Avanti under Shishunaga.

## Imperial Formation
Creation of a large empire through conquest and centralization.

## Magadhan Hegemony
Dominance of Magadha over other Mahajanapadas.

## Inter-State Rivalry
Competition among Magadha, Kosala, Vatsa, Avanti, and others.

## Marriage Diplomacy
Use of marriage to form political alliances.

## War Diplomacy
Use of war, treaties, and intrigue to expand power.

## Internal Dissension
Weakening of enemy states by creating divisions within them.

## Centralization
Concentration of political power in the king and administration.

## Militarization
Expansion and professionalization of armies.

## Revenue Extraction
State collection of surplus from peasants, traders, and conquered areas.

---

# 57. MAGADHA’S RIVAL STATES

## Anga as Rival
Anga was an early rival conquered by Bimbisara.

## Kosala as Rival
Kosala competed with Magadha over Kashi and regional dominance.

## Vajji as Rival
Vajji was a powerful republican confederacy defeated by Ajatashatru.

## Avanti as Rival
Avanti was a major western rival absorbed under Shishunaga.

## Vatsa as Rival
Vatsa was an important kingdom but did not match Magadha’s expansion.

## Kashi as Contested Region
Kashi was contested between Kosala and Magadha due to revenue and strategic value.

## Gandhara as Separate Power
Gandhara remained important in the north-west but was affected by Persian and later Greek influence.

---

# 58. HIGH-YIELD MAGADHA EXPANSION SEQUENCE

## Step 1: Bimbisara Strengthens Magadha
Bimbisara used conquest and marriage alliances to strengthen Magadha.

## Step 2: Anga Annexed
Bimbisara conquered Anga and gained Champa.

## Step 3: Ajatashatru Defeats Kosala
Ajatashatru fought Kosala over Kashi and secured Magadha’s position.

## Step 4: Ajatashatru Defeats Vajji
Ajatashatru defeated the Vajji confederacy after a long war.

## Step 5: Pataligrama Fortified
Magadha fortified Pataligrama, later Pataliputra.

## Step 6: Udayin Shifts Capital
Udayin shifted the capital to Pataliputra.

## Step 7: Shishunaga Defeats Avanti
Avanti was absorbed, ending a major rivalry.

## Step 8: Nandas Build Large Empire
Mahapadma Nanda expanded Magadha further.

## Step 9: Dhana Nanda Falls
Dhana Nanda was overthrown by Chandragupta Maurya.

---

# 59. HIGH-YIELD UPSC COMPARISONS

## Jana vs Janapada
Jana means tribe. Janapada means territory occupied by a tribe.

## Janapada vs Mahajanapada
Janapada is a territorial state. Mahajanapada is a larger and more powerful territorial state.

## Monarchy vs Gana-Sangha
Monarchy is rule by a king. Gana-Sangha is rule by an assembly of clan elites.

## Rajagriha vs Pataliputra
Rajagriha was Magadha’s early hill-protected capital. Pataliputra was its later river-based imperial capital.

## Bimbisara vs Ajatashatru
Bimbisara expanded by conquest and marriage alliances. Ajatashatru expanded through major wars against Kosala and Vajji.

## Haryanka vs Shishunaga
Haryankas began historical Magadhan expansion. Shishunagas ended Avanti’s rivalry and further strengthened Magadha.

## Shishunaga vs Nanda
Shishunaga consolidated Magadha after Haryankas. Nandas built a larger centralized empire.

## Mahapadma Nanda vs Dhana Nanda
Mahapadma Nanda founded and expanded Nanda power. Dhana Nanda was the last Nanda, overthrown by Chandragupta.

## Magadha vs Kosala
Both were powerful eastern kingdoms, but Magadha eventually became dominant.

## Magadha vs Avanti
Avanti was a major western rival, later annexed by Magadha.

## Republics vs Monarchies
Republics were clan-based oligarchies; monarchies were ruled by kings with stronger central power.

## NBPW vs PGW
PGW is associated with earlier Later Vedic and early Janapada culture. NBPW is associated with the second urbanization and Mahajanapada age.

## Punch-Marked Coins vs Later Coins
Punch-marked coins were early irregular metal coins with symbols; later coins became more dynastic and inscribed.

---

# 60. HIGH-YIELD CAPITALS FOR UPSC

## Anga
Champa.

## Magadha
Rajagriha, later Pataliputra.

## Kashi
Varanasi.

## Kosala
Shravasti; Saketa/Ayodhya also important.

## Vajji
Vaishali.

## Malla
Kushinagar and Pava.

## Chedi
Suktimati.

## Vatsa
Kaushambi.

## Kuru
Indraprastha or Hastinapura.

## Panchala
Ahichhatra and Kampilya.

## Matsya
Viratanagara.

## Shurasena
Mathura.

## Ashmaka
Potana or Potali.

## Avanti
Ujjain and Mahishmati.

## Gandhara
Taxila.

## Kamboja
Rajapura.

---

# 61. HIGH-YIELD RULER-CAPITAL-REGION CLUSTER

## Bimbisara
Magadha; Rajagriha.

## Ajatashatru
Magadha; Rajagriha and Pataligrama context.

## Udayin
Magadha; shifted capital to Pataliputra.

## Shishunaga
Magadha; Rajagriha/Vaishali traditions.

## Kalashoka
Magadha; Pataliputra; Second Buddhist Council.

## Mahapadma Nanda
Magadha; Pataliputra.

## Dhana Nanda
Magadha; Pataliputra.

## Prasenajit
Kosala; Shravasti.

## Udayana
Vatsa; Kaushambi.

## Chanda Pradyota
Avanti; Ujjain.

## Porus
Punjab region; fought Alexander.

## Ambhi
Taxila; allied with Alexander.

---

# 62. HIGH-YIELD EVENTS FOR UPSC

## Rise of Mahajanapadas
Emergence of sixteen large territorial states around the 6th century BCE.

## Second Urbanization
Growth of cities in the Ganga valley.

## Use of Iron
Helped agriculture, warfare, and forest clearance.

## Bimbisara Conquers Anga
First major expansion of Magadha.

## Ajatashatru Defeats Vajji
Major victory over a powerful republic.

## Fortification of Pataligrama
Strategic step in Magadha’s expansion.

## Udayin Shifts Capital
Pataliputra becomes Magadha’s capital.

## Shishunaga Defeats Avanti
Magadha removes a major western rival.

## Second Buddhist Council
Held at Vaishali during Kalashoka’s reign according to tradition.

## Mahapadma Nanda Expands Empire
Nanda power grows over much of north India.

## Alexander Invades India
North-western India enters Greek accounts.

## Battle of Hydaspes
Alexander defeats Porus but respects his bravery.

## Beas Mutiny
Alexander’s troops refuse to advance further east.

## Dhana Nanda Overthrown
Chandragupta Maurya replaces the Nandas.

---

# 63. HIGH-YIELD TERMS CONNECTED WITH MAGADHA

## Rajagriha
Early capital of Magadha.

## Pataliputra
Later capital and imperial center.

## Ganga
Major river supporting Magadha’s economy and expansion.

## Son
River important for Pataliputra’s location.

## Iron Ore
Resource helping Magadha’s rise.

## Elephants
Military resource of Magadha.

## Bimbisara
Expansionist Haryanka ruler.

## Ajatashatru
Conqueror of Vajji.

## Udayin
Founder of Pataliputra as capital.

## Shishunaga
Conqueror of Avanti.

## Kalashoka
Associated with Second Buddhist Council.

## Mahapadma Nanda
Founder of Nanda power.

## Dhana Nanda
Last Nanda ruler.

## Chanakya
Strategist behind Chandragupta’s rise.

## Chandragupta Maurya
Founder of Mauryan Empire.

---

# 64. IMPORTANT BUDDHIST AND JAIN CONTEMPORARIES

## Gautama Buddha
Founder of Buddhism, contemporary of Bimbisara and Ajatashatru.

## Mahavira
24th Tirthankara of Jainism, contemporary of Bimbisara and Ajatashatru.

## Makkhali Gosala
Ajivika teacher and contemporary religious figure.

## Ajita Kesakambalin
Materialist teacher mentioned in Buddhist texts.

## Pakudha Kaccayana
Contemporary teacher mentioned in Buddhist texts.

## Sanjaya Belatthiputta
Skeptical teacher mentioned in Buddhist texts.

## Purana Kassapa
Contemporary teacher mentioned in Buddhist texts.

## Nigantha Nataputta
Name for Mahavira in Buddhist texts.

## Six Contemporary Teachers
A group of non-Buddhist teachers mentioned in Buddhist texts, showing the intellectual diversity of the period.

---

# 65. IMPORTANT POLITICAL TERMS IN PALI/SANSKRIT CONTEXT

## Mahajanapada
Great territorial state.

## Janapada
Territorial state.

## Gama
Village.

## Nigama
Market town.

## Nagara
Town or city.

## Rajan
King.

## Raja
King.

## Gana
Political group or republic.

## Sangha
Confederacy or association.

## Setthi
Banker or wealthy merchant.

## Gahapati
Householder or landowner.

## Sarthavaha
Caravan leader.

## Dasa
Servant or slave.

## Kammakara
Worker or labourer.

## Amacca
Minister, Pali form of Amatya.

## Senapati
Commander.

## Duta
Messenger.

## Bali
Tribute.

## Bhaga
Royal share.

## Kara
Tax.

## Shulka
Toll.

---

# 66. CHRONOLOGICAL SNAPSHOT

## Stage 1: Later Vedic Background
Tribal groups settled into territories, agriculture expanded, iron use increased, and Janapadas emerged.

## Stage 2: Rise of Janapadas
Small territorial states developed from older tribal identities.

## Stage 3: Rise of Mahajanapadas
Sixteen large states emerged by the 6th century BCE, including Magadha, Kosala, Vatsa, Avanti, Vajji, and others.

## Stage 4: Second Urbanization
Cities, trade, coinage, guilds, and merchant classes expanded in the Ganga valley.

## Stage 5: Religious Ferment
Buddhism, Jainism, Ajivikas, and other Shramana movements emerged in the same social context.

## Stage 6: Magadha under Bimbisara
Magadha expanded through conquest of Anga and marriage alliances with Kosala, Licchavis, and others.

## Stage 7: Magadha under Ajatashatru
Magadha defeated Kosala and Vajji, developed war machines, and fortified Pataligrama.

## Stage 8: Pataliputra’s Rise
Udayin shifted the capital to Pataliputra, giving Magadha a strategic river-based capital.

## Stage 9: Shishunaga Consolidation
Shishunaga defeated Avanti and removed a major rival.

## Stage 10: Nanda Expansion
Mahapadma Nanda built a large empire with a huge army and treasury.

## Stage 11: Alexander’s Invasion
Alexander entered north-western India but did not reach the Gangetic heartland.

## Stage 12: Fall of the Nandas
Dhana Nanda was overthrown by Chandragupta Maurya with Chanakya’s help, beginning the Mauryan Empire.

---

# 67. FINAL REVISION CLUSTER FOR UPSC PRELIMS

## Must Remember Period
6th century BCE was the age of Mahajanapadas, second urbanization, coinage, Jainism, Buddhism, and Magadha’s rise.

## Must Remember Sixteen Mahajanapadas
Anga, Magadha, Kashi, Kosala, Vajji, Malla, Chedi, Vatsa, Kuru, Panchala, Matsya, Shurasena, Ashmaka, Avanti, Gandhara, Kamboja.

## Must Remember Four Powerful Monarchies
Magadha, Kosala, Vatsa, and Avanti.

## Must Remember Important Republics
Vajji, Malla, Shakya, Koliya, Moriya, Kalama, and others.

## Must Remember Magadha’s Early Capital
Rajagriha.

## Must Remember Magadha’s Later Capital
Pataliputra.

## Must Remember Why Magadha Rose
Fertile soil, iron ore, forests, elephants, rivers, trade routes, strong rulers, strategic capitals, and military power.

## Must Remember Haryanka Rulers
Bimbisara, Ajatashatru, Udayin.

## Must Remember Shishunaga Rulers
Shishunaga and Kalashoka.

## Must Remember Nanda Rulers
Mahapadma Nanda and Dhana Nanda.

## Must Remember Bimbisara
Conquered Anga and used marriage alliances.

## Must Remember Ajatashatru
Defeated Vajji and used war machines.

## Must Remember Udayin
Shifted capital to Pataliputra.

## Must Remember Shishunaga
Defeated Avanti.

## Must Remember Kalashoka
Associated with Second Buddhist Council.

## Must Remember Mahapadma Nanda
Founder of Nanda power and destroyer of Kshatriyas in Puranic tradition.

## Must Remember Dhana Nanda
Last Nanda ruler defeated by Chandragupta Maurya.

## Must Remember Alexander
Invaded north-west India in 326 BCE and fought Porus at Hydaspes.

## Must Remember Immediate Pre-Mauryan Situation
Nanda power was large but unpopular; north-west was unstable after Alexander; Chandragupta and Chanakya used this context to establish Mauryan rule.

## One-Line Essence
The Mahajanapada age marks the transition from tribal Janas to territorial states, the rise of cities and money economy, the emergence of Buddhism and Jainism, and the transformation of Magadha into the strongest power of north India before the Mauryan Empire.


------

# MAURYAN EMPIRE GLOSSARY FOR UPSC PRELIMS
## Chronological Coverage: Pre-Mauryan Background → Chandragupta Maurya → Bindusara → Ashoka → Mauryan Administration → Economy → Society → Dhamma → Art and Architecture → Decline → Post-Mauryan Transition

> Note:
> The Mauryan Empire was the first large empire to unite most of the Indian subcontinent under one political authority.
> It began with Chandragupta Maurya, expanded under Bindusara, reached its greatest extent under Ashoka, and declined after Ashoka.
> For UPSC Prelims, focus especially on: Chandragupta, Chanakya/Kautilya, Arthashastra, Megasthenes, Ashoka, Kalinga War, Dhamma, Ashokan edicts, Mauryan administration, economy, art, pillars, caves, and decline.

---

# 1. BASIC TERMS OF THE MAURYAN EMPIRE

## Mauryan Empire
The first major empire of ancient India, founded by Chandragupta Maurya around the late 4th century BCE.

## Maurya Dynasty
The ruling dynasty of the Mauryan Empire. Important rulers include Chandragupta Maurya, Bindusara, Ashoka, and later weaker successors.

## First Pan-Indian Empire
The Mauryan Empire is often called the first pan-Indian empire because it controlled most of the Indian subcontinent.

## Imperial State
A large political system controlling many regions, peoples, cities, villages, and provinces.

## Centralized Monarchy
A system where the king and central administration had strong control over the empire.

## Pataliputra
Capital of the Mauryan Empire, located near modern Patna in Bihar.

## Magadha
The eastern Indian region that formed the political base of the Mauryan Empire.

## Chandragupta Maurya
Founder of the Mauryan Empire. He overthrew the Nandas and established Mauryan rule.

## Bindusara
Son of Chandragupta Maurya and father of Ashoka.

## Ashoka
The greatest Mauryan ruler, known for the Kalinga War, Dhamma policy, inscriptions, and Buddhist patronage.

## Brihadratha Maurya
The last Mauryan ruler, killed by Pushyamitra Shunga.

## Chanakya
The political strategist and adviser of Chandragupta Maurya. Also known as Kautilya and Vishnugupta.

## Kautilya
Another name for Chanakya, traditionally credited with writing the Arthashastra.

## Vishnugupta
Another name associated with Chanakya/Kautilya.

## Arthashastra
A treatise on statecraft, administration, economy, taxation, law, espionage, diplomacy, and war.

## Megasthenes
Greek ambassador to Chandragupta Maurya’s court. He wrote the Indica.

## Indica
Book written by Megasthenes describing Mauryan India. The original is lost, but fragments survive in later Greek writings.

## Ashokan Edicts
Inscriptions issued by Ashoka on rocks, pillars, and caves to communicate his Dhamma and administrative instructions.

## Dhamma
Ashoka’s ethical policy based on moral conduct, compassion, non-violence, respect, and welfare.

---

# 2. CHRONOLOGICAL FRAMEWORK

## Pre-Mauryan Background
The period before Chandragupta Maurya, marked by the rise of Magadha, Nanda power, Alexander’s invasion, and political instability in north-west India.

## Nanda Dynasty
The dynasty that ruled Magadha before the Mauryas. It was overthrown by Chandragupta Maurya.

## Dhana Nanda
The last Nanda ruler, defeated by Chandragupta Maurya with Chanakya’s help according to tradition.

## Alexander’s Invasion
Alexander of Macedon invaded north-west India in 326 BCE, creating political disturbance in the region.

## North-Western Political Vacuum
The instability created after Alexander’s retreat, which helped Chandragupta expand.

## Mauryan Foundation
The establishment of Mauryan rule by Chandragupta Maurya after defeating the Nandas.

## Mauryan Expansion
The enlargement of the empire through conquest, diplomacy, and administration under Chandragupta, Bindusara, and Ashoka.

## Mauryan Zenith
The highest point of Mauryan power, reached under Ashoka.

## Post-Ashokan Decline
The weakening of the empire after Ashoka’s death due to political, economic, and administrative problems.

## Fall of Mauryas
The end of Mauryan rule after Brihadratha was killed by Pushyamitra Shunga.

---

# 3. SOURCES FOR MAURYAN HISTORY

## Literary Sources
Texts such as Arthashastra, Indica, Puranas, Buddhist texts, Jain texts, and later Sanskrit works.

## Archaeological Sources
Material remains such as pillars, inscriptions, caves, sculptures, pottery, coins, and city remains.

## Epigraphic Sources
Inscriptions, especially Ashokan edicts, are the most important direct sources.

## Numismatic Sources
Coins, especially punch-marked coins, help understand the economy.

## Foreign Accounts
Greek and Roman accounts provide information about Chandragupta’s court, administration, society, and geography.

## Arthashastra as Source
The Arthashastra gives information about statecraft, administration, taxation, economy, espionage, law, and war.

## Indica as Source
Megasthenes’ Indica gives information about Pataliputra, administration, society, economy, and geography.

## Ashokan Edicts as Source
Ashoka’s edicts are direct official records of his policies, Dhamma, administration, and religious attitude.

## Puranic Sources
Puranas preserve dynastic lists of Mauryan rulers, though they contain legendary material.

## Buddhist Sources
Texts such as Dipavamsa, Mahavamsa, Divyavadana, and Ashokavadana provide information about Ashoka and Buddhism.

## Jain Sources
Jain traditions provide information about Chandragupta Maurya, Bhadrabahu, and Shravanabelagola.

## Greek Sources
Writers such as Strabo, Arrian, Pliny, Justin, and Plutarch preserve fragments about India and the Mauryas.

## Tamil Sources
Early Tamil literature gives indirect information about Mauryan contacts with the far south.

## Sri Lankan Chronicles
Dipavamsa and Mahavamsa describe Ashoka, the Third Buddhist Council, and Buddhist missions to Sri Lanka.

## Divyavadana
A Buddhist Sanskrit text containing legends about Ashoka and other figures.

## Ashokavadana
A text narrating legends about Ashoka’s life and conversion.

## Mahavamsa
Sri Lankan Buddhist chronicle important for Ashoka and Buddhist missions.

## Dipavamsa
Sri Lankan chronicle important for early Buddhist history and Ashoka’s role.

## Mudrarakshasa
A Sanskrit drama by Vishakhadatta, composed much later, describing Chandragupta’s rise with Chanakya’s help.

## Vishakhadatta
Author of Mudrarakshasa.

## Parishishtaparvan
Jain text by Hemachandra containing traditions about Chandragupta and Chanakya.

## Hemachandra
Jain scholar who wrote Parishishtaparvan.

---

# 4. PRE-MAURYAN BACKGROUND

## Magadha’s Rise
Magadha became the strongest state before the Mauryas due to fertile land, iron ore, elephants, forests, rivers, and strong rulers.

## Haryanka Dynasty
Early Magadhan dynasty with rulers like Bimbisara and Ajatashatru.

## Bimbisara
Magadhan ruler who expanded Magadha by conquest and marriage alliances.

## Ajatashatru
Magadhan ruler who defeated the Vajji confederacy and strengthened Magadha.

## Shishunaga Dynasty
Magadhan dynasty that succeeded the Haryankas and defeated Avanti.

## Nanda Dynasty
Powerful dynasty before the Mauryas, known for wealth, army, and centralized control.

## Mahapadma Nanda
Founder and greatest Nanda ruler, described as a powerful empire-builder.

## Dhana Nanda
Last Nanda ruler, overthrown by Chandragupta Maurya.

## Pataliputra before Mauryas
Already an important capital under later Magadhan rulers before Chandragupta.

## Nanda Army
A huge army mentioned in Greek accounts, showing Magadha’s military strength before the Mauryas.

## Nanda Treasury
Large royal treasury that supported administration and army.

## Chanakya’s Conflict with Nanda
Traditional story that Chanakya was insulted by Dhana Nanda and vowed to overthrow him.

## Chandragupta’s Early Career
Traditions differ, but he rose during the political instability after Alexander and Nanda decline.

---

# 5. CHANDRAGUPTA MAURYA

## Chandragupta Maurya
Founder of the Mauryan Empire. He overthrew the Nandas and built a large empire from Magadha.

## Founder of Mauryan Empire
Chandragupta is considered the founder because he established Mauryan rule in Magadha.

## Overthrow of Nandas
Chandragupta defeated Dhana Nanda with Chanakya’s help and captured Pataliputra.

## Chanakya and Chandragupta
Chanakya guided Chandragupta in political strategy, diplomacy, and conquest according to tradition.

## Chandragupta and North-West India
Chandragupta took advantage of the political vacuum after Alexander’s retreat.

## Chandragupta and Seleucus
Chandragupta fought Seleucus Nicator and concluded a treaty with him.

## Seleucus Nicator
One of Alexander’s generals and ruler of the Seleucid Empire.

## Chandragupta-Seleucus Treaty
Treaty by which Chandragupta received territories in the north-west, while Seleucus received 500 war elephants.

## 500 War Elephants
Given by Chandragupta to Seleucus under the treaty; they later helped Seleucus in western battles.

## Territorial Gains from Seleucus
Chandragupta likely gained Arachosia, Gedrosia, Paropamisadae, and parts of Aria.

## Arachosia
Region around Kandahar, ceded or linked to Mauryan control after treaty with Seleucus.

## Gedrosia
Region around Balochistan, associated with Mauryan-Seleucid settlement.

## Paropamisadae
Region near Kabul and Hindu Kush, associated with north-western Mauryan expansion.

## Aria
Region around Herat, sometimes discussed in relation to Mauryan-Seleucid treaty.

## Diplomatic Marriage Theory
Some Greek sources mention a marriage alliance between Chandragupta and Seleucus, but details are debated.

## Megasthenes at Mauryan Court
Megasthenes was sent as ambassador by Seleucus to Chandragupta’s court.

## Chandragupta’s Empire
Chandragupta controlled most of northern India and parts of the north-west.

## Chandragupta and Jainism
Jain tradition says Chandragupta became a Jain monk under Bhadrabahu and migrated to Karnataka.

## Bhadrabahu
Jain teacher associated with Chandragupta’s later life in Jain tradition.

## Shravanabelagola
Jain site in Karnataka associated with Chandragupta and Bhadrabahu tradition.

## Chandragiri Hill
Hill at Shravanabelagola linked with Chandragupta Maurya in Jain tradition.

## Sallekhana of Chandragupta
Jain tradition says Chandragupta died by Sallekhana, a ritual fast unto death.

---

# 6. CHANAKYA / KAUTILYA

## Chanakya
Political adviser, teacher, and strategist traditionally credited with helping Chandragupta establish the Mauryan Empire.

## Kautilya
Name associated with the author of Arthashastra.

## Vishnugupta
Another name linked with Kautilya.

## Arthashastra Author
Traditionally Kautilya, though the text may have undergone later additions.

## Realpolitik
Practical politics based on power, strategy, diplomacy, and state interest. Kautilya’s ideas are often described this way.

## Saptanga Theory
Theory that the state has seven limbs: king, ministers, territory, fort, treasury, army, and allies.

## Mandala Theory
Kautilya’s theory of foreign policy based on circles of neighboring states.

## Matsya Nyaya
“Law of fish”, meaning the strong swallow the weak when there is no ruler or law.

## Dandaniti
Science of punishment and governance.

## Rajadharma
Duties of the king.

## Arthashastra State
A highly organized state with departments, taxes, spies, officials, and legal rules.

---

# 7. ARTHASHASTRA TERMS

## Arthashastra
A manual of statecraft dealing with governance, economy, law, military, espionage, diplomacy, and administration.

## Artha
Material prosperity, political power, and economic interest.

## Shastra
Treatise or systematic text.

## Saptanga State
Seven elements of state: Swamin, Amatya, Janapada, Durga, Kosa, Danda, and Mitra.

## Swamin
The king or ruler.

## Amatya
Minister or official.

## Janapada
Territory and population.

## Durga
Fortified capital or fort.

## Kosa
Treasury.

## Danda
Army or coercive force.

## Mitra
Ally.

## Vijigishu
The ruler who desires conquest.

## Ari
Enemy.

## Mitra
Ally.

## Ari-Mitra
Enemy’s ally.

## Mitra-Mitra
Ally’s ally.

## Madhyama
Middle king, powerful enough to affect conflict.

## Udasina
Neutral king.

## Six Measures of Foreign Policy
Peace, war, neutrality, marching, alliance, and dual policy.

## Sandhi
Peace or treaty.

## Vigraha
War.

## Asana
Remaining quiet or neutrality.

## Yana
Marching or preparing for expedition.

## Samsraya
Seeking shelter or alliance.

## Dvaidhibhava
Dual policy of peace with one ruler and war with another.

## Sama
Conciliation.

## Dana
Gift or concession.

## Bheda
Division or creating dissension.

## Danda
Punishment or force.

## Upaya
Means or strategy.

## Espionage
Use of spies to gather information and control threats.

## Gudhapurusha
Secret agent or spy.

## Sanstha
Stationary spy.

## Sanchara
Wandering spy.

## Tirtha
High officer or department head in Arthashastra context.

## Adhyaksha
Superintendent or head of a department.

## Vyavahara
Legal procedure or judicial matter.

## Kantakashodhana
Removal of thorns; department dealing with crime, anti-social elements, and public order.

## Dharmasthiya
Court dealing with civil law.

## Rajashasana
Royal order.

---

# 8. BINDUSARA

## Bindusara
Second Mauryan ruler, son of Chandragupta Maurya and father of Ashoka.

## Amitraghata
A title of Bindusara meaning “slayer of enemies”.

## Amitrochates
Greek form often identified with Bindusara.

## Bindusara’s Expansion
