Bindusara is believed to have extended Mauryan control into the Deccan.

## Bindusara and Deccan
Tradition suggests Bindusara conquered the land between the Arabian Sea and Bay of Bengal, except parts of the far south.

## Bindusara and Greeks
Bindusara maintained diplomatic relations with Hellenistic rulers.

## Deimachus
Greek ambassador to Bindusara’s court, sent by Antiochus I.

## Antiochus I
Seleucid ruler who had diplomatic relations with Bindusara.

## Dionysius
Greek envoy possibly sent by Ptolemy II to the Mauryan court.

## Bindusara and Ajivikas
Some traditions associate Bindusara with interest in Ajivikas.

## Bindusara’s Sons
Ashoka and Susima were among his sons according to tradition.

## Susima
Elder brother or rival of Ashoka in Buddhist traditions.

## Ashoka as Prince
Ashoka served as prince-governor before becoming emperor.

## Taxila Revolt under Bindusara
Traditions mention unrest in Taxila during Bindusara’s reign.

## Ujjain Governorship
Ashoka is traditionally said to have served as governor of Ujjain.

---

# 9. ASHOKA: EARLY LIFE AND ACCESSION

## Ashoka
Third and greatest Mauryan emperor, known for conquest of Kalinga and later policy of Dhamma.

## Ashoka Meaning
The name Ashoka means “without sorrow”.

## Devanampiya
Title used by Ashoka in inscriptions, meaning “Beloved of the Gods”.

## Piyadasi
Title used by Ashoka, meaning “of gracious appearance” or “he who looks with affection”.

## Devanampiya Piyadasi
Most common title used by Ashoka in his edicts.

## Ashoka’s Identification
Ashoka was identified with Devanampiya Piyadasi through inscriptions such as the Maski inscription.

## Maski Inscription
Important inscription that directly mentions the name Ashoka.

## Ashoka as Governor
Tradition says Ashoka governed Ujjain or Taxila before becoming emperor.

## Ashoka’s Accession
Ashoka became king after Bindusara, possibly after a succession struggle.

## Ashoka’s Coronation
Ashoka’s formal coronation is traditionally placed a few years after accession.

## Ashoka’s Early Reign
Before the Kalinga War, Ashoka followed conventional imperial policies.

## Chandashoka
A legendary title meaning “Ashoka the Fierce”, used in Buddhist traditions for his early life.

## Dharmashoka
A legendary title meaning “Ashoka of Dhamma”, used for Ashoka after his moral transformation.

---

# 10. KALINGA WAR

## Kalinga
Region roughly corresponding to coastal Odisha and northern Andhra Pradesh.

## Kalinga War
Major war fought by Ashoka against Kalinga, usually dated around the 8th year of his reign.

## Kalinga Conquest
Ashoka conquered Kalinga, but the suffering caused by war deeply affected him.

## Major Rock Edict XIII
The most important edict describing the Kalinga War and Ashoka’s remorse.

## Casualties of Kalinga War
Ashoka’s edict mentions large numbers killed, deported, and affected by the war.

## Ashoka’s Remorse
Ashoka expressed sorrow over the suffering caused by the conquest of Kalinga.

## Turning Point of Ashoka
The Kalinga War changed Ashoka’s policy from aggressive conquest to moral conquest.

## Dhammavijaya
Conquest by Dhamma or moral conquest, promoted by Ashoka after Kalinga.

## Bherighosha
Sound of war drum.

## Dhammaghosha
Sound or proclamation of Dhamma.

## From Bherighosha to Dhammaghosha
Ashoka’s shift from military conquest to moral persuasion.

## Kalinga Edicts
Separate edicts issued for Kalinga, especially at Dhauli and Jaugada.

## Dhauli
Ashokan inscription site in Odisha associated with Kalinga edicts.

## Jaugada
Ashokan inscription site in Odisha associated with Kalinga edicts.

---

# 11. ASHOKA’S DHAMMA

## Dhamma
Ashoka’s ethical and social policy, not a sectarian religion.

## Ashoka’s Dhamma
A moral code emphasizing compassion, non-violence, respect for elders, generosity, truthfulness, and religious tolerance.

## Dhammavijaya
Victory through morality instead of violence.

## Dhamma-Mangala
Auspicious ceremony of Dhamma, involving moral conduct rather than empty rituals.

## Dhamma-Yatra
Tour of Dhamma, replacing royal pleasure tours.

## Vihara-Yatra
Pleasure tour or royal hunt, which Ashoka reduced after adopting Dhamma.

## Dhamma-Mahamatta
Officials appointed by Ashoka to spread and supervise Dhamma.

## Moral Welfare
Ashoka’s concern for ethical improvement of people.

## Social Harmony
Ashoka promoted respect between religious sects, families, officials, and communities.

## Religious Tolerance
Ashoka asked people to respect all sects and avoid criticizing others unfairly.

## Non-Violence
Ashoka discouraged unnecessary killing and cruelty.

## Limited Animal Slaughter
Ashoka restricted animal slaughter in royal kitchens and rituals.

## Compassion for Animals
Ashoka promoted care for animals and banned killing of some species on certain days.

## Respect for Parents
A key part of Ashoka’s Dhamma.

## Respect for Elders
Ashoka emphasized obedience and respect toward elders.

## Respect for Brahmanas and Shramanas
Ashoka repeatedly asked people to honor Brahmanas and Shramanas.

## Kindness to Servants
Ashoka encouraged humane treatment of servants and workers.

## Charity
Giving to Brahmanas, Shramanas, friends, relatives, and the poor was encouraged.

## Truthfulness
Moral truthfulness was part of Dhamma.

## Purity of Conduct
Clean and ethical personal behavior.

## Self-Control
Control over anger, cruelty, pride, and jealousy.

## Gratitude
A moral quality promoted by Ashoka.

## Firm Devotion
Moral commitment to Dhamma.

## Dhamma as Practical Ethics
Ashoka’s Dhamma focused more on everyday morality than on metaphysical doctrine.

## Dhamma and Buddhism
Ashoka personally supported Buddhism, but his Dhamma was broader and meant for all subjects.

## Dhamma and State Policy
Ashoka used the state machinery to promote moral behavior and welfare.

---

# 12. ASHOKAN INSCRIPTIONS: BASIC TERMS

## Edict
An official order or message inscribed on stone, pillar, or cave wall.

## Rock Edict
An inscription carved on a natural rock surface.

## Pillar Edict
An inscription engraved on a stone pillar.

## Cave Inscription
An inscription carved inside or near caves.

## Major Rock Edicts
A group of important inscriptions explaining Ashoka’s Dhamma, administration, Kalinga War, and foreign relations.

## Minor Rock Edicts
Shorter inscriptions, often more personal and directly linked to Ashoka’s Buddhist commitment.

## Major Pillar Edicts
Important inscriptions on Ashokan pillars dealing with Dhamma, administration, justice, and welfare.

## Minor Pillar Edicts
Shorter pillar inscriptions, often linked with Buddhist Sangha or specific sacred places.

## Separate Kalinga Edicts
Special edicts issued for Kalinga at Dhauli and Jaugada.

## Bilingual Inscriptions
Inscriptions written in two languages, such as Greek and Aramaic.

## Greek Edict
Ashokan inscription in Greek, found in north-western regions.

## Aramaic Edict
Ashokan inscription in Aramaic, used in north-western regions.

## Brahmi Script
Main script used in most Ashokan inscriptions.

## Kharosthi Script
Script used in north-western Ashokan inscriptions, written from right to left.

## Greek Script
Used in some Ashokan inscriptions in Afghanistan.

## Aramaic Script
Used in some Ashokan inscriptions in Afghanistan and north-west regions.

## Prakrit Language
Main language used in most Ashokan edicts.

## Magadhi Prakrit
Eastern Prakrit form used in several Ashokan inscriptions.

## Northwestern Prakrit
Prakrit form used in Kharosthi inscriptions.

## Decipherment of Brahmi
James Prinsep deciphered Brahmi script in the 19th century.

## James Prinsep
Scholar who deciphered Brahmi and Kharosthi, making Ashokan inscriptions readable.

---

# 13. MAJOR ROCK EDICTS

## Major Rock Edict I
Deals with prohibition or restriction of animal sacrifice and reduction of animal killing in royal kitchen.

## Major Rock Edict II
Mentions medical treatment for humans and animals, planting of medicinal herbs, wells, and trees.

## Major Rock Edict III
Orders officials to spread Dhamma and instruct people in moral conduct.

## Major Rock Edict IV
Says Dhamma has reduced cruelty and increased morality.

## Major Rock Edict V
Mentions appointment of Dhamma Mahamattas.

## Major Rock Edict VI
Emphasizes the king’s availability for public business and welfare.

## Major Rock Edict VII
Promotes religious tolerance and harmony among sects.

## Major Rock Edict VIII
Mentions Ashoka’s Dhamma-yatras instead of pleasure tours.

## Major Rock Edict IX
Criticizes empty ceremonies and promotes Dhamma-mangala.

## Major Rock Edict X
Rejects worldly fame and emphasizes fame through Dhamma.

## Major Rock Edict XI
Explains Dhamma as moral conduct and generosity.

## Major Rock Edict XII
Promotes respect among all religious sects.

## Major Rock Edict XIII
Describes Kalinga War, Ashoka’s remorse, and Dhammavijaya.

## Major Rock Edict XIV
Explains that Ashoka’s edicts were issued in different forms and lengths across the empire.

---

# 14. MAJOR PILLAR EDICTS

## Major Pillar Edict I
Explains Ashoka’s principles of Dhamma and moral administration.

## Major Pillar Edict II
Mentions Dhamma as compassion, charity, truthfulness, purity, gentleness, and goodness.

## Major Pillar Edict III
Warns against sins such as cruelty, anger, pride, and jealousy.

## Major Pillar Edict IV
Deals with duties of Rajukas and justice.

## Major Pillar Edict V
Deals with protection of animals and restrictions on killing.

## Major Pillar Edict VI
Emphasizes Ashoka’s concern for all sects and moral welfare.

## Major Pillar Edict VII
A summary of Ashoka’s Dhamma policy and achievements.

---

# 15. MINOR ROCK AND PILLAR INSCRIPTIONS

## Minor Rock Edict I
Shows Ashoka’s personal commitment to Buddhism and Dhamma.

## Minor Rock Edict II
Gives moral instructions to officials and people.

## Bhabru Edict
Also called Bairat Edict; shows Ashoka’s respect for Buddhist scriptures.

## Bairat Edict
Another name for Bhabru Edict.

## Maski Inscription
Important because it directly uses the name Ashoka.

## Gujarra Inscription
Also mentions Ashoka by name.

## Nittur Inscription
Minor Rock Edict site in Karnataka.

## Udegolam Inscription
Minor Rock Edict site in Karnataka.

## Brahmagiri Inscription
Minor Rock Edict site in Karnataka.

## Siddapur Inscription
Minor Rock Edict site in Karnataka.

## Jatinga-Rameshwar Inscription
Minor Rock Edict site in Karnataka.

## Rummindei Pillar Inscription
Inscription at Lumbini marking Buddha’s birthplace and granting tax concession.

## Lumbini Inscription
Another name for Rummindei inscription.

## Nigali Sagar Pillar Inscription
Inscription recording Ashoka’s enlargement of the stupa of Kanakamuni Buddha.

## Sarnath Schism Edict
Minor Pillar Edict warning against division in the Buddhist Sangha.

## Sanchi Schism Edict
Edict dealing with unity of the Buddhist Sangha.

## Kaushambi Schism Edict
Edict warning monks and nuns against causing schism.

## Queen’s Edict
Inscription mentioning donations by Ashoka’s queen Karuvaki.

## Karuvaki
Queen of Ashoka mentioned in the Queen’s Edict.

## Tivara
Son of Ashoka and Karuvaki, mentioned in the Queen’s Edict.

## Barabar Cave Inscriptions
Inscriptions recording Ashoka’s donation of caves to Ajivikas.

## Nagarjuni Cave Inscriptions
Inscriptions of Dasharatha Maurya donating caves to Ajivikas.

---

# 16. IMPORTANT ASHOKAN INSCRIPTION SITES

## Girnar
Major Rock Edict site in Gujarat.

## Shahbazgarhi
Major Rock Edict site in present-day Pakistan, written in Kharosthi.

## Mansehra
Major Rock Edict site in present-day Pakistan, written in Kharosthi.

## Kalsi
Major Rock Edict site in Uttarakhand.

## Sopara
Major Rock Edict site in Maharashtra.

## Dhauli
Major Rock Edict and Separate Kalinga Edict site in Odisha.

## Jaugada
Separate Kalinga Edict site in Odisha.

## Erragudi
Major and Minor Rock Edict site in Andhra Pradesh.

## Sannati
Important Ashokan inscription site in Karnataka.

## Kandahar
Site of Greek and Aramaic Ashokan inscriptions in Afghanistan.

## Laghman
Aramaic inscription site in Afghanistan.

## Taxila
North-western region with Ashokan inscriptional and Mauryan importance.

## Delhi-Topra Pillar
Ashokan pillar originally from Topra, later moved to Delhi by Firoz Shah Tughlaq.

## Delhi-Meerut Pillar
Ashokan pillar originally from Meerut, later moved to Delhi.

## Lauriya Nandangarh
Ashokan pillar site in Bihar.

## Lauriya Araraj
Ashokan pillar site in Bihar.

## Rampurva
Ashokan pillar site in Bihar, famous for bull and lion capitals.

## Sarnath
Ashokan pillar site famous for Lion Capital.

## Sanchi
Ashokan pillar and stupa site in Madhya Pradesh.

## Lumbini
Ashokan pillar site marking Buddha’s birthplace.

## Nigali Sagar
Ashokan pillar site associated with Kanakamuni Buddha.

## Allahabad-Kosambi Pillar
Ashokan pillar later carrying inscriptions of Samudragupta and Jahangir.

---

# 17. ASHOKAN TITLES AND PHRASES

## Devanampiya
Beloved of the Gods.

## Piyadasi
He who looks with affection or gracious appearance.

## Raja Piyadasi
King Piyadasi.

## Devanampiya Piyadasi Raja
Beloved of the Gods, King Piyadasi.

## Ashoka
Personal name confirmed in some inscriptions.

## Laja
Prakrit form of Raja in inscriptions.

## Dhamma
Moral law or ethical conduct.

## Dhammalipi
Dhamma inscription.

## Dhammavijaya
Conquest through Dhamma.

## Dhammayatra
Tour of Dhamma.

## Dhamma Mahamatta
Officer of Dhamma.

## Savapasanda
All sects or religious communities.

## Brahmana-Shramana
Brahmanas and renunciants, often mentioned together in Ashokan edicts.

---

# 18. MAURYAN ADMINISTRATION: CENTRAL GOVERNMENT

## Mauryan Administration
A highly organized administrative system with central, provincial, district, urban, and village levels.

## King
The supreme authority in the Mauryan state.

## Divine Kingship
The Mauryan king was powerful, but Ashoka projected himself more as a moral father than as a god.

## Paternal Kingship
Ashoka said all people were his children, showing a welfare-oriented royal image.

## Mantriparishad
Council of ministers advising the king.

## Mantrin
Minister.

## Amatya
High official or administrator.

## Mahamatra
High-ranking official in Mauryan administration.

## Sachiva
Secretary or ministerial officer.

## Purohita
Royal priest or adviser.

## Senapati
Commander-in-chief of the army.

## Yuvaraja
Crown prince.

## Kumar
Prince, often appointed as provincial governor.

## Rajaputra
Royal prince.

## Royal Secretariat
Administrative office assisting the king and ministers.

## Centralized Bureaucracy
System of appointed officials controlling revenue, law, military, economy, and welfare.

## Bureaucracy
Government run through officials and departments.

## Departmental Administration
Mauryan administration had departments for mines, trade, forests, agriculture, weights, taxes, and more.

## Adhyaksha
Superintendent or head of a department.

## Tirtha
High official or major administrative post in Arthashastra.

---

# 19. MAURYAN ADMINISTRATION: IMPORTANT OFFICIALS

## Samaharta
Chief revenue collector.

## Sannidhata
Treasurer or officer in charge of the state treasury and stores.

## Akshapataladhyaksha
Chief accountant or keeper of records.

## Sitadhyaksha
Superintendent of agriculture or crown lands.

## Panyadhyaksha
Superintendent of commerce.

## Sulkadhyaksha
Superintendent of tolls and customs.

## Pautavadhyaksha
Superintendent of weights and measures.

## Manadhyaksha
Superintendent of measurements.

## Akaradhyaksha
Superintendent of mines.

## Lohadhyaksha
Superintendent of iron or metals.

## Suvarnadhyaksha
Superintendent of gold.

## Lavanadhyaksha
Superintendent of salt.

## Navadhyaksha
Superintendent of ships or navigation.

## Pattanadhyaksha
Superintendent of ports.

## Suradhyaksha
Superintendent of liquor.

## Sutradhyaksha
Superintendent of spinning and weaving.

## Kupyadhyaksha
Superintendent of forest produce.

## Hastyadhyaksha
Superintendent of elephants.

## Ashvadhyaksha
Superintendent of horses.

## Goadhyaksha
Superintendent of cattle.

## Ayudhagaradhyaksha
Superintendent of armoury.

## Mudradhyaksha
Superintendent of passports or seals.

## Bandhanagaradhyaksha
Superintendent of prisons.

## Ganikaadhyaksha
Superintendent of courtesans.

## Devatadhyaksha
Superintendent of temples or religious establishments.

## Nagaraka
City superintendent.

## Pradeshika
Provincial or district-level officer.

## Rajuka
Officer responsible for revenue, survey, and justice in rural areas.

## Yukta
Subordinate official or clerk.

## Gopa
Village-level record keeper or officer over groups of households.

## Sthanika
Officer over a local administrative unit.

## Dhamma Mahamatta
Officer appointed by Ashoka to promote Dhamma.

## Anta Mahamatta
Officer posted in frontier regions.

## Itijhaka Mahamatta
Officer concerned with women or royal women, according to some interpretations.

## Purusha
Official or agent mentioned in Ashokan inscriptions.

## Pativedaka
Reporter or informant who conveyed public matters to the king.

## Vachabhumikas
Officers related to cattle or pasture, mentioned in some contexts.

---

# 20. PROVINCIAL ADMINISTRATION

## Province
Large administrative division of the empire.

## Provincial Governor
Official or prince governing a province.

## Kumara as Governor
Princes were often appointed as governors of important provinces.

## Aryaputra
Royal prince or noble appointed in provincial administration.

## Uttarapatha Province
North-western province with Taxila as a major center.

## Taxila
Important provincial capital in the north-west.

## Avantiratha Province
Western province centered around Ujjain.

## Ujjain
Important provincial capital in western India.

## Dakshinapatha Province
Southern province with Suvarnagiri as an important center.

## Suvarnagiri
Important southern provincial center, probably linked with gold regions.

## Kalinga Province
Province added after Ashoka’s conquest of Kalinga.

## Tosali
Provincial capital or administrative center in Kalinga.

## Samapa
Administrative center in Kalinga region mentioned in edicts.

## Prachya
Eastern core region around Magadha.

## Pataliputra as Central Capital
The main imperial capital from which the emperor and central administration ruled.

## Provincial Council
Officials assisting provincial governors.

## Provincial Autonomy
Some provinces had local flexibility but remained under central control.

## Taxila Revolts
Revolts in Taxila show tension between provincial populations and officials.

---

# 21. DISTRICT AND LOCAL ADMINISTRATION

## District Administration
Administration below the provincial level.

## Janapada Administration
Management of rural territory and population.

## Pradeshika
Officer who supervised local administration and toured districts.

## Rajuka
Officer with powers over land measurement, revenue, and justice.

## Yukta
Subordinate officer involved in record-keeping and execution of orders.

## Gopa
Officer keeping records of households, villages, and taxes.

## Sthanika
Officer supervising a group of villages or local unit.

## Grama
Village.

## Gramika
Village headman.

## Village Administration
Basic rural governance through headmen, elders, and state officials.

## Land Survey
Measurement and classification of land for taxation.

## Census
Counting population, households, livestock, and resources for administrative purposes.

## Record-Keeping
Maintaining records of land, taxes, births, deaths, and property.

## Royal Tours
Tours by officials and king for inspection and moral instruction.

## Administrative Inspection
Checking officials, revenue collection, justice, and public works.

---

# 22. MUNICIPAL ADMINISTRATION

## Municipal Administration
Administration of cities and towns.

## Nagaraka
Chief city officer.

## Pataliputra Municipal Board
Megasthenes describes a municipal administration with committees.

## Six Municipal Committees
According to Megasthenes, Pataliputra had six boards dealing with different urban functions.

## Industrial Committee
Committee supervising crafts and industries.

## Foreigners Committee
Committee looking after foreigners, their residence, safety, and property.

## Births and Deaths Committee
Committee recording births and deaths.

## Trade Committee
Committee regulating trade and markets.

## Manufactured Goods Committee
Committee supervising sale and quality of manufactured goods.

## Tax Committee
Committee collecting tax on sold goods.

## Urban Sanitation
Maintenance of cleanliness, roads, drainage, and public order.

## Market Regulation
Control of trade, prices, weights, measures, and fraud.

## Foreign Visitor Supervision
State control over foreign travelers and merchants.

## Urban Record System
System of recording population and commercial activity in cities.

---

# 23. MILITARY ADMINISTRATION

## Mauryan Army
One of the largest armies of ancient India.

## Standing Army
Permanent army maintained by the state.

## Chaturangabala
Fourfold army consisting of infantry, cavalry, chariots, and elephants.

## Infantry
Foot soldiers.

## Cavalry
Horse soldiers.

## Chariotry
War chariot units.

## Elephant Corps
War elephants used in battle.

## Navy
Mauryan state likely had water transport and naval arrangements, especially for rivers and coasts.

## War Office
Military administration described by Megasthenes.

## Military Board
Megasthenes mentions a board of thirty members divided into six committees.

## Six Military Committees
Committees for navy, transport, infantry, cavalry, chariots, and elephants.

## Senapati
Commander-in-chief.

## Nayaka
Military leader or officer.

## Dandanayaka
Officer connected with punishment or military authority.

## Ayudhagara
Armoury or weapons store.

## Ayudhagaradhyaksha
Superintendent of armoury.

## Hastyadhyaksha
Superintendent of elephants.

## Ashvadhyaksha
Superintendent of horses.

## Rathadhyaksha
Superintendent of chariots.

## Padyadhyaksha
Superintendent of infantry.

## War Elephant
Important military asset of Magadha and Mauryas.

## Fortification
Military defense through forts and fortified cities.

## Durga
Fort.

## Skandhavara
Military camp.

## Espionage in Military
Use of spies for military intelligence and enemy weakness.

## Logistics
Supply of food, animals, weapons, transport, and equipment to the army.

---

# 24. REVENUE ADMINISTRATION

## Revenue System
System of collecting taxes and income for the state.

## Samaharta
Chief revenue collector.

## Sannidhata
Treasurer.

## Kosa
Treasury.

## Bhaga
King’s share of agricultural produce, often understood as land revenue.

## Bali
Tribute or traditional payment.

## Kara
Tax.

## Shulka
Customs duty or toll.

## Pindakara
A tax collected from groups of villages.

## Hiranya
Cash payment or gold payment.

## Udranga
Additional tax or levy.

## Uparikara
Extra tax or surcharge.

## Visti
Forced labour or unpaid labour demanded by the state.

## State Monopoly
State control over important resources like mines, salt, forests, and liquor.

## Crown Land
Land directly owned or managed by the state.

## Sita Land
Crown land or state agricultural land.

## Sitadhyaksha
Officer in charge of crown lands and agriculture.

## Irrigation Tax
Tax collected for use of state irrigation facilities.

## Water Tax
Payment for state-provided water or irrigation.

## Trade Tax
Tax on trade goods.

## Transit Duty
Tax on goods moving through roads, rivers, or frontiers.

## Customs Duty
Tax on imported or exported goods.

## Sales Tax
Tax on sale of goods, mentioned by Megasthenes as a tenth of sale price.

## Tithe
One-tenth tax, often associated with trade in Greek descriptions.

## Fines
Revenue collected through penalties for legal offences.

## Confiscation
State seizure of property as punishment or revenue measure.

---

# 25. ECONOMY OF THE MAURYAN EMPIRE

## Mauryan Economy
A mixed economy based on agriculture, trade, craft production, taxation, state control, and long-distance exchange.

## Agrarian Economy
Agriculture was the main economic base.

## Agricultural Surplus
Extra produce supported cities, army, officials, and artisans.

## Crown Agriculture
Agriculture on state-owned lands.

## Private Cultivation
Cultivation by peasants and landholders.

## Peasant
Agricultural cultivator.

## Gahapati
Wealthy householder or landowner.

## Irrigation
Artificial watering of fields through canals, tanks, wells, and reservoirs.

## Sudarshana Lake
Artificial lake in Gujarat originally associated with Mauryan period under Chandragupta’s governor Pushyagupta.

## Pushyagupta
Governor under Chandragupta Maurya associated with construction of Sudarshana Lake.

## Tushaspha
Yavana governor under Ashoka associated with later improvements to Sudarshana Lake.

## Junagadh Inscription
Later inscription of Rudradaman mentioning Sudarshana Lake and Mauryan officials.

## State Farming
Cultivation managed by the state on crown lands.

## Taxation of Agriculture
The state collected a share of produce from cultivators.

## Animal Husbandry
Rearing cattle, horses, elephants, sheep, goats, and other animals.

## Cattle Wealth
Cattle remained important for agriculture, dairy, transport, and economy.

## Elephant Forests
Forests reserved for capturing and maintaining elephants.

## Forest Economy
Use of forests for timber, animals, minerals, honey, medicinal plants, and other produce.

## Mining
Extraction of metals and minerals under state supervision.

## Metallurgy
Production and working of metals.

## Iron
Important for tools, weapons, agriculture, and state expansion.

## Copper
Used for tools, vessels, and coins.

## Gold
Used for ornaments and high-value objects.

## Silver
Used especially in punch-marked coins.

## Salt
Important state-controlled commodity.

## Liquor
State-regulated commodity in Arthashastra.

## Textile Production
Important craft sector involving spinning, weaving, and dyeing.

## Weaving
Production of cloth.

## Spinning
Making thread from cotton, wool, or other fibers.

## State Workshops
Workshops controlled by the state for production of goods.

## Guilds
Associations of merchants and artisans.

## Shreni
Guild or professional association.

## Trade
Exchange of goods within and outside the empire.

## Internal Trade
Trade within the Mauryan Empire.

## External Trade
Trade with foreign regions such as Hellenistic West, Central Asia, and Sri Lanka.

## Uttarapatha
Northern trade route connecting the Ganga valley to north-west India and Central Asia.

## Dakshinapatha
Southern trade route connecting north India with Deccan and south India.

## River Trade
Trade through rivers like Ganga, Yamuna, Son, and Indus.

## Maritime Trade
Trade through coastal and sea routes.

## Port
A coastal center used for trade.

## Tamralipti
Important eastern port associated with trade and Buddhist missions.

## Bharukachchha
Western port known later as Barygaza, important for trade.

## Sopara
Western coastal port in Maharashtra region.

## Pataliputra as Economic Centre
Capital city and major administrative-commercial center.

## Taxila as Trade Centre
North-western trade and learning center.

## Ujjain as Trade Centre
Important city on routes connecting north, west, and Deccan.

---

# 26. COINS AND MONEY

## Punch-Marked Coins
Early coins used during Mauryan and pre-Mauryan periods, marked with punched symbols.

## Silver Punch-Marked Coins
Most common early coins, used for trade and taxation.

## Karshapana
A common coin or monetary unit.

## Pana
Monetary unit mentioned in Arthashastra.

## Mashaka
Small coin or unit.

## Kakani
Very small monetary unit.

## Rupa
Metallic form or coin-like object; later root of rupee.

## Rupadarshaka
Officer who examined coins.

## Lakshanadhyaksha
Superintendent of mint or coinage.

## Minting
Process of making coins.

## Coin Standard
Official weight and quality of coinage.

## Money Economy
An economy using coins for exchange, wages, and taxation.

## Barter
Exchange of goods without coins, still present especially in rural areas.

---

# 27. TRADE AND COMMERCE

## Commerce
Buying and selling of goods.

## Merchant
Person engaged in trade.

## Vanij
Trader.

## Sarthavaha
Caravan leader.

## Sartha
Caravan.

## Panyadhyaksha
Superintendent of trade and commodities.

## Market
Place where goods were exchanged.

## Price Control
State regulation of prices.

## Profit Regulation
Arthashastra mentions regulation of profit margins.

## Weights and Measures
Standard units used in trade.

## Pautavadhyaksha
Superintendent of weights.

## Manadhyaksha
Superintendent of measures.

## Customs House
Place where trade taxes were collected.

## Sulkadhyaksha
Superintendent of tolls and customs.

## Import
Goods brought from outside.

## Export
Goods sent outside.

## Transit Trade
Trade passing through a region.

## Royal Road
Major road maintained by the state.

## Roadside Facilities
Ashoka mentions wells, trees, and rest facilities for humans and animals.

## Caravan Trade
Long-distance trade using groups of merchants and animals.

## Maritime Trade
Sea-based trade.

## Navigation
Movement by rivers and sea.

## Navadhyaksha
Superintendent of ships or water transport.

---

# 28. SOCIETY UNDER THE MAURYAS

## Mauryan Society
A diverse society with peasants, artisans, merchants, officials, soldiers, monks, Brahmanas, Shramanas, tribes, and foreigners.

## Varna System
Fourfold social classification of Brahmana, Kshatriya, Vaishya, and Shudra.

## Brahmana
Priestly and learned group.

## Kshatriya
Ruling and warrior group.

## Vaishya
Producer group associated with agriculture, trade, and cattle.

## Shudra
Service and laboring group.

## Jati
Birth-based social group or community.

## Megasthenes’ Seven Classes
Megasthenes described Indian society in seven groups, though this does not match the varna system exactly.

## Philosophers
One of Megasthenes’ classes, likely including Brahmanas and Shramanas.

## Farmers
Agricultural producers.

## Herders
People engaged in animal rearing.

## Artisans
Craft workers.

## Soldiers
Military class.

## Overseers
Officials supervising public activities.

## Councillors
Advisers and administrators.

## Slavery Debate
Megasthenes claimed there was no slavery in India, but Indian sources mention dasas and forms of servitude.

## Dasa
Servant, slave, or dependent worker.

## Karmakara
Laborer or worker.

## Women in Mauryan Society
Women participated in household life, some economic activities, court life, and religious patronage.

## Royal Women
Women of the royal household, including queens like Karuvaki.

## Karuvaki
Ashoka’s queen mentioned in an inscription.

## Female Officials
Arthashastra mentions officials connected with women’s quarters and women’s welfare.

## Ganika
Courtesan, regulated by the state in Arthashastra.

## Ganikaadhyaksha
Superintendent of courtesans.

## Urban Society
City-based population including merchants, artisans, officials, monks, and foreigners.

## Rural Society
Village-based population mainly involved in agriculture and animal husbandry.

## Tribal Communities
Forest and frontier communities living within or near the empire.

## Atavikas
Forest tribes or forest people mentioned in Ashokan inscriptions.

## Frontier Peoples
People living near the empire’s borders, addressed by Ashoka through Dhamma policy.

---

# 29. RELIGION UNDER THE MAURYAS

## Religious Diversity
The Mauryan Empire included Brahmanas, Buddhists, Jains, Ajivikas, and other sects.

## Brahmanism
Vedic-Brahmanical tradition continued during the Mauryan period.

## Buddhism
Received major patronage under Ashoka.

## Jainism
Associated with Chandragupta in Jain tradition and continued under later Mauryas.

## Ajivika Sect
Ascetic sect that received cave donations from Ashoka and Dasharatha.

## Shramana
Renunciant traditions such as Buddhism, Jainism, and Ajivikas.

## Brahmana-Shramana
Pair frequently mentioned by Ashoka to show respect for different religious groups.

## Religious Tolerance
Ashoka promoted respect for all sects.

## Sectarian Harmony
Ashoka asked religious groups to avoid insulting each other.

## Animal Sacrifice Restriction
Ashoka discouraged or restricted animal sacrifice.

## Buddhist Patronage
Ashoka supported Buddhist institutions, stupas, and missions.

## Third Buddhist Council
Traditionally held at Pataliputra under Ashoka’s patronage.

## Moggaliputta Tissa
Buddhist elder associated with the Third Buddhist Council.

## Buddhist Missions
Missions sent to different regions during Ashoka’s reign according to Buddhist tradition.

## Mahinda
Ashoka’s son, traditionally sent to Sri Lanka as a Buddhist missionary.

## Sanghamitta
Ashoka’s daughter, traditionally associated with taking the Bodhi tree branch to Sri Lanka.

## Devanampiya Tissa
Sri Lankan ruler who accepted Buddhism during Ashoka’s time.

## Bodhi Tree
Tree under which Buddha attained enlightenment; Ashoka patronized Bodh Gaya.

## Stupa Worship
Veneration of relic mounds, promoted in Buddhist tradition under Ashoka.

## Ajivika Patronage
Ashoka donated Barabar caves to Ajivikas.

---

# 30. ASHOKA AND BUDDHISM

## Ashoka’s Conversion
Tradition says Ashoka became a Buddhist after the Kalinga War, though the process may have been gradual.

## Upagupta
Buddhist monk associated in legends with Ashoka’s pilgrimage and guidance.

## Moggaliputta Tissa
Buddhist elder linked with Ashoka and the Third Council.

## Third Buddhist Council
Council traditionally held at Pataliputra to purify the Sangha and settle doctrinal issues.

## Kathavatthu
Text traditionally associated with Moggaliputta Tissa and the Third Council.

## Ashoka’s Pilgrimage
Ashoka visited Buddhist sacred places such as Lumbini and Bodh Gaya according to inscriptions and tradition.

## Lumbini Visit
Ashoka visited Buddha’s birthplace and reduced taxes there.

## Kanakamuni Buddha Stupa
Ashoka enlarged a stupa of the previous Buddha Kanakamuni at Nigali Sagar.

## Buddhist Sangha
Monastic community supported but also regulated by Ashoka.

## Schism Edicts
Ashoka warned monks and nuns against causing division in the Sangha.

## Ashoka and Stupas
Tradition credits Ashoka with building or enlarging many stupas.

## Relic Redistribution
Tradition says Ashoka redistributed Buddha’s relics into numerous stupas.

## Ashoka’s Buddhism vs Dhamma
Ashoka personally supported Buddhism, but Dhamma was broader moral policy for all subjects.

---

# 31. MAURYAN ART

## Mauryan Art
Art and architecture produced during the Mauryan period, including pillars, capitals, caves, sculptures, and polished stone works.

## Court Art
Art sponsored by the Mauryan state, such as pillars and capitals.

## Popular Art
Art produced outside royal workshops, including Yaksha and Yakshi sculptures.

## Mauryan Polish
Highly smooth, shiny polish seen on Mauryan stone pillars and sculptures.

## Ashokan Pillars
Monolithic stone pillars erected by Ashoka with inscriptions and animal capitals.

## Monolithic Pillar
A pillar made from a single piece of stone.

## Chunar Sandstone
Stone from Chunar quarries used for many Mauryan pillars.

## Pillar Shaft
Long smooth cylindrical part of a pillar.

## Bell Capital
Lotus-like inverted bell shape below the animal capital.

## Abacus
The platform above the bell capital, often decorated with animals or wheels.

## Animal Capital
Top part of the pillar showing animals such as lion, bull, elephant, or horse.

## Lion Capital
The most famous Ashokan capital, especially at Sarnath.

## Sarnath Lion Capital
Four-lion capital from Sarnath, adopted as India’s National Emblem.

## Dharma Chakra
Wheel symbol on Sarnath capital and Indian national flag.

## Rampurva Bull Capital
Beautiful bull capital from Rampurva.

## Sankisa Elephant Capital
Elephant capital associated with Sankisa/Sankassa.

## Lauriya Nandangarh Lion Capital
Lion capital from Bihar.

## Dhauli Elephant
Rock-cut elephant figure at Dhauli in Odisha.

## Yaksha Sculpture
Large male nature-spirit sculpture, part of popular religious art.

## Yakshi Sculpture
Female nature-spirit sculpture, often associated with fertility and prosperity.

## Didarganj Yakshi
Famous polished stone female sculpture from Patna region, often associated with Mauryan or early post-Mauryan art.

## Parkham Yaksha
Large Yaksha sculpture from Mathura region.

## Besnagar Yakshi
Early Yakshi sculpture associated with popular art tradition.

## Ring Stones
Decorated stone objects from Mauryan and post-Mauryan contexts; their function is debated.

## Terracotta Art
Clay figurines and objects used by common people.

---

# 32. MAURYAN ARCHITECTURE

## Mauryan Architecture
Architecture of the Mauryan period including palaces, pillars, stupas, caves, and city structures.

## Pataliputra Palace
Mauryan palace described by Greek writers as magnificent, possibly influenced by Achaemenid models.

## Wooden Architecture
Many Mauryan buildings used wood, especially at Pataliputra.

## Pillared Hall at Kumrahar
Archaeological remains near Patna, often linked with Mauryan palace architecture.

## Kumrahar
Site near Patna with remains of a pillared hall.

## Achaemenid Influence
Persian influence seen in pillars, polish, palace style, and administrative ideas.

## Stupa
Buddhist relic mound. Ashoka is traditionally credited with building many stupas.

## Brick Stupa
Stupa made of brick.

## Sanchi Stupa
Buddhist stupa in Madhya Pradesh, originally associated with Ashoka and later enlarged.

## Bharhut Stupa
Early Buddhist stupa site, developed more in post-Mauryan period but rooted in early stupa tradition.

## Dharmarajika Stupa
Name associated with Ashokan stupas in several places.

## Barabar Caves
Rock-cut caves in Bihar donated by Ashoka to Ajivikas.

## Nagarjuni Caves
Caves donated by Dasharatha Maurya to Ajivikas.

## Rock-Cut Architecture
Architecture carved directly into rock, beginning in a major way under the Mauryas.

## Lomas Rishi Cave
Famous Barabar cave with an early chaitya-arch facade.

## Sudama Cave
Barabar cave donated by Ashoka to Ajivikas.

## Karna Chaupar Cave
Barabar cave associated with Ashoka’s donation.

## Gopi Cave
Nagarjuni cave donated by Dasharatha.

## Vapiya Cave
Nagarjuni cave associated with Dasharatha.

## Vadathika Cave
Nagarjuni cave associated with Dasharatha.

## Chaitya Arch
Horseshoe-shaped arch motif seen at Lomas Rishi cave.

## Polished Cave Interior
Barabar caves have highly polished interiors.

---

# 33. PATALIPUTRA

## Pataliputra
Capital of the Mauryan Empire and one of the largest cities of ancient India.

## Palibothra
Greek name for Pataliputra.

## Location of Pataliputra
Located near the confluence of Ganga, Son, Gandak, and other river systems.

## Strategic Location
Pataliputra controlled river trade, military movement, and administration.

## Wooden Palisade
Greek accounts and archaeology suggest Pataliputra had wooden defensive structures.

## City Wall
Pataliputra had fortifications, possibly wooden palisades and ditches.

## Moat
A defensive ditch around the city.

## Megasthenes’ Pataliputra
Megasthenes described Pataliputra as a large and well-administered city.

## Mauryan Palace
Royal complex at Pataliputra admired by foreign visitors.

## Kumrahar Remains
Archaeological remains linked with Mauryan palace or assembly hall.

## Bulandibagh
Site associated with ancient Pataliputra fortifications.

---

# 34. FOREIGN RELATIONS

## Hellenistic World
The Greek-ruled kingdoms that emerged after Alexander’s death.

## Seleucid Empire
Empire founded by Seleucus Nicator, connected with Chandragupta through war and treaty.

## Chandragupta-Seleucus Relations
Included conflict, treaty, territorial settlement, and diplomatic exchange.

## Megasthenes
Seleucid ambassador at Chandragupta’s court.

## Bindusara’s Greek Relations
Bindusara maintained contacts with Hellenistic rulers.

## Antiochus I
Seleucid ruler who had diplomatic relations with Bindusara.

## Deimachus
Greek envoy to Bindusara.

## Ptolemy II
Hellenistic ruler of Egypt, possibly connected with Mauryan diplomacy.

## Dionysius
Greek envoy possibly sent to the Mauryan court by Ptolemy II.

## Ashoka’s Foreign Relations
Ashoka’s edicts mention Hellenistic rulers and neighboring peoples.

## Antiochus II
Hellenistic ruler mentioned in Ashoka’s edicts as Amtiyoka.

## Ptolemy II Philadelphus
Hellenistic ruler mentioned indirectly in Ashoka’s foreign references.

## Antigonus Gonatas
Macedonian ruler mentioned in Ashokan edictal tradition.

## Magas of Cyrene
Hellenistic ruler mentioned among Ashoka’s foreign contacts.

## Alexander of Epirus
One of the Hellenistic rulers mentioned in Ashokan edictal context.

## Amtiyoka
Ashokan Prakrit form of Antiochus.

## Turamaya
Ashokan Prakrit form of Ptolemy.

## Amtikini
Ashokan Prakrit form of Antigonus.

## Maka
Ashokan Prakrit form of Magas.

## Alikasudara
Ashokan Prakrit form of Alexander.

## Sri Lanka Relations
Ashoka sent Buddhist missions to Sri Lanka according to Buddhist tradition.

## Cholas
South Indian polity mentioned in Ashokan edicts as outside direct Mauryan rule.

## Pandyas
South Indian polity mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

## Satyaputras
South Indian polity mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

## Keralaputras
South Indian polity mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

## Tamraparni
Sri Lanka or possibly a region connected with Sri Lanka, mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

## Yonas
Greeks or people of Greek origin.

## Kambojas
North-western people mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

## Gandharas
People of Gandhara region.

## Rashtrikas
People mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

## Bhojas
People mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

## Pitinikas
People mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

## Andhras
People mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

## Pulindas
Tribal people mentioned in Ashokan edicts.

---

# 35. MAURYAN EMPIRE AND SOUTH INDIA

## Southern Limits of Mauryan Empire
The empire extended into the Deccan but did not directly control the far southern kingdoms.

## Deccan under Mauryas
Bindusara and Ashoka extended Mauryan influence into parts of the Deccan.

## Suvarnagiri
Important southern provincial center.

## Karnataka Edicts
Ashokan inscriptions in Karnataka show Mauryan control or influence in the south.

## Brahmagiri
Ashokan inscription site in Karnataka.

## Maski
Ashokan inscription site in Karnataka, important for identifying Ashoka.

## Nittur
Ashokan inscription site in Karnataka.

## Udegolam
Ashokan inscription site in Karnataka.

## Siddapur
Ashokan inscription site in Karnataka.

## Jatinga-Rameshwar
Ashokan inscription site in Karnataka.

## Cholas
Tamil polity outside direct Mauryan control.

## Pandyas
Tamil polity outside direct Mauryan control.

## Satyaputras
South Indian polity mentioned by Ashoka.

## Keralaputras
Kerala region polity mentioned by Ashoka.

## Tamilakam
The ancient Tamil region, mostly outside direct Mauryan rule.

## Mauryan Contact with South
Ashokan edicts show diplomatic, moral, and possibly trade contacts with the far south.

---

# 36. LAW AND JUSTICE

## Mauryan Justice
A system of courts, punishments, fines, and royal supervision.

## Danda
Punishment or coercive authority.

## Dandaniti
Policy of punishment and governance.

## Dharmasthiya Court
Court dealing with civil disputes in Arthashastra.

## Kantakashodhana Court
Court dealing with crime, public order, and removal of anti-social elements.

## Vyavahara
Legal procedure or dispute.

## Rajuka and Justice
Ashoka gave Rajukas authority to reward and punish.

## Judicial Tours
Officials were ordered to tour and ensure justice and Dhamma.

## Death Penalty
Existed in Mauryan law, though Ashoka introduced delay and mercy measures.

## Three-Day Respite
Ashoka gave condemned prisoners time before execution for appeal, charity, or spiritual preparation.

## Prison Administration
Prisons were supervised by state officials.

## Bandhanagara
Prison.

## Fines
Common punishment for offences.

## Torture and Harsh Punishment
Mentioned in Arthashastra; Ashoka tried to soften some aspects of justice.

## Equality in Justice
Ashoka emphasized fairness and impartiality in punishment and legal procedure.

---

# 37. ESPIONAGE AND INTERNAL SECURITY

## Spy System
Network of secret agents used to monitor officials, enemies, and public opinion.

## Gudhapurusha
Secret agent.

## Sanstha Spy
Stationary spy based in one location.

## Sanchara Spy
Wandering spy.

## Tapasa Spy
Spy disguised as ascetic.

## Vaidehaka Spy
Spy disguised as trader.

## Grihapati Spy
Spy disguised as householder.

## Agent Provocateur
Spy who provoked or tested loyalty.

## Secret Reporting
Spies reported directly or indirectly to the king.

## Official Surveillance
State monitoring of officials to prevent corruption.

## Internal Security
Protection against rebellion, crime, corruption, and enemy agents.

## Frontier Security
Control of border areas and tribal regions.

---

# 38. WELFARE MEASURES

## Welfare State Features
Ashoka emphasized public welfare, morality, health, and infrastructure.

## Medical Treatment
Ashoka arranged medical facilities for humans and animals.

## Medicinal Herbs
Ashoka ordered planting of useful medicinal plants.

## Wells
Wells were dug for public benefit.

## Roadside Trees
Trees were planted along roads for shade.

## Rest Houses
Facilities for travelers and animals.

## Animal Welfare
Protection and medical care for animals.

## Public Instruction
Officials spread moral teachings.

## Prisoner Welfare
Ashoka introduced some mercy measures for prisoners.

## Moral Welfare
Promotion of ethical conduct among subjects.

## People as Children
Ashoka described all subjects as his children.

---

# 39. MAURYAN FRONTIER POLICY

## Frontier Peoples
Communities living at the edges of the empire.

## Anta
Frontier or border region.

## Anta Mahamatta
Officer responsible for frontier areas.

## Atavikas
Forest people or tribal communities mentioned by Ashoka.

## Forest Tribes
Communities living in forested areas, sometimes difficult for the state to control.

## Conciliation of Frontier People
Ashoka used moral persuasion and warning toward frontier communities.

## Frontier Control
Administration and military supervision of border regions.

## Frontier Diplomacy
Maintaining peaceful relations with neighboring states and peoples.

## Moral Warning
Ashoka warned forest tribes that the king had power to punish but preferred repentance and Dhamma.

---

# 40. MAURYAN DECLINE

## Mauryan Decline
The weakening of the empire after Ashoka’s death.

## Post-Ashokan Weakness
Later rulers were weaker and could not hold the empire together.

## Succession Problems
Disputes among royal heirs weakened central authority.

## Administrative Overcentralization
The empire may have depended too much on a strong king and central control.

## Financial Strain
Large army, bureaucracy, welfare activities, and public works may have strained resources.

## Decline of Revenue
Reduced control over provinces could weaken tax collection.

## Provincial Revolts
Distant provinces may have rebelled or become independent.

## North-Western Pressure
Foreign invasions and pressure from Indo-Greeks affected the north-west.

## Brahmanical Reaction Theory
Some historians once argued that Ashoka’s Buddhist policy caused Brahmanical reaction, but this explanation alone is not sufficient.

## Ahimsa Policy Theory
Some argued Ashoka’s non-violence weakened the army, but this is debated and oversimplified.

## Economic Crisis Theory
Theory that economic pressure contributed to decline.

## Weak Successors Theory
The most common explanation that later Mauryan rulers lacked the ability of Chandragupta and Ashoka.

## Division of Empire
The empire may have been divided among successors, weakening unity.

## Rise of Regional Powers
Regions such as north-west, Deccan, and eastern India became less dependent on Pataliputra.

## Pushyamitra Shunga
General who killed Brihadratha Maurya and founded the Shunga dynasty.

## Brihadratha’s Assassination
Event marking the end of the Mauryan dynasty.

## Shunga Dynasty
Dynasty that succeeded the Mauryas in parts of north India.

---

# 41. LATER MAURYAN RULERS

## Dasharatha Maurya
Grandson of Ashoka and later Mauryan ruler. He donated caves to Ajivikas.

## Samprati
Later Mauryan ruler remembered in Jain tradition as a patron of Jainism.

## Salisuka
Later Mauryan ruler mentioned in Puranic lists.

## Devavarman
Later Mauryan ruler mentioned in dynastic lists.

## Satadhanvan
Later Mauryan ruler.

## Brihadratha Maurya
Last Mauryan ruler.

## Kunala
Ashoka’s son in Buddhist legends, sometimes connected with succession traditions.

## Jalauka
Name mentioned in some traditions as a son or successor of Ashoka, especially in Kashmir traditions.

## Tivara
Son of Ashoka and Karuvaki, known from Queen’s Edict.

## Mahendra
Ashoka’s son in Buddhist tradition, associated with mission to Sri Lanka.

## Sanghamitra
Ashoka’s daughter in Buddhist tradition, associated with Sri Lanka mission.

---

# 42. MAURYAN ART: IMPORTANT OBJECTS AND SITES

## Sarnath Lion Capital
Most famous Mauryan sculpture and India’s National Emblem.

## Rampurva Bull
Highly polished bull capital from Rampurva.

## Rampurva Lion
Lion capital from Rampurva.

## Lauriya Nandangarh Pillar
Ashokan pillar with lion capital.

## Lauriya Araraj Pillar
Ashokan pillar in Bihar.

## Sanchi Pillar
Ashokan pillar near Sanchi stupa.

## Vaishali Pillar
Ashokan pillar with lion capital.

## Sankisa Capital
Elephant capital associated with Sankisa.

## Dhauli Elephant
Rock-cut elephant at Dhauli.

## Didarganj Yakshi
Highly polished stone sculpture, often discussed with Mauryan art.

## Parkham Yaksha
Large Yaksha sculpture from Mathura region.

## Barabar Caves
Earliest surviving rock-cut caves in India.

## Lomas Rishi Cave
Famous for chaitya-arch facade.

## Sudama Cave
Cave donated by Ashoka to Ajivikas.

## Nagarjuni Caves
Caves donated by Dasharatha to Ajivikas.

## Pataliputra Palace
Wooden palace admired by foreign visitors.

## Kumrahar Pillared Hall
Archaeological evidence of large pillared structure near Pataliputra.

---

# 43. ASHOKAN PILLARS: STRUCTURE

## Monolithic Shaft
Single stone pillar shaft.

## Polished Surface
Smooth shining finish known as Mauryan polish.

## Lotus Base
Inverted lotus or bell-shaped base of capital.

## Abacus
Decorated slab above the lotus base.

## Animal Figure
Animal sculpture on top, such as lion, bull, horse, or elephant.

## Wheel Motif
Dharmachakra motif used in decoration.

## Lion
Symbol of royalty and Buddha’s teachings as lion’s roar.

## Bull
Symbol of strength and fertility.

## Elephant
Symbol associated with Buddha’s conception and royal power.

## Horse
Symbol associated with Buddha’s renunciation and movement.

## Four Lions
Sarnath capital has four lions standing back to back.

## National Emblem
India adopted the Sarnath Lion Capital as its national emblem.

## Ashoka Chakra
Wheel from Sarnath capital, used in the Indian national flag.

---

# 44. MAURYAN MATERIAL CULTURE

## Northern Black Polished Ware
Fine glossy pottery common in the Mauryan and early historic period.

## NBPW
Short form of Northern Black Polished Ware.

## Punch-Marked Coins
Coins used widely during Mauryan period.

## Ring Wells
Early historic urban structures made of terracotta rings, used for water or drainage.

## Terracotta Figurines
Clay figurines used by common people.

## Iron Tools
Tools for agriculture, craft, and war.

## Urban Fortifications
City defenses such as walls, moats, and palisades.

## Wooden Structures
Common in Mauryan architecture but rarely survive.

## Brick Structures
Used in buildings, stupas, wells, and urban works.

## Stone Sculpture
Highly polished stone sculpture became important.

## State Workshops
Production centers controlled by the state.

---

# 45. MAURYAN EMPIRE EXTENT

## Core Area
Magadha and the middle Ganga valley.

## North-Western Region
Controlled after Chandragupta’s campaigns and treaty with Seleucus.

## Western India
Included regions such as Gujarat and Malwa.

## Deccan
Large parts came under Mauryan influence or control.

## Kalinga
Conquered by Ashoka.

## Far South
Cholas, Pandyas, Satyaputras, and Keralaputras remained outside direct Mauryan rule.

## Afghanistan Region
Parts of modern Afghanistan were under Mauryan control or influence.

## Baluchistan Region
Associated with Mauryan territory after Seleucid treaty.

## Nepal Terai
Included sacred Buddhist sites like Lumbini under Ashoka’s influence.

## Largest Mauryan Extent
Reached under Ashoka after the conquest of Kalinga.

---

# 46. MAURYAN COMMUNICATION AND TRANSPORT

## Royal Road
Major road connecting important cities and provinces.

## Uttarapatha Route
Northern route connecting Pataliputra, Taxila, and north-western regions.

## Dakshinapatha Route
Southern route connecting the Ganga valley with Deccan.

## River Transport
Movement of goods and officials through rivers.

## Ganga Route
Important river route through the heart of the empire.

## Roadside Trees
Ashoka planted trees for travelers.

## Wells Along Roads
Ashoka ordered wells to be dug for public benefit.

## Rest Houses
Facilities for travelers.

## Messenger System
Officials and messengers carried royal orders.

## Pativedaka
Reporter who informed the king of public affairs.

## Duta
Messenger or envoy.

## Passport System
Arthashastra mentions state control over movement and identity through seals.

## Mudra
Seal or official mark.

---

# 47. MAURYAN DIPLOMACY AND WAR THEORY

## Mandala Theory
Kautilya’s theory that neighboring states are natural enemies and enemy’s enemy is a natural ally.

## Six-Fold Policy
Kautilya’s six methods of foreign policy: peace, war, neutrality, marching, alliance, and dual policy.

## Four Upayas
Sama, Dana, Bheda, and Danda.

## Sama
Conciliation or negotiation.

## Dana
Gifts or concessions.

## Bheda
Creating division among enemies.

## Danda
Use of force.

## Treaty
Agreement between rulers.

## Alliance
Political partnership between states.

## Neutrality
Remaining inactive in conflict.

## Conquest
Expansion through war.

## Dharmavijaya
Ashoka’s idea of moral conquest.

## Digvijaya
Conquest of directions or military conquest.

## Chakravartin Ideal
Ideal of a universal ruler.

---

# 48. IMPORTANT MAURYAN CONCEPTS FROM ARTHASHASTRA

## Yogakshema
Welfare and security of subjects.

## Raksha
Protection.

## Palana
Administration or maintenance.

## Labha
Acquisition.

## Vardhana
Expansion or increase.

## Rakshana
Protection of acquired territory.

## Palanadharma
Duty of governance.

## Kosa-Mula Danda
The army depends on treasury; financial strength supports military power.

## Treasury as State Limb
The treasury is one of the seven limbs of the state.

## Fort as State Limb
The fort protects the kingdom and capital.

## Army as State Limb
Army enforces authority and protects territory.

## Ally as State Limb
Allies are essential in foreign policy.

## King’s Discipline
The king must be educated, self-controlled, and active.

## Daily Routine of King
Arthashastra describes a strict schedule for the king’s work.

## Public Accessibility
Ashoka said he was available for public work at all times.

---

# 49. ASHOKA’S ADMINISTRATIVE REFORMS

## Dhamma Mahamattas
New officials appointed to promote Dhamma.

## Rajuka Empowerment
Ashoka gave Rajukas authority in justice and administration.

## Administrative Tours
Officials were ordered to tour and instruct people in Dhamma.

## Five-Year Tours
Some officials were instructed to tour every five years for Dhamma propagation.

## Welfare Administration
Ashoka linked administration with public welfare.

## Humane Justice
Ashoka emphasized fairness, restraint, and mercy.

## Prisoner Respite
Condemned prisoners were given time before execution.

## Religious Neutrality of State
Ashoka respected all sects while personally supporting Buddhism.

## Communication through Edicts
Ashoka used inscriptions to directly communicate with subjects.

---

# 50. IMPORTANT ASHOKAN DHAMMA VALUES

## Obedience to Parents
Respect and service to parents.

## Respect for Elders
Honoring age and experience.

## Generosity to Brahmanas and Shramanas
Giving gifts and respect to religious persons.

## Kindness to Servants
Humane treatment of servants and dependents.

## Compassion to Animals
Avoiding unnecessary harm to animals.

## Truthfulness
Speaking truth.

## Purity
Moral cleanliness.

## Gentleness
Soft and non-cruel behavior.

## Gratitude
Thankfulness and recognition of help.

## Firm Devotion
Commitment to moral life.

## Restraint in Speech
Avoiding harsh criticism of other sects.

## Tolerance
Respecting different beliefs.

## Moral Self-Examination
Checking one’s own conduct.

## Non-Cruelty
Avoiding harshness and violence.

---

# 51. ASHOKA’S DHAMMA AND RELIGION

## Dhamma Is Not Buddhism Alone
Ashoka’s Dhamma was wider than Buddhism and meant for all subjects.

## Dhamma Is Not Vedic Dharma
Ashoka’s Dhamma was a practical moral policy, not the same as Brahmanical ritual duty.

## Dhamma Is Not Sectarian
It did not force conversion to Buddhism.

## Dhamma and Social Ethics
It focused on family duty, kindness, charity, and harmony.

## Dhamma and Political Control
It helped unify a diverse empire through shared moral values.

## Dhamma and Welfare
It supported public welfare measures.

## Dhamma and Non-Violence
It reduced violence but did not completely abolish punishment or army.

## Dhamma and Tolerance
It promoted respect among all religious groups.

---

# 52. MAURYAN CONNECTION WITH AJIVIKAS

## Ajivikas
Ancient ascetic sect associated with belief in fate or determinism.

## Makkhali Gosala
Founder or major teacher of Ajivika tradition.

## Ashoka and Ajivikas
Ashoka donated caves at Barabar to Ajivikas.

## Dasharatha and Ajivikas
Dasharatha donated Nagarjuni caves to Ajivikas.

## Barabar Caves for Ajivikas
Earliest surviving rock-cut caves in India, donated to Ajivikas.

## Ajivika Patronage
Shows Mauryan religious tolerance beyond Buddhism.

---

# 53. MAURYAN EMPIRE AND BUDDHIST MISSIONS

## Buddhist Missions
Missionary activities sent to different regions under Ashoka according to Buddhist tradition.

## Mission to Sri Lanka
Led by Mahinda according to Sri Lankan chronicles.

## Mahinda
Ashoka’s son and Buddhist missionary to Sri Lanka.

## Sanghamitta
Ashoka’s daughter who brought Bodhi tree branch to Sri Lanka according to tradition.

## Mission to Kashmir-Gandhara
Mission associated with Majjhantika.

## Majjhantika
Missionary sent to Kashmir and Gandhara according to tradition.

## Mission to Mahishamandala
Mission to south Indian region according to Buddhist tradition.

## Mahadeva
Missionary associated with Mahishamandala.

## Mission to Vanavasi
Mission to Karnataka region.

## Rakkhita
Missionary associated with Vanavasi.

## Mission to Aparanta
Mission to western coastal region.

## Yona Dhammarakkhita
Greek Buddhist monk associated with mission to Aparanta.

## Mission to Maharattha
Mission to Maharashtra region.

## Mahadhammarakkhita
Missionary associated with Maharattha.

## Mission to Yona Country
Mission to Greek regions.

## Maharakkhita
Missionary associated with Yona country.

## Mission to Suvarnabhumi
Mission to Southeast Asian region according to tradition.

## Sona and Uttara
Missionaries associated with Suvarnabhumi.

## Suvarnabhumi
“Land of gold”, often linked with Southeast Asia in Buddhist tradition.

---

# 54. MAURYAN ADMINISTRATION AND MEGASTHENES

## Megasthenes
Greek ambassador who described Mauryan administration and society.

## Indica
Megasthenes’ work on India.

## Palibothra
Greek name for Pataliputra.

## Municipal Committees
Megasthenes described six committees of Pataliputra.

## Military Committees
Megasthenes described six committees for the army.

## No Slavery Claim
Megasthenes claimed Indians had no slavery, though this is debated.

## Seven Social Classes
Megasthenes divided Indian society into seven classes.

## Farmers Protected in War
Megasthenes said farmers were not disturbed during war, though this may be idealized.

## Royal Palace Description
Megasthenes praised the Mauryan palace at Pataliputra.

## Indian Philosophers
Megasthenes described Brahmanas and Shramanas as philosophers.

## Foreigners Supervision
Megasthenes noted state care and monitoring of foreigners.

---

# 55. IMPORTANT MAURYAN LOCATIONS

## Pataliputra
Capital of the empire.

## Rajagriha
Earlier Magadhan capital, still important.

## Taxila
North-western provincial center.

## Ujjain
Western provincial center.

## Tosali
Kalinga administrative center.

## Samapa
Kalinga administrative center.

## Suvarnagiri
Southern provincial center.

## Girnar
Ashokan inscription site and region of Sudarshana Lake.

## Sanchi
Buddhist stupa and pillar site.

## Sarnath
Pillar site with Lion Capital.

## Lumbini
Buddha’s birthplace, visited by Ashoka.

## Bodh Gaya
Place of Buddha’s enlightenment, patronized by Ashoka.

## Dhauli
Kalinga edict site.

## Jaugada
Kalinga edict site.

## Barabar
Cave site donated to Ajivikas.

## Nagarjuni
Cave site donated by Dasharatha.

## Shravanabelagola
Jain site associated with Chandragupta tradition.

## Kandahar
Greek-Aramaic inscription site.

## Shahbazgarhi
Kharosthi inscription site.

## Mansehra
Kharosthi inscription site.

## Maski
Inscription site naming Ashoka.

---

# 56. MAURYAN POLITICAL IDEOLOGY

## Chakravartin
Universal ruler ideal.

## Devanampiya
Beloved of the Gods; Ashoka’s title.

## Paternal Ruler
Ashoka presented himself as father of his subjects.

## Welfare Kingship
Kingship based on people’s welfare and moral guidance.

## Conquest by Dhamma
Ashoka’s idea that moral influence is superior to military conquest.

## State and Morality
Ashoka used state power to promote ethical behavior.

## Royal Responsibility
The king was responsible for administration, justice, protection, welfare, and morality.

## Kautilyan Kingship
Kingship based on power, order, revenue, security, and expansion.

## Ashokan Kingship
Kingship based on welfare, Dhamma, moral instruction, and humane administration.

---

# 57. MAURYAN COMPARISON: KAUTILYA AND ASHOKA

## Kautilya’s State
Practical, strategic, revenue-focused, and security-oriented.

## Ashoka’s State
Moral, welfare-oriented, tolerant, and ethically interventionist.

## Kautilya on War
War and diplomacy are valid tools for state expansion.

## Ashoka on War
After Kalinga, Ashoka preferred Dhammavijaya over military conquest.

## Kautilya on Spies
Spies are essential to state security.

## Ashoka on Officials
Officials should promote justice, welfare, and Dhamma.

## Kautilya on Revenue
The treasury is central to state power.

## Ashoka on Welfare
Public welfare and moral improvement are royal duties.

## Common Element
Both support a strong state and active kingship.

---

# 58. MAURYAN EMPIRE AND NATIONAL SYMBOLS OF INDIA

## Sarnath Lion Capital
Adopted as the National Emblem of India.

## Ashoka Chakra
Wheel from the Sarnath capital, placed in the Indian national flag.

## National Emblem Motto
“Satyameva Jayate” is from the Mundaka Upanishad, not Ashokan edicts.

## Four Lions
Symbolize power, courage, confidence, and pride in modern interpretation.

## Dharma Chakra
Symbol of law, morality, and movement of Dharma.

## Abacus Animals
Sarnath capital has animals such as elephant, bull, horse, and lion separated by wheels.

## Inverted Lotus
Base form of the Sarnath capital.

---

# 59. COMMONLY CONFUSED TERMS

## Chandragupta Maurya vs Chandragupta I
Chandragupta Maurya founded the Mauryan Empire. Chandragupta I was a Gupta ruler much later.

## Bindusara vs Bimbisara
Bindusara was Mauryan, son of Chandragupta. Bimbisara was earlier Haryanka ruler of Magadha.

## Ashoka vs Ashvaghosha
Ashoka was Mauryan emperor. Ashvaghosha was a Buddhist scholar-poet of Kushana period.

## Dhamma vs Dharma
Ashoka’s Dhamma was an ethical policy. Dharma has wider meanings in Indian traditions.

## Dhamma Mahamatta vs Mahamatra
Dhamma Mahamattas promoted Dhamma. Mahamattas were high officials generally.

## Rajuka vs Pradeshika
Rajuka handled rural administration, survey, and justice. Pradeshika was a higher territorial officer.

## Samaharta vs Sannidhata
Samaharta was chief revenue collector. Sannidhata was treasurer.

## Arthashastra vs Indica
Arthashastra is an Indian statecraft text. Indica is a Greek account by Megasthenes.

## Brahmi vs Kharosthi
Brahmi was used in most of India. Kharosthi was used in the north-west and written right to left.

## Major Rock Edict XIII vs Minor Rock Edict
Major Rock Edict XIII describes Kalinga War. Minor Rock Edicts are shorter and more personal.

## Ashokan Pillars vs Gupta Pillars
Ashokan pillars are Mauryan and often polished monoliths. Gupta pillars are later.

## Sarnath Lion Capital vs Ashoka Pillar
The Lion Capital is the top sculpture of an Ashokan pillar at Sarnath.

## Barabar Caves vs Ajanta Caves
Barabar caves are Mauryan and donated to Ajivikas. Ajanta caves are Buddhist and mostly later.

## Kalinga War vs Kalinga Edicts
Kalinga War was Ashoka’s conquest. Kalinga Edicts were special administrative edicts issued after conquest.

## Buddhist Dhamma vs Ashokan Dhamma
Buddhist Dhamma means Buddha’s teaching. Ashokan Dhamma means moral policy for society.

---

# 60. IMPORTANT MAURYAN RULERS: QUICK GLOSSARY

## Chandragupta Maurya
Founder; defeated Nandas; fought Seleucus; established empire.

## Bindusara
Second ruler; maintained empire; likely expanded into Deccan.

## Ashoka
Greatest ruler; conquered Kalinga; promoted Dhamma; issued edicts.

## Dasharatha
Later ruler; donated Nagarjuni caves to Ajivikas.

## Samprati
Later ruler remembered in Jain tradition.

## Salisuka
Later Mauryan ruler mentioned in Puranic lists.

## Devavarman
Later Mauryan ruler.

## Satadhanvan
Later Mauryan ruler.

## Brihadratha
Last Mauryan ruler; killed by Pushyamitra Shunga.

---

# 61. IMPORTANT NON-ROYAL PERSONALITIES

## Chanakya
Strategist behind Chandragupta’s rise.

## Kautilya
Authorial name of Arthashastra.

## Megasthenes
Greek ambassador to Chandragupta’s court.

## Seleucus Nicator
Hellenistic ruler who made treaty with Chandragupta.

## Deimachus
Greek ambassador to Bindusara.

## Dionysius
Greek envoy possibly linked with Bindusara’s court.

## Moggaliputta Tissa
Buddhist elder associated with Ashoka and Third Buddhist Council.

## Mahinda
Ashoka’s son and missionary to Sri Lanka.

## Sanghamitta
Ashoka’s daughter associated with Bodhi tree mission to Sri Lanka.

## Karuvaki
Ashoka’s queen mentioned in inscription.

## Tivara
Son of Ashoka and Karuvaki.

## Pushyagupta
Chandragupta’s governor associated with Sudarshana Lake.

## Tushaspha
Yavana governor under Ashoka associated with Sudarshana Lake improvement.

## Pushyamitra Shunga
General who ended Mauryan rule and founded Shunga dynasty.

---

# 62. HIGH-YIELD INSCRIPTION CLUSTER

## Maski
Mentions Ashoka by name.

## Gujarra
Mentions Ashoka by name.

## Major Rock Edict XIII
Kalinga War and Ashoka’s remorse.

## Major Rock Edict II
Medical facilities for humans and animals.

## Major Rock Edict V
Dhamma Mahamattas.

## Major Rock Edict XII
Religious tolerance.

## Rummindei
Lumbini; Buddha’s birthplace; tax concession.

## Nigali Sagar
Kanakamuni Buddha stupa enlargement.

## Bhabru
Ashoka’s respect for Buddhist texts.

## Queen’s Edict
Mentions Karuvaki and Tivara.

## Sarnath Schism Edict
Warning against Sangha division.

## Barabar Cave Inscriptions
Ashoka’s donations to Ajivikas.

## Nagarjuni Cave Inscriptions
Dasharatha’s donations to Ajivikas.

## Kandahar Bilingual Inscription
Greek and Aramaic inscription showing Ashoka’s reach.

---

# 63. HIGH-YIELD ADMINISTRATION CLUSTER

## King
Supreme authority.

## Mantriparishad
Council of ministers.

## Amatya
Minister or official.

## Mahamatra
High officer.

## Dhamma Mahamatra
Officer for Dhamma.

## Samaharta
Chief revenue collector.

## Sannidhata
Treasurer.

## Rajuka
Rural officer with judicial and revenue powers.

## Pradeshika
Territorial officer.

## Yukta
Subordinate official.

## Nagaraka
City superintendent.

## Gopa
Record keeper over households or villages.

## Sthanika
Local officer.

## Adhyaksha
Departmental superintendent.

## Senapati
Commander-in-chief.

## Kumara
Prince-governor.

---

# 64. HIGH-YIELD ECONOMY CLUSTER

## Main Economic Base
Agriculture.

## Main Revenue Source
Land revenue.

## Main Coin
Punch-marked coin.

## State Monopolies
Mines, salt, forests, liquor, and some industries.

## Important Trade Routes
Uttarapatha and Dakshinapatha.

## Important Ports
Tamralipti, Sopara, Bharukachchha.

## Important Economic Text
Arthashastra.

## Important Irrigation Work
Sudarshana Lake.

## Important Officer for Revenue
Samaharta.

## Important Officer for Treasury
Sannidhata.

## Important Officer for Trade
Panyadhyaksha.

## Important Officer for Agriculture
Sitadhyaksha.

## Important Officer for Mines
Akaradhyaksha.

---

# 65. HIGH-YIELD ART AND ARCHITECTURE CLUSTER

## Mauryan Polish
Highly shiny polish on stone.

## Ashokan Pillars
Monolithic polished stone pillars.

## Sarnath Lion Capital
India’s National Emblem.

## Ashoka Chakra
Wheel in Indian national flag.

## Barabar Caves
Earliest surviving rock-cut caves.

## Lomas Rishi Cave
Famous chaitya-arch facade.

## Sanchi Stupa
Originally associated with Ashoka.

## Pataliputra Palace
Wooden palace admired by Greeks.

## Kumrahar
Pillared hall remains near Patna.

## Didarganj Yakshi
Famous polished stone sculpture.

## Dhauli Elephant
Rock-cut elephant figure.

---

# 66. HIGH-YIELD DHAMMA CLUSTER

## Dhamma
Ashoka’s moral policy.

## Dhamma Is Not Sectarian
It was not meant only for Buddhists.

## Main Values
Respect for parents, elders, Brahmanas, Shramanas, kindness, truthfulness, non-violence, and tolerance.

## Dhamma Mahamattas
Officials appointed to spread Dhamma.

## Dhammavijaya
Moral conquest.

## Dhamma-Yatra
Tour for moral instruction.

## Major Rock Edict XIII
Best source for Kalinga War and Dhammavijaya.

## Religious Tolerance Edict
Major Rock Edict XII.

## Animal Protection Edict
Major Pillar Edict V.

## Welfare Edict
Major Rock Edict II.

---

# 67. HIGH-YIELD FOREIGN RELATIONS CLUSTER

## Seleucus Nicator
Fought and made treaty with Chandragupta.

## Megasthenes
Ambassador to Chandragupta.

## Antiochus
Hellenistic ruler mentioned in Ashoka’s edicts.

## Ptolemy
Hellenistic ruler mentioned in Ashoka’s edicts.

## Antigonus
Hellenistic ruler mentioned in Ashoka’s edicts.

## Magas
Hellenistic ruler mentioned in Ashoka’s edicts.

## Alexander
Hellenistic ruler mentioned in Ashoka’s edicts.

## Cholas
Southern polity outside direct Mauryan rule.

## Pandyas
Southern polity outside direct Mauryan rule.

## Satyaputras
Southern polity mentioned by Ashoka.

## Keralaputras
Southern polity mentioned by Ashoka.

## Tamraparni
Sri Lanka or associated region.

---

# 68. CHRONOLOGICAL SNAPSHOT

## Stage 1: Magadhan Foundation
Magadha became powerful under Haryankas, Shishunagas, and Nandas before the Mauryas.

## Stage 2: Nanda Overthrow
Chandragupta Maurya, aided by Chanakya, overthrew Dhana Nanda.

## Stage 3: Chandragupta’s Expansion
Chandragupta consolidated Magadha, controlled north India, and expanded into the north-west.

## Stage 4: Treaty with Seleucus
Chandragupta defeated or checked Seleucus and gained north-western territories.

## Stage 5: Bindusara’s Rule
Bindusara maintained the empire and probably expanded into the Deccan.

## Stage 6: Ashoka’s Accession
Ashoka became emperor after Bindusara, possibly after a succession struggle.

## Stage 7: Kalinga War
Ashoka conquered Kalinga but was deeply affected by the suffering caused by war.

## Stage 8: Dhamma Policy
Ashoka promoted Dhamma, welfare, non-violence, religious tolerance, and moral administration.

## Stage 9: Edictal Communication
Ashoka issued inscriptions across the empire to communicate directly with officials and subjects.

## Stage 10: Buddhist Patronage
Ashoka supported Buddhism, visited sacred sites, and traditionally sent missions abroad.

## Stage 11: Post-Ashokan Weakness
The empire weakened under later rulers due to succession issues, provincial independence, and administrative strain.

## Stage 12: Fall of Mauryas
Brihadratha was killed by Pushyamitra Shunga, ending Mauryan rule.

---

# 69. FINAL REVISION CLUSTER FOR UPSC PRELIMS

## Must Remember Founder
Chandragupta Maurya.

## Must Remember Adviser
Chanakya or Kautilya.

## Must Remember Text on Statecraft
Arthashastra.

## Must Remember Greek Ambassador
Megasthenes.

## Must Remember Greek Text
Indica.

## Must Remember Second Ruler
Bindusara.

## Must Remember Greatest Ruler
Ashoka.

## Must Remember Ashoka’s Titles
Devanampiya and Piyadasi.

## Must Remember Ashoka’s Turning Point
Kalinga War.

## Must Remember Edict on Kalinga War
Major Rock Edict XIII.

## Must Remember Ashoka’s Policy
Dhamma.

## Must Remember Dhamma Officials
Dhamma Mahamattas.

## Must Remember Ashokan Scripts
Brahmi, Kharosthi, Greek, and Aramaic.

## Must Remember Ashokan Language
Mostly Prakrit.

## Must Remember Inscription Identifying Ashoka
Maski.

## Must Remember Buddhist Site Inscription
Rummindei/Lumbini inscription.

## Must Remember National Emblem
Sarnath Lion Capital.

## Must Remember National Flag Link
Ashoka Chakra.

## Must Remember Earliest Rock-Cut Caves
Barabar Caves.

## Must Remember Ajivika Donations
Barabar caves by Ashoka and Nagarjuni caves by Dasharatha.

## Must Remember Main Capital
Pataliputra.

## Must Remember Provincial Centers
Taxila, Ujjain, Tosali, Suvarnagiri.

## Must Remember Revenue Officers
Samaharta and Sannidhata.

## Must Remember Rural Officer
Rajuka.

## Must Remember City Officer
Nagaraka.

## Must Remember Economic Base
Agriculture and land revenue.

## Must Remember Coins
Punch-marked coins.

## Must Remember Important Lake
Sudarshana Lake.

## Must Remember Southern Polities Outside Direct Rule
Cholas, Pandyas, Satyaputras, Keralaputras.

## Must Remember Last Mauryan Ruler
Brihadratha.

## Must Remember End of Mauryas
Brihadratha was killed by Pushyamitra Shunga.

## One-Line Essence
The Mauryan Empire was the first great imperial state of India, founded by Chandragupta, organized through a powerful bureaucracy and economy, morally transformed under Ashoka’s Dhamma after the Kalinga War, and remembered for inscriptions, pillars, welfare policy, and the political unification of most of the subcontinent.


-----


# INDIAN ART AND CULTURE HISTORY GLOSSARY FOR UPSC PRELIMS
## Chronological Coverage: Prehistoric Art → Harappan Culture → Vedic Culture → Buddhist-Jain Art → Mauryan Art → Post-Mauryan Schools → Gupta Classical Age → Early Medieval Temples → Indo-Islamic Art → Bhakti-Sufi Culture → Mughal and Regional Arts → Colonial and Modern Art → Performing Arts, Literature, Crafts, and Cultural Heritage

> Scope:
> This is a UPSC Prelims-oriented glossary of Indian Art and Culture in chronological order.
> It covers architecture, sculpture, painting, literature, religion, philosophy, language, scripts, music, dance, theatre, crafts, textiles, festivals, cultural institutions, and important artistic styles.
>
> Core UPSC Areas:
> 1. Architecture
> 2. Sculpture
> 3. Painting
> 4. Religion and philosophy
> 5. Literature and language
> 6. Music and dance
> 7. Theatre and folk traditions
> 8. Crafts and textiles
> 9. Scripts and inscriptions
> 10. Cultural movements and heritage sites

---

# 1. BASIC ART AND CULTURE TERMS

## Culture
The total way of life of a society, including beliefs, customs, language, food, dress, art, music, literature, rituals, festivals, and social practices.

## Civilization
A complex society with cities, institutions, economy, technology, social organization, and cultural development.

## Art
Creative expression through painting, sculpture, architecture, music, dance, theatre, literature, or craft.

## Material Culture
Physical objects made and used by people, such as tools, pottery, buildings, ornaments, coins, and sculptures.

## Non-Material Culture
Ideas, beliefs, language, rituals, values, music, oral traditions, and knowledge systems.

## Heritage
The cultural and natural legacy inherited from the past.

## Tangible Heritage
Physical heritage such as monuments, temples, forts, caves, sculptures, manuscripts, and artifacts.

## Intangible Heritage
Living traditions such as music, dance, festivals, rituals, oral traditions, crafts, and performing arts.

## Monument
A historically or culturally important structure.

## Iconography
The study of symbols, images, attributes, and visual features used to identify deities, saints, rulers, or ideas.

## Icon
A sacred image or representation, especially of a deity or spiritual figure.

## Motif
A repeated design or symbol in art.

## Symbolism
Use of signs, objects, animals, colors, or gestures to represent deeper meanings.

## Patronage
Support given by rulers, merchants, guilds, temples, monasteries, or communities to artists and cultural institutions.

## Court Art
Art produced under royal patronage.

## Popular Art
Art produced by common people or local communities.

## Folk Art
Traditional art of ordinary people, often passed down orally or through community practice.

## Classical Art
Art based on refined rules, theory, training, and long-established traditions.

## Sacred Art
Art made for religious or spiritual purposes.

## Secular Art
Art made for non-religious purposes, such as court scenes, portraits, daily life, and decoration.

## Syncretism
Blending of different cultural or religious traditions.

## Assimilation
Absorption of one cultural element into another.

## Acculturation
Cultural change due to contact between different groups.

## Cultural Diffusion
Spread of cultural elements from one region or society to another.

## Tradition
Practices and beliefs passed from generation to generation.

## School of Art
A recognizable artistic style associated with a region, period, patron, or technique.

## Style
Distinctive manner of artistic expression.

## Aesthetic
Sense of beauty or artistic taste.

## Canon
Accepted rules or standards in art, literature, religion, or performance.

## Treatise
A systematic written work on a subject.

## Shastra
A technical or authoritative text in Indian tradition.

## Sutra
A concise rule-like text.

---

# 2. PREHISTORIC ART AND CULTURE

## Prehistoric Art
Art created before written records, mainly known from rock paintings, engravings, ornaments, and symbolic objects.

## Rock Art
Paintings or engravings made on rock surfaces, caves, and shelters.

## Rock Painting
Painting made on cave or rock surfaces using natural pigments.

## Petroglyph
Rock engraving or carving.

## Pictograph
Rock painting or drawn symbol.

## Bhimbetka
Famous prehistoric rock shelter site in Madhya Pradesh with paintings from different periods.

## Bhimbetka Rock Paintings
Paintings showing animals, hunting, dancing, rituals, and daily life.

## Mesolithic Rock Art
Rock art generally associated with hunting-gathering communities and microlithic culture.

## Hunting Scene
Painting showing humans hunting animals.

## Dancing Scene
Painting showing group dance or ritual performance.

## Animal Figure
Representation of animals such as deer, bison, elephant, tiger, boar, and antelope.

## Human Figure
Representation of people in hunting, dancing, or social activities.

## Geometric Design
Abstract patterns like circles, lines, dots, grids, and triangles.

## Handprint
Impression or outline of a human hand on rock.

## Red Ochre
Natural red pigment used in rock paintings and burials.

## Hematite
Iron-rich mineral used as red pigment.

## White Pigment
Pigment made from lime, clay, or other minerals.

## Superimposition
One painting made over another, helping establish relative chronology.

## Symbolic Behaviour
