Use of art, ornaments, burial practices, or rituals to express meaning.

## Ostrich Eggshell Beads
Upper Palaeolithic and Mesolithic ornaments showing early decoration and symbolic culture.

## Burial Goods
Objects placed with the dead, showing belief, identity, or ritual.

## Ochre Burial
Burial using red pigment, possibly symbolic.

## Prehistoric Music
Inferred from dancing scenes and possible use of rhythm, though direct evidence is limited.

## Prehistoric Dance
Suggested by rock paintings showing group movement and ritual activity.

## Prehistoric Ritual
Inferred from burials, symbolic objects, rock paintings, and special deposits.

---

# 3. HARAPPAN / INDUS VALLEY ART AND CULTURE

## Harappan Art
Art of the Indus Valley Civilization, including seals, sculptures, pottery, terracotta figurines, beads, ornaments, and metal objects.

## Indus Valley Civilization
Bronze Age urban civilization known for planned cities, drainage, seals, weights, trade, and crafts.

## Harappan Civilization
Another name for the Indus Valley Civilization.

## Bronze Age Art
Art made during a period when bronze technology was important.

## Seal
Small object, often made of steatite, used to make impressions and carrying animal motifs and script.

## Steatite Seal
Harappan seal made from soft stone called steatite.

## Unicorn Seal
Most common Harappan seal type, showing a one-horned mythical animal.

## Pashupati Seal
Seal from Mohenjo-daro showing a horned seated figure surrounded by animals. Its identification as proto-Shiva is debated.

## Standard Device
Mysterious object shown before the unicorn on many seals.

## Indus Script
Undeciphered script found on seals, pottery, copper tablets, and other objects.

## Dholavira Signboard
Large inscription-like sign from Dholavira, important for Indus script studies.

## Dancing Girl
Bronze figurine from Mohenjo-daro showing metal-casting skill.

## Lost-Wax Technique
Metal casting method used to make objects like the Dancing Girl.

## Cire Perdue
French term for lost-wax technique.

## Priest-King
Stone sculpture from Mohenjo-daro showing a bearded male figure. Its identification is uncertain.

## Bearded Man
Another name for the so-called Priest-King sculpture.

## Mother Goddess Figurines
Terracotta female figurines often interpreted as fertility figures, though interpretation is debated.

## Terracotta Art
Baked clay art including toys, carts, animals, human figures, and ornaments.

## Terracotta Bull
Common Harappan figurine showing importance of cattle.

## Toy Cart
Terracotta cart model showing knowledge of wheeled transport.

## Faience
Glazed material used for beads, bangles, and small ornaments.

## Carnelian Beads
Semi-precious reddish beads, highly valued in Harappan craft.

## Etched Carnelian Beads
Carnelian beads decorated with white designs.

## Shell Bangles
Bangles made from marine shells.

## Bead-Making
Important Harappan craft centered at sites such as Lothal, Chanhudaro, and Gujarat regions.

## Lothal Bead Factory
Evidence of bead-making at Lothal.

## Chanhudaro Craft Centre
Harappan site known for bead-making, seal-making, and craft specialization.

## Harappan Pottery
Wheel-made pottery, often red with black painted designs.

## Black-on-Red Ware
Common Harappan pottery style.

## Perforated Jar
Harappan vessel with holes, possibly used for filtering, brewing, or ritual purposes.

## Dish-on-Stand
Common Harappan pottery form.

## Pipal Motif
Tree motif found in Harappan art, later important in Indian religious symbolism.

## Swastika Motif
Auspicious symbol found in Harappan contexts and later Indian traditions.

## Harappan Urban Culture
Culture of planned cities, drainage, craft specialization, seals, weights, trade, and public works.

## Great Bath
Large public bathing tank at Mohenjo-daro, possibly used for ritual bathing.

## Harappan Craft Specialization
Specialized production of beads, seals, pottery, metals, shell objects, and textiles.

## Harappan Textile Evidence
Cotton use is associated with Harappan civilization.

## Cotton
Important textile fibre used by Harappans.

---

# 4. VEDIC ART AND CULTURE

## Vedic Culture
Culture associated with the Vedas, sacrificial rituals, oral tradition, hymns, early Sanskrit, and social-religious institutions.

## Vedas
Oldest sacred texts of India: Rigveda, Samaveda, Yajurveda, and Atharvaveda.

## Shruti
Revealed sacred literature, including Vedas, Brahmanas, Aranyakas, and Upanishads.

## Smriti
Remembered tradition, including later texts such as Dharmasutras, Epics, Puranas, and Dharmashastras.

## Oral Tradition
Transmission of knowledge by memorization and recitation.

## Vedic Recitation
Highly precise chanting of Vedic hymns.

## Svara
Accent or tone in Vedic chanting.

## Samhita Patha
Continuous recitation of Vedic text.

## Pada Patha
Word-by-word recitation.

## Ghana Patha
Highly complex method of Vedic recitation.

## Rigveda
Oldest Veda, containing hymns to deities like Indra, Agni, Soma, and Varuna.

## Samaveda
Veda of melodies and chants, important for Indian music tradition.

## Yajurveda
Veda of sacrificial formulas.

## Atharvaveda
Veda containing charms, healing hymns, household rituals, and philosophical ideas.

## Yajna
Sacrificial ritual involving offerings into fire.

## Vedic Altar
Ritual structure used in sacrifices.

## Shulba Sutras
Texts dealing with geometry of sacrificial altars.

## Vedic Geometry
Mathematical knowledge used in altar construction.

## Fire Altar
Ritual altar used in Vedic sacrifice.

## Syena Chiti
Falcon-shaped fire altar.

## Agnihotra
Daily fire ritual.

## Soma Ritual
Ritual involving Soma offering.

## Brahmana Texts
Texts explaining Vedic rituals and sacrifices.

## Aranyakas
Forest texts dealing with ritual symbolism and meditation.

## Upanishads
Philosophical texts discussing Brahman, Atman, karma, rebirth, and moksha.

## Vedic Music
Early sacred chanting tradition, especially associated with Samaveda.

## Saman
Melodic chant of the Samaveda.

## Chandas
Vedic metre.

## Gayatri Metre
Vedic metre of 24 syllables.

## Trishtubh Metre
Common Rigvedic metre of 44 syllables.

## Anushtubh Metre
Metre later common in epic poetry.

## Vedic Sanskrit
Language of the Vedas.

## Painted Grey Ware
Pottery associated with Later Vedic culture and early Janapada regions.

## PGW
Short form of Painted Grey Ware.

## Vedic Social Culture
Culture based on family, clan, cattle, yajna, oral learning, varna, and later ashrama ideas.

## Ashrama System
Four stages of life: Brahmacharya, Grihastha, Vanaprastha, and Sannyasa.

## Samskara
Life-cycle ritual.

## Upanayana
Initiation into Vedic learning.

## Vivaha
Marriage ritual.

## Antyeshti
Funeral ritual.

---

# 5. SHRAMANA CULTURE: BUDDHISM, JAINISM, AND AJIVIKAS

## Shramana Tradition
Renunciant traditions that questioned Vedic ritualism and emphasized karma, rebirth, asceticism, meditation, and liberation.

## Buddhism
Religion founded by Gautama Buddha, emphasizing Four Noble Truths, Eightfold Path, and Nirvana.

## Jainism
Religion associated with 24 Tirthankaras, emphasizing non-violence, austerity, karma, and liberation.

## Ajivikas
Ancient ascetic sect associated with Makkhali Gosala and belief in fate.

## Monastic Culture
Culture based on monks, nuns, monasteries, discipline, and renunciation.

## Sangha
Buddhist or Jain religious community.

## Bhikkhu
Buddhist monk.

## Bhikkhuni
Buddhist nun.

## Sadhu
Jain monk.

## Sadhvi
Jain nun.

## Vihara
Buddhist monastery.

## Chaitya
Buddhist prayer hall.

## Stupa
Buddhist mound-like structure containing relics or symbolizing Buddha.

## Jinalaya
Jain temple.

## Basadi
Jain temple, especially in Karnataka.

## Derasar
Jain temple, especially in western India.

## Relic Worship
Veneration of physical remains of Buddha or saints.

## Non-Vedic Culture
Culture not based on Vedic authority.

## Ahimsa
Non-violence, especially central to Jainism and important in Buddhism.

## Karma Theory
Belief that actions produce consequences affecting future existence.

## Renunciation
Leaving household life for spiritual pursuit.

---

# 6. MAURYAN ART AND CULTURE

## Mauryan Art
Art of the Mauryan Empire, known for polished stone pillars, animal capitals, caves, stupas, and Yaksha-Yakshi sculptures.

## Court Art
Official imperial art produced under royal patronage.

## Popular Art
Non-court art such as Yaksha and Yakshi images.

## Mauryan Polish
Highly smooth and shiny polish on stone pillars and sculptures.

## Ashokan Pillars
Monolithic stone pillars erected by Ashoka with inscriptions and animal capitals.

## Monolithic Pillar
Pillar made from a single stone block.

## Chunar Sandstone
Stone used for many Ashokan pillars.

## Pillar Capital
Sculpted top portion of a pillar.

## Bell Capital
Inverted lotus-like base of an Ashokan pillar capital.

## Abacus
Decorated slab above the bell base of a pillar capital.

## Animal Capital
Animal sculpture on top of a pillar, such as lion, bull, elephant, or horse.

## Sarnath Lion Capital
Four-lion capital from Sarnath, adopted as India’s National Emblem.

## Ashoka Chakra
Wheel motif from Ashokan art, used in the Indian national flag.

## Rampurva Bull Capital
Famous Mauryan bull capital.

## Lauriya Nandangarh Pillar
Ashokan pillar site in Bihar.

## Dhauli Elephant
Rock-cut elephant figure at Dhauli in Odisha.

## Barabar Caves
Earliest surviving rock-cut caves in India, donated by Ashoka to Ajivikas.

## Lomas Rishi Cave
Barabar cave famous for its chaitya-arch facade.

## Sudama Cave
Barabar cave donated to Ajivikas.

## Nagarjuni Caves
Caves donated by Dasharatha Maurya to Ajivikas.

## Rock-Cut Architecture
Architecture carved directly into rock.

## Chaitya Arch
Horseshoe-shaped arch motif, seen at Lomas Rishi cave.

## Pataliputra Palace
Mauryan palace admired by Greek writers, likely using wooden architecture.

## Kumrahar Pillared Hall
Archaeological remains near Patna associated with Mauryan architecture.

## Yaksha
Male nature-spirit figure in early Indian art.

## Yakshi
Female nature-spirit figure associated with fertility and prosperity.

## Didarganj Yakshi
Highly polished stone female figure, often discussed with Mauryan or early post-Mauryan art.

## Parkham Yaksha
Large Yaksha sculpture from Mathura region.

## Ashokan Edicts
Inscriptions spreading Ashoka’s Dhamma and administrative messages.

## Brahmi Script
Main script used in Ashokan inscriptions.

## Kharosthi Script
Script used in north-western Ashokan inscriptions.

## Prakrit Language
Main language of most Ashokan inscriptions.

## Dhamma
Ashoka’s ethical policy emphasizing morality, welfare, tolerance, and non-violence.

---

# 7. BUDDHIST ARCHITECTURE AND ART

## Stupa
A Buddhist relic mound or symbolic structure representing Buddha.

## Anda
Dome of a stupa.

## Harmika
Square railing on top of the stupa dome.

## Chhatra
Umbrella-like structure above the stupa.

## Chhatravali
Series of umbrellas above a stupa.

## Yasti
Central pole supporting the chhatras.

## Medhi
Circular terrace used for circumambulation.

## Vedika
Railing around a stupa.

## Torana
Decorative gateway of a stupa.

## Pradakshina Patha
Path for clockwise circumambulation.

## Relic Casket
Container holding sacred relics.

## Sanchi Stupa
Important Buddhist stupa in Madhya Pradesh, originally associated with Ashoka and later enlarged.

## Bharhut Stupa
Early Buddhist stupa famous for railings, inscriptions, and narrative reliefs.

## Amaravati Stupa
Major Buddhist stupa in Andhra region known for limestone relief sculpture.

## Dhamek Stupa
Important stupa at Sarnath.

## Chaitya Hall
Buddhist prayer hall containing a stupa.

## Vihara
Buddhist monastery.

## Rock-Cut Chaitya
Prayer hall carved into rock.

## Rock-Cut Vihara
Monastery carved into rock.

## Apsidal Plan
Plan with a rounded end, common in chaitya halls.

## Barrel-Vaulted Roof
Curved roof seen in chaitya halls.

## Horseshoe Arch
Arched window motif in Buddhist caves.

## Gavaksha
Chaitya-window motif.

## Karle Chaitya
One of the finest Buddhist chaitya halls in Maharashtra.

## Bhaja Caves
Early Buddhist cave site in Maharashtra.

## Bedsa Caves
Buddhist cave site with chaitya architecture.

## Kanheri Caves
Large Buddhist cave complex near Mumbai.

## Nasik Caves
Buddhist cave site with inscriptions.

## Ajanta Caves
Buddhist cave complex famous for paintings and sculptures.

## Ellora Buddhist Caves
Buddhist caves in the Ellora complex.

## Aniconic Art
Early Buddhist art representing Buddha through symbols instead of human form.

## Iconic Art
Art showing Buddha in human form.

## Empty Throne
Symbol of Buddha in early aniconic art.

## Bodhi Tree
Symbol of Buddha’s enlightenment.

## Footprints of Buddha
Aniconic symbol of Buddha.

## Dharmachakra
Wheel of Dharma, symbol of Buddha’s teaching.

## Riderless Horse
Symbol of Buddha’s renunciation.

## Lotus
Symbol of purity and spiritual awakening.

## Jataka Scenes
Art showing stories of Buddha’s previous births.

## Narrative Relief
Sculptural panel telling a story.

---

# 8. GANDHARA, MATHURA, AND AMARAVATI SCHOOLS

## Gandhara School
Buddhist art style of north-west India influenced by Greek-Roman elements.

## Greco-Buddhist Art
Buddhist art showing Hellenistic artistic influence.

## Grey Schist
Stone commonly used in Gandhara sculpture.

## Stucco
Material used in Gandhara sculpture.

## Wavy Hair
Common feature of Gandhara Buddha images.

## Toga-like Robe
Draped robe style in Gandhara Buddha images.

## Realistic Anatomy
Naturalistic body form in Gandhara art.

## Bodhisattva Maitreya
Often shown in Gandhara art with princely ornaments.

## Mathura School
Art style centered at Mathura, using red sandstone and indigenous Indian features.

## Red Sandstone
Common material of Mathura sculpture.

## Mathura Buddha
Buddha image with strong body, thin robe, and Indian features.

## Mathura Jain Images
Mathura was also an important Jain art center.

## Kankali Tila
Jain archaeological site at Mathura.

## Kushana Art
Art flourishing under Kushana patronage, especially Gandhara and Mathura schools.

## Amaravati School
Buddhist art style of Andhra region known for elegant limestone reliefs.

## White Limestone
Material commonly used in Amaravati sculpture.

## Dynamic Movement
Feature of Amaravati art showing lively figures and movement.

## Nagarjunakonda
Important Buddhist art center in Andhra Pradesh.

## Ayaka Pillars
Pillars associated with Andhra Buddhist stupas.

## Aniconic to Iconic Transition
Shift from symbolic Buddha representation to human Buddha images.

---

# 9. JAIN ART AND ARCHITECTURE

## Jain Art
Art connected with Tirthankaras, Yakshas, Yakshis, temples, manuscripts, and pilgrimage sites.

## Tirthankara Image
Image of a Jain spiritual teacher, usually seated or standing in meditation.

## Jina Image
Image of a spiritual conqueror.

## Kayotsarga
Standing meditation posture in Jain art.

## Padmasana
Lotus sitting posture.

## Lanchhana
Symbol used to identify a Tirthankara.

## Srivatsa
Auspicious mark on the chest of Tirthankara images.

## Yaksha-Yakshi
Attendant deities of Tirthankaras.

## Ayagapata
Jain votive tablet, especially from Mathura.

## Manastambha
Tall pillar in front of Jain temples symbolizing humility.

## Chaumukha
Four-faced Jain image or shrine.

## Dilwara Temples
Jain temples at Mount Abu famous for marble carving.

## Ranakpur Temple
Famous Jain temple in Rajasthan dedicated to Adinatha.

## Palitana
Major Jain pilgrimage center in Gujarat.

## Shatrunjaya
Sacred hill at Palitana.

## Girnar
Jain pilgrimage site associated with Neminatha.

## Shravanabelagola
Major Jain center in Karnataka famous for Bahubali statue.

## Bahubali
Jain figure symbolizing renunciation and meditation.

## Gommateshwara Statue
Huge monolithic statue of Bahubali at Shravanabelagola.

## Udayagiri-Khandagiri Caves
Jain caves in Odisha associated with Kharavela.

## Hathigumpha Inscription
Inscription of Kharavela near Udayagiri.

## Ellora Jain Caves
Jain caves in the Ellora complex.

## Indra Sabha
Famous Jain cave at Ellora.

## Sittanavasal
Jain cave site in Tamil Nadu famous for paintings.

---

# 10. EARLY HINDU ART AND ICONOGRAPHY

## Hindu Iconography
System of visual representation of Hindu deities, symbols, weapons, vehicles, and postures.

## Murti
Sacred image of a deity.

## Pratima
Image or idol.

## Prana Pratishtha
Ritual consecration of an image.

## Shiva
Major Hindu deity associated with destruction, transformation, asceticism, and cosmic dance.

## Vishnu
Major Hindu deity associated with preservation and avatars.

## Devi
Goddess or divine feminine power.

## Brahma
Creator deity in later Hindu tradition.

## Linga
Symbolic form of Shiva.

## Yoni
Symbol associated with creative energy, often paired with linga.

## Nandi
Bull vehicle of Shiva.

## Garuda
Eagle-like vehicle of Vishnu.

## Lakshmi
Goddess of wealth and prosperity.

## Saraswati
Goddess of learning, speech, and music.

## Durga
Warrior goddess.

## Mahishasuramardini
Durga as slayer of the buffalo demon Mahishasura.

## Ganesha
Elephant-headed deity associated with beginnings and wisdom.

## Kartikeya
War god, also called Skanda or Murugan.

## Surya
Sun god.

## Sapta Matrikas
Seven mother goddesses.

## Trimurti
Trinity of Brahma, Vishnu, and Shiva.

## Avatar
Incarnation of a deity, especially Vishnu.

## Dashavatara
Ten avatars of Vishnu.

## Varaha
Boar avatar of Vishnu.

## Narasimha
Man-lion avatar of Vishnu.

## Vamana
Dwarf avatar of Vishnu.

## Krishna
Avatar of Vishnu and central figure in Bhakti tradition.

## Rama
Avatar of Vishnu and hero of Ramayana.

## Nataraja
Shiva as cosmic dancer.

## Tandava
Powerful cosmic dance of Shiva.

## Lasya
Graceful dance associated with Parvati.

## Mudra
Symbolic hand gesture.

## Abhaya Mudra
Gesture of fearlessness.

## Varada Mudra
Gesture of blessing or gift-giving.

## Dhyana Mudra
Meditation gesture.

## Chakra
Disc weapon of Vishnu.

## Shankha
Conch of Vishnu.

## Gada
Mace.

## Padma
Lotus.

## Trishula
Trident of Shiva.

## Damru
Drum of Shiva.

# 11. GUPTA ART AND CULTURE

## Gupta Age
Period often called the classical age of ancient Indian art, literature, science, and Sanskrit culture.

## Classical Sanskrit Culture
Refined Sanskrit literature, drama, poetry, inscriptions, and court culture.

## Gupta Sculpture
Sculpture known for grace, balance, spiritual calm, and idealized human form.

## Sarnath School
Gupta art style known for smooth Buddha images with spiritual expression.

## Mathura Gupta Art
Continuation of Mathura tradition with Gupta refinement.

## Gupta Buddha
Buddha image with calm face, thin robe, downcast eyes, and spiritual expression.

## Halo
Circular disc behind the head, common in Gupta sculpture.

## Udayagiri Caves
Gupta-period caves in Madhya Pradesh, famous for Varaha relief.

## Varaha Relief
Large sculpture of Vishnu’s boar avatar rescuing the earth.

## Deogarh Dashavatara Temple
Important Gupta-period temple showing early Hindu temple architecture.

## Dashavatara Temple
Temple at Deogarh dedicated to Vishnu.

## Early Structural Temple
Temple built with stone or brick rather than carved into rock.

## Gupta Temple Architecture
Early development of garbhagriha, mandapa, and shikhara forms.

## Bhitargaon Temple
Gupta-period brick temple in Uttar Pradesh.

## Tigawa Temple
Early Gupta temple in Madhya Pradesh.

## Sanchi Temple 17
Early Gupta temple with simple flat-roofed structure.

## Gupta Coins
Gold coins showing rulers, deities, rituals, and artistic skill.

## Dinara
Gold coin of Gupta period.

## Kalidasa
Great Sanskrit poet and dramatist.

## Abhijnanashakuntalam
Famous play by Kalidasa.

## Meghaduta
Lyric poem by Kalidasa.

## Kumarasambhava
Epic poem by Kalidasa.

## Raghuvamsha
Epic poem by Kalidasa.

## Vishakhadatta
Author of Mudrarakshasa and Devichandraguptam.

## Shudraka
Author traditionally associated with Mrichchhakatika.

## Mrichchhakatika
Sanskrit drama meaning “Little Clay Cart”.

## Aryabhata
Mathematician and astronomer of Gupta age.

## Aryabhatiya
Mathematical and astronomical work by Aryabhata.

## Varahamihira
Scholar of astronomy and astrology.

## Brihat Samhita
Encyclopedic work by Varahamihira.

## Amarasimha
Author of Amarakosha.

## Amarakosha
Sanskrit lexicon.

---

# 12. AJANTA, BAGH, AND CLASSICAL PAINTING

## Ajanta Paintings
Buddhist cave paintings in Maharashtra showing Jataka tales, Buddha, Bodhisattvas, royal scenes, and daily life.

## Mural Painting
Painting done on walls or ceilings.

## Fresco
Wall painting technique on wet plaster; Ajanta is often described as tempera-like rather than true fresco.

## Tempera Technique
Painting on dry plaster with pigments mixed with binding material.

## Jataka Painting
Painting showing previous births of Buddha.

## Padmapani
Famous Bodhisattva painting at Ajanta.

## Vajrapani
Famous Bodhisattva painting at Ajanta.

## Cave 1 Ajanta
Famous for Padmapani and Vajrapani paintings.

## Cave 2 Ajanta
Known for painted ceilings and narrative scenes.

## Cave 16 Ajanta
Important Vakataka-period cave.

## Cave 17 Ajanta
Famous for murals and Jataka scenes.

## Cave 26 Ajanta
Chaitya cave with Mahaparinirvana sculpture.

## Vakataka Patronage
Patronage of later Ajanta caves under Vakataka rulers and nobles.

## Bagh Caves
Buddhist caves in Madhya Pradesh known for paintings.

## Bagh Paintings
Wall paintings similar in spirit to Ajanta, with strong human figures.

## Sigiriya Paintings
Sri Lankan paintings often compared with Ajanta in broader South Asian art.

## Classical Indian Painting
Painting tradition emphasizing line, expression, storytelling, and spiritual mood.

---

# 13. TEMPLE ARCHITECTURE: BASIC TERMS

## Temple Architecture
Architecture of Hindu, Jain, and Buddhist sacred buildings.

## Hindu Temple
Sacred structure housing a deity image and used for worship.

## Garbhagriha
Sanctum sanctorum or innermost shrine of a temple.

## Mandapa
Pillared hall in front of the sanctum.

## Antarala
Vestibule between sanctum and hall.

## Shikhara
Tower above the sanctum in north Indian temples.

## Vimana
Tower above the sanctum in south Indian temples.

## Gopuram
Large gateway tower in south Indian temple complexes.

## Amalaka
Ribbed stone disc on top of Nagara shikhara.

## Kalasha
Pot-like finial at the top of temple tower.

## Jagati
Raised platform on which a temple stands.

## Pradakshina Patha
Circumambulatory path around the sanctum.

## Ardhamandapa
Entrance porch or front hall.

## Mahamandapa
Large main hall.

## Nandi Mandapa
Hall containing Nandi before Shiva temples.

## Sabha Mandapa
Assembly hall.

## Natya Mandapa
Dance hall.

## Kalyana Mandapa
Hall used for ceremonial marriage of deity.

## Bhoga Mandapa
Hall for offering food to deity.

## Devakoshtha
Niche in temple wall for subsidiary deities.

## Dvarapala
Door guardian figure.

## Mithuna Figure
Amorous couple sculpture symbolizing fertility, auspiciousness, or worldly life.

## Salabhanjika
Female figure holding or bending a tree branch, associated with fertility and beauty.

## Kirtimukha
Decorative face motif, often above doorways.

## Makara
Mythical aquatic creature used in temple decoration.

## Torana
Decorative gateway or arch.

## Prastara
Entablature or horizontal superstructure element.

## Adhisthana
Base or plinth of a temple.

## Jangha
Wall portion of a temple.

## Kapota
Cornice-like architectural element.

## Sikhara
Alternative spelling of Shikhara.

## Rekha
Curvilinear form of Nagara shikhara.

## Latina
Simple curvilinear Nagara tower.

## Bhumija
A subtype of Nagara temple tower with miniature spires arranged in rows.

## Phamsana
Pyramidal roof form, often over mandapas.

## Valabhi
Barrel-roofed temple form.

---

# 14. NAGARA TEMPLE STYLE

## Nagara Style
North Indian temple style marked by curvilinear shikhara, square plan, and amalaka.

## Rekha Prasada
Curvilinear tower of Nagara temples.

## Latina Shikhara
Simple curving tower of Nagara style.

## Shekhari Shikhara
Nagara tower with many attached miniature spires.

## Bhumija Shikhara
Nagara tower type with grid-like arrangement of miniature spires.

## Amalaka
Ribbed circular stone at the top of Nagara shikhara.

## Kalasha
Pot-like finial above amalaka.

## Panchayatana Plan
Temple plan with main shrine and four subsidiary shrines at corners.

## Sandhara Temple
Temple with circumambulatory path around sanctum.

## Nirandhara Temple
Temple without circumambulatory path.

## Khajuraho Temples
Chandella temples in Madhya Pradesh, famous for Nagara style and sculpture.

## Kandariya Mahadeva Temple
Famous Khajuraho temple dedicated to Shiva.

## Lakshmana Temple Khajuraho
Important Vishnu temple at Khajuraho.

## Odisha Temple Style
Regional Nagara style found in Odisha.

## Kalinga Architecture
Temple style of Odisha.

## Rekha Deul
Sanctum tower in Odisha temples.

## Pidha Deul
Pyramidal hall structure in Odisha temples.

## Khakhara Deul
Barrel-roofed Odisha temple form, often associated with goddess temples.

## Lingaraja Temple
Major Shiva temple in Bhubaneswar.

## Mukteswara Temple
Odisha temple famous for ornamental gateway and refined carving.

## Rajarani Temple
Temple in Bhubaneswar known for sculptural elegance.

## Jagannath Temple
Famous temple at Puri dedicated to Jagannath.

## Konark Sun Temple
13th-century Sun temple in Odisha designed like a stone chariot.

## Sun Temple
Temple dedicated to Surya.

## Modhera Sun Temple
Sun temple in Gujarat built under Solanki patronage.

## Martand Sun Temple
Sun temple in Kashmir.

---

# 15. DRAVIDA TEMPLE STYLE

## Dravida Style
South Indian temple style marked by pyramidal vimana, large temple complexes, gopurams, and enclosed courtyards.

## Vimana
Pyramidal tower above the sanctum in Dravida temples.

## Gopuram
Monumental gateway tower of south Indian temples.

## Prakara
Enclosure wall around a temple complex.

## Mandapa
Pillared hall.

## Kalyana Mandapa
Marriage hall for temple rituals.

## Temple Tank
Water tank associated with temple rituals.

## Pushkarini
Sacred temple tank.

## Dravida Shikhara
Pyramidal superstructure above sanctum.

## Stupi
Finial at the top of Dravida vimana.

## Pallava Architecture
South Indian temple architecture under Pallavas.

## Mahabalipuram
Pallava site famous for rock-cut temples, rathas, reliefs, and Shore Temple.

## Mamallapuram
Another name for Mahabalipuram.

## Pancha Rathas
Five monolithic temples at Mahabalipuram.

## Shore Temple
Structural Pallava temple at Mahabalipuram.

## Descent of the Ganga
Large rock relief at Mahabalipuram, also called Arjuna’s Penance.

## Kailasanatha Temple Kanchipuram
Pallava structural temple dedicated to Shiva.

## Vaikuntha Perumal Temple
Pallava temple at Kanchipuram.

## Chola Architecture
Temple architecture under Cholas, known for massive vimanas and bronze sculptures.

## Brihadisvara Temple
Great Chola temple at Thanjavur built by Rajaraja I.

## Gangaikonda Cholapuram Temple
Chola temple built by Rajendra I.

## Airavatesvara Temple
Chola temple at Darasuram.

## Chola Vimana
Tall pyramidal tower over sanctum, especially at Brihadisvara.

## Chola Bronze
Metal sculpture tradition, especially Nataraja images.

## Nataraja Bronze
Iconic Chola image of Shiva as cosmic dancer.

## Vijayanagara Architecture
South Indian temple architecture with large gopurams, mandapas, and composite pillars.

## Raya Gopuram
Large gateway tower of Vijayanagara and later temples.

## Kalyana Mandapa Vijayanagara
Elaborate ceremonial hall.

## Composite Pillar
Pillar with sculpted animals, warriors, and mythical creatures.

## Musical Pillars
Pillars that produce musical sounds when struck, associated with some South Indian temples.

## Hampi
Capital of Vijayanagara, famous for temples and urban remains.

## Virupaksha Temple
Important temple at Hampi.

## Vittala Temple
Hampi temple famous for stone chariot and musical pillars.

## Madurai Meenakshi Temple
Large temple complex with gopurams, mainly developed under Nayaka patronage.

## Srirangam Temple
Large temple complex dedicated to Vishnu.

## Rameswaram Temple
Temple famous for long corridors.

---

# 16. VESARA AND DECCAN TEMPLE STYLE

## Vesara Style
Hybrid temple style combining Nagara and Dravida features, especially in Deccan.

## Deccan Architecture
Temple architecture of the plateau region, influenced by both northern and southern styles.

## Chalukya Architecture
Architecture of Badami Chalukyas, seen at Aihole, Badami, and Pattadakal.

## Badami Caves
Rock-cut temples of Chalukyas.

## Aihole
Important Chalukyan temple site, often called a laboratory of Indian temple architecture.

## Durga Temple Aihole
Apsidal temple at Aihole.

## Lad Khan Temple
Early Chalukyan temple at Aihole.

## Pattadakal
UNESCO-style temple complex showing Nagara and Dravida forms.

## Virupaksha Temple Pattadakal
Chalukyan temple inspired by Pallava architecture.

## Papanatha Temple
Pattadakal temple showing mixed features.

## Rashtrakuta Architecture
Architecture under Rashtrakutas, especially at Ellora.

## Kailasanatha Temple Ellora
Massive rock-cut temple built under Rashtrakutas.

## Ellora
Rock-cut cave complex with Buddhist, Hindu, and Jain caves.

## Elephanta Caves
Caves near Mumbai famous for Trimurti Shiva sculpture.

## Trimurti Shiva
Three-faced Shiva sculpture at Elephanta.

## Western Chalukya Architecture
Later Deccan temple style under Kalyani Chalukyas.

## Hoysala Architecture
Temple style of Karnataka, known for star-shaped plans, soapstone carving, and ornate sculpture.

## Soapstone
Soft stone used in Hoysala temples.

## Stellate Plan
Star-shaped temple plan.

## Belur
Hoysala site famous for Chennakesava Temple.

## Halebidu
Hoysala site famous for Hoysaleswara Temple.

## Somnathpur
Hoysala site famous for Keshava Temple.

## Lathe-Turned Pillars
Highly polished pillars shaped using lathe-like technique, common in Hoysala temples.

## Hoysala Sculpture
Detailed carving of deities, dancers, animals, epics, and decorative bands.

---

# 17. EARLY MEDIEVAL REGIONAL TEMPLE SCHOOLS

## Chandella Architecture
Temple architecture of Khajuraho region.

## Paramara Architecture
Central Indian temple style under Paramaras.

## Solanki Architecture
Temple architecture of Gujarat under Chaulukyas/Solankis.

## Maru-Gurjara Style
Western Indian temple style known for intricate carving, used in Hindu and Jain temples.

## Dilwara Marble Style
Highly ornate marble temple style at Mount Abu.

## Kashmir Temple Architecture
Temple style with Gandhara, Gupta, and local influences.

## Martand Sun Temple
Important Kashmir temple dedicated to Surya.

## Pandrethan Temple
Kashmir temple with distinctive stone architecture.

## Bengal Temple Architecture
Later regional temple style using brick and terracotta.

## Terracotta Temple
Temple decorated with baked clay panels.

## Bengal Chala Roof
Temple roof inspired by thatched huts of Bengal.

## Ek-Ratna Temple
Bengal temple with one tower.

## Pancha-Ratna Temple
Bengal temple with five towers.

## Navaratna Temple
Bengal temple with nine towers.

## Kerala Temple Architecture
Temple style adapted to heavy rainfall, using sloping roofs and wood.

## Sloping Roof Temple
Kerala temple roof form suited to monsoon climate.

## Koothambalam
Temple theatre hall in Kerala.

## Wooden Temple Architecture
Important in Kerala and Himalayan regions.

## Himachal Temple Architecture
Mountain temple style using wood and stone.

## Pagoda Style
Multi-tiered roof style in Himalayan temples.

## Kath-Kuni Technique
Traditional Himalayan building method using wood and stone.

---

# 18. INDO-ISLAMIC ARCHITECTURE: BASIC TERMS

## Indo-Islamic Architecture
Architecture formed by interaction of Islamic building traditions with Indian materials, craftsmen, and regional styles.

## Sultanate Architecture
Architecture under Delhi Sultanate and regional Sultanates.

## Mughal Architecture
Architecture under Mughal rulers, known for symmetry, gardens, domes, arches, marble, and pietra dura.

## Arch
Curved structural opening.

## True Arch
Arch made with wedge-shaped stones, able to bear weight.

## Corbelled Arch
Arch-like opening made by projecting stones inward step by step.

## Dome
Rounded roof structure.

## True Dome
Dome built using proper radiating construction.

## Minaret
Tall tower associated with mosque or victory monument.

## Mosque
Islamic place of worship.

## Mihrab
Niche in mosque wall indicating direction of Mecca.

## Qibla
Direction of Mecca for prayer.

## Minbar
Pulpit in a mosque.

## Iwan
Large vaulted hall or entrance, open on one side.

## Jali
Perforated stone screen.

## Chhatri
Small domed pavilion.

## Chajja
Projecting eave or balcony.

## Charbagh
Four-part garden layout, especially in Mughal tombs.

## Pietra Dura
Inlay work using colored stones in marble.

## Hasht-Bihisht
Eight-part architectural plan, common in Persian-Mughal tomb design.

## Calligraphy
Decorative writing, especially Quranic inscriptions in Islamic architecture.

## Arabesque
Decorative pattern of flowing plant forms.

## Geometric Decoration
Use of mathematical patterns in Islamic art.

## Stucco
Plaster used for decoration.

## Glazed Tiles
Colored tiles used in decoration.

---

# 19. DELHI SULTANATE ARCHITECTURE

## Slave Dynasty Architecture
Early Sultanate architecture under rulers like Qutbuddin Aibak and Iltutmish.

## Qutb Minar
Tall minaret in Delhi begun by Qutbuddin Aibak and completed by Iltutmish.

## Quwwat-ul-Islam Mosque
Early mosque in Delhi built using spolia from earlier temples.

## Adhai Din ka Jhonpra
Early mosque at Ajmer.

## Iltutmish Tomb
Early Sultanate tomb in Delhi.

## Alai Darwaza
Gateway built by Alauddin Khalji, known for true arch and dome.

## Khalji Architecture
Sultanate architecture with stronger use of true arch and dome.

## Tughlaq Architecture
Architecture known for sloping walls, strength, simplicity, and massive forms.

## Batter
Sloping wall used in Tughlaq architecture.

## Tughlaqabad Fort
Fort built by Ghiyasuddin Tughlaq.

## Ghiyasuddin Tughlaq Tomb
Tomb showing sloping walls and fortress-like form.

## Firoz Shah Kotla
Fort complex of Firoz Shah Tughlaq.

## Lodi Architecture
Late Sultanate architecture known for garden tombs and octagonal tombs.

## Lodi Tombs
Tombs in Delhi showing early garden-tomb tradition.

## Bara Gumbad
Lodi-period structure in Delhi.

## Shish Gumbad
Lodi-period tomb.

## Octagonal Tomb
Tomb plan common in Lodi architecture.

## Square Tomb
Another common Sultanate tomb type.

---

# 20. REGIONAL SULTANATE ARCHITECTURE

## Bengal Sultanate Architecture
Regional style using brick, terracotta, curved cornices, and multiple domes.

## Curved Cornice
Curved roofline inspired by Bengal huts.

## Adina Mosque
Large mosque in Bengal.

## Eklakhi Tomb
Bengal Sultanate tomb.

## Gujarat Sultanate Architecture
Style known for delicate carving, jalis, and fusion of Islamic and local traditions.

## Jama Masjid Ahmedabad
Important mosque of Gujarat Sultanate.

## Sidi Saiyyed Jali
Famous stone lattice screen in Ahmedabad.

## Jaunpur Architecture
Regional Sultanate style known for massive gateways and mosques.

## Atala Mosque
Important mosque at Jaunpur.

## Malwa Architecture
Architecture of Mandu region.

## Mandu
Important Malwa Sultanate site.

## Jahaz Mahal
Palace at Mandu appearing like a ship between water bodies.

## Hindola Mahal
Mandu palace with sloping walls.

## Deccan Sultanate Architecture
Architecture of Bahmani and Deccan Sultanates.

## Bahmani Architecture
Early Deccan Sultanate architecture.

## Gulbarga Mosque
Important Bahmani mosque.

## Bidar
Bahmani and Barid Shahi architectural center.

## Bijapur Architecture
Adil Shahi architecture known for large domes.

## Gol Gumbaz
Massive dome tomb of Muhammad Adil Shah at Bijapur.

## Ibrahim Rauza
Bijapur monument known for elegant design.

## Charminar
Iconic monument of Hyderabad built by Qutb Shahis.

## Golconda Fort
Fort of Qutb Shahi rulers.

---

# 21. MUGHAL ARCHITECTURE

## Mughal Architecture
Imperial architecture combining Persian, Central Asian, Timurid, and Indian elements.

## Babur’s Gardens
Babur introduced formal garden culture inspired by Central Asia.

## Humayun’s Tomb
Tomb in Delhi built by Haji Begum, considered a precursor to Taj Mahal.

## Akbar’s Architecture
Architecture marked by red sandstone, massive forms, and synthesis of regional styles.

## Agra Fort
Major Mughal fort developed by Akbar and later rulers.

## Fatehpur Sikri
Akbar’s planned capital near Agra.

## Buland Darwaza
Grand gateway at Fatehpur Sikri.

## Panch Mahal
Five-storeyed pavilion at Fatehpur Sikri.

## Diwan-i-Khas
Hall of private audience.

## Diwan-i-Aam
Hall of public audience.

## Jodha Bai Palace
Palace complex at Fatehpur Sikri.

## Ibadat Khana
House of worship built by Akbar for religious discussions.

## Jahangir’s Architecture
Marked by refinement, gardens, tombs, and naturalistic decoration.

## Itimad-ud-Daulah Tomb
Tomb in Agra, famous for white marble and pietra dura, often called jewel box.

## Shah Jahan’s Architecture
High point of Mughal architecture, known for marble, symmetry, elegance, and pietra dura.

## Taj Mahal
Mausoleum built by Shah Jahan for Mumtaz Mahal in Agra.

## Red Fort Delhi
Fort built by Shah Jahan in Delhi.

## Jama Masjid Delhi
Large mosque built by Shah Jahan.

## Moti Masjid
Pearl Mosque, name used for several Mughal mosques.

## Peacock Throne
Famous jeweled throne of Shah Jahan.

## Aurangzeb’s Architecture
More restrained but includes monuments such as Badshahi Mosque and Bibi ka Maqbara.

## Bibi ka Maqbara
Tomb in Aurangabad associated with Aurangzeb’s period.

## Mughal Garden
Formal garden based on symmetry, water channels, and charbagh layout.

## Charbagh Tomb
Tomb placed in a four-part garden.

## Red Sandstone
Common material in Akbar’s architecture.

## White Marble
Common material in Shah Jahan’s architecture.

## Pietra Dura
Decorative inlay using semi-precious stones.

## Jali Work
Perforated stone screen used for light, air, and decoration.

---

# 22. INDIAN PAINTING TRADITIONS

## Painting
Art of creating images using pigments on walls, cloth, paper, palm leaf, or other surfaces.

## Mural Painting
Painting on walls or ceilings.

## Miniature Painting
Small, detailed painting, usually on paper or manuscript.

## Manuscript Painting
Painting made to illustrate manuscripts.

## Palm-Leaf Painting
Painting on palm-leaf manuscripts.

## Paper Manuscript
Manuscript on paper, used widely in medieval period.

## Ajanta Painting
Classical Buddhist mural painting.

## Bagh Painting
Buddhist mural painting from Madhya Pradesh.

## Pala Painting
Eastern Indian Buddhist manuscript painting under Palas.

## Jain Manuscript Painting
Western Indian miniature tradition illustrating Jain texts.

## Western Indian School
Miniature painting style associated with Jain manuscripts in Gujarat and Rajasthan.

## Apabhramsha Style
Early western Indian manuscript painting style with angular figures and bright colors.

## Mughal Painting
Court painting under Mughals, known for naturalism, portraits, manuscripts, and historical scenes.

## Persian Influence
Influence on Mughal painting through artists and manuscripts.

## Hamzanama
Large illustrated manuscript produced under Akbar.

## Akbarnama Paintings
Paintings illustrating Akbar’s reign.

## Baburnama Paintings
Illustrations of Babur’s memoirs.

## Jahangir Painting
Known for naturalistic portraits, animals, birds, and European influence.

## Ustad Mansur
Famous Mughal painter known for natural history paintings.

## Bishandas
Mughal portrait painter.

## Basawan
Important painter of Akbar’s court.

## Daswanth
Important painter of Akbar’s court.

## Mir Sayyid Ali
Persian artist at Mughal court.

## Abdus Samad
Persian artist at Mughal court.

## Rajput Painting
Regional painting style of Rajasthan, often based on epics, Bhakti themes, ragas, and court life.

## Rajasthani School
Painting tradition including Mewar, Marwar, Bundi, Kota, Kishangarh, Jaipur, and Bikaner.

## Mewar School
Rajput painting school with bold colors and devotional themes.

## Marwar School
Rajasthani painting style of Jodhpur region.

## Bundi School
Known for lush landscapes and court scenes.

## Kota School
Known for hunting scenes and dynamic animals.

## Kishangarh School
Known for lyrical Radha-Krishna paintings and Bani Thani.

## Bani Thani
Famous Kishangarh painting idealizing feminine beauty.

## Jaipur School
Rajput painting influenced by Mughal naturalism.

## Bikaner School
Rajput painting with strong Mughal and Deccan influence.

## Pahari Painting
Hill-state painting tradition of Himachal and Jammu region.

## Basohli School
Early Pahari style with bold colors and intense expression.

## Guler School
Pahari style with delicate naturalism.

## Kangra School
Pahari school famous for lyrical Radha-Krishna themes.

## Garhwal School
Pahari painting style of Garhwal region.

## Chamba School
Pahari painting style of Chamba region.

## Deccan Painting
Painting tradition of Deccan Sultanates, known for rich colors, fantasy, and Persian-Turkish-Indian blend.

## Ahmednagar School
Deccan painting style.

## Bijapur School
Deccan painting known for elegance and fantasy.

## Golconda School
Deccan painting with rich colors and textiles.

## Company Painting
Painting made under British East India Company patronage, blending Indian and European styles.

## Patna Kalam
Company-period painting style from Patna, often showing daily life and occupations.

## Kalighat Painting
19th-century painting tradition from Kolkata, known for bold lines and social themes.

## Bengal School
Modern Indian art movement led by Abanindranath Tagore, reacting against academic realism.

## Wash Technique
Soft painting technique used by Bengal School artists.

## Bharat Mata Painting
Famous work by Abanindranath Tagore.

## Raja Ravi Varma
Modern Indian painter known for oil paintings of mythological themes in European academic style.

## Jamini Roy
Modern painter inspired by folk and Kalighat styles.

## Amrita Sher-Gil
Modern Indian painter known for expressive works on Indian life.

## Progressive Artists’ Group
Modern Indian art group founded in Bombay after independence.

## M. F. Husain
Modern Indian painter associated with Progressive Artists’ Group.

## S. H. Raza
Modern Indian painter known for bindu motif.

## F. N. Souza
Modern Indian painter associated with Progressive Artists’ Group.

---

# 23. FOLK AND TRIBAL PAINTINGS

## Folk Painting
Traditional painting practiced by local communities.

## Tribal Painting
Painting traditions of tribal communities.

## Madhubani Painting
Folk painting of Mithila region in Bihar, known for geometric patterns, deities, nature, and bright colors.

## Mithila Painting
Another name for Madhubani painting.

## Warli Painting
Tribal painting of Maharashtra using simple white geometric figures on mud walls.

## Pattachitra
Traditional cloth or scroll painting of Odisha and Bengal.

## Odisha Pattachitra
Painting on cloth showing Jagannath, Krishna, and mythological themes.

## Bengal Patachitra
Scroll painting tradition accompanied by songs.

## Kalamkari
Painted or block-printed textile tradition from Andhra Pradesh and Telangana.

## Srikalahasti Kalamkari
Hand-painted Kalamkari tradition.

## Machilipatnam Kalamkari
Block-printed Kalamkari tradition.

## Phad Painting
Rajasthan scroll painting narrating stories of local deities like Pabuji and Devnarayan.

## Pithora Painting
Ritual painting of Rathwa and Bhil communities of Gujarat and Madhya Pradesh.

## Gond Painting
Tribal painting tradition of Gond community with dots, lines, animals, and nature.

## Sanjhi Art
Paper-cutting or stencil art associated with Krishna worship.

## Mandana Painting
Wall and floor painting tradition of Rajasthan and Madhya Pradesh.

## Alpana
Ritual floor painting of Bengal.

## Kolam
South Indian ritual floor design made with rice flour.

## Rangoli
Decorative floor art made with colors, rice flour, flowers, or powder.

## Aipan
Ritual floor and wall art of Uttarakhand.

## Sohrai Painting
Tribal wall painting tradition of Jharkhand.

## Khovar Painting
Marriage-related wall painting tradition of Jharkhand.

## Cheriyal Scroll Painting
Narrative scroll painting tradition of Telangana.

## Thangka Painting
Tibetan Buddhist religious painting on cloth.

## Tanjore Painting
South Indian painting tradition using gold foil and devotional themes.

## Mysore Painting
Classical South Indian painting tradition known for delicate work and gold leaf.

---

# 24. LITERATURE: BASIC TERMS

## Literature
Written or oral creative expression, including poetry, drama, stories, epics, religious texts, and philosophical works.

## Oral Literature
Literature transmitted by memory and performance.

## Written Literature
Literature recorded in manuscripts or inscriptions.

## Sacred Literature
Religious texts.

## Secular Literature
Non-religious literature.

## Kavya
Classical Sanskrit poetry.

## Mahakavya
Great epic-style poem.

## Nataka
Drama or play.

## Champu
Literary form mixing prose and poetry.

## Prabandha
Narrative literary form.

## Itihasa
Epic tradition, especially Ramayana and Mahabharata.

## Purana
Religious narrative text containing myths, genealogies, cosmology, and sacred geography.

## Sutra Literature
Concise rule-based texts.

## Shastra Literature
Technical or systematic texts.

## Bhashya
Commentary.

## Tika
Sub-commentary.

## Vritti
Explanatory gloss.

## Katha
Story.

## Akhyana
Narrative.

## Gatha
Verse or song.

## Doha
Couplet form common in medieval devotional literature.

## Pad
Lyric devotional poem.

## Bhajan
Devotional song.

## Kirtan
Devotional singing, often collective.

## Abhanga
Marathi devotional poem, especially of Varkari saints.

## Vachana
Kannada prose-poem associated with Virashaiva saints.

---

# 25. ANCIENT INDIAN LITERATURE

## Vedic Literature
Oldest Indian literature including Vedas, Brahmanas, Aranyakas, and Upanishads.

## Rigveda
Oldest Veda.

## Samaveda
Veda of melodies.

## Yajurveda
Veda of sacrificial formulas.

## Atharvaveda
Veda of charms, healing, and household concerns.

## Brahmanas
Texts explaining rituals.

## Aranyakas
Forest texts dealing with ritual symbolism and meditation.

## Upanishads
Philosophical texts on Brahman, Atman, karma, rebirth, and moksha.

## Vedangas
Six auxiliary disciplines of Vedic study.

## Shiksha
Phonetics.

## Kalpa
Ritual procedure.

## Vyakarana
Grammar.

## Nirukta
Etymology.

## Chandas
Metre.

## Jyotisha
Astronomy and calendar science.

## Ramayana
Epic traditionally attributed to Valmiki, narrating the life of Rama.

## Mahabharata
Epic traditionally attributed to Vyasa, containing the Bhagavad Gita.

## Bhagavad Gita
Philosophical dialogue between Krishna and Arjuna in the Mahabharata.

## Puranas
Texts containing myths, genealogies, cosmology, sacred geography, and religious teachings.

## Dharmasutras
Texts dealing with duties, social conduct, and law.

## Dharmashastras
Later legal-religious texts, such as Manusmriti.

## Manusmriti
Important Dharmashastra text.

## Arthashastra
Text on statecraft traditionally attributed to Kautilya.

## Kamasutra
Text on love, aesthetics, and social life attributed to Vatsyayana.

## Natyashastra
Text on drama, dance, music, aesthetics, and performance attributed to Bharata Muni.

## Ashtadhyayi
Grammar of Sanskrit by Panini.

## Mahabhashya
Patanjali’s commentary on Panini.

## Amarakosha
Sanskrit lexicon by Amarasimha.

---

# 26. BUDDHIST AND JAIN LITERATURE

## Pali Literature
Buddhist literature in Pali language.

## Tripitaka
Three baskets of Buddhist scriptures.

## Vinaya Pitaka
Basket of monastic discipline.

## Sutta Pitaka
Basket of Buddha’s discourses.

## Abhidhamma Pitaka
Basket of higher doctrine.

## Dhammapada
Popular Buddhist verse text.

## Jataka
Stories of Buddha’s previous births.

## Milindapanha
Dialogue between King Milinda and monk Nagasena.

## Buddhacharita
Sanskrit biography of Buddha by Ashvaghosha.

## Mahavamsa
Sri Lankan Buddhist chronicle.

## Dipavamsa
Sri Lankan Buddhist chronicle.

## Lalitavistara
Sanskrit Buddhist text on Buddha’s life.

## Divyavadana
Collection of Buddhist stories.

## Jain Agamas
Canonical scriptures of Svetambara Jainism.

## Acharanga Sutra
Jain text on monastic conduct and Mahavira’s life.

## Sutrakritanga
Jain text explaining doctrine and criticizing rival views.

## Bhagavati Sutra
Important Jain canonical text.

## Kalpa Sutra
Jain text on lives of Tirthankaras, especially Mahavira.

## Tattvartha Sutra
Important Jain philosophical text by Umasvati.

## Samayasara
Digambara Jain text by Kundakunda.

## Paumachariya
Jain Ramayana by Vimalasuri.

## Trishashti Shalaka Purusha Charitra
Jain universal history by Hemachandra.

---

# 27. CLASSICAL SANSKRIT LITERATURE

## Classical Sanskrit
Refined Sanskrit used in literature, court poetry, drama, inscriptions, and philosophy.

## Kalidasa
Great Sanskrit poet and dramatist.

## Abhijnanashakuntalam
Famous play by Kalidasa.

## Meghaduta
Lyrical poem by Kalidasa.

## Kumarasambhava
Poem on birth of Kumara by Kalidasa.

## Raghuvamsha
Epic poem on Raghu dynasty by Kalidasa.

## Bharavi
Author of Kiratarjuniya.

## Kiratarjuniya
Mahakavya based on Arjuna and Shiva.

## Magha
Author of Shishupalavadha.

## Shishupalavadha
Mahakavya based on Krishna killing Shishupala.

## Sriharsha
Author of Naishadhacharita.

## Naishadhacharita
Mahakavya based on Nala and Damayanti.

## Bhasa
Early Sanskrit dramatist.

## Svapnavasavadatta
Drama attributed to Bhasa.

## Shudraka
Author associated with Mrichchhakatika.

## Mrichchhakatika
Sanskrit drama meaning Little Clay Cart.

## Vishakhadatta
Author of Mudrarakshasa.

## Mudrarakshasa
Drama on Chandragupta Maurya and Chanakya.

## Bhavabhuti
Sanskrit dramatist known for Uttararamacharita and Malatimadhava.

## Bana
Author of Harshacharita and Kadambari.

## Harshacharita
Biography of Harsha by Banabhatta.

## Kadambari
Prose romance by Banabhatta.

## Dandin
Author of Dashakumaracharita and Kavyadarsha.

## Kavyadarsha
Text on poetics by Dandin.

## Subandhu
Author of Vasavadatta.

## Panchatantra
Collection of animal fables and political wisdom.

## Hitopadesha
Collection of moral stories inspired by Panchatantra.

## Brihatkatha
Lost story collection attributed to Gunadhya.

## Kathasaritsagara
Sanskrit story collection by Somadeva based on Brihatkatha tradition.

# 28. SANGAM AND TAMIL LITERATURE

## Sangam Literature
Early Tamil literature composed by poets of ancient Tamilakam.

## Tamilakam
Ancient Tamil region including Tamil Nadu and parts of Kerala, Karnataka, and Andhra.

## Sangam
Academy or gathering of Tamil poets.

## Tolkappiyam
Earliest surviving Tamil grammar text.

## Ettuthokai
Eight Anthologies of Sangam literature.

## Pattuppattu
Ten Idylls of Sangam literature.

## Pathinenkilkanakku
Eighteen Lesser Texts, including moral works.

## Tirukkural
Tamil ethical text by Tiruvalluvar.

## Tiruvalluvar
Author of Tirukkural.

## Akam
Sangam poetry dealing with love and inner life.

## Puram
Sangam poetry dealing with war, charity, heroism, and public life.

## Thinai
Landscape-based poetic classification in Sangam literature.

## Kurinji
Mountain landscape.

## Mullai
Forest-pastoral landscape.

## Marutam
Agricultural landscape.

## Neital
Coastal landscape.

## Palai
Dry landscape.

## Silappadikaram
Tamil epic about Kannagi and Kovalan.

## Manimekalai
Buddhist Tamil epic.

## Jivaka Chintamani
Jain Tamil epic.

## Kambaramayanam
Tamil Ramayana by Kamban.

## Kamban
Tamil poet who composed Kambaramayanam.

# 29. MEDIEVAL REGIONAL LITERATURE

## Regional Literature
Literature written in Indian regional languages.

## Apabhramsha Literature
Late Middle Indo-Aryan literature that influenced modern north Indian languages.

## Kannada Literature
Regional literature enriched by Jain, Virashaiva, and Vaishnava traditions.

## Pampa
Important Kannada Jain poet.

## Ranna
Important Kannada Jain poet.

## Ponna
Kannada Jain poet.

## Basavanna
Virashaiva saint and composer of Vachanas.

## Vachana Literature
Kannada devotional prose-poetry of Virashaiva saints.

## Telugu Literature
Literature of Andhra-Telangana region.

## Nannaya
Early Telugu poet associated with Andhra Mahabharatam.

## Tikkana
Telugu poet who continued Mahabharata translation.

## Errana
Telugu poet who completed the Mahabharata tradition.

## Malayalam Literature
Literature of Kerala.

## Manipravalam
Literary style mixing Sanskrit and Malayalam/Tamil elements.

## Marathi Literature
Literature enriched by Bhakti saints.

## Jnaneshwar
Marathi Bhakti saint and author of Jnaneshwari.

## Jnaneshwari
Marathi commentary on Bhagavad Gita.

## Tukaram
Marathi Varkari saint known for Abhangas.

## Namdev
Marathi Bhakti saint.

## Eknath
Marathi saint-poet.

## Bengali Literature
Literature enriched by Vaishnava Bhakti and later modern movements.

## Charyapada
Early mystical Buddhist songs, important for eastern Indo-Aryan languages.

## Chaitanya Literature
Bengali Vaishnava devotional literature.

## Assamese Literature
Literature shaped by Sankardev and Vaishnavism.

## Sankardev
Assamese saint who promoted Ekasarana Dharma and cultural forms like Ankiya Nat.

## Borgeet
Devotional songs composed by Sankardev and Madhavdev.

## Odia Literature
Regional literature with Jagannath and Bhakti traditions.

## Sarala Das
Odia poet known for Odia Mahabharata.

## Hindi Literature
Literature including Bhakti poetry, Riti poetry, and modern prose.

## Kabir
Nirguna Bhakti saint-poet.

## Tulsidas
Author of Ramcharitmanas.

## Surdas
Krishna Bhakti poet.

## Mirabai
Krishna devotee and poet.

## Guru Granth Sahib
Sacred scripture of Sikhism containing hymns of Sikh Gurus and Bhakti saints.

## Adi Granth
Original compilation of Sikh scripture by Guru Arjan.

# 30. BHAKTI MOVEMENT

## Bhakti
Devotion to a personal god.

## Bhakti Movement
Religious movement emphasizing personal devotion, equality, emotional worship, and accessibility.

## Alvars
Tamil Vaishnava poet-saints devoted to Vishnu.

## Nayanars
Tamil Shaiva poet-saints devoted to Shiva.

## Divya Prabandham
Collection of Alvar hymns.

## Tevaram
Collection of Shaiva hymns by Nayanar saints.

## Andal
Female Alvar saint.

## Appar
Nayanar saint.

## Sambandar
Nayanar saint.

## Sundarar
Nayanar saint.

## Manikkavachakar
Tamil Shaiva saint-poet.

## Ramanuja
Vaishnava philosopher of Vishishtadvaita.

## Vishishtadvaita
Qualified non-dualism of Ramanuja.

## Madhvacharya
Vaishnava philosopher of Dvaita.

## Dvaita
Dualist Vedanta philosophy.

## Vallabhacharya
Founder of Shuddhadvaita and Pushtimarg.

## Shuddhadvaita
Pure non-dualism of Vallabhacharya.

## Pushtimarg
Path of grace associated with Vallabhacharya.

## Nimbarka
Vaishnava philosopher associated with Dvaitadvaita.

## Ramananda
Bhakti saint who influenced north Indian devotional traditions.

## Kabir
Nirguna saint criticizing ritualism and caste.

## Nirguna Bhakti
Devotion to a formless divine.

## Saguna Bhakti
Devotion to a personal god with form.

## Mirabai
Rajput princess and Krishna devotee.

## Surdas
Krishna Bhakti poet.

## Tulsidas
Rama Bhakti poet and author of Ramcharitmanas.

## Chaitanya Mahaprabhu
Bengal Vaishnava saint devoted to Krishna.

## Haridasa Movement
Vaishnava devotional movement in Karnataka.

## Purandara Dasa
Carnatic music saint, often called father of Carnatic music.

## Kanakadasa
Kannada Bhakti saint.

## Varkari Tradition
Maharashtra Bhakti tradition devoted to Vithoba.

## Vithoba
Form of Krishna/Vishnu worshipped at Pandharpur.

## Pandharpur
Major Varkari pilgrimage center.

## Abhanga
Marathi devotional poem.

# 31. SUFI CULTURE

## Sufism
Mystical tradition within Islam emphasizing love, devotion, inner purification, and union with God.

## Sufi
Mystic practitioner of Islam.

## Tasawwuf
Islamic mysticism.

## Khanqah
Sufi hospice or spiritual center.

## Dargah
Tomb-shrine of a Sufi saint.

## Pir
Sufi teacher or spiritual guide.

## Murid
Disciple of a Sufi teacher.

## Silsila
Sufi order or spiritual lineage.

## Sama
Musical spiritual gathering.

## Qawwali
Devotional Sufi music.

## Zikr
Remembrance of God.

## Chishti Order
Sufi order known for tolerance, music, and closeness to common people.

## Khwaja Muinuddin Chishti
Famous Chishti saint of Ajmer.

## Ajmer Sharif
Dargah of Khwaja Muinuddin Chishti.

## Qutbuddin Bakhtiyar Kaki
Chishti saint of Delhi.

## Baba Farid
Chishti saint whose verses are included in Guru Granth Sahib.

## Nizamuddin Auliya
Famous Chishti saint of Delhi.

## Amir Khusrau
Poet, musician, and disciple of Nizamuddin Auliya.

## Suhrawardi Order
Sufi order with more acceptance of state contact.

## Bahauddin Zakariya
Important Suhrawardi saint of Multan.

## Naqshbandi Order
Sufi order emphasizing orthodoxy and silent zikr.

## Ahmad Sirhindi
Naqshbandi saint also called Mujaddid Alf Sani.

## Qadiri Order
Sufi order that spread in India, associated with devotion and scholarship.

## Dara Shikoh
Mughal prince interested in Sufi-Vedantic dialogue.

## Majma-ul-Bahrain
Work by Dara Shikoh comparing Hindu and Islamic mystical thought.

# 32. INDIAN MUSIC: BASIC TERMS

## Music
Art of organized sound, rhythm, melody, and expression.

## Sangita
Indian term covering vocal music, instrumental music, and dance.

## Nada
Sound.

## Shruti
Microtone or smallest audible pitch difference in Indian music.

## Swara
Musical note.

## Saptak
Octave of seven notes.

## Sa Re Ga Ma Pa Dha Ni
Seven basic notes of Indian music.

## Raga
Melodic framework with specific notes, mood, and rules.

## Tala
Rhythmic cycle.

## Laya
Tempo.

## Alap
Slow introductory improvisation in a raga.

## Bandish
Fixed composition in Hindustani music.

## Kriti
Composed song form in Carnatic music.

## Gamaka
Ornamentation of notes.

## Meend
Glide between notes.

## Tan
Fast melodic passage.

## Drone
Continuous background pitch, often produced by tanpura.

## Tanpura
Drone instrument.

## Veena
Ancient string instrument.

## Sitar
Plucked string instrument of Hindustani music.

## Sarod
String instrument of Hindustani music.

## Sarangi
Bowed string instrument.

## Santoor
String instrument struck with mallets.

## Tabla
Pair of drums used in Hindustani music.

## Pakhawaj
Barrel drum used in Dhrupad.

## Mridangam
Main percussion instrument of Carnatic music.

## Ghatam
Clay pot percussion instrument.

## Kanjira
Frame drum used in Carnatic music.

## Nadaswaram
South Indian wind instrument.

## Shehnai
North Indian wind instrument.

## Flute
Wind instrument associated with Krishna and classical music.

---

# 33. HINDUSTANI MUSIC

## Hindustani Music
Classical music tradition of north India.

## Dhrupad
Oldest major form of Hindustani classical vocal music, serious and devotional.

## Dhamar
Dhrupad-related form associated with Holi.

## Khayal
Dominant modern form of Hindustani vocal music, allowing improvisation.

## Tarana
Composition using syllables like tanana, yalali, and nom-tom.

## Thumri
Semi-classical romantic-devotional form.

## Dadra
Light classical vocal form.

## Tappa
Fast, ornamental vocal form.

## Ghazal
Poetic-musical form based on Urdu poetry.

## Bhajan
Devotional song.

## Qawwali
Sufi devotional music.

## Gharana
Musical lineage or style.

## Gwalior Gharana
One of the oldest Khayal gharanas.

## Kirana Gharana
Known for note purity and slow elaboration.

## Agra Gharana
Known for strong voice and dhrupad influence.

## Jaipur-Atrauli Gharana
Known for complex ragas.

## Patiala Gharana
Known for ornamentation and fast taans.

## Rampur-Sahaswan Gharana
Known for clarity and taan patterns.

## Benares Gharana
Known for Thumri, tabla, and semi-classical styles.

## Maihar Gharana
Instrumental gharana associated with Allauddin Khan.

## Dhrupad Bani
Stylistic tradition in Dhrupad.

## Darbhanga Dhrupad
Dhrupad tradition of Bihar.

## Dagar Bani
Dhrupad tradition associated with Dagar family.

---

# 34. CARNATIC MUSIC

## Carnatic Music
Classical music tradition of south India.

## Kriti
Main compositional form in Carnatic music.

## Varnam
Composition used for practice and performance opening.

## Ragam-Tanam-Pallavi
Major improvisational form in Carnatic music.

## Ragam
Melodic improvisation.

## Tanam
Rhythmic melodic improvisation.

## Pallavi
Composed line used for improvisation.

## Melakarta
Parent scale system in Carnatic music.

## Janya Raga
Derived raga.

## Trinity of Carnatic Music
Tyagaraja, Muthuswami Dikshitar, and Syama Sastri.

## Tyagaraja
Carnatic composer devoted to Rama.

## Muthuswami Dikshitar
Carnatic composer known for Sanskrit compositions.

## Syama Sastri
Carnatic composer known for devotional works.

## Purandara Dasa
Bhakti saint called father of Carnatic music.

## Annamacharya
Telugu composer devoted to Venkateswara.

## Swati Tirunal
Composer-king of Travancore.

## Tillana
Rhythmic composition often used in dance.

## Padam
Expressive Carnatic composition used in dance.

## Javali
Light classical composition with romantic theme.

---

# 35. INDIAN DANCE: BASIC TERMS

## Dance
Art of movement, rhythm, expression, and storytelling.

## Natya
Drama or theatrical performance.

## Nritta
Pure dance without specific meaning.

## Nritya
Expressive dance with meaning and emotion.

## Natya
Dramatic representation involving dance, music, and acting.

## Abhinaya
Expression or acting in Indian performance.

## Angika Abhinaya
Expression through body movement.

## Vachika Abhinaya
Expression through speech and song.

## Aharya Abhinaya
Expression through costume, makeup, and stage decoration.

## Sattvika Abhinaya
Expression through inner emotion.

## Mudra
Hand gesture.

## Hasta
Hand gesture in dance.

## Rasa
Aesthetic emotion experienced by audience.

## Bhava
Emotion or mood expressed by performer.

## Natyashastra
Ancient treatise on drama, dance, music, and aesthetics.

## Bharata Muni
Traditional author of Natyashastra.

## Rasa Theory
Theory of aesthetic emotions in Indian art.

## Lasya
Graceful dance associated with feminine movement.

## Tandava
Powerful dance associated with Shiva.

## Margi
Classical or pan-Indian tradition.

## Desi
Regional or folk tradition.

---

# 36. CLASSICAL DANCES OF INDIA

## Bharatanatyam
Classical dance of Tamil Nadu, known for geometry, bhakti, and expressive abhinaya.

## Sadir
Earlier form of Bharatanatyam associated with temple dancers.

## Devadasi
Temple dancer tradition historically linked with Bharatanatyam.

## Alarippu
Opening item in Bharatanatyam.

## Jatiswaram
Pure dance item in Bharatanatyam.

## Varnam
Central and elaborate item in Bharatanatyam.

## Padam
Expressive item in Bharatanatyam.

## Tillana
Rhythmic concluding item.

## Kathak
Classical dance of north India, known for spins, footwork, storytelling, and Mughal-court influence.

## Kathakar
Storyteller; root of Kathak tradition.

## Tatkar
Footwork in Kathak.

## Chakkar
Spin in Kathak.

## Kathak Gharanas
Stylistic lineages such as Lucknow, Jaipur, and Banaras.

## Lucknow Gharana
Kathak style known for grace and abhinaya.

## Jaipur Gharana
Kathak style known for strong footwork and rhythm.

## Banaras Gharana
Kathak style with distinct rhythmic patterns.

## Kathakali
Classical dance-drama of Kerala, known for elaborate makeup, costumes, and stories from epics.

## Chutti
White facial border makeup in Kathakali.

## Pacha
Green face makeup for noble heroes in Kathakali.

## Kathi
Knife-type makeup for arrogant or anti-hero characters.

## Kari
Black makeup for demonic characters.

## Mohiniyattam
Classical dance of Kerala, graceful and feminine in style.

## Kuchipudi
Classical dance of Andhra Pradesh, combining dance and drama.

## Yakshagana Influence on Kuchipudi
Kuchipudi has dance-drama elements.

## Tarangam
Kuchipudi item performed on a brass plate.

## Odissi
Classical dance of Odisha, known for tribhanga posture and Jagannath devotion.

## Tribhanga
Three-bend posture in Odissi.

## Chauka
Square stance in Odissi.

## Mahari
Temple dancer tradition of Odisha.

## Gotipua
Young male dancers who helped preserve Odissi tradition.

## Manipuri
Classical dance of Manipur, known for Vaishnava themes and graceful movement.

## Ras Lila
Krishna devotional dance-drama of Manipur.

## Pung Cholom
Manipuri drum dance.

## Sattriya
Classical dance of Assam, developed in Vaishnava monasteries called Satras.

## Satra
Vaishnava monastery in Assam.

## Ankiya Nat
One-act play tradition of Assam associated with Sankardev.

---

# 39. INDIAN TEXTILES

## Textile
Woven or decorated cloth.

## Handloom
Cloth woven manually on a loom.

## Weaving
Making fabric from threads.

## Spinning
Making thread from fibre.

## Dyeing
Coloring yarn or cloth.

## Block Printing
Printing designs on cloth using carved wooden blocks.

## Resist Dyeing
Dyeing technique where parts of cloth are protected from dye.

## Ikat
Resist-dyeing technique where yarn is dyed before weaving.

## Bandhani
Tie-dye textile tradition of Gujarat and Rajasthan.

## Patola
Double ikat silk textile of Gujarat.

## Pochampally Ikat
Ikat textile of Telangana.

## Sambalpuri Ikat
Ikat textile of Odisha.

## Kalamkari
Painted or printed textile from Andhra-Telangana.

## Chikankari
Embroidery tradition of Lucknow.

## Kantha
Embroidery tradition of Bengal.

## Phulkari
Embroidery tradition of Punjab.

## Zardozi
Metal-thread embroidery.

## Kanjivaram Silk
Silk sari tradition of Tamil Nadu.

## Banarasi Brocade
Silk textile of Varanasi with zari work.

## Chanderi
Fine textile from Madhya Pradesh.

## Maheshwari
Textile from Maheshwar in Madhya Pradesh.

## Paithani
Silk sari tradition of Maharashtra.

## Baluchari
Bengal sari with narrative motifs.

## Jamdani
Fine muslin weaving tradition of Bengal.

## Muslin
Fine cotton textile historically associated with Bengal.

## Pashmina
Fine wool textile from Kashmir.

## Kani Shawl
Kashmiri shawl woven with small wooden sticks.

## Ajrakh
Block-printed textile tradition of Gujarat and Sindh.

## Bagru Printing
Block printing tradition of Rajasthan.

## Sanganeri Printing
Block printing tradition of Rajasthan.

## Leheriya
Tie-dye pattern of Rajasthan.

## Kota Doria
Light woven fabric from Rajasthan.

## Muga Silk
Golden silk of Assam.

## Eri Silk
Non-violent silk associated with Assam and north-east India.

## Tussar Silk
Wild silk produced in eastern and central India.

Object made by hand using traditional skill.

## Pottery
Clay craft.

## Terracotta
Baked clay craft.

## Blue Pottery
Pottery tradition of Jaipur using blue glaze.

## Black Pottery
Pottery tradition seen in places like Nizamabad.

## Bidriware
Metal craft from Bidar using blackened alloy and silver inlay.

## Dhokra
Lost-wax metal craft of central and eastern India.

## Dokra
Alternative spelling of Dhokra.

## Channapatna Toys
Lacquered wooden toys from Karnataka.

## Kondapalli Toys
Wooden toy tradition of Andhra Pradesh.

## Etikoppaka Toys
Lacquered wooden toys from Andhra Pradesh.

## Ivory Carving
Craft using ivory, now restricted due to wildlife protection.

## Wood Carving
Traditional carving of wood.

## Sandalwood Carving
Wood craft especially associated with Karnataka.

## Stone Carving
Sculpting stone for temples, icons, and decoration.

## Metal Casting
Making metal objects by casting molten metal.

## Lost-Wax Casting
Technique used in Chola bronzes and Dhokra craft.

## Filigree
Delicate metal wire work.

## Cuttack Filigree
Silver filigree craft of Odisha.

## Meenakari
Enamel work on metal.

## Thewa
Gold work on glass from Rajasthan.

## Lac Craft
Craft using lacquer.

## Bamboo Craft

## Cane Craft
Craft using cane.

Craft using paper pulp, especially in Kashmir.

## Carpet Weaving
Craft of woven carpets.

## Namda

# 41. SCRIPTS, INSCRIPTIONS, AND MANUSCRIPTS

## Script
System of writing.

## Brahmi Script
Ancient Indian script from which many later Indian scripts developed.

## Kharosthi Script
North-western script written right to left.

## Indus Script
Undeciphered script of Harappan civilization.

## Devanagari
Script used for Sanskrit, Hindi, Marathi, and other languages.

## Grantha Script
Script used in south India for Sanskrit.

## Tamil-Brahmi
Early script used for Tamil inscriptions.

## Vatteluttu
Old script used in Tamil and Malayalam regions.

## Sharada Script
Script used in Kashmir and north-western India.

## Modi Script
Script used historically for Marathi administration.

## Persian Script
Used for Persian and Urdu in medieval India.

## Nastaliq
Calligraphic style used for Persian and Urdu.

## Inscription
Writing engraved on stone, metal, pillar, wall, or other hard surface.

## Epigraphy
Study of inscriptions.

## Prashasti
Eulogistic inscription praising a ruler.

## Copper Plate Inscription
Inscription on copper plates, often recording land grants.

## Ashokan Edicts
Earliest major imperial inscriptions of India.

## Allahabad Pillar Inscription
Gupta inscription of Samudragupta composed by Harisena.

## Aihole Inscription
Inscription of Pulakeshin II composed by Ravikirti.

## Hathigumpha Inscription
Inscription of Kharavela in Odisha.

## Junagadh Inscription
Inscription of Rudradaman, important for Sanskrit prose and Sudarshana Lake.

## Manuscript
Handwritten text.

## Palm-Leaf Manuscript
Manuscript written on palm leaves.

## Birch Bark Manuscript
Manuscript written on birch bark, especially in Kashmir and Himalayan regions.

## Paper Manuscript
Manuscript written on paper, common in medieval India.

## Calligraphy
Artistic writing.

## Illumination
Decorative manuscript painting or ornamentation.

# 42. COINS AND NUMISMATIC ART

## Numismatics
Study of coins.

## Punch-Marked Coins
Early coins with symbols punched on them.

## Cast Coins
Coins made by casting metal in moulds.

## Die-Struck Coins
Coins struck using engraved dies.

## Indo-Greek Coins
Coins with Greek and Indian elements, often with portraits and bilingual inscriptions.

## Kushana Coins
Coins showing rulers, Iranian, Greek, Buddhist, and Indian deities.

## Gupta Coins
Gold coins known for high artistic quality and royal imagery.

## Dinara
Gupta gold coin.

## Samudragupta Lyrist Coin
Coin showing Samudragupta playing a veena-like instrument.

## Ashvamedha Coin
Gupta coin type commemorating horse sacrifice.

## Lakshmi Coin Motif
Common motif in ancient and medieval coins.

## Coin Legend
Inscription on a coin.

## Obverse
Front side of a coin.

## Reverse
Back side of a coin.

## Mint
Place where coins are made.

## Symbolic Coinage
Coins using symbols, deities, animals, or royal titles to convey power and legitimacy.

European architectural style used in colonial buildings.

## Gateway of India
Colonial monument in Mumbai.

## Lutyens’ Delhi

## India Gate
War memorial in New Delhi.

Circular colonial-era building designed by Lutyens and Baker.

## High Court Buildings
Colonial buildings combining European and Indian styles.

Colonial monument in Kolkata.

Colonial church architecture.

European architecture seen in Goa, Daman, and Diu.

Large church in Goa.

Architecture seen in Puducherry and Chandernagore.

Post-independence architecture combining modernism and Indian needs.

## Chandigarh

Architect associated with Chandigarh.

Bahai House of Worship in Delhi.

Art inspired by Indian traditions and anti-colonial consciousness.

Protecting heritage from damage.

Institution preserving and displaying objects of cultural, historical, or artistic value.

## Archive
Collection of records, manuscripts, documents, and historical materials.

## Excavated Object
Artifact found through archaeological excavation.

Ancient object of historical or artistic value.

# 47. PHILOSOPHY AND AESTHETICS

## Darshana

## Astika

## Nastika
School rejecting Vedic authority.

## Nyaya
School of logic.

## Vaisheshika
School of atomism and categories.

Philosophy and practice system associated with Patanjali.

## Mimamsa

## Vedanta
Philosophy based on Upanishads.

## Advaita

## Vishishtadvaita

## Dvaita

## Shunyavada

## Madhyamaka

## Yogachara
Buddhist consciousness-only school.

## Anekantavada
Jain doctrine of many-sided reality.

## Syadvada
Jain doctrine of conditional expression.

## Rasa Theory
Theory of aesthetic emotion in Indian art.

## Nava Rasa
Nine aesthetic emotions.

## Shringara
Love or beauty.

## Hasya
Laughter.

## Karuna
Compassion or pathos.

## Raudra
Anger.

## Vira
Heroism.

## Bhayanaka
Fear.

## Bibhatsa
Disgust.

## Adbhuta
Wonder.

## Shanta
Peace.

## Dhvani

## Alamkara
Figure of speech or ornamentation.

## Vakrokti
Oblique expression in poetics.

## Auchitya
Propriety or appropriateness in literature.

# 49. CULTURAL GEOGRAPHY

## Sacred Geography
Network of places considered holy.

## Pilgrimage
Religious journey to sacred places.

## Tirtha
Sacred crossing place or pilgrimage site.

## Char Dham
Four major Hindu pilgrimage sites in different directions.

## Jyotirlinga
Sacred Shiva shrines.

## Shakti Peetha
Sacred goddess sites.

## Divya Desam
Sacred Vishnu temples praised by Alvars.

## Pancha Bhuta Sthalams
Five Shiva temples representing five elements.

## Buddhist Circuit
Places associated with Buddha’s life.

## Jain Tirthas
Jain pilgrimage sites.

## Sufi Dargah Network
Network of Sufi shrines across India.

## Sacred River
River with religious importance, such as Ganga, Yamuna, Narmada, Godavari, Kaveri.

## Temple Town
Town centered around a major temple.

## Matha
Monastic institution, often linked with pilgrimage and teaching.

## Monastic University
Large religious-educational institution like Nalanda or Vikramashila.

---

# 50. CHRONOLOGICAL STORY TIMELINE OF INDIAN ART AND CULTURE

## Stage 1: Prehistoric Culture
Rock paintings, ornaments, burials, symbolic objects, and early ritual behavior show the first cultural expressions.

## Stage 2: Harappan Urban Culture
Planned cities, seals, script, bronze sculpture, terracotta figurines, pottery, beads, textiles, and craft specialization flourished.

## Stage 3: Vedic Culture
Oral tradition, Vedic chanting, yajna, sacred metres, ritual geometry, early music, and philosophical speculation developed.

## Stage 4: Shramana Culture
Buddhism, Jainism, and Ajivikas promoted monastic institutions, stupas, caves, ethics, and new religious art.

## Stage 5: Mauryan Imperial Art
Ashokan pillars, polished stone, animal capitals, edicts, Barabar caves, and early stupas marked the first major imperial art.

## Stage 6: Post-Mauryan Buddhist-Jain-Hindu Expansion
Sanchi, Bharhut, Amaravati, Gandhara, Mathura, chaityas, viharas, and early iconic images developed.

## Stage 7: Gupta Classical Age
Sanskrit literature, refined sculpture, early temples, Ajanta paintings, science, drama, and classical aesthetics reached high development.

## Stage 8: Early Medieval Temple Age
Nagara, Dravida, Vesara, Pallava, Chalukya, Rashtrakuta, Chola, Hoysala, Chandella, Odisha, and Solanki styles flourished.

## Stage 9: Bhakti and Regional Culture
Regional languages, devotional poetry, temple music, dance traditions, and vernacular religious culture expanded.

## Stage 10: Indo-Islamic Cultural Synthesis
Sultanate architecture, Persianate culture, Sufi traditions, Indo-Islamic decorative forms, and new urban aesthetics emerged.

## Stage 11: Mughal and Regional Courts
Mughal architecture, miniature painting, gardens, manuscripts, music, Rajput painting, Deccan painting, and regional cultures flourished.

## Stage 12: Colonial Cultural Transformation
European architecture, Company painting, print culture, reform movements, museums, modern education, and new art schools developed.

## Stage 13: Modern Indian Cultural Revival
Bengal School, modern painting, cinema, theatre, national institutions, folk revival, and heritage conservation became important.

## Stage 14: Contemporary Heritage
Classical arts, folk traditions, crafts, festivals, museums, archives, and intangible heritage continue to shape Indian cultural identity.

---

# 51. HIGH-YIELD ARCHITECTURE CLUSTER

## Prehistoric
Rock shelters and rock art.

## Harappan
Planned cities, Great Bath, drainage, dockyard-like basin, reservoirs.

## Mauryan
Pillars, capitals, caves, polished stone.

## Buddhist
Stupa, chaitya, vihara.

## Jain
Jinalaya, Basadi, Derasar, Manastambha.

## Hindu
Garbhagriha, mandapa, shikhara, vimana, gopuram.

## Nagara
North Indian temple style.

## Dravida
South Indian temple style.

## Vesara
Deccan hybrid temple style.

## Sultanate
Arches, domes, minarets, mosques, tombs, forts.

## Mughal
Charbagh, marble, red sandstone, pietra dura, symmetry.

## Colonial
Indo-Saracenic, Gothic, Neo-Classical, Lutyens’ Delhi.

---

# 52. HIGH-YIELD SCULPTURE CLUSTER

## Harappan
Dancing Girl, Priest-King, terracotta figurines.

## Mauryan
Lion Capital, Yaksha-Yakshi, polished stone.

## Gandhara
Greco-Buddhist Buddha with wavy hair and robe.

## Mathura
Red sandstone Buddha, Jain, and Hindu images.

## Amaravati
White limestone Buddhist reliefs.

## Gupta
Classical Buddha and Hindu icons.

## Chola
Bronze Nataraja and metal icons.

## Hoysala
Intricate soapstone sculpture.

## Vijayanagara
Composite pillars and monumental forms.

## Jain
Tirthankara images, Bahubali, Ayagapatas.

---

# 53. HIGH-YIELD PAINTING CLUSTER

## Prehistoric Painting
Bhimbetka rock paintings.

## Classical Mural
Ajanta and Bagh.

## Buddhist Manuscript Painting
Pala tradition.

## Jain Manuscript Painting
Western Indian school.

## Mughal Painting
Portraits, manuscripts, naturalism.

## Rajput Painting
Bhakti, epics, ragas, court life.

## Pahari Painting
Krishna Bhakti and lyrical landscapes.

## Deccan Painting
Rich colors and fantasy.

## Company Painting
Indian-European hybrid style.

## Bengal School
Nationalist modern art revival.

## Folk Painting
Madhubani, Warli, Pattachitra, Phad, Gond, Kalamkari.

---

# 54. HIGH-YIELD LITERATURE CLUSTER

## Vedic
Vedas, Brahmanas, Aranyakas, Upanishads.

## Epics
Ramayana and Mahabharata.

## Buddhist
Tripitaka, Jataka, Dhammapada, Milindapanha.

## Jain
Agamas, Kalpa Sutra, Tattvartha Sutra.

## Sanskrit Classical
Kalidasa, Bhasa, Shudraka, Vishakhadatta, Bana.

## Tamil
Sangam literature, Tirukkural, Silappadikaram.

## Medieval Bhakti
Kabir, Tulsidas, Surdas, Mirabai, Tukaram, Jnaneshwar.

## Persianate
Amir Khusrau, court chronicles, Sufi literature.

## Modern
Tagore, Bankim, Premchand, Subramania Bharati, modern Indian literature.

---

# 55. HIGH-YIELD MUSIC AND DANCE CLUSTER

## Vedic Music
Samaveda chanting.

## Classical Music Text
Natyashastra.

## Hindustani Music
Dhrupad, Khayal, Thumri, Gharanas.

## Carnatic Music
Kriti, Varnam, Ragam-Tanam-Pallavi, Trinity.

## Main Music Concepts
Raga, Tala, Swara, Shruti, Laya.

## Classical Dances
Bharatanatyam, Kathak, Kathakali, Mohiniyattam, Kuchipudi, Odissi, Manipuri, Sattriya.

## Dance Theory
Nritta, Nritya, Natya, Abhinaya, Rasa, Bhava.

## Folk Dances
Bihu, Garba, Ghoomar, Chhau, Lavani, Bhangra, Yakshagana, Theyyam.

---

# 56. HIGH-YIELD CRAFT AND TEXTILE CLUSTER

## Ancient Crafts
Bead-making, pottery, terracotta, metal casting, shell work.

## Metal Craft
Dhokra, Bidriware, Chola bronze.

## Textile Techniques
Ikat, Bandhani, Kalamkari, embroidery, brocade.

## Silk Traditions
Kanjivaram, Muga, Tussar, Paithani.

## Cotton Traditions
Muslin, Chanderi, Maheshwari, Kota Doria.

## Embroidery
Chikankari, Kantha, Phulkari, Zardozi.

## Block Printing
Bagru, Sanganeri, Ajrakh.

## Folk Crafts
Toys, pottery, bamboo, papier-mache, carpets.

---

# 57. COMMONLY CONFUSED TERMS

## Stupa vs Chaitya
Stupa is a relic mound. Chaitya is a prayer hall, often containing a stupa.

## Chaitya vs Vihara
Chaitya is a worship hall. Vihara is a monastery.

## Shikhara vs Vimana
