Shikhara is the tower in Nagara style. Vimana is the tower in Dravida style.

## Gopuram vs Vimana
Gopuram is gateway tower. Vimana is tower above sanctum.

## Nagara vs Dravida
Nagara is north Indian temple style. Dravida is south Indian temple style.

## Vesara vs Nagara
Vesara is Deccan hybrid style. Nagara is northern style.

## Fresco vs Mural
Mural is any wall painting. Fresco is a specific wall-painting technique.

## Miniature vs Mural
Miniature is small painting on paper/manuscript. Mural is wall painting.

## Gandhara vs Mathura
Gandhara has Greco-Roman influence. Mathura has indigenous Indian features.

## Amaravati vs Gandhara
Amaravati is Andhra limestone Buddhist art. Gandhara is north-western Greco-Buddhist art.

## Dhrupad vs Khayal
Dhrupad is older and more austere. Khayal is more flexible and improvisational.

## Nritta vs Nritya
Nritta is pure dance. Nritya is expressive dance.

## Bhakti vs Sufi
Bhakti is devotional Hindu movement. Sufi is mystical Islamic tradition.

## Folk vs Classical
Folk is community-based and local. Classical is rule-based and formally trained.

## Tangible vs Intangible Heritage
Tangible is physical. Intangible is living tradition.

---

# 58. FINAL REVISION CLUSTER FOR UPSC PRELIMS

## Must Remember Earliest Art
Prehistoric rock paintings, especially Bhimbetka.

## Must Remember Harappan Art
Seals, Dancing Girl, Priest-King, terracotta figurines, beads, pottery.

## Must Remember Vedic Culture
Oral tradition, Samaveda music, yajna, altar geometry, Upanishadic philosophy.

## Must Remember Mauryan Art
Ashokan pillars, Lion Capital, Barabar caves, Mauryan polish.

## Must Remember Buddhist Architecture
Stupa, Chaitya, Vihara, Sanchi, Bharhut, Amaravati, Ajanta.

## Must Remember Art Schools
Gandhara, Mathura, Amaravati, Gupta, Pala, Chola, Hoysala.

## Must Remember Temple Styles
Nagara, Dravida, Vesara.

## Must Remember North Indian Temple Elements
Shikhara, Amalaka, Kalasha.

## Must Remember South Indian Temple Elements
Vimana, Gopuram, Prakara, Temple Tank.

## Must Remember Indo-Islamic Features
Arch, Dome, Minaret, Mihrab, Jali, Charbagh, Pietra Dura.

## Must Remember Mughal Architecture
Humayun’s Tomb, Fatehpur Sikri, Taj Mahal, Red Fort, Jama Masjid.

## Must Remember Paintings
Ajanta, Bagh, Mughal, Rajput, Pahari, Deccan, Company, Bengal School.

## Must Remember Classical Dances
Bharatanatyam, Kathak, Kathakali, Mohiniyattam, Kuchipudi, Odissi, Manipuri, Sattriya.

## Must Remember Music Traditions
Hindustani and Carnatic.

## Must Remember Music Concepts
Raga, Tala, Swara, Shruti, Laya.

## Must Remember Literature
Vedas, Epics, Tripitaka, Jain Agamas, Sangam literature, Sanskrit classics, Bhakti poetry.

## Must Remember Bhakti Saints
Alvars, Nayanars, Kabir, Tulsidas, Surdas, Mirabai, Tukaram, Jnaneshwar, Chaitanya.

## Must Remember Sufi Saints
Muinuddin Chishti, Nizamuddin Auliya, Baba Farid, Amir Khusrau.

## Must Remember Folk Arts
Madhubani, Warli, Pattachitra, Phad, Gond, Kalamkari, Tanjore.

## Must Remember Textiles
Ikat, Patola, Bandhani, Banarasi, Kanjivaram, Chikankari, Kantha, Phulkari.

## Must Remember Scripts
Indus, Brahmi, Kharosthi, Tamil-Brahmi, Devanagari, Sharada, Persian.

## Must Remember One-Line Essence
Indian art and culture developed from prehistoric rock paintings and Harappan crafts into Vedic oral traditions, Buddhist-Jain monuments, Mauryan imperial art, Gupta classicism, temple architecture, Bhakti-Sufi devotional cultures, Indo-Islamic synthesis, Mughal refinement, regional creativity, colonial transformation, and modern national-cultural expression.


======


# INDIAN ECONOMY / INDIAN ECONOMICS GLOSSARY FOR UPSC PRELIMS
## Chronological + Thematic Coverage
## Colonial Economy → National Movement Economic Thought → Planning Era → Green Revolution → Bank Nationalisation → Poverty Programmes → 1991 Reforms → Liberalisation, Privatisation, Globalisation → Fiscal Federalism → GST → Digital Economy → Inclusive Growth → Sustainable Development

> Scope:
> This glossary covers Indian Economy for UPSC Prelims and foundational Mains understanding.
> It avoids current numerical values because GDP growth rates, inflation rates, fiscal deficit, repo rate, forex reserves, tax collections, and Budget figures change frequently.
>
> Core Areas:
> 1. Basic economics
> 2. National income
> 3. Planning and economic development
> 4. Agriculture
> 5. Industry
> 6. Services
> 7. Money and banking
> 8. RBI and monetary policy
> 9. Inflation
> 10. Public finance and Budget
> 11. Taxation
> 12. Fiscal federalism
> 13. External sector
> 14. Balance of payments
> 15. Poverty and unemployment
> 16. Inclusive growth
> 17. Infrastructure
> 18. Financial markets
> 19. Digital economy
> 20. Sustainable development
> 21. Important institutions, reports, indices, and schemes

---

# 1. BASIC ECONOMICS TERMS

## Economy
The system through which a country produces, distributes, and consumes goods and services.

## Indian Economy
The economic system of India, consisting of agriculture, industry, services, government, households, markets, financial institutions, trade, and welfare systems.

## Economics
The study of how people, firms, and governments use scarce resources to satisfy unlimited wants.

## Microeconomics
The branch of economics that studies individual consumers, firms, markets, prices, demand, and supply.

## Macroeconomics
The branch of economics that studies the economy as a whole, including GDP, inflation, unemployment, money supply, fiscal policy, and external trade.

## Positive Economics
Economics that explains what is, based on facts and data.

## Normative Economics
Economics that explains what ought to be, based on value judgments.

## Scarcity
The condition where resources are limited but human wants are unlimited.

## Choice
The act of selecting one option among alternatives because resources are limited.

## Opportunity Cost
The value of the next best alternative given up when a choice is made.

## Production
The process of creating goods and services.

## Consumption
Use of goods and services to satisfy needs and wants.

## Distribution
The way income, goods, and services are shared among people.

## Exchange
Buying and selling of goods and services.

## Goods
Physical products such as food, clothes, machines, and vehicles.

## Services
Non-physical economic activities such as banking, education, transport, healthcare, and software.

## Final Goods
Goods purchased for final use, not for further production.

## Intermediate Goods
Goods used as inputs for producing other goods.

## Consumer Goods
Goods used directly by consumers.

## Capital Goods
Goods used to produce other goods, such as machinery and tools.

## Durable Goods
Goods used for a long time, such as cars, refrigerators, and machines.

## Non-Durable Goods
Goods consumed quickly, such as food and fuel.

## Public Goods
Goods that are non-excludable and non-rival, such as national defence and street lighting.

## Private Goods
Goods that are excludable and rival, such as clothes and mobile phones.

## Merit Goods
Goods that society believes people should consume more, such as education and healthcare.

## Demerit Goods
Goods whose consumption society wants to discourage, such as tobacco and alcohol.

## Free Goods
Goods available without economic cost, such as sunlight and air.

## Economic Goods
Goods that are scarce and have economic value.

## Factor of Production
Inputs used to produce goods and services.

## Land
Natural resources used in production.

## Labour
Human effort used in production.

## Capital
Man-made resources used in production.

## Entrepreneur
Person who organizes land, labour, and capital and takes risk to produce goods or services.

## Rent
Income earned from land or natural resources.

## Wage
Income earned by labour.

## Interest
Income earned from lending capital.

## Profit
Income earned by entrepreneur after paying costs.

## Market
A system where buyers and sellers interact.

## Price
Money value of a good or service.

## Demand
Quantity of a good consumers are willing and able to buy at different prices.

## Supply
Quantity of a good producers are willing and able to sell at different prices.

## Law of Demand
When price rises, demand usually falls; when price falls, demand usually rises.

## Law of Supply
When price rises, supply usually rises; when price falls, supply usually falls.

## Equilibrium Price
Price at which demand equals supply.

## Excess Demand
Situation where demand is greater than supply.

## Excess Supply
Situation where supply is greater than demand.

## Elasticity
Responsiveness of demand or supply to changes in price, income, or other factors.

## Price Elasticity of Demand
Responsiveness of demand to change in price.

## Income Elasticity of Demand
Responsiveness of demand to change in income.

## Cross Elasticity of Demand
Responsiveness of demand for one good to change in price of another good.

## Substitute Goods
Goods that can replace each other, such as tea and coffee.

## Complementary Goods
Goods used together, such as car and petrol.

## Normal Goods
Goods whose demand rises when income rises.

## Inferior Goods
Goods whose demand falls when income rises.

## Giffen Goods
Inferior goods whose demand rises when price rises, under special conditions.

## Utility
Satisfaction derived from consuming a good or service.

## Marginal Utility
Extra satisfaction from consuming one more unit.

## Diminishing Marginal Utility
The idea that extra satisfaction falls as more units are consumed.

## Cost
Expenditure incurred in production.

## Fixed Cost
Cost that does not change with output in the short run.

## Variable Cost
Cost that changes with output.

## Marginal Cost
Additional cost of producing one more unit.

## Revenue
Income earned by selling goods or services.

## Marginal Revenue
Additional revenue from selling one more unit.

## Profit Maximisation
Objective of earning the highest possible profit.

## Economies of Scale
Reduction in average cost when production increases.

## Diseconomies of Scale
Increase in average cost when production becomes too large.

## Competition
Situation where many sellers compete for buyers.

## Perfect Competition
Market with many buyers and sellers, identical products, and free entry and exit.

## Monopoly
Market with a single seller.

## Oligopoly
Market dominated by a few large firms.

## Monopolistic Competition
Market with many sellers selling differentiated products.

## Market Failure
Situation where the market does not allocate resources efficiently.

## Externality
Effect of an economic activity on a third party.

## Positive Externality
Benefit to a third party, such as vaccination.

## Negative Externality
Cost imposed on a third party, such as pollution.

## Information Asymmetry
Situation where one party has more information than another.

## Moral Hazard
Risky behaviour because someone else bears the cost.

## Adverse Selection
Problem arising when one side has hidden information before a transaction.

## Public Intervention
Government action to correct market failure or promote welfare.

---

# 2. BASIC INDIAN ECONOMY CLASSIFICATION

## Primary Sector
Sector involving direct use of natural resources, such as agriculture, forestry, fishing, mining, and quarrying.

## Secondary Sector
Sector involving manufacturing, construction, electricity, gas, water supply, and industrial production.

## Tertiary Sector
Service sector, including trade, transport, banking, education, healthcare, IT, tourism, and communication.

## Agriculture Sector
Sector involving crop cultivation, livestock, fisheries, forestry, and allied activities.

## Industrial Sector
Sector involving manufacturing, mining, construction, electricity, and related activities.

## Services Sector
Sector providing intangible services such as finance, IT, education, transport, and tourism.

## Organised Sector
Sector where enterprises are registered, regulated, and provide formal employment benefits.

## Unorganised Sector
Sector with small, informal, unregistered enterprises and limited social security.

## Formal Sector
Economic activities recorded, regulated, and taxed by the state.

## Informal Sector
Economic activities outside formal regulation and taxation.

## Rural Economy
Economic activity in villages and rural areas, mainly agriculture and allied activities, rural industries, and services.

## Urban Economy
Economic activity in towns and cities, mainly industry, services, trade, construction, and administration.

## Mixed Economy
An economy where both public sector and private sector coexist.

## Socialist Pattern of Society
Post-independence Indian policy goal emphasizing social justice, public sector, planning, and reduction of inequality.

## Market Economy
Economy where prices and production are mainly guided by demand and supply.

## Command Economy
Economy where the state controls production, prices, and distribution.

## Liberal Economy
Economy with greater role for markets, private sector, trade, and investment.

## Welfare State
State that actively works for social welfare through health, education, social security, and redistribution.

## Developmental State
State that actively promotes economic development through planning, infrastructure, industry, and human development.

---

# 3. CHRONOLOGICAL EVOLUTION OF INDIAN ECONOMY

## Colonial Economy
Indian economy under British rule, marked by deindustrialisation, commercialization of agriculture, drain of wealth, famines, and dependence on raw material exports.

## Deindustrialisation
Decline of traditional Indian handicrafts and industries during colonial rule.

## Drain of Wealth
Transfer of Indian wealth to Britain without adequate economic return.

## Dadabhai Naoroji
Indian nationalist economist who explained the drain of wealth theory.

## Poverty and Un-British Rule in India
Book by Dadabhai Naoroji explaining economic exploitation under British rule.

## R. C. Dutt
Economic nationalist who wrote on colonial economic exploitation and Indian famines.

## Commercialisation of Agriculture
Shift from food crops to cash crops for market and export under colonial rule.

## Land Revenue Systems
Colonial systems of collecting land revenue: Permanent Settlement, Ryotwari, and Mahalwari.

## Permanent Settlement
Land revenue system introduced in Bengal where zamindars became revenue collectors and landholders.

## Ryotwari System
Land revenue system where peasants paid revenue directly to the state.

## Mahalwari System
Land revenue system where village communities or mahals were responsible for revenue payment.

## Zamindar
Landholder or revenue collector under colonial land systems.

## Ryot
Cultivator or peasant.

## Mahal
Revenue unit, often a village or group of villages.

## Plantation Economy
Colonial economy based on tea, coffee, indigo, rubber, and other plantations.

## Indigo Cultivation
Cash crop cultivation imposed on peasants in some areas, causing resistance.

## Deccan Riots
Peasant unrest in western India caused by debt, revenue pressure, and moneylenders.

## Famines under Colonial Rule
Mass food shortages worsened by colonial policies, poverty, and poor relief.

## Railways in Colonial India
Introduced for administrative, military, and commercial purposes; also integrated markets.

## Modern Industry under Colonial Rule
Industries like cotton textiles, jute, iron and steel, coal, and plantations developed slowly.

## Tata Iron and Steel Company
Early modern Indian steel enterprise established before independence.

## Bombay Plan
Economic plan proposed by leading Indian industrialists before independence, supporting state-led industrialisation.

## People’s Plan
Plan proposed by M. N. Roy, emphasizing people-oriented development and nationalization.

## Gandhian Plan
Plan inspired by Mahatma Gandhi, emphasizing villages, cottage industries, and decentralization.

## Sarvodaya
Gandhian idea of welfare of all.

## Trusteeship
Gandhian idea that wealthy people should hold wealth in trust for society.

## Swadeshi
Use of indigenous goods and rejection of foreign goods.

## Khadi
Handspun cloth promoted by Gandhi as symbol of self-reliance.

## Village Economy
Gandhian idea of self-reliant villages as the foundation of Indian economy.

---

# 4. POST-INDEPENDENCE ECONOMIC STRATEGY

## Planned Economy
Economy where the state uses plans to guide development priorities and resource allocation.

## Planning Commission
Institution created in 1950 to prepare Five-Year Plans. It was later replaced by NITI Aayog.

## Five-Year Plan
Medium-term development plan for five years.

## First Five-Year Plan
Focused mainly on agriculture, irrigation, power, and rehabilitation after Partition.

## Second Five-Year Plan
Focused on heavy industry and public sector, based on Mahalanobis model.

## Mahalanobis Model
Development strategy emphasizing heavy industries and capital goods.

## P. C. Mahalanobis
Statistician and economist associated with India’s Second Five-Year Plan.

## Third Five-Year Plan
Aimed at self-reliance and balanced growth but was affected by wars and droughts.

## Plan Holiday
Break from Five-Year Plans during crisis years, when annual plans were used.

## Fourth Five-Year Plan
Focused on growth with stability and self-reliance.

## Fifth Five-Year Plan
Focused on poverty removal and self-reliance.

## Garibi Hatao
Political slogan meaning “remove poverty”, associated with poverty-focused policy.

## Rolling Plan
Plan approach introduced during Janata period, where plans were revised continuously.

## Sixth Five-Year Plan
Focused on poverty reduction, technology, and modernization.

## Seventh Five-Year Plan
Emphasized food, work, and productivity.

## Eighth Five-Year Plan
First plan after 1991 reforms, focused on human development and liberalization.

## Ninth Five-Year Plan
Focused on growth with social justice.

## Tenth Five-Year Plan
Emphasized faster and more inclusive growth.

## Eleventh Five-Year Plan
Focused on inclusive growth.

## Twelfth Five-Year Plan
Focused on faster, sustainable, and more inclusive growth.

## NITI Aayog
Policy think tank that replaced the Planning Commission.

## Cooperative Federalism
Centre and states working together for development.

## Competitive Federalism
States competing to improve governance, investment, and development outcomes.

## Aspirational Districts Programme
Programme to improve development indicators in underdeveloped districts.

## Indicative Planning
Planning where the state guides the economy without controlling all decisions.

## Centralised Planning
Planning controlled mainly by the central government.

## Decentralised Planning
Planning involving states, districts, local bodies, and communities.

## District Planning
Planning at district level.

## Gram Panchayat Development Plan
Village-level development planning by Gram Panchayats.

---

# 5. ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT CONCEPTS

## Economic Growth
Increase in output or income of an economy, usually measured by GDP growth.

## Economic Development
Broader improvement in living standards, health, education, equality, and welfare.

## Human Development
Development focused on health, education, and standard of living.

## Inclusive Growth
Growth whose benefits reach all sections of society, especially the poor and vulnerable.

## Sustainable Development
Development that meets present needs without harming future generations.

## Balanced Growth
Growth across sectors and regions without excessive imbalance.

## Unbalanced Growth
Growth strategy where selected sectors are developed first to create linkages.

## Self-Reliance
Ability of a country to meet essential needs without excessive dependence on imports.

## Import Substitution
Policy of producing goods domestically instead of importing them.

## Export Promotion
Policy of increasing exports to earn foreign exchange and expand markets.

## Structural Transformation
Shift of labour and output from agriculture to industry and services.

## Demographic Dividend
Economic advantage from a large working-age population.

## Human Capital
Skills, health, education, and abilities of people.

## Physical Capital
Machines, buildings, roads, and infrastructure used in production.

## Social Capital
Trust, networks, institutions, and cooperation in society.

## Natural Capital
Natural resources such as land, water, forests, minerals, and biodiversity.

## Capital Formation
Creation of productive assets.

## Gross Capital Formation
Total investment in fixed assets and inventories.

## Gross Fixed Capital Formation
Investment in fixed assets such as machinery, buildings, and infrastructure.

## Savings
Income not consumed.

## Investment
Expenditure on assets that create future income or output.

## Incremental Capital Output Ratio
Amount of capital needed to produce one additional unit of output.

## ICOR
Short form of Incremental Capital Output Ratio.

## Productivity
Output produced per unit of input.

## Labour Productivity
Output per worker or per hour worked.

## Total Factor Productivity
Efficiency with which all inputs are used together.

## Technology
Application of knowledge to production.

## Innovation
Creation or adoption of new products, processes, or methods.

---

# 6. NATIONAL INCOME ACCOUNTING

## National Income
Total income earned by residents of a country during a period.

## GDP
Gross Domestic Product; total value of final goods and services produced within domestic territory during a year.

## GNP
Gross National Product; GDP plus net factor income from abroad.

## NDP
Net Domestic Product; GDP minus depreciation.

## NNP
Net National Product; GNP minus depreciation.

## Depreciation
Loss in value of capital due to wear and tear or obsolescence.

## Net Factor Income from Abroad
Income earned by residents from abroad minus income earned by foreigners domestically.

## NFIA
Short form of Net Factor Income from Abroad.

## GDP at Market Price
GDP measured at prices paid by buyers, including taxes and excluding subsidies.

## GDP at Factor Cost
GDP measured as income received by factors of production.

## Basic Price
Price received by producers, excluding product taxes and including product subsidies.

## GVA
Gross Value Added; value of output minus intermediate consumption.

## GDP and GVA Relationship
GDP equals GVA plus product taxes minus product subsidies.

## Nominal GDP
GDP measured at current prices.

## Real GDP
GDP adjusted for inflation using constant prices.

## GDP Deflator
Ratio of nominal GDP to real GDP, used as a broad price index.

## Per Capita Income
Average income per person.

## National Disposable Income
Income available to residents for consumption and saving.

## Personal Income
Income received by households and individuals before personal taxes.

## Disposable Personal Income
Personal income after paying personal taxes.

## Factor Income
Income earned by factors of production: rent, wages, interest, and profit.

## Transfer Payment
Payment made without receiving goods or services in return, such as pensions and subsidies.

## Final Consumption Expenditure
Expenditure on final goods and services by households and government.

## Private Final Consumption Expenditure
Household spending on consumption.

## Government Final Consumption Expenditure
Government spending on goods and services for current use.

## Gross Domestic Capital Formation
Investment in physical assets and inventories.

## Net Exports
Exports minus imports.

## Expenditure Method
GDP calculation by adding consumption, investment, government spending, and net exports.

## Income Method
GDP calculation by adding factor incomes.

## Production Method
GDP calculation by adding value added across sectors.

## Base Year
Reference year used for constant price calculations.

## CSO
Former Central Statistics Office; now part of National Statistical Office.

## NSO
National Statistical Office under MoSPI.

## MoSPI
Ministry of Statistics and Programme Implementation.

## MCA-21 Database
Corporate database used in national accounts estimation.

## Informal Sector Estimation
Estimation of unorganised sector output using surveys and indicators.

## Green GDP
GDP adjusted for environmental damage and natural resource depletion.

---

# 7. POVERTY AND INEQUALITY

## Poverty
Condition where people lack sufficient income or resources to meet basic needs.

## Absolute Poverty
Poverty measured against a fixed minimum standard of living.

## Relative Poverty
Poverty measured compared to average living standards in society.

## Poverty Line
Minimum income or consumption level needed to meet basic needs.

## Headcount Ratio
Percentage of population below poverty line.

## Poverty Gap
Average shortfall of the poor from the poverty line.

## Multidimensional Poverty
Poverty measured through health, education, and living standards, not only income.

## MPI
Multidimensional Poverty Index.

## Consumption Expenditure
Household spending on goods and services, often used to measure poverty.

## Tendulkar Committee
Committee that estimated poverty using consumption expenditure and broader basic needs.

## Rangarajan Committee
Committee that proposed a revised poverty estimation method.

## Lakdawala Committee
Earlier committee on poverty estimation using calorie norms and consumption.

## Calorie Norm
Minimum calorie intake used in older poverty estimation.

## Inequality
Unequal distribution of income, wealth, opportunities, or assets.

## Income Inequality
Unequal distribution of income.

## Wealth Inequality
Unequal distribution of assets and wealth.

## Gini Coefficient
Measure of inequality ranging from 0 to 1.

## Lorenz Curve
Graph showing distribution of income or wealth.

## Social Exclusion
Process by which certain groups are denied opportunities and resources.

## Vulnerability
Risk of falling into poverty due to shocks like illness, job loss, crop failure, or inflation.

## Poverty Alleviation
Policies aimed at reducing poverty.

## Direct Benefit Transfer
Transfer of subsidy or welfare benefits directly into bank accounts.

## DBT
Short form of Direct Benefit Transfer.

## JAM Trinity
Jan Dhan, Aadhaar, and Mobile used for targeted delivery of benefits.

## Jan Dhan
Financial inclusion programme for bank accounts.

## Aadhaar
Unique identity number used for authentication and welfare delivery.

## Mobile Connectivity
Use of mobile phones for communication, payments, and welfare delivery.

---

# 8. EMPLOYMENT AND UNEMPLOYMENT

## Employment
Work that earns income or contributes to production.

## Unemployment
Condition where a person willing and able to work cannot find work.

## Labour Force
People who are working or actively seeking work.

## Workforce
People who are actually employed.

## Labour Force Participation Rate
Percentage of working-age population in the labour force.

## LFPR
Short form of Labour Force Participation Rate.

## Worker Population Ratio
Percentage of population that is employed.

## WPR
Short form of Worker Population Ratio.

## Unemployment Rate
Percentage of labour force that is unemployed.

## Usual Status
Employment status based on a long reference period.

## Current Weekly Status
Employment status based on activity during the last seven days.

## CWS
Short form of Current Weekly Status.

## Current Daily Status
Employment status based on daily activity.

## CDS
Short form of Current Daily Status.

## PLFS
Periodic Labour Force Survey, major official employment survey.

## NSSO
National Sample Survey Office, now part of NSO.

## Open Unemployment
Visible unemployment where people are without work and seeking jobs.

## Disguised Unemployment
More people working than needed, common in agriculture.

## Seasonal Unemployment
Unemployment during off-season periods.

## Structural Unemployment
Unemployment due to mismatch between skills and available jobs.

## Frictional Unemployment
Short-term unemployment while moving between jobs.

## Cyclical Unemployment
Unemployment caused by downturns in business cycle.

## Educated Unemployment
Unemployment among educated people.

## Underemployment
Working less than desired or below skill level.

## Informal Employment
Employment without formal contracts or social security.

## Formal Employment
Employment with contracts, benefits, and legal protection.

## Self-Employment
Working for oneself rather than an employer.

## Casual Labour
Short-term or daily-wage labour.

## Regular Wage Employment
Employment with regular wages or salary.

## Gig Work
Work through digital platforms or short-term tasks.

## Platform Worker
Worker using online platforms for work, such as delivery or ride-hailing.

## Female Labour Force Participation
Participation of women in labour force.

## Skill Development
Training people for employable skills.

## Demographic Dividend
Potential economic gain from a large working-age population.

## Jobless Growth
Economic growth without adequate job creation.

## Labour-Intensive Growth
Growth that creates many jobs per unit of output.

## MGNREGA
Mahatma Gandhi National Rural Employment Guarantee Act, providing wage employment in rural areas.

## Wage Employment Programme
Programme that provides paid work to unemployed or underemployed people.

## Livelihood Programme
Programme supporting income-generating activities.

---

# 9. AGRICULTURE IN INDIA

## Agriculture
Cultivation of crops and rearing of animals for food, fibre, and other products.

## Indian Agriculture
Agriculture in India, marked by small holdings, monsoon dependence, diversity of crops, and large rural population.

## Primary Sector
Sector including agriculture, forestry, fishing, mining, and allied activities.

## Allied Activities
Livestock, dairy, fisheries, poultry, forestry, and other activities linked to agriculture.

## Subsistence Farming
Farming mainly for family consumption.

## Commercial Farming
Farming mainly for market sale.

## Intensive Farming
High use of labour, inputs, and irrigation on small land.

## Extensive Farming
Cultivation over large land with relatively lower input per unit area.

## Mixed Farming
Combination of crop cultivation and animal rearing.

## Plantation Agriculture
Large-scale cultivation of crops like tea, coffee, rubber, and spices.

## Dryland Farming
Farming in areas with low rainfall and limited irrigation.

## Rainfed Agriculture
Agriculture dependent on rainfall.

## Irrigated Agriculture
Agriculture using artificial water supply.

## Cropping Pattern
Distribution of area under different crops.

## Crop Diversification
Shift from one or few crops to multiple crops or high-value crops.

## Food Crops
Crops grown mainly for food, such as rice, wheat, pulses, and millets.

## Cash Crops
Crops grown mainly for sale, such as cotton, sugarcane, jute, tea, coffee, and tobacco.

## Kharif Crops
Crops grown during monsoon season, such as rice, maize, cotton, soybean, and pulses.

## Rabi Crops
Crops grown in winter season, such as wheat, barley, mustard, gram, and peas.

## Zaid Crops
Short-season crops grown between Rabi and Kharif, such as watermelon, cucumber, and fodder.

## Cereals
Grain crops such as rice, wheat, maize, barley, and millets.

## Pulses
Protein-rich crops such as gram, tur, urad, moong, and lentil.

## Oilseeds
Crops used for oil, such as mustard, groundnut, soybean, sunflower, and sesame.

## Millets
Nutrinut, soybean, sunflower, and sesame.

## Millets
Nutri-cereals such as jowar, bajra, ragi, foxtail millet, kodo millet, and little millet.

## Nutri-Cereals
Millets promoted for nutrition and climate resilience.

## Horticulture
Cultivation of fruits, vegetables, flowers, spices, plantation crops, and medicinal plants.

## Floriculture
Cultivation of flowers.

## Sericulture
Rearing of silkworms for silk.

## Apiculture
Beekeeping.

## Pisciculture
Fish farming.

## Aquaculture
Cultivation of aquatic organisms.

## Dairy Farming
Milk production through cattle and buffalo rearing.

## Poultry
Rearing birds for eggs and meat.

## Animal Husbandry
Rearing animals for milk, meat, eggs, wool, draught power, and other products.

## Landholding
Area of land operated by a farmer.

## Marginal Farmer
Farmer with very small landholding.

## Small Farmer
Farmer with small landholding.

## Tenant Farmer
Farmer cultivating leased land.

## Sharecropper
Farmer who gives part of produce to landowner as rent.

## Land Fragmentation
Division of land into small scattered plots.

## Consolidation of Holdings
Combining fragmented plots into larger operational holdings.

## Land Reforms
Policies to change land ownership and tenancy structures.

## Zamindari Abolition
Removal of intermediary landlords after independence.

## Tenancy Reform
Reform to protect tenants and regulate rent.

## Land Ceiling
Legal limit on maximum landholding.

## Bhoodan Movement
Voluntary land donation movement led by Vinoba Bhave.

## Gramdan
Village-level land donation idea.

---

# 10. AGRICULTURAL INPUTS AND TECHNOLOGY

## Agricultural Inputs
Resources used in farming, such as seeds, fertilizers, water, credit, labour, and machinery.

## HYV Seeds
High-yielding variety seeds used in Green Revolution.

## Green Revolution
Increase in foodgrain production through HYV seeds, irrigation, fertilizers, pesticides, and mechanization.

## Norman Borlaug
Agricultural scientist associated with high-yielding wheat varieties.

## M. S. Swaminathan
Indian scientist associated with Green Revolution in India.

## Fertilizer
Chemical or organic material added to soil to increase fertility.

## Urea
Nitrogenous fertilizer widely used in India.

## DAP
Diammonium phosphate fertilizer.

## NPK
Nitrogen, phosphorus, and potassium fertilizers.

## Biofertilizer
Fertilizer using living organisms to improve soil fertility.

## Pesticide
Chemical used to control pests.

## Insecticide
Chemical used to kill insects.

## Herbicide
Chemical used to kill weeds.

## Fungicide
Chemical used to control fungal diseases.

## Mechanization
Use of machines in agriculture.

## Tractor
Machine used for ploughing and other farm operations.

## Harvester
Machine used to harvest crops.

## Combine Harvester
Machine that cuts, threshes, and cleans grain.

## Drip Irrigation
Water-saving irrigation method delivering water directly to plant roots.

## Sprinkler Irrigation
Irrigation method spraying water like rainfall.

## Micro-Irrigation
Efficient irrigation system including drip and sprinkler.

## Watershed Development
Management of land and water resources in a drainage area.

## Soil Health Card
Scheme providing information on soil nutrients and fertilizer recommendations.

## Organic Farming
Farming without synthetic fertilizers and pesticides.

## Natural Farming
Low-input farming relying on natural processes and local resources.

## Zero Budget Natural Farming
Natural farming approach aiming to reduce purchased inputs.

## Climate-Smart Agriculture
Agriculture that improves productivity, resilience, and reduces emissions.

## Precision Agriculture
Use of data, sensors, GPS, and technology for efficient farming.

## Agri-Tech
Use of technology in agriculture.

## Farm Mechanisation
Use of machines to reduce labour and increase efficiency.

## Seed Replacement Rate
Percentage of area sown with certified or quality seeds instead of farm-saved seeds.

## Irrigation Intensity
Ratio of gross irrigated area to net irrigated area.

## Cropping Intensity
Ratio of gross cropped area to net sown area.

## Multiple Cropping
Growing more than one crop on the same land in a year.

## Intercropping
Growing two or more crops together on the same field.

## Mixed Cropping
Growing different crops together without fixed row arrangement.

## Crop Rotation
Growing different crops sequentially to maintain soil fertility.

---

# 11. AGRICULTURAL MARKETING AND PRICES

## Agricultural Marketing
Process of moving farm produce from farmers to consumers.

## APMC
Agricultural Produce Market Committee, regulating agricultural mandis.

## Mandi
Agricultural market yard.

## Regulated Market
Market governed by rules for weighing, grading, auctions, and payments.

## MSP
Minimum Support Price announced by government for selected crops.

## Minimum Support Price
Price at which government promises to procure certain crops from farmers.

## Procurement
Government purchase of agricultural produce.

## Public Procurement
Purchase of foodgrains by government agencies for food security and buffer stocks.

## FCI
Food Corporation of India, responsible for procurement, storage, and distribution of foodgrains.

## Buffer Stock
Stock of foodgrains maintained to ensure food security and price stability.

## Central Issue Price
Price at which foodgrains are issued through public distribution system.

## CACP
Commission for Agricultural Costs and Prices, recommends MSP.

## Market Intervention Scheme
Government support for perishable commodities when prices fall.

## Price Deficiency Payment
Payment to farmers when market price falls below a benchmark price.

## e-NAM
Electronic National Agriculture Market for online trading of agricultural produce.

## Contract Farming
Agreement between farmers and buyers to produce and supply crops under agreed conditions.

## Farmer Producer Organisation
Collective of farmers to improve bargaining power and market access.

## FPO
Short form of Farmer Producer Organisation.

## Value Chain
Sequence from production to processing, storage, transport, and sale.

## Cold Chain
Temperature-controlled storage and transport system.

## Warehousing
Storage of agricultural goods.

## Warehouse Receipt
Document proving ownership of stored goods, usable for credit.

## Grading
Sorting produce based on quality.

## Standardisation
Ensuring uniform quality standards.

## Agmark
Quality certification mark for agricultural products.

## Food Processing
Conversion of raw agricultural produce into value-added food products.

## Post-Harvest Loss
Loss of produce after harvesting due to poor storage, transport, or processing.

## Supply Chain
Network moving goods from producers to consumers.

---

# 12. FOOD SECURITY AND PUBLIC DISTRIBUTION

## Food Security
Availability, access, and affordability of sufficient nutritious food for all.

## Availability
Sufficient food supply through production, stocks, and imports.

## Access
People’s ability to obtain food.

## Affordability
Food being economically within reach.

## Nutrition Security
Access to balanced and nutritious food.

## Public Distribution System
Government system of distributing subsidised foodgrains.

## PDS
Short form of Public Distribution System.

## Targeted Public Distribution System
PDS focused on identified poor and vulnerable households.

## TPDS
Short form of Targeted Public Distribution System.

## National Food Security Act
Law providing subsidised foodgrains to eligible population.

## NFSA
Short form of National Food Security Act.

## Antyodaya Anna Yojana
Scheme for the poorest households under PDS.

## Priority Household
Household eligible for subsidised foodgrains under NFSA.

## Ration Card
Document allowing households to access PDS.

## One Nation One Ration Card
Portability system allowing beneficiaries to access ration across India.

## Fair Price Shop
Shop distributing subsidised foodgrains under PDS.

## Buffer Norms
Minimum stock levels of foodgrains required for food security.

## Open Market Sale Scheme
Government sale of foodgrains in open market to control prices.

## Malnutrition
Condition caused by inadequate or imbalanced nutrition.

## Undernutrition
Insufficient nutrition.

## Stunting
Low height for age due to chronic undernutrition.

## Wasting
Low weight for height due to acute undernutrition.

## Anaemia
Low haemoglobin level, often due to iron deficiency.

## Hidden Hunger
Micronutrient deficiency.

## Poshan Abhiyaan
National nutrition mission.

## Mid-Day Meal Scheme
School meal programme, now under PM POSHAN framework.

## ICDS
Integrated Child Development Services for children, pregnant women, and lactating mothers.

## Anganwadi
Village-level centre delivering nutrition, health, and preschool services.

---

# 13. INDUSTRY IN INDIA

## Industry
Economic activity involving manufacturing, mining, construction, electricity, and processing.

## Industrialisation
Growth of industries in an economy.

## Manufacturing
Production of goods using labour, machines, and raw materials.

## Heavy Industry
Industry producing capital goods, machinery, steel, and equipment.

## Light Industry
Industry producing consumer goods.

## Capital Goods Industry
Industry producing machines and tools used in other industries.

## Consumer Goods Industry
Industry producing goods for final consumption.

## Basic Industry
Industry producing essential inputs for other industries, such as steel, cement, and power.

## Core Industries
Key infrastructure industries tracked in India: coal, crude oil, natural gas, refinery products, fertilizers, steel, cement, and electricity.

## Index of Eight Core Industries
Index measuring output of eight key infrastructure industries.

## IIP
Index of Industrial Production, measuring industrial output.

## Factory Sector
Registered manufacturing units under factory laws.

## MSME
Micro, Small and Medium Enterprises.

## Micro Enterprise
Very small enterprise based on investment and turnover criteria.

## Small Enterprise
Enterprise larger than micro but smaller than medium.

## Medium Enterprise
Enterprise larger than small but below large industry threshold.

## Cottage Industry
Small-scale industry usually household-based and labour-intensive.

## Village Industry
Rural industry using local resources and traditional skills.

## Handloom
Manual weaving industry.

## Handicraft
Traditional craft industry.

## Khadi and Village Industries
Rural industries promoted for employment and self-reliance.

## Industrial Policy
Government policy toward industry, investment, licensing, public sector, and private sector.

## Industrial Policy Resolution 1948
Early industrial policy defining role of state and private sector.

## Industrial Policy Resolution 1956
Policy emphasizing public sector and commanding heights.

## Commanding Heights
Strategic sectors controlled by the state.

## Industrial Licensing
System where firms needed government permission to start or expand production.

## Licence-Permit Raj
Pre-reform system of extensive controls, licensing, quotas, and permits.

## MRTP Act
Monopolies and Restrictive Trade Practices Act aimed at controlling monopolies.

## FERA
Foreign Exchange Regulation Act, pre-reform law regulating foreign exchange.

## Industrial Policy 1991
Policy that reduced licensing, opened economy, encouraged private sector and foreign investment.

## Liberalisation
Reduction of government controls.

## Privatisation
Increasing private sector role or reducing government ownership.

## Globalisation
Greater integration with world economy.

## Disinvestment
Sale of government stake in public sector enterprises.

## Strategic Disinvestment
Sale of substantial government stake with transfer of management control.

## Public Sector Enterprise
Enterprise owned by government.

## CPSE
Central Public Sector Enterprise.

## Maharatna
Top category of large public sector enterprises with greater autonomy.

## Navratna
Category of public sector enterprises with operational autonomy.

## Miniratna
Category of profitable public sector enterprises with some autonomy.

## Make in India
Initiative to promote manufacturing and investment in India.

## Production Linked Incentive
Scheme giving incentives based on incremental production.

## PLI
Short form of Production Linked Incentive.

## Industrial Corridor
Large infrastructure and industrial development zone.

## SEZ
Special Economic Zone with special rules to promote exports and investment.

## Export Oriented Unit
Unit focused on export production.

## Cluster Development
Policy to support groups of small industries in one region.

## Ease of Doing Business
Quality of business environment in terms of regulations, approvals, and compliance.

## Start-up
New innovative business with growth potential.

## Start-up India
Government initiative to promote start-ups.

## Unicorn
Start-up valued at one billion dollars or more.

---

# 14. SERVICES SECTOR

## Services Sector
Sector providing intangible services such as trade, transport, finance, education, healthcare, tourism, IT, and communication.

## Service-Led Growth
Growth driven mainly by services rather than manufacturing.

## IT Sector
Information technology sector including software, services, and digital solutions.

## IT-BPM
Information Technology and Business Process Management.

## BPO
Business Process Outsourcing.

## KPO
Knowledge Process Outsourcing.

## Software Exports
Export of software and IT services.

## Digital Services
Services delivered through digital platforms.

## Financial Services
Banking, insurance, securities, asset management, and fintech.

## Tourism
Travel for leisure, business, religion, health, or culture.

## Medical Tourism
Travel for medical treatment.

## Education Services
Schools, colleges, universities, coaching, and skill training.

## Health Services
Hospitals, clinics, diagnostics, insurance, and public health.

## Logistics
Movement, storage, and delivery of goods.

## E-Commerce
Buying and selling goods and services online.

## Platform Economy
Economic activity enabled by digital platforms.

## Gig Economy
Short-term task-based work through platforms.

## Creative Economy
Economy based on culture, art, design, media, entertainment, and creativity.

## Orange Economy
Another term for creative economy.

---

# 15. MONEY AND BANKING

## Money
Anything generally accepted as medium of exchange, store of value, unit of account, and standard of deferred payment.

## Currency
Physical money issued by monetary authority.

## Legal Tender
Money legally accepted for payment of debts.

## Fiat Money
Money whose value comes from government authority, not intrinsic value.

## Token Money
Money whose face value is greater than intrinsic value.

## Commodity Money
Money with intrinsic value, such as gold or silver.

## Bank Money
Deposits in banks that can be used for payments.

## Digital Money
Money stored and transferred electronically.

## Money Supply
Total stock of money available in an economy.

## Narrow Money
Highly liquid money, usually currency and demand deposits.

## Broad Money
Narrow money plus time deposits and other less liquid components.

## M0
Reserve money or high-powered money.

## M1
Currency with public, demand deposits, and other deposits with RBI.

## M2
M1 plus savings deposits with post office savings banks.

## M3
Broad money; M1 plus time deposits with banks.

## M4
M3 plus total post office deposits excluding National Savings Certificates.

## High-Powered Money
Currency issued by RBI plus reserves of banks.

## Reserve Money
Another term for high-powered money.

## Money Multiplier
Ratio of broad money to reserve money.

## Liquidity
Ease with which an asset can be converted into cash.

## Bank
Financial institution accepting deposits and giving loans.

## Commercial Bank
Bank that accepts deposits and lends money for profit.

## Scheduled Bank
Bank included in the Second Schedule of RBI Act.

## Non-Scheduled Bank
Bank not included in the Second Schedule of RBI Act.

## Public Sector Bank
Bank majority-owned by government.

## Private Sector Bank
Bank owned by private shareholders.

## Foreign Bank
Bank incorporated outside India but operating in India.

## Regional Rural Bank
Bank serving rural areas, especially small farmers and rural workers.

## RRB
Short form of Regional Rural Bank.

## Cooperative Bank
Bank owned and operated by members on cooperative principles.

## Urban Cooperative Bank
Cooperative bank operating in urban areas.

## Rural Cooperative Bank
Cooperative bank serving rural credit needs.

## Payments Bank
Bank that can accept small deposits and provide payments services but cannot lend.

## Small Finance Bank
Bank focused on small borrowers, micro enterprises, and financial inclusion.

## Development Finance Institution
Institution providing long-term finance for development projects.

## DFI
Short form of Development Finance Institution.

## NABARD
National Bank for Agriculture and Rural Development.

## SIDBI
Small Industries Development Bank of India.

## EXIM Bank
Export-Import Bank of India.

## NHB
National Housing Bank.

## Deposit
Money kept in a bank account.

## Demand Deposit
Deposit withdrawable on demand.

## Time Deposit
Deposit kept for a fixed period.

## Savings Account
Bank account for small savings.

## Current Account
Bank account mainly used by businesses for frequent transactions.

## Fixed Deposit
Deposit kept for a fixed time at fixed interest.

## Recurring Deposit
Deposit made regularly over time.

## Loan
Money borrowed with obligation to repay.

## Credit
Borrowed money or ability to borrow.

## Interest Rate
Cost of borrowing or return on saving.

## Collateral
Asset pledged as security for a loan.

## Mortgage
Loan secured by property.

## Priority Sector Lending
Mandatory lending by banks to sectors such as agriculture, MSMEs, education, housing, and weaker sections.

## PSL
Short form of Priority Sector Lending.

## Financial Inclusion
Providing affordable financial services to all sections of society.

## No-Frills Account
Basic bank account with low or no minimum balance.

## Basic Savings Bank Deposit Account
Basic bank account for financial inclusion.

## Jan Dhan Account
Bank account opened under Pradhan Mantri Jan Dhan Yojana.

## Microfinance
Small loans and financial services for low-income groups.

## Self-Help Group
Small community group that saves and borrows collectively.

## SHG
Short form of Self-Help Group.

## SHG-Bank Linkage
Programme linking self-help groups with banks.

## Joint Liability Group
Group whose members jointly guarantee loans.

## Kisan Credit Card
Credit facility for farmers.

## KCC
Short form of Kisan Credit Card.

---

# 16. RBI AND MONETARY POLICY

## RBI
Reserve Bank of India, India’s central bank.

## Central Bank
Institution that controls monetary policy, currency, banking regulation, and financial stability.

## Monetary Policy
Policy controlling money supply, credit, and interest rates to maintain price stability and growth.

## Monetary Policy Committee
Committee that decides policy repo rate under inflation targeting framework.

## MPC
Short form of Monetary Policy Committee.

## Inflation Targeting
Monetary policy framework targeting a specified inflation range.

## Repo Rate
Rate at which RBI lends short-term funds to banks against securities.

## Reverse Repo Rate
Rate at which RBI borrows funds from banks.

## Bank Rate
Rate at which RBI lends long-term funds to banks without repurchase agreement.

## CRR
Cash Reserve Ratio; percentage of bank deposits kept with RBI as cash.

## SLR
Statutory Liquidity Ratio; percentage of deposits banks must keep in liquid assets.

## Open Market Operations
Buying or selling government securities by RBI to manage liquidity.

## OMO
Short form of Open Market Operations.

## Liquidity Adjustment Facility
RBI facility to manage short-term liquidity through repo and reverse repo.

## LAF
Short form of Liquidity Adjustment Facility.

## Marginal Standing Facility
Facility allowing banks to borrow overnight funds from RBI at a penal rate.

## MSF
Short form of Marginal Standing Facility.

## Standing Deposit Facility
Facility allowing banks to deposit excess funds with RBI without collateral.

## SDF
Short form of Standing Deposit Facility.

## Cash Management Bills
Short-term government securities used for cash management.

## Treasury Bills
Short-term government debt instruments.

## Government Securities
Debt instruments issued by central or state governments.

## G-Secs
Short form of Government Securities.

## Liquidity
Availability of cash or easily usable funds in the financial system.

## Tight Monetary Policy
Policy reducing money supply or increasing interest rates to control inflation.

## Easy Monetary Policy
Policy increasing liquidity or reducing interest rates to support growth.

## Hawkish Policy
Monetary stance focused on controlling inflation.

## Dovish Policy
Monetary stance focused on supporting growth.

## Transmission of Monetary Policy
Process through which RBI policy changes affect lending rates, deposits, investment, consumption, and inflation.

## External Benchmark Lending Rate
Lending rate linked to external benchmark such as repo rate.

## Base Rate
Earlier benchmark lending rate system.

## MCLR
Marginal Cost of Funds Based Lending Rate.

## Quantitative Tools
Monetary tools affecting overall money supply, such as repo, CRR, SLR, and OMO.

## Qualitative Tools
Selective credit controls affecting specific sectors or types of credit.

## Moral Suasion
Central bank persuasion to influence banks.

## Credit Rationing
Limiting amount of credit to certain sectors.

## Selective Credit Control
Policy to restrict credit for specific purposes.

## Lender of Last Resort
RBI’s role of providing emergency liquidity to banks.

## Banker to Government
RBI’s role of managing government accounts, borrowing, and payments.

## Banker’s Bank
RBI’s role as bank for commercial banks.

## Currency Issuer
RBI’s role in issuing currency notes.

## Financial Stability
Smooth functioning of financial system without crisis.

---

# 17. INFLATION

## Inflation
Sustained rise in general price level.

## Deflation
Sustained fall in general price level.

## Disinflation
Decline in the rate of inflation.

## Reflation
Policy-induced increase in economic activity and prices after slowdown.

## Headline Inflation
Overall inflation including all items.

## Core Inflation
Inflation excluding volatile items like food and fuel.

## Food Inflation
Rise in prices of food items.

## Fuel Inflation
Rise in prices of fuel and energy.

## Retail Inflation
Inflation faced by consumers, usually measured by CPI.

## Wholesale Inflation
Inflation at wholesale level, usually measured by WPI.

## CPI
Consumer Price Index.

## WPI
Wholesale Price Index.

## GDP Deflator
Broad measure of price change for all domestically produced goods and services.

## Demand-Pull Inflation
Inflation caused by excess demand.

## Cost-Push Inflation
Inflation caused by rising production costs.

## Built-In Inflation
Inflation caused by wage-price expectations.

## Imported Inflation
Inflation caused by rise in import prices or currency depreciation.

## Structural Inflation
Inflation caused by supply bottlenecks and structural constraints.

## Creeping Inflation
Low and gradual inflation.

## Walking Inflation
Moderate inflation.

## Galloping Inflation
Very high inflation.

## Hyperinflation
Extremely high and uncontrollable inflation.

## Stagflation
High inflation with low growth and high unemployment.

## Skewflation
Inflation in only a few commodities while others remain stable.

## Phillips Curve
Relationship suggesting inverse relation between inflation and unemployment in short run.

## Inflation Tax
Loss of purchasing power due to inflation.

## Purchasing Power
Ability of money to buy goods and services.

## Real Income
Income adjusted for inflation.

## Nominal Income
Income measured in current money terms.

## Indexation
Adjustment of values according to inflation.

## Cost of Living
Amount of money needed to maintain a standard of living.

## Base Effect
Effect of previous year’s price level on current inflation rate.

## Monetary Inflation Control
Using interest rates and liquidity tools to control inflation.

## Supply-Side Inflation Control
Improving supply of goods to control prices.

## Buffer Stock Policy
Using public stocks to stabilise prices.

## Price Stabilisation Fund
Fund used to reduce excessive price volatility of essential commodities.

---

# 18. PUBLIC FINANCE

## Public Finance
Study of government revenue, expenditure, borrowing, and debt.

## Government Revenue
Income received by government.

## Government Expenditure
Spending by government.

## Public Debt
Debt owed by government.

## Fiscal Policy
Government policy on taxation, expenditure, and borrowing.

## Expansionary Fiscal Policy
Increasing spending or cutting taxes to boost demand.

## Contractionary Fiscal Policy
Reducing spending or increasing taxes to control inflation or deficit.

## Budget
Annual financial statement of government receipts and expenditure.

## Union Budget
Budget of the central government.

## State Budget
Budget of a state government.

## Annual Financial Statement
Constitutional name for the Union Budget.

## Revenue Receipt
Government receipt that does not create liability or reduce assets.

## Capital Receipt
Receipt that creates liability or reduces assets.

## Revenue Expenditure
Expenditure that does not create assets or reduce liabilities.

## Capital Expenditure
Expenditure that creates assets or reduces liabilities.

## Plan Expenditure
Old classification of expenditure related to Five-Year Plans.

## Non-Plan Expenditure
Old classification of expenditure not directly linked to plans.

## Central Sector Scheme
Scheme fully funded and implemented by central government.

## Centrally Sponsored Scheme
Scheme funded jointly by Centre and states but implemented mainly by states.

## CSS
Short form of Centrally Sponsored Scheme.

## Fiscal Deficit
Total expenditure minus total receipts excluding borrowings.

## Revenue Deficit
Revenue expenditure minus revenue receipts.

## Primary Deficit
Fiscal deficit minus interest payments.

## Effective Revenue Deficit
Revenue deficit minus grants for creation of capital assets.

## Budget Deficit
Old concept where total expenditure exceeded total receipts.

## Monetised Deficit
Deficit financed by borrowing from central bank.

## Fiscal Consolidation
Policy of reducing fiscal deficit and debt.

## FRBM Act
Fiscal Responsibility and Budget Management Act, aimed at fiscal discipline.

## Public Debt Management
Management of government borrowing and debt repayment.

## Internal Debt
Government debt owed within the country.

## External Debt
Debt owed to foreign lenders.

## Sovereign Debt
Debt issued by national government.

## Market Borrowing
Government borrowing from market through securities.

## Ways and Means Advances
Temporary borrowing facility from RBI for government cash mismatch.

## WMA
Short form of Ways and Means Advances.

## Deficit Financing
Financing government deficit through borrowing or money creation.

## Off-Budget Borrowing
Borrowing not shown directly in Budget deficit but ultimately government liability.

## Contingent Liability
Potential liability that may arise in future.

## Guarantee
Promise by government to repay if borrower fails.

## Subsidy
Government financial support to reduce cost of goods or services.

## Explicit Subsidy
Subsidy shown clearly in Budget.

## Implicit Subsidy
Hidden subsidy through underpricing or concessional terms.

## Merit Subsidy
Subsidy for socially beneficial goods.

## Non-Merit Subsidy
Subsidy with weaker social justification.

---

# 19. TAXATION

## Tax
Compulsory payment to government without direct quid pro quo.

## Direct Tax
Tax paid directly by person on whom it is imposed.

## Indirect Tax
Tax imposed on goods and services, paid indirectly by consumers.

## Income Tax
Tax on income of individuals and entities.

## Corporate Tax
Tax on profits of companies.

## Capital Gains Tax
Tax on profit from sale of capital assets.

## Securities Transaction Tax
Tax on securities market transactions.

## Wealth Tax
Tax on wealth; abolished in India.

## Estate Duty
Tax on inherited property; abolished in India.

## Gift Tax
Tax on gifts under specified rules.

## GST
Goods and Services Tax, a destination-based indirect tax on supply of goods and services.

## Goods and Services Tax
Indirect tax that subsumed many central and state taxes.

## CGST
Central GST collected by Centre on intra-state supply.

## SGST
State GST collected by state on intra-state supply.

## UTGST
Union Territory GST.

## IGST
Integrated GST on inter-state supply and imports.

## GST Council
Constitutional body recommending GST rates, exemptions, and rules.

## Destination-Based Tax
Tax collected by state where goods or services are consumed.

## Input Tax Credit
Credit for tax paid on inputs, reducing tax cascading.

## Tax Cascading
Tax on tax effect.

## Value Added Tax
Tax on value added at each stage of production or distribution.

## VAT
Short form of Value Added Tax.

## Excise Duty
Tax on manufacture of goods.

## Customs Duty
Tax on imports or exports.

## Basic Customs Duty
Main customs duty on imports.

## Anti-Dumping Duty
Duty imposed to protect against unfairly cheap imports.

## Countervailing Duty
Duty to offset subsidies given by exporting country.

## Safeguard Duty
Temporary duty to protect domestic industry from import surge.

## Sin Tax
Higher tax on harmful goods such as tobacco or alcohol.

## Tax Base
Income, goods, or assets on which tax is imposed.

## Tax Rate
Percentage or amount at which tax is levied.

## Progressive Tax
Tax rate rises as income rises.

## Regressive Tax
Tax burden is higher on lower-income groups.

## Proportional Tax
Same tax rate for all.

## Tax Buoyancy
Responsiveness of tax revenue to GDP growth.

## Tax Elasticity
Responsiveness of tax revenue to tax base after adjusting for discretionary changes.

## Tax-GDP Ratio
Tax revenue as percentage of GDP.

## Laffer Curve
Idea that beyond a point, higher tax rates can reduce tax revenue.

## Tax Avoidance
Legal reduction of tax liability using loopholes.

## Tax Evasion
Illegal non-payment or underpayment of tax.

## Black Money
Income not disclosed to tax authorities.

## Benami Transaction
Property held in someone else’s name to hide ownership.

## Tax Haven
Jurisdiction with low taxes and secrecy.

## BEPS
Base Erosion and Profit Shifting by multinational companies.

## Transfer Pricing
Pricing of transactions between related companies.

## Equalisation Levy
Tax on certain digital transactions with foreign companies.

---

# 20. FISCAL FEDERALISM

## Fiscal Federalism
Division of financial powers between Centre and states.

## Finance Commission
Constitutional body recommending distribution of tax revenues between Centre and states.

## Vertical Devolution
Sharing of central taxes between Centre and states.

## Horizontal Devolution
Distribution of states’ share among different states.

## Tax Devolution
Transfer of tax revenue from Centre to states.

## Grants-in-Aid
Financial assistance from Centre to states.

## Revenue Deficit Grant
Grant to states with revenue gap.

## Local Body Grant
Grant for Panchayats and municipalities.

## Disaster Management Grant
Grant for disaster response and mitigation.

## Centrally Sponsored Scheme
Scheme funded jointly by Centre and states.

## State Finance Commission
Body recommending distribution of funds to local bodies within a state.

## Consolidated Fund of India
Main government account where revenues and loans are credited and expenditures are made.

## Contingency Fund of India
Emergency fund for urgent unforeseen expenditure.

## Public Account of India
Account for money held by government in trust, such as provident funds and small savings.

## Consolidated Fund of State
Main account of a state government.

## Cess
Tax collected for a specific purpose.

## Surcharge
Additional charge on tax.

## Divisible Pool
Central taxes shared with states, excluding cesses and surcharges.

## GST Compensation
Compensation to states for revenue loss after GST implementation, based on law.

## Cooperative Federalism
Centre-state cooperation in policy and development.

## Competitive Federalism
States competing for investment, governance, and development outcomes.

---

# 21. EXTERNAL SECTOR

## External Sector
Part of economy dealing with trade, foreign investment, foreign exchange, external debt, and balance of payments.

## International Trade
Exchange of goods and services between countries.

## Export
Goods or services sold to other countries.

## Import
Goods or services bought from other countries.

## Merchandise Trade
Trade in physical goods.

## Services Trade
Trade in services such as IT, tourism, transport, finance, and consulting.

## Trade Balance
Exports of goods minus imports of goods.

## Trade Deficit
Imports exceed exports.

## Trade Surplus
Exports exceed imports.

## Current Account
Part of balance of payments recording goods, services, income, and transfers.

## Current Account Deficit
Current account payments exceed receipts.

## CAD
Short form of Current Account Deficit.

## Capital Account
Part of balance of payments recording capital transfers and non-produced assets.

## Financial Account
Part of BOP recording foreign investment, loans, banking capital, and reserves.

## Balance of Payments
Record of all economic transactions between residents and rest of world.

## BOP
Short form of Balance of Payments.

## Forex Reserves
Foreign exchange assets held by RBI.

## Foreign Exchange
Foreign currency and assets used for international payments.

## Exchange Rate
Price of one currency in terms of another.

## Rupee Depreciation
Fall in value of rupee against foreign currency.

## Rupee Appreciation
Rise in value of rupee against foreign currency.

## Devaluation
Official reduction in currency value under fixed exchange rate.

## Revaluation
Official increase in currency value under fixed exchange rate.

## Nominal Exchange Rate
Actual quoted exchange rate.

## Real Exchange Rate
Exchange rate adjusted for inflation differences.

## NEER
Nominal Effective Exchange Rate.

## REER
Real Effective Exchange Rate.

## Managed Float
Exchange rate system where market determines rate but central bank intervenes to reduce volatility.

## Convertibility
Ability to convert domestic currency into foreign currency.

## Current Account Convertibility
Freedom to convert currency for current transactions like trade and remittances.

## Capital Account Convertibility
Freedom to convert currency for capital transactions like investment and loans.

## Tariff
Tax on imports or exports.

## Non-Tariff Barrier
Trade restriction other than tariff, such as quotas and standards.

## Quota
Limit on quantity of imports or exports.

## Dumping
Selling goods abroad below normal value.

## Anti-Dumping Duty
Duty imposed to counter dumping.

## Free Trade Agreement
Agreement reducing trade barriers between countries.

## FTA
Short form of Free Trade Agreement.

## Preferential Trade Agreement
Agreement giving lower tariffs to selected countries.

## Customs Union
Trade bloc with free internal trade and common external tariff.

## Common Market
Trade bloc allowing free movement of goods, services, capital, and labour.

## WTO
World Trade Organization, global body governing trade rules.

## GATT
General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade.

## Most Favoured Nation
WTO principle of non-discrimination among trading partners.

## MFN
Short form of Most Favoured Nation.

## National Treatment
WTO principle requiring equal treatment of foreign and domestic goods after entry.

## TRIPS
WTO agreement on intellectual property rights.

## TRIMS
WTO agreement on trade-related investment measures.

## Agreement on Agriculture
WTO agreement dealing with agricultural trade rules.

## Export Promotion
Policies to increase exports.

## Import Substitution
Policy to reduce imports by domestic production.

## Remittances
Money sent by migrants to their home country.

## NRI Deposits
Deposits by non-resident Indians in Indian banks.

## External Commercial Borrowing
Foreign borrowing by Indian entities.

## ECB
Short form of External Commercial Borrowing.

## Sovereign External Debt
Foreign debt of government.

## Commercial External Debt
Foreign debt of private firms.

## Short-Term External Debt
External debt due within one year.

---

# 22. FOREIGN INVESTMENT

## Foreign Investment
Investment from foreign individuals, firms, or institutions.

## FDI
Foreign Direct Investment, involving lasting interest and control in an enterprise.

## FPI
Foreign Portfolio Investment, investment in financial assets like shares and bonds.

## FII
Foreign Institutional Investor, older term for foreign investors in Indian securities.

## FDI Equity Inflow
Foreign investment in ownership capital.

## Automatic Route
FDI route where prior government approval is not needed.

## Government Route
FDI route requiring government approval.

## Brownfield Investment
Investment in existing business or facility.

## Greenfield Investment
Investment in new project or facility.

## FDI Cap
Maximum permitted foreign ownership in a sector.

## Portfolio Flow
Foreign investment in stocks, bonds, and financial assets.

## Hot Money
Short-term speculative capital that can quickly enter or leave.

## Capital Flight
Large outflow of capital from a country.

## External Vulnerability
Risk arising from external debt, trade deficit, currency pressure, or capital outflows.

## Ease of Doing Business
Business environment affecting investment.

## Bilateral Investment Treaty
Agreement protecting investments between two countries.

## BIT
Short form of Bilateral Investment Treaty.

## Double Taxation Avoidance Agreement
Agreement preventing same income from being taxed twice.

## DTAA
Short form of Double Taxation Avoidance Agreement.

---

# 23. FINANCIAL MARKETS

## Financial Market
Market where financial assets are bought and sold.

## Money Market
Market for short-term funds.

## Capital Market
Market for long-term funds.

## Primary Market
Market where new securities are issued.

## Secondary Market
Market where existing securities are traded.

## Stock Market
Market for shares.

## Bond Market
Market for debt securities.

## Equity
Ownership share in a company.

## Share
Unit of ownership in a company.

## Debt
Borrowed money that must be repaid.

## Bond
Debt instrument issued by government or company.

## Debenture
Long-term debt instrument issued by company.

## Government Security
Debt instrument issued by government.

## Treasury Bill
Short-term government debt instrument.

## Commercial Paper
Short-term unsecured debt issued by companies.

## Certificate of Deposit
Short-term deposit instrument issued by banks.

## Call Money Market
Market for overnight funds between banks.

## Repo Market
Market for repurchase agreements.

## Mutual Fund
Investment vehicle pooling money from investors.

## ETF
Exchange Traded Fund.

## Index Fund
Fund tracking a market index.

## Hedge Fund
Investment fund using advanced strategies and higher risk.

## Pension Fund
Fund managing retirement savings.

## Insurance
Risk protection through premium payment.

## Derivative
Financial contract whose value depends on underlying asset.

## Futures
Derivative contract to buy or sell asset at future date and price.

## Options
Contract giving right but not obligation to buy or sell.

## Forward Contract
Customised agreement to buy or sell in future.

## Swap
Contract to exchange cash flows.

## Commodity Market
Market for commodities like gold, crude oil, and agricultural goods.

## SEBI
Securities and Exchange Board of India, regulator of securities markets.

## IRDAI
Insurance Regulatory and Development Authority of India.

## PFRDA
Pension Fund Regulatory and Development Authority.

## AMFI
Association of Mutual Funds in India.

## Stock Exchange
Platform for trading securities.

## NSE
National Stock Exchange.

## BSE
Bombay Stock Exchange.

## Sensex
Benchmark index of BSE.

## Nifty
Benchmark index of NSE.

## Market Capitalisation
Total market value of a company’s shares.

## IPO
Initial Public Offering; first sale of shares to public.

## FPO
Follow-on Public Offer.

## Rights Issue
Issue of shares to existing shareholders.

## Bonus Issue
Free shares issued to existing shareholders.

## Buyback
Company repurchasing its own shares.

## Insider Trading
Trading using unpublished price-sensitive information.

## Market Manipulation
Artificially influencing security prices.

## Investor Protection
Regulation to protect investors from fraud and unfair practices.

---

# 24. BANKING SECTOR ISSUES

## NPA
Non-Performing Asset; loan where repayment is overdue beyond specified period.

## Non-Performing Asset
Bad loan not generating regular income.

## Gross NPA
Total bad loans before provisioning.

## Net NPA
Gross NPA minus provisions.

## Provisioning
Setting aside money to cover expected loan losses.

## Stressed Asset
Loan under stress, including NPAs and restructured loans.

## Restructured Loan
Loan whose terms are changed to help borrower repay.

## Write-Off
Removal of loan from bank books, though recovery may continue.

## Wilful Defaulter
Borrower who can repay but deliberately does not.

## Twin Balance Sheet Problem
Stress in both corporate balance sheets and bank balance sheets.

## Asset Quality Review
RBI exercise to identify stressed loans properly.

## Capital Adequacy Ratio
Bank capital as percentage of risk-weighted assets.

## CAR
Short form of Capital Adequacy Ratio.

## CRAR
Capital to Risk-Weighted Assets Ratio.

## Basel Norms
International banking standards on capital, risk, and liquidity.

## Basel III
Banking norms strengthening capital and liquidity standards.

## Prompt Corrective Action
RBI framework restricting weak banks to restore financial health.

## PCA
Short form of Prompt Corrective Action.

## Bank Recapitalisation
Infusion of capital into banks, often by government for public sector banks.

## Bank Consolidation
Merger of banks to create stronger institutions.

## IBC
Insolvency and Bankruptcy Code.

## Insolvency
Inability to pay debts.

## Bankruptcy
Legal status of inability to repay debts.

## NCLT
National Company Law Tribunal.

## Insolvency Resolution
Process of resolving debt of insolvent companies.

## Haircut
Loss accepted by lenders during debt resolution.

## Bad Bank
Institution created to take over bad loans from banks.

## ARC
Asset Reconstruction Company.

## NARCL
National Asset Reconstruction Company Limited.

## Credit Rating
Assessment of borrower’s ability to repay.

## Credit Risk
Risk of borrower default.

## Systemic Risk
Risk that failure of one institution affects entire financial system.

---

# 25. CAPITAL, INVESTMENT, AND BUSINESS CYCLE

## Capital Formation
Creation of productive assets.

## Investment Rate
Investment as percentage of GDP.

## Savings Rate
Savings as percentage of GDP.

## Domestic Savings
Savings by households, firms, and government.

## Household Savings
Savings by households in financial and physical assets.

## Corporate Savings
Savings by companies.

## Public Savings
Savings by government.

## Business Cycle
Fluctuations in economic activity.

## Boom
Period of high growth and demand.

## Recession
Period of decline or slowdown in economic activity.

## Depression
Severe and prolonged downturn.

## Recovery
Phase when economy starts improving.

## Expansion
Phase of rising output, employment, and income.

## Slowdown
Decline in growth rate, though output may still rise.

## Output Gap
Difference between actual output and potential output.

## Potential GDP
Maximum sustainable output without high inflation.

## Capacity Utilisation
Percentage of production capacity being used.

## Animal Spirits
Investor confidence and willingness to take risk.

## Crowding Out
Government borrowing reducing funds available for private investment.

## Crowding In
Government spending encouraging private investment.

## Multiplier Effect
Initial spending leading to larger total increase in income.

## Accelerator Effect
Increase in investment due to rising demand.

---

# 26. INFRASTRUCTURE

## Infrastructure
Basic physical and social facilities needed for economic activity.

## Physical Infrastructure
Roads, railways, ports, airports, power, irrigation, telecom, and logistics.

## Social Infrastructure
Education, health, sanitation, housing, and social services.

## Economic Infrastructure
Infrastructure directly supporting production and trade.

## Public Infrastructure
Infrastructure built or owned by government.

## Private Infrastructure
Infrastructure built or operated by private sector.

## PPP
Public-Private Partnership.

## Public-Private Partnership
Collaboration between government and private sector for infrastructure or services.

## BOT
Build-Operate-Transfer model.

## BOOT
Build-Own-Operate-Transfer model.

## HAM
Hybrid Annuity Model used in road projects.

## EPC
Engineering, Procurement, and Construction model.

## National Infrastructure Pipeline
Pipeline of infrastructure projects across sectors.

## PM Gati Shakti
National master plan for integrated infrastructure and logistics planning.

## Logistics
Movement, storage, and management of goods.

## Logistics Cost
Cost of transporting, storing, and handling goods.

## Multimodal Transport
Use of multiple modes like road, rail, water, and air.

## Bharatmala
Road development programme.

## Sagarmala
Port-led development programme.

## Dedicated Freight Corridor
Rail corridor dedicated to freight movement.

## DFC
Short form of Dedicated Freight Corridor.

## Inland Waterways
Rivers and canals used for transport.

## UDAN
Regional air connectivity scheme.

## Smart Cities Mission
Urban development programme for technology-enabled infrastructure and services.

## AMRUT
Urban mission for water, sewerage, and basic infrastructure.

## Metro Rail
Urban mass rapid transit system.

## High-Speed Rail
Rail system designed for very high speeds.

## Bullet Train
Common term for high-speed rail.

---

# 27. ENERGY ECONOMY

## Energy Security
Availability of reliable and affordable energy.

## Primary Energy
Energy from natural sources such as coal, crude oil, natural gas, solar, wind, and hydro.

## Secondary Energy
Energy produced from primary energy, such as electricity and refined petroleum products.

## Fossil Fuels
Coal, petroleum, and natural gas.

## Coal
Major energy source in India, especially for electricity generation.

## Crude Oil
Raw petroleum used to produce fuels.

## Natural Gas
Cleaner fossil fuel used for power, industry, and households.

## Renewable Energy
Energy from sources that replenish naturally.

## Solar Energy
Energy from sunlight.

## Wind Energy
Energy from wind.

## Hydropower
Electricity generated from flowing water.

## Biomass Energy
Energy from organic material.

## Green Hydrogen
Hydrogen produced using renewable energy.

## Energy Transition
Shift from fossil fuels to cleaner energy.

## Energy Mix
Share of different energy sources in total energy use.

## Installed Capacity
Maximum electricity generation capacity.

## Electricity Generation
Actual production of electricity.

## Transmission
Movement of electricity from power plants to distribution networks.

## Distribution
Delivery of electricity to consumers.

## DISCOM
Power distribution company.

## AT&C Losses
Aggregate Technical and Commercial losses in power distribution.

## Cross-Subsidy
Charging some consumers more to subsidise others.

## Open Access
Allowing consumers to buy electricity from suppliers of choice.

## Power Purchase Agreement
Contract between power generator and buyer.

## PPA
Short form of Power Purchase Agreement.

## UDAY
Scheme for financial turnaround of DISCOMs.

## Energy Efficiency
Using less energy for same output.

## Perform Achieve and Trade
Energy efficiency trading scheme for industries.

## PAT
Short form of Perform Achieve and Trade.

## LED Programme
Energy-saving lighting initiative.

## Ethanol Blending
Mixing ethanol with petrol to reduce oil imports and emissions.

## Strategic Petroleum Reserve
Emergency crude oil storage.

---

# 28. URBAN ECONOMY

## Urbanisation
