Increase in share of population living in urban areas.

## Urban Economy
Economic activity in cities and towns.

## Agglomeration Economy
Benefits firms and workers get from being located close together.

## Urban Infrastructure
Water, sewerage, roads, transport, housing, and waste management.

## Municipal Finance
Revenue and expenditure of urban local bodies.

## Property Tax
Tax on property collected by urban local bodies.

## User Charges
Fees paid for public services.

## Urban Local Body
Municipal governance institution.

## Municipal Corporation
Urban local government for large cities.

## Municipality
Urban local body for smaller towns.

## Nagar Panchayat
Urban local body for transitional areas.

## Smart City
City using technology and planning to improve services.

## Affordable Housing
Housing accessible to low and middle-income groups.

## Slum
Urban settlement with inadequate housing and basic services.

## Urban Poverty
Poverty in cities.

## Migration
Movement of people from one place to another.

## Rural-Urban Migration
Movement from villages to towns or cities.

## Circular Migration
Repeated movement between home and work destination.

## Informal Settlement
Settlement lacking legal title or formal services.

## Street Vendor
Small informal trader operating on streets.

## Urban Transport
Transport systems in cities.

## Mass Transit
Public transport system carrying large numbers of people.

## Transit-Oriented Development
Urban planning around public transport corridors.

---

# 29. RURAL ECONOMY

## Rural Economy
Economic activity in villages, including agriculture, allied sectors, rural industries, and services.

## Rural Development
Improvement of rural income, infrastructure, education, health, and livelihoods.

## Panchayati Raj
Local self-government system in rural areas.

## Gram Panchayat
Village-level local government.

## Gram Sabha
Assembly of all adult voters in a village.

## Rural Infrastructure
Roads, irrigation, electricity, housing, sanitation, schools, and health centres.

## Rural Credit
Loans available to rural households, farmers, and enterprises.

## Rural Indebtedness
Debt burden of rural households.

## Moneylender
Informal lender, often charging high interest.

## Cooperative Credit
Credit provided by cooperative institutions.

## Rural Non-Farm Sector
Rural activities outside agriculture, such as trade, construction, transport, and small manufacturing.

## Rural Livelihoods
Income sources of rural households.

## Livelihood Diversification
Shift from single source of income to multiple sources.

## Rural-Urban Linkage
Economic connection between villages and towns.

## MGNREGA
Rural wage employment guarantee programme.

## Self-Help Groups
Community savings and credit groups, often involving women.

## NRLM
National Rural Livelihoods Mission.

## DAY-NRLM
Deendayal Antyodaya Yojana - National Rural Livelihoods Mission.

## Rural Housing
Housing support in rural areas.

## Rural Sanitation
Sanitation infrastructure and behaviour change in villages.

## Rural Electrification
Providing electricity to villages and households.

## Rural Roads
Road connectivity for villages.

---

# 30. SOCIAL SECTOR ECONOMICS

## Social Sector
Sectors directly improving human welfare, such as health, education, nutrition, sanitation, and social protection.

## Human Development
Expansion of people’s capabilities through health, education, and income.

## HDI
Human Development Index.

## Health Economics
Study of healthcare, public health, insurance, and health spending.

## Public Health
Health of population through prevention, sanitation, immunization, and health systems.

## Primary Healthcare
First level of healthcare.

## Secondary Healthcare
Specialist care at district or sub-district level.

## Tertiary Healthcare
Advanced hospital care.

## Health Insurance
Financial protection against health expenses.

## Out-of-Pocket Expenditure
Health spending paid directly by households.

## Universal Health Coverage
Access to quality healthcare without financial hardship.

## Ayushman Bharat
Health initiative including health and wellness centres and insurance coverage for vulnerable families.

## PM-JAY
Pradhan Mantri Jan Arogya Yojana.

## Health and Wellness Centre
Primary healthcare facility under Ayushman Bharat.

## Education Economics
Study of education spending, access, quality, and human capital.

## Literacy Rate
Percentage of people who can read and write.

## Gross Enrolment Ratio
Total enrolment in a level of education as percentage of relevant age group.

## GER
Short form of Gross Enrolment Ratio.

## Dropout Rate
Percentage of students leaving school before completion.

## Skill Development
Training for employability and productivity.

## Vocational Education
Education focused on practical job skills.

## Demographic Dividend
Economic potential from working-age population.

## Social Protection
Policies protecting people from poverty, illness, unemployment, old age, and shocks.

## Social Security
Income or service support during vulnerability.

## Pension
Regular income after retirement or for vulnerable groups.

## Insurance
Protection against risk.

## Food Subsidy
Government support for subsidised food distribution.

## Fertilizer Subsidy
Government support reducing fertilizer prices.

## LPG Subsidy
Support for cooking gas affordability.

---

# 31. INCLUSIVE GROWTH

## Inclusive Growth
Economic growth that creates opportunities for all and distributes benefits fairly.

## Financial Inclusion
Access to banking, credit, insurance, pension, and digital payments.

## Social Inclusion
Participation of all groups in economic and social life.

## Gender Inclusion
Equal access for women to education, work, finance, property, and decision-making.

## Regional Inclusion
Reduction of development gaps among regions.

## Digital Inclusion
Access to digital connectivity, devices, skills, and services.

## Inclusive Development
Development that benefits poor, women, children, elderly, disabled, minorities, and marginalized groups.

## Vulnerable Groups
Groups more exposed to poverty and exclusion.

## SC Development
Policies for Scheduled Castes.

## ST Development
Policies for Scheduled Tribes.

## OBC Development
Policies for Other Backward Classes.

## Minority Development
Policies for religious and linguistic minorities.

## Gender Budgeting
Budgeting that considers gender-specific needs and outcomes.

## Child Budgeting
Budgeting focused on child welfare.

## Disability Inclusion
Policies ensuring access and opportunities for persons with disabilities.

## Social Justice
Fairness in distribution of opportunities, rights, and resources.

## Empowerment
Increasing ability of people to make choices and control their lives.

---

# 32. DIGITAL ECONOMY

## Digital Economy
Economy based on digital technologies, data, platforms, internet, and electronic transactions.

## Digital India
Programme to transform India into a digitally empowered society and knowledge economy.

## Digital Public Infrastructure
Digital systems built for public use, such as identity, payments, and data exchange.

## DPI
Short form of Digital Public Infrastructure.

## Aadhaar
Digital identity system.

## UPI
Unified Payments Interface, real-time digital payment system.

## NPCI
National Payments Corporation of India.

## RuPay
Indian card payment network.

## BHIM
Digital payments app based on UPI.

## AePS
Aadhaar Enabled Payment System.

## DigiLocker
Digital document storage platform.

## e-Sign
Digital signature service.

## Account Aggregator
Framework allowing consent-based sharing of financial data.

## ONDC
Open Network for Digital Commerce.

## Open Digital Ecosystem
Digital system with open standards and interoperability.

## DBT
Direct Benefit Transfer.

## JAM Trinity
Jan Dhan, Aadhaar, Mobile.

## Fintech
Technology-based financial services.

## Digital Lending
Loan delivery through digital platforms.

## Peer-to-Peer Lending
Direct lending between individuals through platforms.

## CBDC
Central Bank Digital Currency.

## Digital Rupee
India’s central bank digital currency.

## Cryptocurrency
Private digital asset using cryptography.

## Blockchain
Distributed digital ledger technology.

## Tokenisation
Replacing sensitive data with non-sensitive tokens.

## Cybersecurity
Protection of digital systems from attacks.

## Data Governance
Rules for collection, use, sharing, and protection of data.

## Data Localisation
Requirement to store data within national borders.

## Digital Divide
Gap between those with digital access and those without.

## Platform Monopoly
Dominance of one or few digital platforms.

## Network Effect
Value of a service increasing as more people use it.

---

# 33. ENVIRONMENTAL ECONOMICS AND SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT

## Environmental Economics
Study of economic activities and environmental impacts.

## Sustainable Development
Development that meets current needs without harming future generations.

## SDGs
Sustainable Development Goals adopted by the United Nations.

## Climate Change
Long-term change in climate due to natural and human factors.

## Global Warming
Rise in average global temperature.

## Carbon Emissions
Release of carbon dioxide and other greenhouse gases.

## Greenhouse Gases
Gases trapping heat, such as carbon dioxide, methane, and nitrous oxide.

## Carbon Footprint
Total greenhouse gas emissions caused by an activity or entity.

## Carbon Intensity
Emissions per unit of output.

## Energy Intensity
Energy used per unit of GDP.

## Net Zero
Balancing emissions with removals.

## Carbon Sink
Natural or artificial system absorbing carbon dioxide.

## Forest Carbon
Carbon stored in forests.

## Carbon Tax
Tax on carbon emissions.

## Carbon Market
Market for trading emission permits or carbon credits.

## Carbon Credit
Tradable certificate representing emission reduction or removal.

## Green Finance
Finance for environmentally sustainable projects.

## Climate Finance
Finance for climate mitigation and adaptation.

## Green Bond
Bond issued to finance environmental projects.

## Sovereign Green Bond
Green bond issued by government.

## ESG
Environmental, Social, and Governance criteria.

## Circular Economy
Economy that reduces waste through reuse, recycling, repair, and resource efficiency.

## Linear Economy
Take-make-dispose model.

## Resource Efficiency
Using fewer resources for same output.

## Waste Management
Collection, processing, recycling, and disposal of waste.

## Extended Producer Responsibility
Producer responsibility for post-consumer waste.

## EPR
Short form of Extended Producer Responsibility.

## Renewable Energy
Energy from replenishable sources.

## Clean Energy
Energy with low environmental impact.

## Green Growth
Economic growth with environmental sustainability.

## Blue Economy
Sustainable use of ocean and marine resources.

## Natural Capital Accounting
Accounting for value of natural resources.

## Green GDP
GDP adjusted for environmental degradation.

## Ecosystem Services
Benefits humans get from nature.

## Payment for Ecosystem Services
Payment for conserving ecological benefits.

---

# 34. ECONOMIC REFORMS OF 1991

## Economic Reforms
Policy changes to liberalize and modernize the economy.

## 1991 Crisis
Balance of payments crisis that led India to undertake reforms.

## LPG Reforms
Liberalisation, Privatisation, and Globalisation reforms.

## Liberalisation
Reduction of government controls and licensing.

## Privatisation
Greater role for private sector and sale of public sector stake.

## Globalisation
Integration with the world economy.

## New Industrial Policy 1991
Policy reducing industrial licensing, public sector reservation, and foreign investment restrictions.

## Devaluation of Rupee
Reduction in rupee value to improve export competitiveness during crisis.

## IMF Assistance
Financial assistance received during 1991 crisis with reform conditions.

## Structural Adjustment
Policy reforms to improve macroeconomic stability and efficiency.

## Deregulation
Removal or reduction of government controls.

## Delicensing
Removal of industrial licensing requirements.

## Trade Liberalisation
Reduction of tariffs, quotas, and import restrictions.

## Financial Sector Reform
Reforms in banking, capital markets, interest rates, and regulation.

## Tax Reform
Simplification and rationalisation of tax system.

## Public Sector Reform
Disinvestment, autonomy, and restructuring of public enterprises.

## Exchange Rate Reform
Shift toward market-determined exchange rate.

## Current Account Convertibility
Freedom for current international transactions.

## Capital Account Liberalisation
Gradual relaxation of capital flows.

## Competition Policy
Policy to promote competition and prevent anti-competitive practices.

## Competition Commission of India
Regulator enforcing competition law.

## CCI
Short form of Competition Commission of India.

---

# 35. PLANNING TO MARKET TRANSITION

## State-Led Development
Development model where government leads investment and industrialization.

## Public Sector Dominance
Major role of government-owned enterprises.

## Import Substitution Industrialisation
Strategy to replace imports with domestic production.

## Licence Raj
System of licensing and controls before reforms.

## Controlled Economy
Economy with extensive state regulation.

## Reform Era
Period after 1991 marked by liberalisation and market orientation.

## Market-Oriented Reform
Policy giving greater role to prices, competition, and private enterprise.

## Deregulated Industry
Industry freed from licensing and controls.

## Open Economy
Economy with significant trade and capital flows.

## Private Investment
Investment by private firms and individuals.

## Foreign Investment
Investment from abroad.

## Export Competitiveness
Ability to sell goods and services in global markets.

## Structural Change
Change in sectoral composition of output and employment.

## Services-Led Growth
Growth driven by services sector.

## Manufacturing Challenge
Difficulty in expanding manufacturing share and job creation.

---

# 36. GLOBALISATION AND INDIA

## Globalisation
Integration of economies through trade, investment, technology, migration, and ideas.

## Trade Integration
Greater participation in international trade.

## Financial Integration
Greater movement of capital across countries.

## Technology Transfer
Movement of technology from one country or firm to another.

## Global Value Chain
Production process spread across countries.

## GVC
Short form of Global Value Chain.

## Outsourcing
Contracting work to external firms or countries.

## Offshoring
Shifting business processes to another country.

## IT Outsourcing
Export of IT and software services.

## Global Competitiveness
Ability of a country to compete internationally.

## Protectionism
Policy of restricting imports to protect domestic industry.

## Tariff Protection
Protection through import duties.

## Non-Tariff Protection
Protection through standards, quotas, or regulations.

## Self-Reliant India
Policy idea emphasizing domestic capability and resilience.

## Atmanirbhar Bharat
Self-reliant India initiative.

## Strategic Autonomy in Economy
Maintaining policy independence while engaging globally.

## Supply Chain Resilience
Ability to withstand disruptions in production and trade networks.

---

# 37. BALANCE OF PAYMENTS CRISIS TERMS

## Balance of Payments Crisis
Crisis when a country lacks enough foreign exchange to meet external payments.

## Forex Shortage
Insufficient foreign exchange reserves.

## Import Cover
Number of months of imports that forex reserves can finance.

## External Debt Crisis
Difficulty in servicing foreign debt.

## Sovereign Default
Failure of government to meet debt obligations.

## Gold Pledging
Pledging gold to raise foreign exchange during crisis.

## Stabilisation
Short-term policy to control inflation, deficit, and external imbalance.

## Structural Reform
Long-term policy to improve efficiency and competitiveness.

## Macroeconomic Stability
Stable inflation, sustainable deficit, stable currency, and manageable debt.

---

## Wage Employment Programme
Programme providing wage work.

## Rights-Based Welfare
Welfare through legal entitlements, such as work, food, and education.

## Targeting
Identifying beneficiaries for welfare schemes.

## Universalism
Providing benefits to all citizens or residents.

## Exclusion Error
Eligible person left out of welfare benefit.

## Inclusion Error
Ineligible person receiving welfare benefit.

## Leakage
Loss of welfare benefits before reaching intended beneficiary.

## Direct Transfer
Sending benefit directly to beneficiary.

## Cash Transfer
Transfer of money instead of goods.

## In-Kind Transfer

# 43. AGRICULTURAL REVOLUTIONS IN INDIA

## Green Revolution
Rise in foodgrain production through HYV seeds, irrigation, fertilizers, and pesticides.

## White Revolution
Increase in milk production through dairy cooperatives.

## Operation Flood
Programme that transformed India’s dairy sector.

## Verghese Kurien
Father of White Revolution in India.

## Blue Revolution
Increase in fish production.

## Yellow Revolution
Increase in oilseeds production.

## Golden Revolution
Increase in horticulture and honey production.

## Silver Revolution
Increase in egg production.

## Pink Revolution
Growth in meat or onion/shrimp production depending on context.

## Round Revolution
Increase in potato production.

## Grey Revolution
Increase in fertilizer production.

## Brown Revolution
Associated with leather, cocoa, or non-conventional energy depending on context; use carefully.

## Rainbow Revolution
Integrated development of agriculture and allied sectors.

# 44. COOPERATIVES AND COLLECTIVE ECONOMY

## Cooperative
Organisation owned and managed by members for mutual benefit.

## Cooperative Movement
Movement promoting collective ownership and democratic management.

## Dairy Cooperative
Cooperative for milk collection, processing, and marketing.

## Amul
Famous dairy cooperative brand associated with White Revolution.

## Anand Model
Dairy cooperative model developed in Gujarat.

## Multi-State Cooperative
Cooperative operating in more than one state.

## Primary Agricultural Credit Society
Village-level cooperative credit institution.

## PACS
Short form of Primary Agricultural Credit Society.

## Cooperative Federalism in Economy
Centre and states working together for economic development.

## Producer Cooperative
Cooperative owned by producers.

## Consumer Cooperative
Cooperative owned by consumers.

## Credit Cooperative
Cooperative providing loans to members.

## FPO
Farmer Producer Organisation.

## Farmer Producer Company
Company formed by farmers to collectively market and process produce.

# 45. LAND, LABOUR, AND CAPITAL REFORMS

## Factor Market Reform
Reform of markets for land, labour, and capital.

## Land Reform
Reform of ownership, tenancy, ceilings, and land records.

## Land Record Digitisation
Digital updating of land ownership and title records.

## Land Leasing
Renting land for cultivation or business.

## Land Acquisition
Government acquisition of land for public purpose or development.

## Labour Reform
Changes in labour laws and regulations.

## Labour Codes
Consolidated labour laws on wages, industrial relations, social security, and occupational safety.

## Minimum Wage
Legally fixed minimum payment to workers.

## Living Wage
Wage sufficient for decent standard of living.

## Fair Wage
Wage between minimum and living wage.

## Social Security
Protection against old age, illness, unemployment, and workplace risks.

## EPF
Employees’ Provident Fund.

## ESI
Employees’ State Insurance.

## Capital Market Reform
Reform of securities markets, investor protection, and financial instruments.

## Insolvency Reform
Reform for faster resolution of bankrupt firms.

## Ease of Exit
Ability of firms to close or restructure efficiently.

# 46. DEMOGRAPHY AND ECONOMY

## Demography
Study of population.

## Population Growth
Increase in population.

## Fertility Rate
Average number of children born to a woman.

## Total Fertility Rate
Average number of children expected per woman during reproductive years.

## TFR
Short form of Total Fertility Rate.

## Mortality Rate
Death rate.

## Infant Mortality Rate
Deaths of infants under one year per thousand live births.

## IMR
Short form of Infant Mortality Rate.

## Maternal Mortality Ratio
Maternal deaths per lakh live births.

## MMR
Short form of Maternal Mortality Ratio.

## Life Expectancy
Average years a person is expected to live.

## Dependency Ratio
Ratio of dependent population to working-age population.

## Demographic Dividend
Economic benefit from high share of working-age population.

## Ageing Population
Increase in share of elderly people.

## Migration
Movement of people for work, education, marriage, or distress.

## Urbanisation
Growth of urban population.

## Human Capital Formation
Improving people’s education, health, and skills.

## Population Stabilisation
Achieving stable population growth.

---

# 47. REGIONAL DEVELOPMENT

## Regional Disparity
Unequal development across states or regions.

## Backward Region
Region with low income, infrastructure, health, education, or industrialisation.

## Special Category Status
Earlier classification giving special central assistance to some states with difficult conditions.

## Aspirational District
District targeted for rapid improvement in development indicators.

## Hill Economy
Economy of mountain regions with special constraints.

## Border Area Development
Development of areas near international borders.

## North-Eastern Economy
Economy of north-eastern states, shaped by geography, connectivity, resources, and border trade.

## Coastal Economy
Economy based on ports, fisheries, shipping, tourism, and coastal industries.

## Desert Economy
Economy of arid regions, dependent on water management, livestock, and drought resilience.

## Tribal Economy
Economy of tribal regions based on agriculture, forests, minor forest produce, labour, and local crafts.

## Regional Planning
Planning focused on balanced development of regions.

## Growth Pole
Region or city that drives growth in surrounding areas.

## Industrial Cluster
Geographic concentration of related industries.

## SEZ
Special Economic Zone.

## Economic Corridor
Transport and industrial corridor supporting growth.

---

# 48. INFORMAL ECONOMY

## Informal Economy
Economic activity outside full regulation, taxation, and social security.

## Informal Worker
Worker without formal contract or social protection.

## Informal Enterprise
Small unregistered or lightly regulated business.

## Street Vending
Small-scale retail activity on streets.

## Domestic Work
Paid household work.

## Home-Based Work
Production or services done from home.

## Casual Labour
Daily or temporary wage labour.

## Contract Labour
Workers hired through contractors.

## Social Security Gap
Lack of protection for informal workers.

## Formalisation
Bringing economic activity into formal records, taxation, and social protection.

## GST and Formalisation
GST can encourage formal invoice-based transactions.

## Digital Payments and Formalisation
Digital transactions create records and improve transparency.

## Udyam Registration
Registration system for MSMEs.

## E-Shram Portal
National database for unorganised workers.

---

# 49. MSME ECONOMY

## MSME
Micro, Small and Medium Enterprises.

## Micro Enterprise
Smallest category of enterprise.

## Small Enterprise
Enterprise larger than micro but smaller than medium.

## Medium Enterprise
Enterprise below large enterprise level.

## MSME Importance
MSMEs generate employment, exports, regional development, and entrepreneurship.

## Credit Gap
Shortage of formal credit for MSMEs.

## Collateral-Free Loan
Loan without physical security.

## Credit Guarantee
Guarantee support to encourage lending.

## Delayed Payments
Problem where MSMEs are paid late by buyers.

## TReDS
Trade Receivables Discounting System for MSME invoice financing.

## Cluster-Based Development
Support for MSMEs located in industrial clusters.

## Technology Upgradation
Improving machinery and processes.

## Quality Certification
Certification to meet standards.

## ZED Certification
Zero Defect Zero Effect certification for MSMEs.

## Udyam Portal
Online registration system for MSMEs.

# 50. STARTUPS AND ENTREPRENEURSHIP

## Entrepreneurship
Starting and managing a business with risk-taking and innovation.

## Start-Up
Young business with innovation and growth potential.

## Start-Up Ecosystem
Network of founders, investors, incubators, mentors, customers, and regulators.

## Incubator
Institution supporting early-stage start-ups.

## Accelerator
Programme helping start-ups grow quickly.

## Angel Investor
Individual investing in early-stage start-ups.

## Venture Capital
Investment in high-growth start-ups.

## VC
Short form of Venture Capital.

## Private Equity
Investment in private companies.

## Unicorn
Start-up valued at one billion dollars or more.

## Decacorn
Start-up valued at ten billion dollars or more.

## Bootstrapping
Building a business with own funds.

## Seed Funding
Early-stage start-up funding.

## Series Funding
Rounds of start-up investment.

## Innovation
New product, process, business model, or technology.

## Intellectual Property
Legal rights over creations such as patents, trademarks, and copyrights.

## Patent
Exclusive right over invention.

## Trademark
Legal protection for brand name or symbol.

## Copyright
Legal protection for creative works.

## Geographical Indication
Tag identifying goods linked to a specific region and quality.

## GI Tag
Short form of Geographical Indication tag.

# 51. AGRICULTURE-INDUSTRY-SERVICES LINKAGES

## Sectoral Linkage
Connection between different sectors of economy.

## Forward Linkage
When output of one sector becomes input for another.

## Backward Linkage
When growth in one sector increases demand for inputs from another.

## Agriculture-Industry Linkage
Agriculture supplies raw materials and demand for industry; industry supplies inputs to agriculture.

## Agro-Processing
Industrial processing of agricultural produce.

## Food Processing Industry
Industry processing food products.

## Textile Industry Linkage
Cotton, jute, wool, and silk link agriculture to manufacturing.

## Fertilizer Industry Linkage
Industry supplying inputs to agriculture.

## Tractor Industry Linkage
Manufacturing supporting mechanisation of agriculture.

## Rural Demand
Demand from rural households for industrial goods and services.

## Services Linkage
Services such as finance, transport, storage, insurance, and marketing support agriculture and industry.

---

# 52. ECONOMIC SECURITY

## Economic Security
Protection of economy and citizens from shocks and vulnerabilities.

## Food Security
Access to adequate food.

## Energy Security
Reliable and affordable energy.

## Water Security
Availability of sufficient water.

## Health Security
Protection from health shocks.

## Job Security
Stability of employment.

## Income Security
Stable income support.

## Social Security
Protection against old age, illness, disability, unemployment, and poverty.

## Financial Security
Access to savings, insurance, pension, and credit.

## Cyber Economic Security
Protection of digital financial systems.

## Supply Chain Security
Reliable supply of essential goods.

## Strategic Reserves
Stocks of critical resources for emergencies.

## Buffer Stock
Stock of essential goods such as foodgrains.

# 54. INDIAN ECONOMY AND CONSTITUTION

## Economic Justice
Constitutional goal of reducing economic inequality and exploitation.

## Directive Principles of State Policy
Constitutional principles guiding state policy toward welfare and social justice.

## DPSP
Short form of Directive Principles of State Policy.

## Article 38
Directs state to promote welfare and reduce inequalities.

## Article 39
Directs state policy toward adequate livelihood, equal pay, and preventing concentration of wealth.

## Article 41
Right to work, education, and public assistance within state capacity.

## Article 43
Living wage and decent standard of life for workers.

## Article 43B
Promotion of cooperative societies.

## Article 46
Promotion of educational and economic interests of weaker sections.

## Article 280
Provides for Finance Commission.

## Seventh Schedule
Division of subjects between Union, State, and Concurrent Lists.

## Union List
Subjects mainly under Centre.

## State List
Subjects mainly under states.

## Concurrent List
Subjects where both Centre and states can legislate.

## GST Constitutional Amendment
Amendment creating GST framework and GST Council.

## Money Bill
Bill dealing with taxation, borrowing, expenditure, and Consolidated Fund matters.

## Finance Bill
Bill giving legal effect to tax proposals.

## Appropriation Bill
Bill authorising withdrawal from Consolidated Fund.

## Vote on Account
Temporary approval for government expenditure before full Budget.

## Charged Expenditure
Expenditure not voted by Parliament, though discussed.

## Voted Expenditure
Expenditure requiring parliamentary vote.

# 55. IMPORTANT ECONOMIC TERMS FROM UNION BUDGET

## Budget Estimate
Government estimate of receipts and expenditure for coming year.

## Revised Estimate
Updated estimate for current year.

## Actuals
Final audited figures for past year.

## Capital Outlay
Capital expenditure for creating assets.

## Grants-in-Aid
Transfers to states, institutions, or bodies.

## Revenue Foregone
Tax revenue not collected due to exemptions or concessions.

## Tax Expenditure
Revenue loss due to tax incentives.

## Outcome Budget
Budget linking expenditure with outcomes.

## Gender Budget
Budget statement showing allocations for women.

## Fiscal Roadmap
Plan for fiscal deficit and debt management.

## Gross Borrowing
Total borrowing by government before repayments.

## Net Borrowing
Borrowing after repayments.

## Interest Payment
Payment made on government debt.

## Major Subsidies
Food, fertilizer, and petroleum-related subsidies.

## Centrally Sponsored Scheme Allocation
Funds given for schemes implemented by states.

## Capital Expenditure Multiplier
Larger impact of capital spending on output.

---

# 56. CURRENT ACCOUNT AND RUPEE TERMS

## Exchange Rate Management
RBI action to reduce excessive currency volatility.

## Forex Intervention
Buying or selling foreign exchange by RBI.

## Sterilisation
Offsetting liquidity impact of forex intervention.

## Appreciation Pressure
Pressure for currency value to rise.

## Depreciation Pressure
Pressure for currency value to fall.

## Imported Inflation
Inflation caused by costlier imports due to depreciation or global prices.

## Export Competitiveness
Ability of exports to compete in global markets.

## Terms of Trade
Ratio of export prices to import prices.

## Oil Import Bill
Cost of crude oil and petroleum imports.

## Gold Import
Gold purchases from abroad, affecting trade deficit.

## Remittance Inflow
Money sent by Indians abroad to India.

## Services Surplus
Surplus from export of services over import of services.

## Invisibles
Services, transfers, and income flows in BOP.

## External Sector Resilience
Ability to handle global shocks.

---

# 57. AGRICULTURE RISKS AND INSURANCE

## Crop Risk
Risk of crop loss due to weather, pests, disease, or price fall.

## Drought
Long period of deficient rainfall.

## Flood
Excess water causing crop and property damage.

## Pest Attack
Damage caused by insects or pests.

## Crop Insurance
Insurance protecting farmers against crop loss.

## PMFBY
Pradhan Mantri Fasal Bima Yojana.

## Weather-Based Insurance
Insurance linked to weather parameters.

## Yield-Based Insurance
Insurance based on crop yield loss.

## Price Risk
Risk of fall in crop prices.

## Market Risk
Risk due to uncertain demand, price, or market access.

## Climate Risk
Risk from climate variability and climate change.

## Risk Mitigation
Measures to reduce losses.

## Diversification
Reducing risk by growing multiple crops or income sources.

---

# 58. IMPORTANT ECONOMIC DEBATES IN INDIA

## Growth vs Distribution
Debate between increasing GDP and reducing inequality.

## Growth vs Environment
Debate between economic expansion and ecological protection.

## Subsidy vs Investment
Debate between welfare transfers and capital creation.

## Universalism vs Targeting
Debate on whether benefits should be universal or targeted.

## Cash Transfer vs In-Kind Transfer
Debate on whether welfare should be given as money or goods.

## MSP Reform
Debate on agricultural price support.

## Farm Market Reform
Debate on improving agricultural markets and farmer incomes.

## Labour Reform Debate
Debate on flexibility for firms versus worker protection.

## Fiscal Prudence vs Stimulus
Debate on deficit control versus government spending to support growth.

## Import Substitution vs Export Promotion
Debate on domestic protection versus global competitiveness.

## Manufacturing vs Services
Debate on whether India needs manufacturing-led growth or can continue services-led growth.

## Formalisation Debate
Debate on benefits and costs of moving informal activity into formal economy.

## Privatisation Debate
Debate on efficiency, public interest, and strategic control.

## Freebies Debate
Debate on welfare promises, fiscal sustainability, and social justice.

---

# 59. COMMONLY CONFUSED TERMS

## GDP vs GNP
GDP measures production within domestic territory. GNP measures income of residents including net income from abroad.

## GDP vs GVA
GVA measures value added by sectors. GDP equals GVA plus product taxes minus product subsidies.

## Nominal GDP vs Real GDP
Nominal GDP uses current prices. Real GDP adjusts for inflation.

## Fiscal Deficit vs Revenue Deficit
Fiscal deficit shows total borrowing need. Revenue deficit shows gap in current revenue and current expenditure.

## Primary Deficit vs Fiscal Deficit
Primary deficit excludes interest payments from fiscal deficit.

## Direct Tax vs Indirect Tax
Direct tax is paid by the person on whom imposed. Indirect tax is passed on to consumers.

## CPI vs WPI
CPI measures retail prices faced by consumers. WPI measures wholesale prices.

## Repo Rate vs Reverse Repo Rate
Repo is rate at which RBI lends to banks. Reverse repo is rate at which RBI borrows from banks.

## CRR vs SLR
CRR is cash kept with RBI. SLR is liquid assets kept by banks.

## Bank Rate vs Repo Rate
Bank rate is long-term lending rate without repo agreement. Repo is short-term collateralised lending rate.

## FDI vs FPI
FDI involves lasting control. FPI is investment in financial assets.

## Current Account vs Capital Account
Current account records trade, income, and transfers. Capital/financial account records investment and capital flows.

## Depreciation vs Devaluation
Depreciation is market-driven fall in currency value. Devaluation is official reduction under fixed system.

## Deflation vs Disinflation
Deflation is falling prices. Disinflation is falling inflation rate.

## Stagflation vs Recession
Stagflation is high inflation with low growth. Recession is decline in economic activity.

## Poverty vs Inequality
Poverty is lack of minimum resources. Inequality is unequal distribution.

## Employment vs Labour Force
Employment means working people. Labour force includes employed and unemployed seeking work.

## LFPR vs WPR
LFPR measures labour force participation. WPR measures actual employment.

## MSP vs Procurement Price
MSP is announced support price. Procurement price is actual price paid during government procurement.

## Food Security vs Nutrition Security
Food security means enough food access. Nutrition security means balanced and healthy diet.

## Subsidy vs Transfer
Subsidy reduces price of goods or services. Transfer gives money or benefit directly.

## Capital Expenditure vs Revenue Expenditure
Capital expenditure creates assets or reduces liabilities. Revenue expenditure is current spending.

## Monetary Policy vs Fiscal Policy
Monetary policy is by RBI using money and interest rates. Fiscal policy is by government using taxes and spending.

---

# 60. HIGH-YIELD INDIAN ECONOMY CHRONOLOGY

## Stage 1: Colonial Economic Exploitation
British rule transformed India into a supplier of raw materials and market for British goods, leading to deindustrialisation, drain of wealth, and rural poverty.

## Stage 2: Nationalist Economic Thought
Indian thinkers criticized colonial exploitation and proposed self-reliance, swadeshi, planning, industrialisation, and village economy.

## Stage 3: Early Planning after Independence
India adopted planning, public sector leadership, land reforms, community development, and focus on agriculture and infrastructure.

## Stage 4: Heavy Industry Strategy
Second Five-Year Plan emphasized heavy industries, public sector, and capital goods through Mahalanobis model.

## Stage 5: Food Crisis and Green Revolution
Food shortages led to adoption of HYV seeds, irrigation, fertilizers, and procurement system, increasing foodgrain production.

## Stage 6: Bank Nationalisation and Poverty Focus
Bank nationalisation expanded rural credit and priority lending, while poverty programmes gained importance.

## Stage 7: Public Sector and Licence Raj
State-led industrialisation created capacity but also led to inefficiency, controls, and limited competition.

## Stage 8: 1991 Balance of Payments Crisis
External crisis forced India to adopt liberalisation, privatisation, and globalisation reforms.

## Stage 9: Post-Reform Growth
India saw higher growth, services expansion, foreign investment, financial sector reforms, and greater integration with global economy.

## Stage 10: Rights-Based Welfare
Policies such as employment guarantee, food security, education, and information rights expanded welfare entitlements.

## Stage 11: Fiscal and Tax Reforms
FRBM, VAT, GST, direct tax reforms, and fiscal consolidation reshaped public finance.

## Stage 12: Digital and Financial Inclusion Era
Jan Dhan, Aadhaar, UPI, DBT, digital payments, fintech, and digital public infrastructure transformed delivery and payments.

## Stage 13: Manufacturing and Infrastructure Push
Make in India, PLI, industrial corridors, logistics reforms, and infrastructure pipelines aimed to strengthen production.

## Stage 14: Green and Sustainable Economy
Renewable energy, green hydrogen, climate finance, electric mobility, and circular economy became major policy themes.

## Stage 15: Inclusive and Resilient Growth
Current economic thinking emphasizes jobs, human capital, social protection, resilience, formalisation, innovation, and sustainable development.

---

# 61. HIGH-YIELD UPSC REVISION CLUSTER

## Must Remember Core Sectors
Primary, Secondary, and Tertiary.

## Must Remember GDP Formula
GDP can be measured by production, income, and expenditure methods.

## Must Remember GDP-GVA Link
GDP equals GVA plus product taxes minus product subsidies.

## Must Remember Poverty Concepts
Absolute poverty, relative poverty, poverty line, headcount ratio, multidimensional poverty.

## Must Remember Employment Indicators
LFPR, WPR, unemployment rate, usual status, CWS, CDS, PLFS.

## Must Remember Agriculture Issues
Small holdings, monsoon dependence, MSP, procurement, irrigation, credit, marketing, storage, crop diversification.

## Must Remember Green Revolution
HYV seeds, irrigation, fertilizers, wheat-rice focus, regional imbalance.

## Must Remember Food Security
PDS, TPDS, NFSA, FCI, buffer stock, MSP procurement.

## Must Remember Industry Policy
1956 public sector emphasis and 1991 liberalisation.

## Must Remember 1991 Reforms
Liberalisation, privatisation, globalisation.

## Must Remember RBI Tools
Repo, reverse repo, CRR, SLR, OMO, LAF, MSF, SDF.

## Must Remember Inflation Measures
CPI, WPI, GDP deflator, core inflation, headline inflation.

## Must Remember Fiscal Deficit
Government borrowing requirement.

## Must Remember Revenue Deficit
Revenue expenditure exceeding revenue receipts.

## Must Remember Primary Deficit
Fiscal deficit excluding interest payments.

## Must Remember GST
Destination-based value-added indirect tax.

## Must Remember Finance Commission
Constitutional body for tax devolution and grants.

## Must Remember External Sector
Exports, imports, CAD, BOP, forex reserves, exchange rate.

## Must Remember FDI vs FPI
FDI is long-term control-oriented investment. FPI is financial investment.

## Must Remember Financial Markets
Money market is short term. Capital market is long term.

## Must Remember SEBI
Regulates securities market.

## Must Remember IBC
Framework for insolvency resolution.

## Must Remember NPA
Loan that has stopped generating regular repayment.

## Must Remember Inclusive Growth
Growth with poverty reduction, jobs, financial inclusion, social justice, and regional balance.

## Must Remember Digital Economy
UPI, Aadhaar, DBT, JAM, fintech, digital public infrastructure.

## Must Remember Sustainable Development
Climate action, renewable energy, green finance, circular economy, and resource efficiency.

## Must Remember One-Line Essence
Indian Economy is the story of transition from a colonial, agrarian, low-income economy to a planned mixed economy, then to a liberalised and globally integrated economy, now focused on inclusive growth, digital transformation, manufacturing, infrastructure, human development, and sustainability.
